However, in the portion of Shemini and the like, which is a command and a law, the Torah speaks clearly. From this it is understood that just as a person is obligated to speak in clean language, in the first case so too...

With blessings for success in your holy work and for good tidings.

## 3118

B"H, 26 Nissan, 5715
Brooklyn

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, learned, and diligent worker for the community, Rabbi Mordechai [Rich], may he live.

Peace and blessing!

After a long interruption, I was pleased to read your letter of [date], along with the attached clippings and photos. I read with joy about the success of the *chanukas habayis* of the *yeshiva*. From this, one can be convinced again and again that the Jewish heart is always awake to Torah and *mitzvos*, provided one approaches it with the appropriate words and in a suitable manner. This will surely give courage to all those who participated in the *chanukas habayis* and the preparations to continue doing more, with greater measure and with more strength. This will also certainly add to and increase the blessings of Hashem Yisbarach and success in this, especially since the *yeshiva* is a matter that affects the *rabim* (the many), and the *zechus harabim* is dependent upon them.

I hope it is unnecessary to draw the attention of all the helpers and workers of the *yeshiva* to the fact that one must guard against anything that could be interpreted as partisan (political), even if that party might be considered appropriate by some of the workers. This is to ensure that there is no weakening, even in the slightest degree, of the crossing of the *yeshiva’s* threshold by all Jews who uphold Torah and *mitzvos*, regardless of party affiliation. This has always been the foundation of the success of Lubavitch’s work in various countries and at various times: to conduct the work strictly non-partisan. I hope that you, too, will agree with me in what has been said above, and this will provide enough material to ensure the scope and work of the *yeshiva* is guarded, so that no one can say that it belongs to one party more than to another.

In accordance with your request, I will mention you and all your household members, about whom you write, at the *tziyun* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, *ztzukulleh"h, nbg"m, zi"a*. The *zechus* of your work on behalf of the holy institution *Ohalei Yosef Yitzchok Lubavitch*, which is named after him, will surely assist you all, so that my father-in-law, the Rebbe, may awaken *rachamei shamayim* (heavenly mercy) for each of you regarding what everyone needs, both materially and spiritually.

With blessings for health and for good tidings.

## 3119

B"H, 27 Nissan, 5715
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Rabbi, G-d-fearing, and distinguished scholar, etc., Moreinu Harav Moshe, may he live:

Peace and blessing!

I acknowledge receipt of your letter from Sunday. Perhaps I did not explain my words in my previous letter as clearly as I should have, and it is as follows:

Regarding the Responsa, section 1: I emphasized in my writing that one does not act leniently, even in a time of great need (*sha'as hadchak*), regarding the **decree** of "lest he cast." And since we do not decree a decree upon a decree, this opinion proves that the prohibition of placing wool threads in a linen *tallis* is *d'oraisa*.

Regarding the Responsa, section 58: Concerning old *matzah*, I omitted in my letter the proof that we make an *eruv* for the entire year, which even permits *Shabbos HaGadol*. After the words *Shabbos HaGadol*, there should be the three words "even in a leap year," which is more than twelve months.

Incidentally, regarding the proof that your honor brought in this response—that *matzah* must have a taste of *matzah*—from *Chullin* 121a: It is surprising that you did not cite *Berachos* 38b, where it is explicitly stated that it must have the taste of *matzah*. This is unlike *Chullin*, where the reason is that the *mitzvah* is not "bread of affliction," as the language of the *Gemara* puts it, or because it is not considered bread at all (see there in the *Hagahos Shita Mekubetzes* and in *Tzafnas Paneach* on the *Rambam*, *Hilchos Chametz U’Matzah*, chapter 7, law 6 and law 2).

Likewise, regarding what you noted in that response concerning the words of the *Yerushalmi*—why should we say that one is not careful regarding *chametz* with old *matzah*?—it is explicit in the *Shas* there that it is because it was not made for the sake of *Pesach* (similar to the *Mishnah* in *Sukkah*, chapter 1, *mishnah* 2). Based on this, the proof of the *Ra'avan* is clarified: that it is exactly the same with the *matzah* of the *eruv*, for since it is not guarded from *chametz* throughout the year, it also requires *biur*.

With great respect and blessing.

***

 And this has already been questioned from the *Yerushalmi*, *Pesachim*, chapter 2, *mishnah* 4, where it is stated that it does not need to have the taste of grain. (There is a lengthy discussion on this in *Responsa Ta'amei Yitzchak*, *Orach Chaim*, section 19 (Warsaw, 5686)).

 And what is written in the *Bach* at the end of section 461, s.v. *U'v'matzah hasruyah*, requires further study.

B"H, 27 Nissan, 5715

I am certain you will include this in your next letter.

With blessings for good tidings in all the above,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita

## 3221

B"H, 27 Nissan, 5715
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter from before the holiday of Pesach, in which you write that you do not see a sign of blessing in your studies, etc., and therefore you have various thoughts regarding your future arrangements, and you write the details regarding this.

Regarding what you wrote—that you do not see a sign of blessing in your learning—according to the words of our Sages, "If one says, 'I have labored and not found,' do not believe him; 'I have not labored and have found,' do not believe him; 'I have labored and found,' believe him." The intent here is *his* labor—meaning, he should study in a manner appropriate to his own strengths and talents, and he should toil and labor in Torah. It is understood that a person with good talents does not fulfill this obligation by studying like someone with average talents, for in relation to his own capacity, he is not truly laboring. And since a person cannot testify about himself, the truth of the matter can be known from his *mashpia* and his *mashgiach*, for they know him, his talents, his diligence, and his persistence.

Regarding the proposals you write about, you should consult with three of *anash* who know you and are familiar with the local matters. May the *Ribono shel Olam* grant them the correct insight to advise you in a way that is good for you, both materially and spiritually.

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,
Secretary

***

**To consult with three:** See regarding this *Igros Kodesh* of the Rebbe Rashab, Vol. 3, letter 898.

See below 3235-6, 3294.

## 322

322

## 3223

3223

B.H., 28 Nissan, 5715
Brooklyn

To the participants of the Gemara shiur at the Tzemach Tzedek Nusach HaAri Synagogue here in New York, and in particular to those who lead the shiur, the esteemed Rabbi, the accomplished scholar, G-d-fearing and learned, Rabbi Yechezkel and Rabbi Gershon, may they live:

Greetings and blessings!

It was with pleasure that I received your letter informing me that on the upcoming Shabbos, Rosh Chodesh Iyar, you will be completing Maseches Rosh Hashanah. May it be the will of Hashem, in the accepted and traditional phrasing, that just as you complete this Maseches, so too may Hashem help you to begin other Masechtos and sefarim, and to complete them, to learn and to teach, to observe and to perform, etc. May the learning be with an expansion of the mind, and in such a way that through the study of Torah, the Giver of the Torah is felt, as is explained in many places in the maamarim of Chassidus, that the inner dimension of Torah is the "soul of the Torah."

Regarding the topic of the day, concerning the conclusion of the Maseches:

"Rabban Gamliel would exempt even the people in the fields, and it goes without saying those who are standing here. On the contrary, these are coerced [by distance/circumstance], while these are not coerced. For it was taught, etc., that the people behind the Kohanim are not included in the blessing, unless, etc. Rabban Gamliel only exempted the people in the fields, etc."

One can explain the initial assumption (*kas'd*) and the final conclusion (*maskana*) as follows: The matter of tefillah and the shaliach tzibbur who prays on behalf of others is the request for human needs, and the one who descends before the ark acts as their agent. Therefore, on the face of it, it is simple—and based on the words of our Sages—that one may perform a merit for a person even in his absence (*zakin l'adam shelo bifanav*). This is certainly true, and all the more so, when the one performing the merit has some connection with the one for whom he intends to perform the merit. This is the reason for the initial assumption that the shaliach tzibbur exempts even the people in the fields, even though there is no connection between them, for after all, one may perform a merit for a person in his absence. And it goes without saying for those standing here—where the one performing the merit is right next to the recipient of the merit.

However, the Gemara challenges this, stating that there is a logic to the contrary: "On the contrary, these are coerced, while these are not coerced." This is based on the known principle that although one may perform a merit for a person in his absence, one may not perform a merit for him against his will. Since these people are not coerced, yet they did not arrange their own prayer, this is a matter of "against his will." But since it is not truly "against his will," but rather it is evident that he does not value the matter of prayer—only that it is *similar* to being against his will—the Gemara brings a proof to strengthen this argument and logic, *a fortiori* (*kal v'chomer*).

To understand this, we must first note the distinction between Birchas Kohanim and tefillah. Tefillah is dependent upon the person, for it is he who is pleading and requesting. It is understood that according to how one prepares himself for this, so too will his request be fulfilled. This is not the case with Birchas Kohanim, where the Kohanim bless as agents of the Makom and by His command, as it is written, "Thus shall you bless," etc., and as in the prayer of the Kohanim after Nesias Kapayim: "We have done what You have decreed upon us." From this, it is understood that the preparation of the person is not relevant here, for the hand of Hashem is not shortened even if the person does not prepare himself for it. And yet, it is taught that the people behind the Kohanim are not included in the blessing. This means that even though the blessing comes from Hakadosh Baruch Hu, some preparation must exist on the part of the recipient of the blessing—at the very least, that he stands "face to face," which indicates an affinity of mind toward the matter, and not otherwise. If this is the case for a blessing that comes from Above, and the Kohanim cannot grant merit to those standing behind them because they are not "coerced" in this, then all the more so is this the law regarding tefillah, the essence of which is the person's preparation for his avodah—as it is written, "And to serve Him with all your heart"—"Which is the service of the heart? This is tefillah" (Taanis 2a). Therefore, the conclusion is that Rabban Gamliel only exempted the people in the fields, etc.

From this, one can also understand the concept of "the end is embedded in the beginning, and the beginning in the end"—that this applies to the Torah as a whole, and to every specific part of it. Just as at the conclusion of the Maseches the two extremes are reconciled—the blessing that comes from Above as a free gift, and the fulfillment of human needs which depends on one's avodah and toil, for the Torah is **one** for us, and all its matters are included within one another—so too is it in the avodah of the soul, and so too is it in time. There are two types, as at the beginning of the Maseches: there are two types of "New Years." Those that come from Above without human avodah, such as the first of Tishrei, which is from the beginning of Creation; and the first of Nissan, which was established at the Exodus from Egypt, when by virtue of faith, etc., they were redeemed, etc. (unlike other New Years, which depend on the nature of Creation). These two types are also included in one another, for the first of Tishrei, the Rosh Hashanah for the kingship of the King, Hakadosh Baruch Hu—whose own Rosh Hashanah is the first of Nissan—is like a reflection (and an extension) of the Kingship of the Heavens.

With respect and blessings that Hashem should increase and multiply the number of participants in the shiurim and strengthen the learning, as it is written, "He shall magnify Torah and make it glorious."

## 3205

B"H, 28 Nissan, 5715
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter from 18 Nissan—which was received after a significant delay—I will, as you requested, mention you and all those you wrote about at the resting place of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory. It seems to me that you wrote to me some time ago regarding all these matters, and therefore it is surprising that you do not mention in this letter your study of the revealed Torah and your study of the inner dimension of the Torah—which is called in the holy Zohar the "soul of the Torah"—namely, the teachings of Chassidus. For the Torah is our life and the length of our days, and nothing departs from its simple meaning, which is that it is our life even in this physical world; it is the vessel and the container for receiving the blessings of Hashem, may He be blessed, in all that is needed for a person and his household, may they live.

And although the engagement in spreading Torah, which you write about in your letter, is incomparably great, it is also said regarding this: "Is it not to share your bread with the hungry... when you see the naked, that you cover him?" Our Sages in Tanna D'bei Eliyahu explain that this refers to when one sees a person who is hungry for Torah and naked of mitzvos; one must satisfy his hunger and cover his nakedness. The verse concludes, "and do not hide yourself from your own flesh," for one must increase from time to time in one's own efforts, both in the study of Torah and in the performance of mitzvos with *hiddur*, for these are the matters that pertain to one's own body. Hashem, may He be blessed, provides every person with the ability to accomplish both of these matters together.

Regarding the specific matters you wrote about: you, as well as your wife, may she live, should set aside money for *tzedakah* every weekday before *davening*. Your wife, may she live, should, in addition to this, also give a few coins to *tzedakah* before lighting candles every *Erev Shabbos* and *Erev Yom Tov*, specifically for *hachnasas kallah* and for an institution of education based on *taharas hakodesh*. The measure of the Holy One, blessed be He, is "measure for measure," only many times over, regarding *shidduchim* and an increase in the *yiras shamayim* of your sons and daughters. May Hashem, may He be blessed, grant you success in bringing good news regarding all the above, in good health.

With blessings for good tidings.

329

B”H, Tiferes sheb’Tiferes, 5715
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the participants of the founding meeting of Tzeirei Agudas Chabad in New York, may they live:

Peace and blessing!

I was pleased to receive the report of your first meeting, where, immediately following the farbrengen of Shabbos Mevarchim Chodesh Ziv, you began to engage in the invaluable work of the Tzeirei Agudas Chabad organization—in accordance with the directives of our holy Nasi’im, that the purpose of meetings is to ensure that the inspiration is carried forward and translated into actual deed. This is, of course, also understood from various matters in Torah, where there should be no interruption between the inspiration and the commencement of the action. We learn this as well from the custom we follow—the festival of Pesach—where, at the very beginning of its observances, the *bedikas chametz*, there is no interruption between the *bracha* (which is the inspiration and the drawing down of influence from above) and the act of the search itself. From this, it is also understood that one cannot be satisfied with the activities of the meeting alone, for the intention is to extend these activities outward as well.

Regarding your inquiry about the program of your work and activities—the question and doubt are surprising, as these matters have been detailed in many sichos and at many farbrengens. Especially since Tzeirei Agudas Chabad in Eretz Yisrael has been active for some years now, and as was discussed at the aforementioned farbrengen—you should learn from their accomplishments, and so on.

Nevertheless, to fulfill your request, I have brought down, at least in a few points, a summary:

In general, the work of a person—and you are called "Adam" (man)—is the matter of *kibush* (conquest). As the Mishnah states (end of Kiddushin): "I was created to serve my Creator." The purpose of this service is the ultimate purpose of the creation of the world: that the Holy One, blessed be He, desired to have a dwelling place in the lower worlds. One must conquer the "lower worlds"—that is, the world at large, and this "small world" which is the person in particular—so that they become fit to be a dwelling place for Him, and to actually make them a dwelling place in practice.

From this it is understood that the work, and your work in particular, is divided into two: work with others and work within oneself. And these two are actually four: work with the "other" in the other, and the "inner" in the other; and work with the "inner" in oneself, and the "other" in oneself. My intention here, regarding yourselves and your inner selves:

You are from the community of Chassidei Chabad, and your inner work is in the matters of Chassidus—strengthening and expanding the study of the Torah of Chassidus (the inner dimension of Torah), walking in its ways and customs, and having *hislahavus* and *chayus* in the performance of *mitzvos* in general. This is in addition to maintaining and expanding the study of the revealed Torah and being precise in the fulfillment of *mitzvos*, and so on. Likewise, in the work with others: regarding their "revealed" aspect—influencing them in the study of Torah and the fulfillment of *mitzvos*. And regarding their "inner" aspect—to inform them and teach them well, "set before them" the matters of the Torah of Chassidus, its guidance and customs, and to explain to them that in these days it is a **mitzvah** to reveal these matters, and every single Jew is obligated in them. It is precisely through this that the Jewish people will emerge from exile with mercy and merit the fulfillment of the prophecy, "They shall all know Me, from the smallest to the greatest," and it is written, "And it shall come to pass afterward that I will pour out My spirit upon all flesh, and your sons and daughters shall prophesy."

It is already known that all of the above must be founded upon *ahavas Yisrael*. Therefore, one must strive with every single Jew, regardless of their current state, for they will certainly improve, in accordance with the promise of the one who brings them out, "that no one shall be cast away from Him."

It must be founded upon *ahavas Hashem*, for which reason one must bring every single Jew close to the love of Him (which also includes *yirah*).

And it must be founded upon *ahavas haTorah*, for which reason one must permeate every place with the study of Torah.

As further examples of work with others, one should note: the repeating of *maamarim* of *d'chassidus* in synagogues, the connection with yeshiva students in general and the study of the Torah of Chassidus with them in particular, the connection with students of Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim and students of other yeshivos—after they have left the walls of the yeshiva, the distribution of books and *maamarim* printed from the Torah of our holy Nasi’im, and the like.

Many of these activities are already being done in various ways by *anash*, and the Tzeirei Agudas Chabad should assist in strengthening these matters and expanding them both in quantity and quality, and that they should be done in an organized manner, for then the benefit will be more complete.

The sign of anything living is its growth, development, and evolution—and by its own strength as well, not only through constant inspiration bestowed upon it. So it is also regarding your work—that the work itself will bring about and generate new points for action, and you will be inspired from time to time with additions, not only in the matters done until now, but also in new types of work.

***

It is understood that in truth, as written at the beginning of the letter, all of the above is the duty of every single Jew. As is known from the saying of our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe (the *Baal HaTanya*—the authority on the hidden dimension of Torah—and the *Shulchan Aruch*—the authority on the revealed dimension of Torah) that Chassidus is the portion and inheritance of every single Jew. From time to time, the knowledge of Hashem increases, as the Sages relate: "When it draws close to the days of Mashiach, even the children of the world are destined to find the secrets of wisdom," until, ultimately, "all shall know Me." However, those who have merited and are already actively engaged in the Torah of Chassidus—its inner dimension, guidance, and customs—upon them specifically is placed the holy work to prepare the hearts and to spread the wellsprings into the midst of all the sons and daughters of Israel, until they spread also outward. And all those who possess additional strength and energy, and whose contact and connection with the matters of this world are slight—the measure of their responsibility is according to their strength, and their portion in this work is greater.

Therefore, the youth and the young, who possess these two qualities: additional energy and strength, and less involvement in the matters of this world—it is for them to take the lead in all the details of this work (in accordance with the directive of the elders, and as is known from the Sages regarding the "tearing down of elders," and all the more so—the "building of elders").

And those who work are promised, by the decree of the Heavenly Court, that because of the *mesiras nefesh* of the founder of the Chabad Chassidic path, our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe, their hand will be on top in every matter of Torah, *yiras shamayim*, and good character traits.

With blessings for success in your holy work, and with true joy.

**M. Schneerson**

## 330

B"H, 2 Iyar, 5715
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 28 Nissan, in which you write that you feel tired after studying with your students: surely there are ways to arrange a short break in the middle of the studies, or to ensure that you are properly rested before the studies begin. When one takes hold of the natural way, success is bestowed even beyond the natural way.

Regarding *shidduchim*, one must be precise about the essential matters concerning the prospective partner. When one does so, the secondary matters—and certainly the secondary of the secondary and the external of the external—will not occupy any place at all. As is known, when the *pnimiyus* (inner essence) is revealed, the *chitzoniyus* (externality) is nullified—*farlirt zich in gantzen* (it loses itself entirely). With such an approach, the trials and imagined obstacles will certainly be nullified, and consequently, you will find your proper *zivug* (match) before you, in both material and spiritual matters, very soon. In the vast majority of cases, one eventually realizes that in terms of externality, too, the match is suitable and good.

With blessings for success in all the above, in good health.

## 3,432

3,432

B”H, 2 Iyar, 5715
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter—which lacks a date—in which you write regarding your situation and livelihood, noting that Hashem can provide a livelihood in any place, etc.:

This is certainly true. Therefore, it is also understood that one cannot set conditions for the Ribono shel Olam, insisting that it must be in the specific place that a person prefers. Rather, one must accept it as Hashem directs—not necessarily in the place one prefers, but in the place where Divine Providence brings him, and where he can accomplish more for Yiddishkeit and for a fellow Jew. Through this, one increases the blessings of Hashem in the areas where a Jew—he and his descendants—are in need.

This is the way of the Holy One, blessed be He: *middah k’neged middah* (measure for measure). When one is in a place where there are not many who are in need of the help of another, one cannot claim that merit and blessing. But one can hope that when Hashem sees that one is helping a fellow Jew to bring him closer to Torah and mitzvos—and especially when this is done in a place where there are few who engage in such work—that Hashem will help him in the things he needs many times over.

May Hashem help you to settle in well, in the place that is most fitting for the Holy One, blessed be He, and in a manner that is pleasing to the Holy One, blessed be He—which is the best place for all concerned, both materially and spiritually.

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

Secretary

## 3,733

B”H, 2 Iyar, 5715
Brooklyn

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing and refined, whose work is the work of Heaven,
Moreinu HaRav Schneur Zalman, may he live and be well,

Greetings and blessings!

Following the long interval, I was pleased to receive your letter of the 25th and 26th of Nissan. I have already conveyed, in detail, through the esteemed Chossid, Rabbi Nissan [Nemnov], may he live and be well, that each and every one of you must engage with all your energy and all your strength in the matter of educating the *avreichim* arriving from Morocco. For this is now the holy task: to make this country a receptacle for the Torah of the Baal Shem Tov and his students, and primarily for the Chassidus of Chabad. It depends on them—that they should be the channels and *shluchim* to disseminate the *maayanos* throughout the entire country through the *avreichim* who have come to them. It is a pity to lose even a single moment that is not utilized to its fullest for this holy *shlichus*.

There is room to say that if these aforementioned *avreichim* are educated as they should be, it will be possible to influence through them all our Sephardic brethren who currently find themselves in great confusion and, in my opinion, at a crossroads. Their situation is well-known, both in Eretz Yisrael (may it be rebuilt and established) and in Morocco and its environs. When Divine Providence has chosen four or five people and given them the opportunity to establish hundreds of thousands of Chassidim in a short time, it is a most staggering matter. Yet, despite all this, it has dragged on for several months and even years... And how long will such conduct continue? For "He is standing behind our wall," etc. It is also understood and simple that the magnitude of the reward for anyone who engages in this as they should is beyond expression—both in spiritual matters and in material matters, and certainly regarding physical health.

It is understood that all that has been said above is not directed to him alone; rather, he is a *shaliach* to disseminate this among all his colleagues, the *Roshei Yeshiva* and *Roshei Yeshiva*. May the words act in accordance with the situation as it is, and may he be a *shaliach* to hasten the matter as much as possible.

With blessings for health and success in all the above.

P.S. Regarding your thought to travel here for the upcoming *Yomim Nora’im*, the matter is certainly correct, even though it is of little account compared to the matters mentioned above. You should notify us here of the names and all necessary information, and the request will be sent to you. It is understood that this is all on the condition that your wife (may she live and be well) agrees to it.

With blessings for success in all the above, and for detailed good news soon.

## 3335

B"H, 3 Iyar, 5715
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed and distinguished Rabbi Nassan Dovid, may he live,

Shalom u’Bracha!

In response to your letter in which you inquire regarding the *nekudos* (vowel points) according to the teachings of *Chasidus* and *Nistar*.

Regarding their holiness—and not only the holiness of the points themselves, but even the holiness of their names—it is understood from what is written in *Tikkunei Zohar*, *Tikkun* 5, in the Introduction (7b), and in *Tikkun* 69, and in *Zohar Chadash* (99c) in the *Tikkunim*, that even their names are acronyms for angels.

Regarding their *gematria*, it is according to their form: each *nekudah* (dot) is ten, and each *kav* (line) is six. Therefore, for example, *tzeirei* (..) is twenty, and so on. For an example, see the Introduction to *Tikkunei Zohar*, where *kamatz* has a *gematria* of sixteen, and so forth.

Enclosed is a copy of what was recently printed, which I am certain you will study, as it is relevant to the content.

Sometimes the *nekudos* are calculated according to their **names**, as in the Introduction to *Tikkunei Zohar* mentioned above (7b): *pasach*, when calculating its letters, is *yud* (ten). As the commentators explain, the letters of the **name** of this *nekudah* have a *gematria* of twenty (in *mispar katan*).

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,
Secretary

3335
Published in *Likkutei Sichos*, Vol. 16, p. 574, and completed based on the secretariat’s copy.

**Rabbi Nassan Dovid:** Rosenblum. Additional letters to him: above, Vol. 10, 3225, 3222; below, 3383.

**The holiness of their names:** See also above, letter 3289, and the references in the notes there.

## 3335

B"H, 3 Iyar, 5715
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed and distinguished individual, occupied with communal needs, Moreinu HaRav Yosef, may he live:

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letter from Erev Shabbos Kodesh, at the conclusion of the month marked by miracles and the beginning of the month of Ziv, in which the "radiance of the world" were born—it gave me pleasure to read that you are engaging in holy work in the field of proper chinuch, and specifically in the new district of the city of Chicago. May it be the will of Hashem that you are not discouraged by the difficulties common to such matters, in accordance with the teaching of our Sages that "all beginnings are difficult." On the contrary, this should awaken in you additional strength and the revelation of hidden powers. As is also known from recent discoveries in medical science, in order for the body to withstand severe illnesses (Heaven forbid), they inject into it a faint semblance of that very illness. Through this, the body develops weapons and defenses against the illness so that it does not enter its borders at all; this is what is called vaccination. It is the same regarding the healing of the soul, as is known from the statement of the great teacher, our Rabbi the Rambam, in his *Shemonah Perakim*, regarding the analogy between the healing of the soul and the healing of the body: through a faint, imagined concealment, the soul creates weapons and defenses that nullify actual concealments and obstructions.

May it be the will of Hashem that you succeed in your aforementioned work, to sow and to plant also in the quarter of the city where you intend to establish a proper house of chinuch, and may you instill in the students a love for Hashem, a love for the Torah, and a love for a fellow Jew. It is already known that even in our days, the verse applies: "Avraham was one, and he inherited the land"—and his "seed" refers not only to children in the following generation, but also to his planting and the results of his actions.

Surely you are familiar with the saying of our Rebbes, the Nesi'im: "As one sets oneself up, so it goes." Consequently, you should acquire a suitable plot for a spacious building, and the building itself should be in such a manner, as the verse emphasizes: "Expand your mouth and I will fill it."

With a blessing, as per the saying of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, for a healthy summer for you and your wife, may they live.

## 3337

B"H, 3 Iyar, 5715
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter of 24 Nissan, in which you write regarding the situation of, etc.

Beyond the adherence to the natural path—where one must seek the opinion of a specialist doctor in this field and follow his instructions, for the Torah has granted permission to the physician to heal—you must check the mezuzos in your home, as well as your own tefillin, to ensure they are kosher. Furthermore, in addition to the three daily study portions established by my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory—the Chumash, Tehillim, and Tanya, which are well-known—I am certain you are keeping them.

It is appropriate that every weekday, before davening, you should give a few coins to tzedakah. In addition to all the above, you should strive to fulfill the teaching of our Sages that talmidei chachamim ("all your children shall be learned of Hashem," and see also the introduction to the *Chavas Da'as* on Yoreh De'ah regarding the title *talmid chacham*) increase peace in the world. The precision of the word **increase** (*marbim*) is explained as having no limit, for as much as one occupies oneself with this, it is always possible to add more, as is evident in practice. The measure of the Ribono shel Olam is "measure for measure," to increase peace within your borders—peace in the literal sense, and peace in the *pamalya shel mata*, etc., as explained in *Likutei Torah*, Parshas Matos, in the *maamar* beginning *Hechalutzu*.

With blessings for good tidings in all the above.

## 3339

B"H, 3 Iyar, 5715
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed and distinguished one, engaged in the work of Heaven,
Rabbi Yerahmiel, may he live,

Peace and blessing!

In response to your inquiry regarding the custom of the haircut (*upsherin*) at three years of age, and bringing the child to Meron thereafter:

This custom is cited in several Sefardic books, and in their works of *drush* there are many specific discourses regarding this celebration, which is called *chalakah*. It is also mentioned briefly in *Pri Etz Chaim*, *Shaar Sefirat HaOmer*, Chapter 7, that the Arizal went there to cut his son’s hair with a feast and celebration during those days. See also *Be'er Heitev* and *Shaarei Teshuvah*, *Orach Chaim*, Section 531, subsection 2. It appears that the haircut should not be performed before the child has completed three years. Consequently, this also addresses your question regarding your son, may he live. It should be noted that there are apparently places where the Sefardim have the custom of doing this upon the completion of four years, but we have heard several times from my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, to perform it upon the completion of three years.

In the printed books of *Chassidus*, this is found in the *Siddur Maharid*, at the end of Volume 1, in the *maamar* entitled "The custom to cut the hair of a three-year-old boy."

Regarding delaying the haircut for several months in order to perform it on Lag B'Omer in Meron: If that is the custom in Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established, then "a custom overrides [a law]." If not, it does not seem appropriate to me to have such a long delay for a matter "with which one educates him in the mitzvah of leaving the corners of the head" (*Shaarei Teshuvah*, ibid.).

With blessing.

***

**Rabbi Yerahmiel:** Alperovitz.

**The haircut... to Meron:** Regarding the custom of the haircut on Lag B'Omer, see above, Vol. 9, Letter 2824, and the references in the footnotes there. See also above, Letter 3384.

Regarding the custom of the haircut upon the completion of three years, see the journal *Yagdil Torah* (New York), Issue 48, Section 70.

## 3440

[4 Iyar, 5715]

... 3) Regarding evening classes for working youth: I have already written to several of anash that it is not the business of Chabad activists to disseminate secular studies, nor is it their business to provide endorsements for schools in general, and especially not in the aforementioned case. However, if there is a possibility that those who are studying secular subjects can also be reached to disseminate Jewish studies in general, and the teachings of Chassidus in particular, one should strive to do so **all the more so**, but in a manner that does **not** serve as an endorsement for a school that is not desirable. It is not advisable for one to rely on his own judgment—rather, one should consult with those of anash who are on-site and clarify the points that require caution, as explained above.

## 3,743

## 3449

B"H, 4 Iyar, 5715
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

Following yet another long silence, your letter finally arrived, written on the day of *Malchus sheb’Gevurah*. May it be Hashem’s will that you also make use of the *sefirah* of *Netzach*—that is, to be victorious over the concealments and obstructions that hinder a person’s *avodah* to their Creator, and to likewise overcome the reasons that prevent you from writing detailed letters with good news, both in material and spiritual matters.

I was pleased to hear about the organization of the *Sedarim* in the *beis medrash*, and that every *ke'arah* had *matzah shemurah*. Certainly, according to what is explained in *Chassidus*—that the *hemshech* (drawing down) from every *mo'ed* and *regel* must have a tangible effect until the next *chag*—you will strive to strengthen the channel and the vessels through which the *hisorerus* of *Leil Shimurim* is drawn down throughout the entire year.

I believe I have already prompted you previously regarding the benefit of transcribing your talks on matters of *hisorerus* for *Torah u’mitzvos* and *yiras shamayim*. If you do so, others will be able to utilize them as well, which is not the case when the words remain only oral.

I was pleased to hear that it is possible that this year you will again be invited to the camp... as you were last year. In my opinion, it is not advisable to rely on what is "possible," but rather to strive in a diplomatic manner to ensure that this invitation comes to fruition. There is a *chazakah* (presumption) that *ta'amulah* (outreach) does not return empty, especially when it concerns the youth, whose involvement in matters of business, livelihood, etc., is still minimal or has not yet begun at all.

In connection with *Chag HaPesach*, a letter was also sent to Mrs. ... to be delivered by you. Surely, if she requires explanation, you will find the appropriate words for this. In doing so, you will have another opportunity to inspire her regarding what has been said—and what the Baal Shem Tov emphasized—that one should "serve Hashem with joy." Every word written there is precise: there must be *avodas Hashem*, and it must also be with *simchah*. Especially since we see tangibly that through this, many undesirable concealments and obstacles are nullified and dissipate of their own accord.

With blessings for good tidings in all the above.

## 3745

B"H, 4 Iyar, 5715
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and distinguished individual, occupied with communal needs, R' Shmuel Chaim, may he live:

Peace and blessing!

...Regarding what you wrote concerning the text of the davening and how to explain this to those who are davening: You should examine the introduction to *Shaar HaKollel*, where he quotes our Nasi, the Rebbe, that the *nusach* of the Arizal is a *nusach* that is appropriate for every soul. Regarding the *nusach*, in *Responsa Maharashdam*, Orach Chaim section, he rules that it is permitted to change from *nusach Ashkenaz* to *Sefard*, and likewise in *Responsa Divrei Chaim*, Part 2, Orach Chaim, siman 8. As for the difficulties raised regarding this in *Chasam Sofer*, Orach Chaim and Yoreh Deah sections, and *Responsa Minchas Elazar*, Part 1, siman 11, they addressed all the difficulties, and their conclusion is that it is permitted to change from *nusach Ashkenaz* to *Sefard*, but there is no opinion that permits changing from *nusach Sefard* to *Ashkenaz*.

With blessing.

## 3747

B"H, 5 Iyar, 5715
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

...Regarding what you wrote concerning the questions people ask him about the details of customs, etc...

As for these questions, it is well known from the statement in the Zohar, cited in Iggeres HaKodesh, that "every question comes from the 'other side' [sitra achra]," etc. This is in addition to the well-known saying that "a mere questioner [makshan]..." (cited in the index of the Responsa Chavos Yair, though I do not have it at hand). In the present case, we have seen tangibly that the questioners’ questions arise only after they have already decided to express their dissatisfaction (or something even worse), and they are merely looking for a subject upon which to hang it. Once one detail is answered, they will be bothered to search for another "flaw" or excuse [amta'la] (as it is explained that *amta'la* means *emes-lo*—"not true").

When it is firmly established among anash—especially those who have influence in their surroundings—that Lubavitch is good, and this is expressed with strength—at the very least equal to the dissatisfaction of those mentioned above—then even a little light pushes away much darkness. Conversely, when they see weakness, low spirits, and misplaced humility from anash, it only causes the opponents to become emboldened and puffed up with pride...

Blessings for good tidings in all the above.

## 3448

3448

B"H, 5 Iyar, 5715
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter from the end of Adar, a report on your holy activities. May it be the will of Hashem that for many years you will succeed in fulfilling the ruling of our Sages to "increase in matters of holiness," and that you will continue to increase in the dissemination of Torah in general, and the dissemination of the wellsprings [of Chassidus] in particular, as much as possible, until we all merit the fulfillment of the prophecy, "And a fountain shall come forth from the house of Hashem and shall water [the valley of Shittim]," as this matter is explained at length in the *Hemshech* "V'Kacha" and even more so in the *Kuntres U'Maayan*.

In general, I am not pleased with the splitting of focus and activities, where every matter has a special mechanism and a special name. Aside from the fact that this wastes energy on trivialities, there are many things that are in the category of "a lamp for one is a lamp for a hundred"—they are doubled and tripled. Consequently, the effort is lacking elsewhere. It is understood that sometimes there are reasons why it is impossible to combine things, at least externally, as two matters together; however, this should be the exception, not like the trend among the youth, where every single thing becomes a chapter, and perhaps even a separate book, etc. It would be appropriate to hold a meeting of the administration of Tzeirei Agudas Chabad, with the participation of the elders of Anash, to deliberate on this issue. They should critically examine all the various activities being carried out by Anash, Agudas Chabad, and Tzeirei Agudas Chabad in Jerusalem (may it be rebuilt and established), and seek ways to centralize matters so that the activity may be greater. It has already been decided and concluded that "in the multitude of counselors there is salvation."

With blessings for good tidings in all of the above, and for your success with those you influence, in particular.

P.S.
The name "Ohalei Yosef Yitzchak Lubavitch," or even with the omission of the word "Ohalei," for several reasons regarding activities in Eretz Yisrael (may it be built and established), is, for the time being, only for the schools of the Reshet. It should be removed from other matters.

## 3550

B"H, 5 Iyar, 5715
Brooklyn

To the esteemed Rabbi, the G-d-fearing, Torah-learned, and distinguished, etc., R' M.D. Volner, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

I was pleased to receive your letter of 26 Nissan, in which you write about the visit of Tzeirei Agudas Chabad to their camp and the impression it left. Surely, for one such as yourself, it is unnecessary to be reminded that whenever a movement of the soul occurs in a Jewish man or woman—in the vitality of Yiddishkeit, Torah, and mitzvos—the existence and purpose of this movement is to bring it into actual practice in matters of speech and action, and in daily life. As is hinted at in the saying, "The main thing is not the study, but the action". By this, both the movement and the awakening are tested. It is my hope, consistent with your letter, that this test was passed successfully and that the visit of Tzeirei Agudas Chabad also had an effect regarding action.

Furthermore, according to the interpretation of our Rebbe, the author of the Tanya and Shulchan Aruch, regarding the title *mara d'asra*—that the rabbi of the place is the "master of the house" of that place —surely you, too, will utilize such opportunities to strengthen and disseminate Yiddishkeit, especially in the field of proper chinuch, the work of Hashem, in all places and at all times. This is especially true in these times of *ikvesa d'meshicha*, the days of double and redoubled darkness of galus, and in our Holy Land, upon which the eyes of Hashem your G-d are from the beginning of the year to the end of the year. I look forward to hearing good news regarding this.

With blessings for success in your holy work.

P.S.
Regarding the seforim published by Kehot, they are available in Eretz Yisrael, may it be built and established, through Agudas Chabad at the following address: 22 Frug Street, Tel Aviv.

## 351

B"H, 5 Iyar, 5715
Brooklyn

To my esteemed friend, the G-d-fearing, Torah-learned, and distinguished [name], Moreinu HaRav Peretz, may he live.

Greetings and blessings!

It was surprising to me that I have not received any news from you during all the time since we last met, and I was saddened to receive news just now that your health is not as it should be. As you requested, I will mention you at the holy resting place of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, for proper health—health of the body and health of the soul together. It seems to me that during our conversation, we also touched upon a point that is one of the foundations of the Baal Shem Tov’s approach: "Serve Hashem **with joy."** It is already known what our great teacher, the Rambam, states in *Hilchos De'os*, that one serves Hashem not only during davening or while learning Torah, but also in the affairs of the world. Consequently, this *avodah* is required even during eating and with eating, during a walk and with a walk, and so on. And since one is not asked of more than one’s capacity, every one of us is assured that we are first given the strength to perform this holy and pleasant *avodah* in its entirety.

And through contemplation of this—that it is not like the outlook of idolaters, who believe that His glory is only in the heavens and He is exalted above all nations, but rather that He, may He be blessed, watches over each and every one of us in our daily lives, even in those details that are called in worldly terms "gray" and "insignificant"—there is no basis for any worry whatsoever. It is like the example of a child who is by his father’s side; although regarding the child, the father is "all-powerful" only in the child's imagination, this is not the case in the analogy, for the Father—our Father in Heaven—is all-powerful in reality, as is obvious.

I will await good tidings that you are feeling well, and as is the saying often used by my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory: "Have a healthy and happy summer."

I remain, with blessings,

[Signature]

## 3552

B"H, 6 Iyar, 5715
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Rabbi, the Chassid, G-d-fearing, refined, and distinguished, who engages in communal needs,
Rabbi Sh. Y. [Zevin], may he live.

Peace and blessing!

Regarding what you noted in the Shulchan Aruch of our Alter Rebbe, Siman 158, end of Seif 7, and the difficulty you raised as explained in your letter: in my opinion, the interpretation is as follows.

The text of the Alter Rebbe there states: "And there are those who disagree regarding this, **and therefore** one should be lenient, etc." From this, it is understood that the "those who disagree" are lenient in comparison to the opinion preceding it—namely, the opinion of the Magen Avraham as interpreted by the Alter Rebbe.

This opinion is found in the Taz, as noted in the *mar'eh mekomos*. It is that according to the Magen Avraham, there must be a specific thought for food at the time the honey exits the wax. Two opinions disagree with this: one opinion is the most lenient, which is brought in the Taz in the name of "I heard" (*shema'ti*), that even if one initially thought of it as liquid, one can subsequently change it to food through an action. The second opinion is that, at the very least, when one harvests the honey without a specific intent, the subsequent action defines it as food, and there is no need for an explicit thought for food specifically at the beginning of the harvesting. This is the opinion of the Taz himself.

Seemingly, there is also room for the reasoning of the "I heard" opinion in a case where the owner of the beehive is a non-Jew, for then one could say that his thought does not function to establish the honey as either liquid or food. And even if the owner of the beehive is a Jew, if he is harvesting it for sale, one could say that the action of the buyer establishes its status, especially when the seller himself knows at the time of the harvest that he will sell it later. There are many examples of this in the Gemara, but this is not the place to elaborate...

M. Schneerson

## 353

B"H, 6 Iyar, 5715
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

...I was pleased to learn that the avreich, the G-d-fearing, learned, and refined individual, R' Mordechai Eliezer Sharfstein, may he live, davened at your shul this past Pesach. It so happened that the issue of the mechitza in the shul came up, and according to his account, it sparked an awakening among the congregants regarding this matter (and how profound are the words of our Sages, "Even though I am asleep in exile, my heart is awake to Torah and mitzvos"). It is certainly unnecessary to awaken you, my dear friend, regarding the magnitude of this matter, but I rely on the ruling of our Sages (Sifra, beginning of Parshas Tzav) that "one only encourages those who are already diligent."

Allow me to add a few words on this topic, not out of necessity, but for the sake of adding strength:

Without entering into the technical halachic ruling itself, the situation in recent months is akin to the teaching of our Sages regarding *mayim rishonim* and *mayim acharonim*—that they "fed" [the people, i.e., influenced them]. For the custom of the people—the majority of those who visit the shul and, most importantly, their families—is that the erection of a mechitza in the shul is, in their eyes, a *Kiddush Hashem* in practice. From this, one can understand (based on the teaching of our Sages, "Anyone in whose days the Beis Hamikdash is not rebuilt...") the impression created by the opposite.

Therefore, in my opinion, anyone whom Heaven has blessed with the talent to influence their surroundings—especially those who serve in holy positions, and particularly a Rav who holds an important place even among other Rabbis—should utilize **all** of his influence, morning and evening, until he establishes these words of Torah by erecting a mechitza as required, to satisfy all opinions. Thank G-d, in this recent period, when the darkness is doubled and redoubled, the youth in this country—and even middle-aged people—are much more easily awakened to matters of *yiras shamayim*. The matter depends solely on the awakening of the leaders of the community, the "eyes of the community."

May Hashem grant you the merit and success to bring the above to fruition without difficulties, and very soon.

With blessings for success and for good tidings.

***

**353**

**The issue of the mechitza:** See also above, Vol. 9, Letter 2882, and the references in the notes there. Below, 3595.

**Regarding the teaching of our Sages on mayim rishonim:** Yoma 83b.

**Based on the teaching of our Sages, "Anyone...":** Yerushalmi Yoma, Chapter 1, Halacha 1; see Likkutei Sichos, Vol. 10, p. 150.

## 3,454

B"H, 6 Iyar, 5715
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and distinguished, engaged in communal needs, R' Shalom, may he live:

Shalom u’vracha!

In response to your letter of 3 Iyar, in which you write regarding the proposal you received to print a book of *druch* or *chiddushei Torah*, with the proceeds to benefit the High School or the Yeshiva, and it seems that you yourself must secure donors for the printing costs.

Regarding the business side of the matter, you should consult with the people on-site as to whether this is advisable from a financial perspective, for it is difficult to convince someone who has donated to the Yeshiva for the printing of a book to then, in close proximity to that, donate to the Yeshiva itself. Regarding the matter itself, surely it is not your intention that it be printed in the book that "the Yeshiva printed such-and-such a book," for such a concept is not appropriate for Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim. It seems the intention is that it be written in the book that so-and-so published it, and is dedicating the proceeds to the benefit of this Yeshiva institution. If that is the case, there is room for the aforementioned proposal, in accordance with what you determine regarding the financial question...

With blessings.

## 3550

B"H, 7 Iyar, 5715
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter from the end of the month of Ziv, which is also the beginning of the month of Ziv (and as an addition, see the *maamar* "B'Chodesh," *Rosh Hashanah* 2b). It begins with the good news that your son, Ben Tzion *sheyichyeh*, is studying in the holy Yeshiva Tomchei Tmimim, founded by my father-in-law, the Rebbe, *ztzukulleh"h, nbg"m, zya*, Nasi of the Jewish people. According to what is explained by one of the early authorities in the name of the *Yerushalmi*, the name Ben Tzion is a *segulah* for longevity—both literally, and for longevity in spirituality, meaning that his days and years will be filled with His holy Torah, which is "longer than the earth and broader than the sea." The result of this, according to our Sages of blessed memory, is that "study is great because it leads to action," together with all his children *sheyichyu*.

I was pleased to read in your letter that you poured water over the hands of the famous Rabbi and Chassid, renowned for his righteousness and conduct, etc., Moreinu HaRav Shlomo Alfandari *z"l*. I am interested to know if it is possible to obtain the books of the aforementioned, and I am considering whether this could be done as an exchange for the books published by Kehot. Also, I would like to know if his manuscripts and *chiddushim* in both *nigleh* and *nistar*, which surely remained in his estate, are being prepared for print.

Regarding what you elaborate upon in your letter concerning your situation and the fact that joy does not always dwell in your soul: this is explained at length and in brief in the holy *Tanya* by our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe, particularly in Chapter 31. One should increase this joy through the *hisbonenus* mentioned at the beginning of Chapter 41 of the holy *Tanya*—how the King of Kings, the Holy One, Blessed be He, leaves the supernal and lower beings and stands over him (over every individual Jew), and "the whole earth is full of His glory," etc. It is known that "strength and joy are in His place" (see *Chagigah* 5b, and in the *Sefer Avodas HaKodesh* by the Rabbi, the Maharim Ibn Gabbai, *Chelek HaTachlis*, Chapter 57). Through this *hisbonenus*, joy is strengthened within a person. As this joy of *mitzvah* increases (*mitzvah* in the sense of *tzavta*—connection and bonding with the Creator of the world), then, according to the rule that "joy breaks through barriers," those matters that oppose and limit a person—both physically and spiritually—are diminished. Indeed, the *Shechinah* only dwells amidst the joy of *mitzvah*, as is already known from what the great teacher wrote in his *Yad HaChazakah*, *Hilchos Yesodei HaTorah*, Chapter 7, Halacha 4. It is understood that in all of the above, there is no contradiction to the *avodah* of Hashem when it occasionally requires a sense of bitterness, as explained in the holy *Tanya*, end of Chapter 34, and in *Iggeres HaTeshuvah*, Chapter 11.

I have requested that *anash* *sheyichyu* provide you with some of the books published by Kehot. You will surely treat them with a "good eye" and merit the public with their content in your community and among those you influence, for the merit of the public depends upon you.

With regards and with blessings for success in your holy service.

## 3557

B"H, 9 Iyar, 5715
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

As requested, I mentioned [the names of the individuals] at the holy resting place of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, regarding what each of them requires. Since you were the shaliach in bringing their requests, you will surely convey to them as well that they were mentioned at the holy resting place of my father-in-law, the Nasi of the Jewish people. You should certainly also explain to them what is often said, based on the precise language of our Sages regarding "rains of blessing" (*gishmei brachah*): that there must first be plowing and sowing, and only then does the rain bring blessing in great abundance. It is understood that for a Jewish man and woman—a family—this means, first and foremost, establishing a home that serves as a model and example of a Jewish home—that is, a "miniature sanctuary" (*mikdash me'at*) in its conduct. As is clearly evident, this depends primarily on the conduct of the woman, the foundation of the home, with the husband assisting her to the best of his ability.

It is understood that this is only possible when the husband conducts himself—when sitting in his house, walking by the way, lying down, and rising up—in such a way that all who see him recognize that he is of the seed of Avraham, Yitzchak, and Yaakov.

If this is necessary in every place and at every time, it is all the more so in our generation, where each of us is a "brand plucked from the fire." In His great mercy, the Creator of the world, Hashem, may He be blessed, left us as a remnant to keep many people alive. Furthermore, we are in a land upon which the eyes of Hashem your G-d are from the beginning of the year to the end of the year—where the responsibility and the privilege of such conduct are many times greater. The Holy One, blessed be He, only asks according to the strength of each individual, and from the outset, the strength and the possibilities were given to fulfill all of the above completely, in the time and place where one is found. I would be pleased if you would inform [the individuals]—each of them specifically—about this in the appropriate detail.

With blessings for the fulfillment of this mission in its entirety, and for good tidings in all of this,

M. Schneerson

## 3558

B"H, 9 Iyar, 5715
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and learned, R' Avraham Tzvi, may he live, Hakohen.

Peace and blessing!

It is surprising that since your letter before Pesach, I have had no word from you. May it be Hashem's will that this be a sign of good, in a way that is good, visible, and revealed. Nevertheless, according to the ruling of our holy Torah, *Toras Chaim* (at the beginning of Yoreh Deah), in a place where one can clarify, one does not rely on a presumption—surely you will write explicitly about this.

Regarding your question: since a minor makes a *bracha* on all the *mitzvos* he performs, even though he is doing so only for the sake of *chinuch*, then how is the *chinuch* of putting on *tefillin* different? According to our custom (as recorded in *Hayom Yom*, 2 Menachem Av), it begins two months before the age of thirteen, and at the beginning, it is done without a *bracha*. As the instruction of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, is brought there.

Simply put, it can be said that regarding other *mitzvos* for which a minor makes a *bracha* when performing them for the sake of *chinuch*, there is no deficiency in the manner of performing the *mitzvah* itself, only in the maturity of the one performing it. This is not the case with putting on *tefillin*, where one must be precise about the placement and the binding, etc. One cannot rely on a minor, even after teaching him for a few days. As explained in *Kuntres HaTefillah*, the reason according to *nigleh* is that due to his youth, he does not recognize the great value of the matter—unlike when he is taught about it for a few weeks.

One can sweeten this matter even further, according to *nigleh*, approaching the *pnimiyus haTorah*: the essence of the *mitzvah* of *tefillin* is to subjugate the heart and the mind, as is also recorded in *Shulchan Aruch*. Its primary spiritual essence is the *hemshech* of *mochin*—which is the very concept of *gadlus* (maturity/greatness). Therefore, the concept of *chinuch* is not as applicable here. This is unlike other *mitzvos*, where *gadlus* is merely a condition for being obligated in the *mitzvah*, not the essence of the *mitzvah* itself.

May Hashem grant you success, and may you and your wife, may she live, merit to raise your children, may they live, to be G-d-fearing, Chassidim, and scholars.

With blessing.

359

359

B”H, 9 Iyar, 5715
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

...Although it is generally not my way to express an opinion on a matter that does not have practical application, I am concerned that this also affects the future. It seems that in this shul, there is a practice of hoping that others will busy themselves with its development, while the focus is on giving shiurim after the baalei batim arrive, making speeches before them, and so on. As I believe I have told you in several of our sichos, my view on this is that baalei batim are preoccupied with their businesses. It is enough—more than enough—when one awakens them and requests their effort in a **specific** detail, and they contribute their labor, whether through their physical presence or their money. If you want the building of the shul to be a healthy one, waiting for the baalei batim to come and bring members, friends, and congregants is not the way... May Hashem grant you **success**, as there are some baalei batim who are also interested in the development of the shul. According to what is explained in Chassidus, one must "clothe oneself in the garments of the one being influenced." You should imagine yourself as one of the baalei batim of a shul located some distance away, who has some personal matter or family simcha, and the like. Based on common sense regarding human nature, one should learn a *kal v’chomer*: If the *mara d’asra*—who, in the eyes of the world and in the understanding of the baalei batim in the United States, derives his livelihood from the shul—is holding his own simchos in other places, then it is all the more certain that he must also follow this path, for the time being. When Hashem helps and the shul develops and becomes a *talpiyos*—a place to which everyone turns—then I, too, will do likewise. As I said, I do not wish to dwell on a distressing matter, especially since it seems this is not a temporary occurrence, but a policy.

It is not my intention that you should worry about complaints from anyone, or even wonderings and questions of "Why?" For baalei batim are not interested in looking for problems and questions; they have many other matters that they find "interesting," and the aforementioned issue will not bother them, nor will they come to you with complaints. Rather, there is room for concern, as mentioned above, that they will also act in the same way, and the results of such conduct on the development of the shul are self-evident.

Once again, I must emphasize that even from the perspective of seeking a livelihood, in our day, this search is structured such that one must have a foothold in the ways of nature, and then there is room for success that is *lema'alah miderech hateva* (above the natural order). His foothold in the ways of nature is through the new shul. Instead of ruminating on the fact that his livelihood is not abundant—which consequently brings about a low spirit, sadness, and so on—the contemplation should be on how to widen the channels of livelihood, also within the ways of nature, and this is through the expansion of the shul.

- I had said that he should utilize the days of Pesach for this, by conducting a Seder in that neighborhood where the shul is located. Consequently, there would have been an opportunity for the baalei batim to come to the Seder, and perhaps they would even have been invited to the meal, etc. It seems this was not done.

On Lag B’Omer, or in the days surrounding it, there is room to do something for the children of the neighborhood, and he does not mention this in his letter either.

I once heard—and it is understood based on what is explained in Chassidus regarding "which is their place"—that success, in its true interpretation, is when there are no actions taken to influence an abundant livelihood, and furthermore, when there are even contrary actions. These not only do not cause a lack in livelihood, but on the contrary, these opposing matters—contrary to logic—actually assist in increasing one's livelihood. May it be Hashem’s will that this be the case here as well, and that from now on, he will utilize the concept of success—not that he should be given an abundant livelihood contrary to proper conduct, but that first, there should be an abundant livelihood through proper conduct, and the success should be utilized to add to that many times over.

## 3763

B"H, 10 Iyar, 5715
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

...Regarding what you wrote concerning the main points of the teachings of Chassidus and its perspective: the study of the teachings of Chassidus is similar to the study of any other part of the Torah. To what can this be compared? It is as if someone, before beginning to study Gemara after having studied Mishnah, were to ask for the "main points" of the Gemara, etc. It is understood that one could put such a matter down on paper, both regarding Gemara and regarding the teachings of Chassidus. However, I have never seen such an approach regarding the study of Gemara or the Rishonim, etc. In my opinion, this is not at all relevant to the study of the teachings of Chassidus, even though it is understood that everyone seeks a shortcut, and consequently asks if it is possible that by learning and grasping the "main points," they might learn this Torah "on one foot."

To a significant degree, you will find the main points of the teachings of Chassidus and its perspective in Shaar HaYichud VeHaEmunah (Tanya, Part II), in the Mitzvah of Emunas Elokus in the sefer Derech Mitzvosecha, in several chapters regarding the root of the Mitzvah of Tefillah there, and in the Kuntres Limud Toras HaChassidus.

## 3,755

B"H, 11 Iyar, 5715
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter from Rosh Chodesh Iyar, it gave me pleasure to read that you have set times for the study of the *neshamta d’oraysa*—as the holy *Zohar* terms the inner dimension of the Torah—which in our generation has been revealed through the teachings of Chassidus.

And certainly, in accordance with the dictum of the *Mishnah*, "The study is not the essential thing, but the deed," you are striving with all your ability to observe its guidance and customs.

One of the foundations of these is *ahavas Yisrael*, which leads the true Chassid—and the one who strives to be a Chassid as he ought—to disseminate this Torah and its matters in his immediate environment, and even further afield.

Regarding what you write, that you feel fluctuations in your state of mind concerning your *avodah* of Hashem and your love for Him:

Do not let your heart fall over this, Heaven forbid. As is explained in *Tanya* and in many places in the teachings of Chassidus, this comes from the battle with the *yetzer*, where sometimes one rises and another falls, and sometimes, etc., etc. Just as the conquest of *Eretz Yisrael* the first time followed the order of "little by little I will drive them out," so too is it in the life of every single Jew in the conquest of their spiritual *Eretz Yisrael*—the portion that falls to their lot. The conquest is not accomplished all at once, but little by little, and through toil; for it is specifically in this manner, as our Sages of blessed memory have taught: "You have toiled—and you have found."

The same applies to the matter of focus. Since, in the way of human beings, the situation progresses for the better step by step and not from one extreme to the other (except in exceptional cases), your heart should be confident in the Creator who fashions their hearts together, that the matter depends on the will of the one performing the *avodah*. Even if at times one sees a retreat, the retreat should awaken additional strengths and added courage, and not, Heaven forbid, a falling of the spirit. This is the path to ultimate victory in this battle.

I trust you are reciting *Tehillim* every day after morning *davening*, and that you are also informing those around you of this custom. You will surely find the words to explain that, particularly for those in the military—where the existence of an army depends on *kabbalas ol* and discipline—they must certainly practice *kabbalas ol* [towards Hashem] *a fortiori*. If human beings require such conduct toward their commanders, how much more so is this true in relation to the King of Kings, the Holy One, blessed be He.

With blessings for good tidings in all the above, soon, and with regards to your neighbor, [Name] *shlita* (as per your request, I will mention him and his family *shichyu* at the holy resting place of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, *ztzukulleh"h, nevg"m, zya*, Nasi of Israel).

## 366

B"H, 11 Iyar, 5715
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Rabbi and Chossid, G-d-fearing and distinguished, occupied with communal needs,
Rabbi Yitzchak, may he live, HaKohen

Greetings and blessings,

In response to your letter of 9 Iyar: It is a source of great wonder that although I frequently urge Anash regarding the matters that are the very eyes of our connection to Hashem and His Torah—and the state of our spirituality is what determines our material state—yet even our Temimim and Rabbis write about every other matter, but do not mention the aforementioned even in passing, nor even by way of a hint. It is understood that my intention is not that they should praise me in their letters or recount the activities I have initiated, but rather to mention what is being done in this regard within the environment in which they are located—and certainly within the four cubits of the writer, within his own home. There is no element of pride in this, etc., and there is no need to elaborate on such a simple matter. Regarding the Temimim, it is even more significant, as he does not mention anything regarding what is being done in the Yeshiva, even though a new term of study has just begun.

May it be the will of Hashem that, in accordance with the saying of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, which he heard in the name of the elder Chassidim, "One must arise as a completely different person," that in this matter, too, things will change from one extreme to the other...

With blessings.

## 3767

3767

B"H, 11 Iyar, 5715
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter—which was undated—

It is well known that the instructions of our holy Nasi are that one must fulfill the directives of expert physicians. Regarding your situation, it appears that you are following their instructions only intermittently; that is, for periods of time you stop and conduct yourself contrary to their advice. It has already been explained, both in the revealed Torah and in Chassidus, regarding the preciousness of the body of a Yid, that one must strive to be healthy and whole, for then it is possible to serve Hashem without distractions. On the contrary, as the Baal Shem Tov explains [the mitzvah of] *azov ta'azov imo*—with the body—[it is clear that] conduct to the contrary in our times is often caused by a desire to "show off tricks," or something even worse. Therefore, turn away from this path. In any event, from now on, you should ask your doctor for detailed instructions regarding your conduct in eating, drinking, and so on. Certainly, it should be arranged so that there is no contradiction to the Shulchan Aruch, chas v'shalom, and you should conduct yourself accordingly. Consequently, things will quickly improve for you, and you will return to your full strength.

With blessings for health and good news.

3659

B"H, 11 Iyar, 5715
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and distinguished individual, whose work is the work of Heaven,
Moreinu Harav Eliyahu Leib, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letter of 5 Iyar: It is a well-known saying of the Baal Shem Tov, which we have heard many times from my father-in-law, the Rebbe, that from everything a person sees or hears, one can—and therefore must—derive a lesson for one’s avodah of Hashem. This is all the more true regarding an event that affects many of the Jewish people, and especially when we see that Hashem has delivered the many into the hands of the few in a miraculous fashion. This should arouse in us additional strength to serve Him, may He be blessed. One should not be impressed in the slightest by the fact that there are those who conduct themselves differently and attempt to justify their behavior based on the logic that they are the majority. The aforementioned [miracle] is proof to the contrary: that a majority in quantity is not decisive in the least. Even those who conduct themselves otherwise know this; it is simply that they are not fighting their yetzer hara as they should, and therefore they fall under its dominion. This is, in addition to all other matters, a display of ingratitude of the most alarming kind.

To what can this be compared? To a great and mighty King who shows immense and profound love to a lowly, despised, and base individual, descending to him from His place of honor with all His ministers, and bringing him into **His palace**—the palace of the King (similar to what is explained in Tanya, Chapter 46). Is it possible to say that this base individual would tell the King that this palace does not belong to the King, but to the commoner, and therefore he will conduct himself within it according to his own will? And the beginning of his conduct is to drive the King out of His palace in every possible way—namely, by acting in a coarse manner, contrary to the King’s command, at every single step?! The analogy is understood...

I was also pleased by your letter stating that you distributed matzah shemurah to the parents of the students in your school. Surely, in the other schools of the network, they also followed this good custom. May Hashem grant you success to always bring good tidings regarding both general and personal matters.

With blessing for all the above.

## 3740

B"H, 12 Iyar, 5715
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

...Regarding what you write about traveling here to meet, and that for the time being you do not have the ability to do so: based on what is understood from what is written in Tanya, Chapter 5, you do have the ability even now—and it is even greater than a mere meeting. For it is explained there that when a person studies our holy Torah and strives to understand and grasp it, the person studying becomes unified with a wondrous unity, the likes of which—and the value of which—cannot be found at all in the physical realm, with the subject matter that he is studying.

Therefore, when you study fixed *shiurim* in *Toras HaNigleh* and *Toras HaChassidus*—which those who are here also study—it turns out that you and those who are here are unified with the aforementioned wondrous unity with the subject matter being studied, and, as a matter of course, with one another. This is especially true since, through this, the point explained in Chapter 32 of Tanya also comes to light—that only the bodies are divided, while the souls are all compatible, etc., and therefore all Jews are literally brothers. Regarding the **essence** of the soul, location does not create a separation, for it is above location, as is understood from what is written in *Likutei Torah*, end of *Chelek Devarim*, *d'h* *Mizmor Shir Chanukas HaBayis*.

With blessings for success in all of the above, with *parnassah* and health,

M. Schneerson
