## 3771

B"H, 12 Iyar, 5715
Brooklyn

To the Administration of Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim in Lod,
May they live.

Peace and Blessing!

Following the letter from the Rebbe shlita that has surely already been received, detailed below are several points regarding your previous letters, which will surely also be addressed in your next correspondence:

a) You mention the study of the laws of Shechita and Yoreh Deah. I assume this also refers to the craft of Shechita thereafter, and the study of Yoreh Deah in general. It is understood that, in general, this is a correct approach, especially for Sefardic students (and it is understood that one must take into account the laws in which they differ from Ashkenazic Shechita). However, at the same time, this must be implemented in a manner that does not diminish the reputation of the Yeshiva and its essence in the study of Torah with depth; a word to the wise is sufficient.

b) You mention that you are conducting negotiations regarding the budget of the Vaad HaYeshivos, as the tiny sum allocated to you is truly incomprehensible. This is especially so after Rabbi Shar visited here and stated and reiterated in his conversations that his attitude toward the Tomchei Temimim Yeshivos is good and proper, and he has significant influence in the matters of the aforementioned committee.

c) A letter was received from the village stating that they have allocated a sufficient plot of land for the vocational school.

You will surely inform us of the actual progress in this matter.

d) It would be appropriate to clarify the reason for the lack of approval for the vocational school by the Ministry of Labor. There are surely ways to change their decision through certain improvements in the vocational school. It is understood that this is not, under any circumstances, at the expense of Kodesh studies.

e) For the time being, the report cards and photographs of the vocational school students have not been received.

f) Regarding your question about instituting fines for students for a lack of diligence and the like, in matters such as these, one must take into account the customs of the country in which you are located.

g) Regarding the proposal concerning the buildings in Teveria, there is room to establish a vocational school there, since, as it appears, the students will be from among the Sefardim. Therefore, one must first clarify whether there is suitable personnel to head the administration there (if the teachers are not from Anash, that is one thing, but as for the head of the administration, one cannot compromise on this). It is understood that this also includes clarifying whether it would be possible to establish a branch of Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim there, and perhaps even with greater strength.

What is the news regarding the tender?

With respect and blessing,

A. Quint
Secretary

The letter is signed by the secretary, yet it is evident from the content and style that it was dictated by the Rebbe shlita.

## 3772

B"H, 12 Iyar, 5715
Brooklyn

To the Administration of Agudas Chabad in the Holy Land, may it be built and established,
May they live,

Peace and blessing!

I have received your letter of 5 Iyar, in which you write regarding the various proposals concerning the location for establishing a second Kfar Chabad. It is surprising that there is even a debate regarding establishing it in a remote location—not only far from the current Kfar Chabad, but far from any settlement of observant Jews in general—after you are already aware of the situation regarding this in the Holy Land, may it be built and established. A brief consideration makes it clear that such a proposal has no place.

2) In connection with the above, and as I spoke about in person with Mr. Shazar, may he live, when he was here, and likewise with Mr. Koren, may he live, when he visited me: The establishment of a second Kfar Chabad must be in close proximity to the current Kfar Chabad. If that is absolutely impossible, then at the very least, it must be in close proximity to a settlement where active Chabad people are located, such as Jerusalem, may it be built and established, Tel Aviv, Lod, and the like. And if even that is impossible in any way—then at the very least, it must be in close proximity to a settlement where there is a significant group of Bnei Yisrael who are observant of Torah and mitzvos. And even then, it is a matter of "perhaps"...

Is the location suitable, and are there possibilities for establishing a second Kfar Chabad in Teveria, in the vicinity of the Pagi land buildings, etc.?

With blessings for good tidings in all of the above, and may it be the will of Hashem that it happens soon,

**M. Schneerson**

## 373

B"H, 12 Iyar, 5715
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 10 Iyar: Thank you for the report regarding the students' farbrengen, and for the fact that they shared the *mashke* from the *Seudas Acharon Shel Pesach*—the *Seudas Mashiach*. Surely, you inspired the students regarding the most essential point: *hamaaseh hu haikar*—actual practice—namely, persistence and diligence in their studies (for the movement of one's lips is considered an action, as explained in *Tanya*, Chapter 37) and in the performance of *mitzvos* with *hiddur*.

Regarding what you wrote about [the individual], that for the time being he lacks physical sustenance, etc.: If they had not related to his spiritual sustenance with coldness—which led to the current situation, and consequently caused the lack of physical sustenance—the situation would be different. The two are interdependent. When he increases his spiritual sustenance, they, too, must do their part to assist him as much as possible through all those you mentioned in your letter regarding him.

Then, Hashem will increase His blessing for his physical sustenance. As is known, the story and the ruling of the Alter Rebbe: "You say everything that you need, but you do not say what is needed of you." As the conclusion there states, once he did what was incumbent upon him, all his needs were met, and in abundance.

With blessings for good news regarding all the above, and may it be soon.

## 3749

B"H, 12 Iyar, 5715
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and meticulous in his communal work,

Greetings and blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter from the beginning of Iyar, as well as the one preceding it.

Thank you for the good news regarding the farbrengen, and especially regarding the inspiration of those who participated concerning the days following the farbrengen. Surely, even after this, those who have the ability will ensure that this inspiration is translated into actual practice during the weekdays as well.

Regarding what you wrote—that the people of the West have never seen a Rebbe in their lives, and that even the week that my father-in-law, the Rebbe, spent there was only in a manner of *makif* (encompassing light)—the truth is that a *makif* eventually enters into the *pnimiyus* (internal dimension). One of the ways this happens (from above to below) is by drawing down an even higher *makif*, or (from below to above) by striving to draw the *makif* into the *pnimiyus* through *avodah*. Both of these are in the hands of the elders of *anash* in Jerusalem (may it be rebuilt and established), by repeating *maamarim* of *Chassidus* before them—for the Torah of the Rebbe is his *pnimiyus* and his essence—and by guiding them in his conduct, in the way he instructed us in our daily life.

With blessings for good news in all the above.

## 3,775

B"H, 12 Iyar, 5715
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter from Motzaei Shabbos: It is surprising that you do not mention anything regarding your shiurim in the study of Nigleh and Chassidus, nor regarding your participation in farbrengens and the shiurim taught in public, etc., etc. The beginning of your letter, and even the middle, is concerned only with matters of material parnassah and various opinions regarding it. It is as if, chas v’shalom, you have forgotten what is stated in Bircas Hamazon—which is from the Torah—and its opening, that Hashem is the King of the world, and He specifically is the One who feeds and sustains everyone with kindness and mercy. From this, it is understood, without any doubt, that one must make a "dwelling place" for Him here in one's own place; then the matter of "He who feeds and sustains everyone" will also be fulfilled. You should study, with the appropriate focus, Iggeres HaKodesh, Epistle 9, and in many other places there.

May it be the will of Hashem that from now on, at the very least, this matter will be corrected from its root—the main thing being the actual fulfillment—and surely you will not withhold the good from bringing me good tidings in this regard.

Awaiting good news,

On behalf of the Rebbe shlita,

Secretary

## 376

376

B"H, 12 Iyar, 5715
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing and learned, etc., R' Avraham Tzvi, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letter of 25 Nissan and Rosh Chodesh Iyar, which arrived together... regarding what you wrote about the story concerning the 378 chapters on the topic of *ratzo* and *taanug*—which one compels the other—that my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, wrote for himself when he was young, and later burned them, and subsequently regretted doing so, etc. This is a story from one of the elders of Anash, the esteemed R' Michael Dworkin, of blessed memory, and you ask for an explanation of this matter.

Now, I do not know why an explanation is needed—whether regarding the narrator or the matter itself. Regarding the narrator, you will find references in the margin, as it is understood that the 378 chapters relate to *ratzo* and *taanug*, which are *Keter*, *Atik*, and *Arich* in the lower man, and consequently in the higher man as well. This is also noted in *Hemshech 5666*, where the matter of *ratzo* and *taanug* is discussed.

Regarding the fact that he burned them and later regretted it, one could suggest that since the subject matter pertains to the inner dimension of Torah, he did not want to say anything that he had not heard from his teacher—and one may note the *Zohar Chadash* 221b. He later felt regret over this, because the discussion was about understanding a concept that they had received from their teacher.

- By the way: Regarding what you wrote, and your mnemonic **Yad Yosef**, it seems it was omitted accordingly: it is divided into 14 (*yad*) parts.

With blessing,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

Secretary

Just now received your letter of 9 Iyar.

***

**R' Avraham Tzvi:** Landau.

 *Likutei Torah, Vayikra* 9c; *ibid., Shir HaShirim* 35d, 38c.
 *Maamar* "Lech Lecha" and onwards.

## 3757

B”H, 13 Iyar, 5715
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letters from 27 Nissan and the one preceding it, as well as those from 3 and 6 Iyar, and the telegram regarding the participation of the bochurim in the registration [for the Reshet schools].

It is a great wonder and astonishment to me, even more so than regarding the rest of anash in Eretz Yisrael, for you yourself were in the United States at the time when my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory—the Nasi of Yisrael, and not only of anash—would send the talmidei hatmimim for outreach work regarding kosher education. He would choose the most select students and send them to outlying towns to establish small yeshivos there, where they would teach the Aleph-Beis, Siddur, Chumash, Mishnah, and Gemara, even though these students themselves could have been occupied with the study of Chassidus in addition to the study of Nigleh. You also know about the "Wednesday hour," the purpose of which was to learn with young boys and girls who did not even know how to speak Yiddish, and one had to explain to them about *Modeh Ani*, the foundations of keeping Shabbos, etc., etc.—and for this work, too, my father-in-law, the Rebbe, sent students, even those who were already engaged in the study of Chassidus and the avodah of tefillah, etc., etc., and this was even at a time when the number of students in the Tomchei Temimim yeshiva here was extremely small. And when the question arises in Eretz Yisrael—may it be built and established—and after these students have already participated in the registration work several times, and we are talking about approximately 15 students for only two weeks, you set aside all your affairs and spend money to send a telegram here—perhaps it will be possible to prevent the students from participating in the registration (even though because of this, it is likely that in some places, the new ones and perhaps even the old ones, hundreds of boys and girls will be denied a kosher education...).

It is understood that the delay regarding the buildings for the agricultural and vocational school in Kfar Chabad is "also" distressing—and now youth are arriving from Morocco, and if the buildings were ready for their full intake, it would have been possible to save several tens of these youths, to absorb them into these schools, and to raise a *gevald* about additional new buildings, which is not the case in the current situation. When from time to time another opportunity arises to expand the activities of Chabad in Eretz Yisrael—may it be built and established—and specifically the *hafatzas hamaayanos chutzah* for the fulfillment of the promise "when your wellsprings spread outward, the Master will come"—from time to time another obstacle and delay arises...

I was pleased to receive the news that your visit to the Reshet school in Menachemya made a very good impression on the students. If only they would listen to my words and make such visits more frequently; may it be His will that from now on they do so, and may Hashem grant them success.

With blessings for good tidings in all the above,

**M. Schneerson**

## 3778

B"H, 13 Iyar, 5715
Brooklyn

To the Administration of Tzeirei Agudas Chabad in the Holy City of Jerusalem, may it be rebuilt and established,
May they live,

Peace and Blessing!

I am somewhat surprised by the cessation of your correspondence regarding the continuation of your good activities—activities that surely took advantage of the month of Nissan, in which, according to our Sages (Berachos 57a), miracles were performed, to disseminate the wellsprings outward, as well as the guidance and conduct of the teachings of Chassidus. I am certain you will rectify this at the earliest opportunity.

Regarding what you wrote concerning the evening yeshiva: I trust that our dear relative, the esteemed Chassid, etc., Shmuel Menachem Mendel, may he live, has already conveyed the content of my letter to him, as he also touched upon this question. Out of respect and a love for order, I will repeat and reiterate it here:

It is not beneficial for the success of your holy work to fragment matters excessively, giving every project a specific name, a separate mechanism, and so on. Although there is a benefit in the "jealousy of scribes" [which increases wisdom], and the person heading a private project feels a greater sense of responsibility, the loss outweighs the gain. Many matters that are in the category of "a light for one is a light for a hundred" result in a waste of energy through duplication, and the execution of the work is not as effective, since not all the details are known from one person to the next, and every matter has a separate administration, and so on.

Therefore, I suggest that as soon as possible, you hold a meeting in which all those active in their respective fields of work participate. Without belittling anyone’s stature or infringing upon anyone’s honor, you should centralize matters so that there is complete coordination in the various fields. Consequently, there will be greater activity and more significant results, with fewer expenditures—both in effort, in time, and even in money. It is understood from my previous letters, and from the verse "In the multitude of counselors there is salvation," that it is highly appropriate that this meeting also include some of the elders of Anash in Jerusalem, especially those whom you have consulted with until now, and who therefore understand the course of events—foremost among them our dear relative, the esteemed Chassid, etc., Rabbi Azriel Zelig Slonim, may he live.

I will also reiterate here that for several reasons, the name "Ohalei Yosef Yitzchak"—and even omitting the word "Ohalei"—should be used in the Holy Land only for the institutions of the Reshet. Therefore, your project should simply be called "The Evening Yeshiva under the auspices of..." but not by the aforementioned name. This is the place for me to express my astonishment regarding why you took this name and affixed it to a specific institution without first consulting on the matter. This is the name of our Nasi, the Nasi of Israel, and the designation of such a name imposes a very great responsibility. Who is the person who can decide this based on his own private opinion without the knowledge of the many, and of those who have no personal interest in the matter? One must be assured that it will lead to a Kiddush Hashem and not the opposite. Those who see it do not ask who chose the name or if it was done with the agreement of the many; sometimes they judge the "owner of the name" based on the institution to which it is attached. There is no need to elaborate on what is understood, and I am certain you will rectify the above in an appropriate manner.

It goes without saying—and there is no need to dwell on this—that it is not my intention in any of the above to cause, G-d forbid, a lowering of spirits, and certainly not a collapse of spirits. It goes without saying that this is not a matter of reprimand. On the contrary, on one hand, I am pleased that the matter of education in purity is something that burns within you. But on the other hand, especially in our times, things must be as organized and refined as possible at the inception of any work. Therefore, my hope is strong that you will continue in this project with the greatest energy, and that if there are details that need to be corrected by adding or even by subtracting and removing, this will be done as well. On the contrary, through this, your energy and success will increase.

I await good news and bless you with success in disseminating the wellsprings outward—success that transcends the natural order.

## 379

B"H, 13 Iyar, 5715
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

It gave me pleasure to receive your letter, apparently from the end of Nissan and the period following it, and to read therein that you are fulfilling the command of the Ribono shel Olam through the observance of mitzvos in general, and the mitzvah of tzedakah in particular, which should be performed with joy and a generous eye. Surely, Hashem will fulfill His promise regarding which He says, "And test Me now with this," that through the mitzvah of tzedakah, "I will pour out for you a blessing until there is no end." And measure for measure, this too will come through a channel of joy and the light of the countenance of the Living King, the King of the worlds above. And most importantly, may you soon be able to share the good news that you have found a suitable shidduch for your eldest daughter, may she live.

It is understood that you are correct in what you wrote, that you do not demand of those who propose prestigious matches for her that they study Toras HaChassidus, etc., as a prerequisite to the shidduch. For in our times, yiras shamayim will eventually lead to following the guidance and conduct of Chassidus, and in time, to the study of its teachings as well.

I was pleased by what you wrote, that you are involved among anash and speak with them during the intervening days regarding divrei Torah, Chassidic conduct, etc. It is well-known and famous how much our holy Nesi'im, may the merit of the righteous protect us, derived pleasure from such conduct. It is also understood that all those who fulfill their commands and instructions, and cause them nachas ruach where they reside in the supernal chambers and worlds, surely bring about, through this nachas ruach, an increase in blessing and success in all that is needed for the one who inspires it, for himself and for all his family members, may they live.

With wishes for a mazel tov for your birthday, and with the blessing as per the saying of my father-in-law, the Rebbe: for a healthy and happy summer.

## 3780

3780

B”H, 13 Iyar, 5715
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

I was pleased to receive your letter from the eve of Pesach, written in a much better frame of mind than your previous letters. May it be the will of Hashem that you not only remain in such a state of mind, but on the contrary, that you continue to increase your trust in Hashem, and consequently, your peace of mind and joy, through which your energy in avodas hakodesh will also increase.

I will surely receive news these days regarding the progress of the registration and the outlook for the upcoming school year.

Regarding what you wrote—that you feel you are still in the dark in the field of teaching—this is an **old, familiar** refrain. It applies to **each and every** person, for "man is born a wild ass," and it is therefore understood that one proceeds only step by step along the path and the highway that leads to the house of Hashem, to become a person who fulfills his role of serving his Creator with all his strength and all his ability. And since the goal is to unite with the essence and truth of the Ein Sof, it is understood that the path, too, is infinite. And just as **every** son and daughter of Yisrael has already advanced beyond the initial point of their journey, on the other hand, it is still possible for them to perfect themselves more and more.

And according to our Sages’ teaching that "the feet of the Chayos correspond to them all," as explained in Tanya, end of Chapter 13, all the levels and rungs below are as nothing compared to the level and rung—that is, compared to the point—that one will reach after perfecting oneself little by little to attain completeness. Therefore, the manner of Siyata Dishmaya corresponds to this as well—it is also in such a manner, as explained in Iggeres HaKodesh, Epistle 14, that every single day, higher intellects are drawn down from a higher level that had never shone before (see there). And just as this is true in general and in essential matters, so it is in every profession and endeavor. Consequently, the aforementioned feeling should awaken additional strength and effort, and as a result, there will also be an increase in success and in "finding."

With blessings for success in all the above, and for good news regarding your personal matters and those of your family, may they live.

Published in Likkutei Sichos, Vol. 21, p. 360, and completed based on the secretariat’s copy.

**The registration:** Children to study in the Reshet Oholei Yosef Yitzchok Lubavitch for the upcoming school year.

## 3781

B.H., 13 Iyar, 5715
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

I acknowledge receipt of your letter which you concluded on 4 Iyar, as well as those preceding it. In response to them:

1) You have surely heard the adage of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, that just as in business one must know the status and condition of the enterprise—which is achieved through an accurate accounting—there are specific times for conducting such audits, usually at the end of the year. If one were to calculate every single hour, it would not only waste time and energy, but would also disrupt the business itself. For business, in the vast majority of cases, must be conducted with expansiveness and confidence, as it is written, "Open wide your mouth and I will fill it." Accounting, by its nature, involves measurement, restriction, and a contrary movement.

It is the same regarding the business of Torah and mitzvos, which is the primary occupation of man, for his creation is to serve his Creator. Therefore, our holy Torah, the Torah of life, has established specific times for conducting this accounting—usually at the conclusion of every period. This is why we have the accounting of the day that passed during Krias Shema al Hamitah, and at the end of the year, the month of Elul, and especially the days of Selichos regarding the year that has passed. From the above, it is understood that your method of frequently conducting audits between these times regarding your conduct over the past years, and weighing again and again whether you need to increase your efforts in chinuch, in learning, or in influencing others, is the opposite of the instruction of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, Nasi Yisrael.

2) Regarding the substance of the matter: 613 mitzvos were given to the Children of Israel, and our Sages of blessed memory said that in each one, one must act and be meticulous beyond the letter of the law. The path of Chassidus came and explained that each of them must be performed with enthusiasm and vitality. Yet, it is simple that there is no contradiction between one mitzvah and another, or the other 612 mitzvos; on the contrary, "one mitzvah leads to another."

The same applies to your question, which is repeated in several of your letters. All the matters you mention—your holy work in influencing your surroundings toward Torah and mitzvos, your holy labor in [your profession], and your assistance in the home, where there is great peace between husband and wife, as our Sages of blessed memory said that through this the Shechinah dwells between them—all of these are necessary and all are a great merit. Since the Creator, who fashions their hearts together, has placed all of these upon you at once, there is certainly a possibility to arrange matters so that not only will there be no contradiction between one and the other, but on the contrary, they will assist one another.

Indeed, you write in your letter that your wife (may she live and be well) takes pleasure in the fact that you succeeded in your influence upon a certain youth, through which he became a G-d-fearing person. Even though she surely understands that her pleasure will add vigor and desire in you to continue in such endeavors—which is proof that these actions are in accordance with her will and that she consents to them wholeheartedly—it is understood that from a distance, and even when nearby, it is impossible to determine that from such-and-such an hour to such-and-such an hour you will occupy yourself with this matter, and afterwards until such-and-such an hour you will occupy yourself with the second matter, etc. Everything depends on the conditions of the place and the days, the state of mind, the demands of the situation, etc. But surely, "the Torah was not given to ministering angels," and one should not exaggerate in the demand that matters be arranged to perfectly suit and complement one another.

3) Regarding what you write, that when you look at an avreich or a bochur sitting and learning, while you are occupied with [your profession] or influencing others for our Father in Heaven, you are in doubt whether you have chosen the correct path—there is an explicit verse: "And Hashem (our G-d) commanded us to perform all these statutes, to fear Hashem our G-d," and it is said, "Fear G-d and keep His commandments, for this is the whole of man." From this it is understood that every matter of fear of Heaven, fear of G-d, and the actual keeping of a mitzvah **is** the purpose of the whole of man. This is also understood based on the ruling of the Mishnah: "I was created to serve my Creator," and not to serve myself, even in a **lofty** manner, and in the way mentioned above, as explained in the Rambam at the end of Hilchos Teshuvah.

Since the study of Torah must be because of the love of the Master of all, who commanded it, and when you see one of the Children of Israel—of whom it is said regarding **each** one, "You are children to Hashem your G-d"—and this child is wandering in a thick forest among predatory beasts, and you recall the ruling of Rabbi Akiva that "Love your neighbor as yourself is a great principle in the Torah," it is understood that if you were to abandon the child of the Master of all the earth to his own devices and occupy yourself with study so that you might be called "wise" and "understanding," that this is not the purpose of man's creation, which arose in His will, may He be blessed, that he should serve his Creator...

With blessings for avodah from within joy.

## 3782

14 Iyar, 5715
Brooklyn

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and learned individual, engaged in communal affairs, R’ Yeruchem, may he live.

Greetings and blessings!

It was a pleasure to receive your letter from the conclusion of Shabbos, Parshas Tazria-Metzora, in which you write about the shiurim you are conducting with others—with individuals and also, which is the main thing, with a group of students. May your strength be fortified. It is certainly unnecessary to elaborate on the greatness of this matter, as it is already known from our Sages that among all the virtues of one who teaches Torah to the son of his fellow, and his own son, etc., the highest level is when one "brings forth the precious from the vile" (Bava Metzia 85a).

It is surely unnecessary to caution you to be careful that your teaching with students of specific educational institutions not be interpreted as providing a "hechsher" to that educational institution and its methodology. As I have already written regarding this to several of anash, although it is simple, the caution required here depends on the nature of the place and the institutions, for they are not all the same. In any event, this is achieved by not incorporating your shiurim into the curriculum of the aforementioned institutions, by precluding the intervention of the institution’s administration in the shiurim, etc., and by seeking the counsel of those who are present in that location.

Regarding what you mention—that in your lecture on a Chassidic topic, you propose that girls also participate, but on the condition that they sit in separate rows (and surely you mean on separate sides of the room with a suitable partition in between)—while this should not be publicized as an official policy or a "method," as there will certainly be zealots (whose motives are not for the sake of Heaven) who will invoke the teaching of our Sages regarding one who teaches his daughter Torah, nevertheless, you should **strive** to bring this to fruition (naturally, with the aforementioned caution—that it should not be seen as a hechsher for the institution itself). This is just as the Rebbe, my father-in-law, of blessed memory, organized classes for girls to study Chassidus while he was still in Riga. He even wrote letters to them on such topics, and over time, the fruits and the great benefit of this were seen. For the woman is the "foundation of the home," and even before that, regarding shidduchim. In truth, this is a ruling of Torah law, as is brought in the Shulchan Aruch, Laws of Torah Study, and also in the Laws of Torah Study by our Alter Rebbe, end of Chapter 1, that women are obligated in the aforementioned study, which brings a person to accept the yoke of the Kingdom of Heaven, to fear of Heaven, and to hiddur—in daily life—in matters of Torah and mitzvos. Regarding matters that are well-known and visible to the eye in everyday practice, there is no need for elaboration.

In accordance with the above, the importance of establishing a nucleus, or even a branch, of Agudas Nshei Chabad in Bnei Brak is also understood. You will surely strive for their development in an appropriate manner. I have already written in the past to several branches of Agudas Nshei Chabad that one should not be particular that those joining the association must already be fully convinced and conducting themselves like a "pitz Chabad" from the outset. Since they wish to join this association, it shows their positive attitude toward Chabad. Therefore, one should be confident that the vast majority of them will translate this good intention into action, and in a short time—even if only to the extent of "moistening to moisten" [i.e., a beginning].

With blessings for success in the above.

## 3780

B”H, 17 Iyar, 5715
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings,

In response to your letter of the 10th of Iyar, in which you ask for a *tikkun* for [your past actions] and for the method of how to battle against this in the future, noting that despair is attacking you, etc.

It is explained in many places that despair is one of the tactics and methods of the *yetzer hara* to ensnare a person. It does so by suggesting that since it is impossible for him to defeat the *yetzer hara*, *chas v’shalom*, there is no purpose or benefit in fighting against it. It is understood that this thought is *apikorsus*, *r”l*, and the opposite of the faith that Hashem is the life of the entire world and of man in his entirety, and that *leit atar panui minei* (there is no place void of Him). He has told us in His holy Torah: "I created the *yetzer hara*, and I created for it Torah as an antidote." However, "whoever says 'I have nothing but Torah,' even Torah he does not have." It is already known what our Sages ruled, that if one is not worthy, *chas v’shalom*, the Torah can, *r”l*, become a "potion of death" for him (*Yoma* 72b).

Therefore, *tefillah* before the Master of all is essential, as it is a request for a person’s needs, and all the more so for the salvation of his soul. In order for *tefillah* to be accepted, it must be performed in purity and with an understanding of the words, at the very least. It is also very good to give a few coins to *tzedakah* frequently and often before [davening], in accordance with what our Sages said regarding the verse, "I will behold Your face in righteousness (*tzedek*)."

You should conduct yourself with all of the above, and after the *Shacharis* *davening* each day, you should recite the portion of *Tehillim* as it is divided for the days of the month. When you do all of this—though, as is the custom of Israel, it should be done *bli neder*—then, little by little, the battle will become easier for you, and bit by bit you will drive the *yetzer hara* from your borders.

It would be appropriate for you to memorize the text from the beginning of Chapter 41 in *Tanya* up to the words "as one standing before the King" (*Tanya*, page 56, top of side b). It would also be appropriate for you to have your *tefillin* checked.

With blessings for success in all of the above,

On behalf of the Rebbe, *shlita*,

Secretary

## 3787

B"H, 17 Iyar, 5715
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

...It is certainly unnecessary to remind you that the physical and the spiritual must walk hand in hand, for the creation itself stems from the Simple Unity, and therefore this unity prevails throughout all of creation. However, in order for there to be free choice, two paths were provided, and it is up to man to "choose life," and thereby reveal the unity that exists in all things. This is all the more true regarding the Children of Israel, "one nation on earth." Therefore, when one reports on the state of physical health, it is always appropriate to also report on the state of spiritual health—especially when the matter at hand is a request for a blessing from the "Healer of all flesh and Performer of wonders," since the physical descends from the spiritual. I am certain that in your next letter, you will include details regarding the aforementioned as well.

With blessings for good tidings in all the above.

## 3,788

3,788

When you study in the company of friends, they will strengthen you in walking the path that ascends to the House of Hashem, as it is written: “And you who cleave to Hashem your G-d are all alive today.” There are many yeshivos that are permeated with yiras shamayim, both internally and even externally—that is, in their attire and the like—all of which defines a person and adds to their strength so as not to be enticed by the yetzer hara, which, even if it begins with smooth words, its end is as bitter as wormwood, not only in spirituality but also in physicality.

With blessings for success in all of the above, and soon; and it would be best if it were in one of the yeshivos in Eretz Yisrael (may it be built and established).

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

B"H, 18 Iyar, 5715
Brooklyn

You should examine the notes to Tanya, page 1, and the sources referenced there.

As you requested, I will mention your son, Yosef Yitzchak, may he live, at the Tziyon HaKadosh of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, in particular. Perhaps this is a significant matter. May it be the will of Hashem that he grow to be a G-d-fearing Chassid and a scholar, and may you raise him, along with your other children, may they live, for Torah, chuppah, and good deeds.

With blessings for success.

## 3,393

3,393

B”H, 20 Iyar, 5715
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter—which did not indicate the date it was written—I will, as you requested, mention you at the holy resting place of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, for long life and good years. It would be worthwhile for you to study *Shaar HaBitachon* in the book *Chovos HaLevavos* and contemplate the matters explained therein. When one contemplates, even for a short while, that every single man and woman of Bnei Yisrael believes with simple faith that there is no place void of Him, and considering the ruling of our Sages regarding the verse, “Strength and joy are in His place,” and based on what is written that one should not enter the King’s gate in sackcloth—it is impossible to disturb the joy of the One of whom it is said “strength and joy are in His place” through the sadness of anyone, whoever it may be, even if it seems to him for the moment that there is a basis for it. One must delve into this, for even a brief contemplation is sufficient.

Furthermore, it is a known ruling of the Rambam, cited in *Shulchan Aruch, Orach Chaim* 241, that the service of Hashem must be in **all** your ways. It is also a known ruling that the service of Hashem must be with joy, as it is written, “Because you did not serve [Hashem your G-d with joy and gladness of heart],” and regarding the greatness of the matter of *simchas mitzvah*. Since in “all your ways” there is the possibility of a *mitzvah*, it is understood that joy must be in His dwelling place, as explained by the Rambam at the end of *Hilchos Lulav*, which was also quoted in the letter of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, in his introduction to the *Kuntres Eitz Chaim* and the *Kuntres HaAvodah*. You should divert your attention from your own thoughts and from yourself, and occupy yourself with matters of *ahavas Yisrael* and *ahavas Hashem*. May Hashem grant you long life and good years.

With blessings for good tidings regarding all the above, soon.

## 3494

B"H, 20 Iyar, 5715
Brooklyn

It is surely unnecessary to elaborate that one merits Siyata Dishmaya in this by influencing one’s surroundings to draw them closer to Torah and mitzvos in general, and to Chassidus, its guidance, and its conduct in particular, for the trait of the Ribono shel Olam is "measure for measure" (only many times over).

Your two previous letters were received in due time. Regarding your question concerning the custom of the shul where you serve as the baal korei—that the baal korei wraps himself in a tallis during the reading (unlike our custom), and they are demanding that you also wrap yourself as they do—you should fulfill their request. For: 1) In such matters, the individual should follow the majority. 2) Wrapping in a tallis also involves the matter of "respect for the congregation" (Magen Avraham, Siman 18, subsection 2), and since the congregation, or the majority of it, is particular about this, one should not treat their respect lightly (by not wrapping).

With blessings for success in the above.

## 3790

B”H, 20 Iyar, 5715
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings,

Regarding your question about the plot of land and the building—whether you should occupy yourself with them or not:

It is surprising that each person asks individually, even though I have already answered several of anash and requested that the matter be publicized. The matter of the village is a communal concern, through which the success of the individual also comes, and the merit of our holy Rebbes, the Nesi’im, assists in this. Therefore, any matter that proceeds in a crooked or cunning way is a place that causes harm to others, and is therefore ruled out. From this, it is also understood regarding your situation: in my opinion, you should hand over the plot and the apartment to the village committee, since in the coming months you will be working in the vineyard of Chabad outside the area of this location.

You should have absolute bitachon that the Rebbe, my father-in-law, stands and serves on high to bestow what is needed—both materially and spiritually—to anash in general, and to those who work in his institutions in particular. You have no reason to worry about this, except for what you actually need. As is known, the story of the Chossid of the Alter Rebbe, and the saying of the Alter Rebbe: "You say everything that you need, but for what is needed of you, you do not say." When that Chossid changed his conduct, he returned to his wealth, and even more so. So too, in your case, Hashem will grant you success with peace of mind, with a livelihood as is fitting, and with the fulfillment of your role in achieving the ultimate purpose, as the Mishnah rules: "I was created to serve my Maker."

It is understood that for several reasons, haste in all of this is commendable. As mentioned in my previous letter, you should travel as soon as possible, in a good and auspicious hour, to your place of holy work, and at the appropriate time, your family members, shlita, will also come there, healthy and whole.

With blessings for success.

**3790**

**That I have already answered:** See the letter preceding this one, and the references in the notes there.

3497

B"H, 21 Iyar, 5715
Brooklyn

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and learned R' Yisrael Zussman, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letter of 17 Iyar, in which you ask for the intention behind my statement that even the first point outside the spring is considered "outside."

From the very titles *Nigleh d'Oraisa* and *Nistar d'Oraisa*, the body of Torah and the soul of Torah, it is understood that in every matter and every detail, both aspects exist—both the revealed and the hidden. Since, according to the *Nigleh*, the first point outside the spring is not the spring itself, it must necessarily be the same in the interiority and spirituality of things. See the *Reshimos Tehillim* of the Tzemach Tzedek, 118:19, note 8.

Regarding the practical application: even *anash* and the elders of *anash* must truly know that studying a *maamar* of *Chassidus* or the *avodah* of *tefillah* itself—which is the spring itself—is no guarantee (*baavarenish*) for the moment that follows. One must be careful to draw the *hisorerus* of *tefillah* and study into the moment that follows. This applies even if the matter of that moment is connected to the *avodah* of *tefillah* and the study of the *maamar*, such as reciting *Tehillim* after *tefillah* or studying the *shiur* after *tefillah*. Just as in *Nigleh*, one must be careful not to interrupt the connection between the spring and the trough beside it, as explained in the *Mishnah*, the *Gemara*, and the *poskim*.

Regarding what you wrote concerning the matter of "if he did not merit," G-d forbid, and whether this applies to one who teaches Torah in public, etc.: The story of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, is well known (it is also printed in the *Kuntres*), from which it is understood that this can apply even to public study. However, from the very fact that this story was only publicized once, and was not known before then or even after, it is understood that in the vast majority of cases, this concern is a tactic and maneuver of the *yetzer* to deter a person from participating in public Torah study, where the *zechus harabim* assists him. When the *yetzer* sees he has no other recourse, he comes with cunning, suggesting that out of *yiras shamayim* one should not engage in the matter, etc. We follow the majority.

Regarding your question about how to arrange your situation in the new section of Kfar Chabad, I have already written my opinion to several of *anash* that this is a place that was "delayed" for others, and one should not act with cunning in this matter, even if some permissive ruling could be found. On the other hand, one should strive as much as possible to be a resident of the village. For in my opinion, it is clear that it is the conduit and the vessel for receiving the blessing and success bestowed by my father-in-law, the Rebbe, who stands and serves in that place and awakens *rachamim rabim* upon *anash*, the residents of Kfar Chabad, in particular.

With a blessing for success.

## 3,398

B.H., 21 Iyar, 5715
Brooklyn.

To the Committee of Kfar Chabad,
May they live,

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letter from this past Motzaei Shabbos, in which you write that you have already submitted a full list of the settlers for the second phase: May it be the will of Hashem that it be in a good and auspicious hour, and that matters proceed with alacrity. For in many details, you have already suffered losses due to the complications and the alarming delays in bringing matters to fruition. It is already a known saying of the wise—cited in a letter from my father-in-law, the Rebbe—that the past teaches us to benefit the future. This is certainly understood regarding the buildings of the second phase, as well as regarding the other affairs of the Kfar that have been dragging on for ages. I was particularly pleased that you added plots for professionals, even though eight is insufficient; surely, if it is possible to increase this, you will do everything necessary...

3) Regarding the logic that new tenants should be placed in the apartments being vacated, rather than the Kfar committee choosing them: This initial thought is astonishing, as it is a direct preparation for losing ownership over the entire Kfar, both the old and the new. This is not merely a temporary matter, as it creates a breach and a new order. You must stand firm that you must be the ones to choose the new settlers. It is also understood that this is **not** a matter for warfare. You must immediately prepare a full list for all the apartments that will be vacated. When you come with a **prepared** list from among the *olim*, and explain that these are the people you desire, that they are compatible with your spirit, and that they are in need of housing, etc., you will be able to smoothly convey the point mentioned above—namely, that it is impossible for outsiders to interfere in the spiritual affairs of the Kfar. You will not even need to speak harshly about this, for I am certain that, for the time being, there is no intention to seat unsuitable people in the Kfar. Rather, it is simply impossible for apartments to remain vacant. In truth, it is a wonder that a list such as this is not ready on your part, at a time when it is surely known to you—through the administration of Aguch and through the *shaliach* of the *Vaad Hapoel*, R' Yisrael Leibov—that many of the *olim* were under the influence of Chabad and wish to continue this in Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt speedily. We do not cry over the past; in any event, immediately upon receiving my letter, you should contact the administration of Aguch and prepare a list containing more than the required number, since it is likely that some of those proposed by you will be disqualified by the various offices for one reason or another. It is already known the witticism that a vacant place and a void, etc., is a source for *tzimtzumim* and *dinim*. I am sending this letter of mine via express, and I am certain that the response to it will be received by return mail...

6) It is also a wonder to me that you have not begun to build the *beis knesses* and, to distinguish, the *mikveh*. As for the excuse that you currently have only half the sum: If you had adopted this method in the affairs of the Kfar—to wait until the full sum was available—the situation would be understood. Yet you have already seen tangibly that when one begins, one eventually finishes, even if at the time of the beginning one does not have the full sum in hand. Since the summer is the season for building in Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt speedily, you should certainly begin immediately with the construction of the *beis knesses* and, to distinguish, the *beis hatevilah*.

7) Regarding the name of the Kfar: Here, too, the question is a wonder, since my father-in-law, the Rebbe, named it Kfar Chabad (consequently, in all my letters, I also call it only by this name), and there is no room to change it or to add anything to it...

With blessings for good tidings regarding all of the above, as soon as possible.

## 3,399

B"H, 21 Iyar, 5715
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of the 17th of Iyar, in which you write regarding a marriage proposal you have with the daughter of a Kohen.

It is already known what our holy Torah rules, as brought in the Responsa of the Tzemach Tzedek, Even HaEzer, section 11, where his conclusion is that one should be proficient in one tractate [of the Gemara], and since many have trodden this path, it is permitted.

Regarding what you wrote, that the parents of the prospective bride (and apparently the prospective bride herself as well) do not agree that her head should be covered:

In such a case, if they do not change their minds, Heaven forbid, it is absolutely not worthwhile to involve yourself in this shidduch at all. For in addition to the fact that this is a matter of the law of Moshe and the Jewish people, as brought in the Shas and the Poskim, this itself is proof that they wish to establish and begin the marriage in opposition to the will of the King of the Kings of Kings, the Holy One, Blessed be He. See also the Zohar, Vol. 3, page 126, top of side a. To elaborate on such a simple matter is superfluous. However, if they repent and she conducts herself as a kosher daughter of Israel, then may it be His will that it should be in a good and auspicious hour.

With blessings.

## 3500

B”H, 23 Iyar, 5715
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter from before the holiday of Pesach, in which you write that there are changes in your avodah in general, and in your avodah of tefillah in particular: This matter is explained in many places in the teachings of Chassidus—beginning with the Tanya—that "one nation shall be stronger than the other," and the matter depends on him. However, one must know that just as in the physical conquest of Eretz Yisrael, the order was "little by little I will drive them out," it is the same regarding the conquest of the spiritual Eretz Yisrael within every single Jew [as is explained that *eretz* (land) corresponds to *ratzon* (will), as our Sages of blessed memory said that it wanted (*ratzah*) to do the will of its Creator; and *Yisrael* corresponds to "for you have struggled with Elokim and with men and have prevailed"].

On the contrary, when—G-d forbid—one sees a change for the worse, one must stir up an increase in one’s revealed powers and awaken one’s hidden powers through contemplation of "Why has Hashem done this?" and so forth, as is explained in the Tanya. May Hashem, blessed be He, grant you success in influencing your surroundings in this regard—which in turn adds to the *siyata d’shmaya* regarding yourself.

With blessings for the receiving of the Torah with joy and inwardness,

**M. Schneerson**

Published in Likkutei Sichos, Vol. 19, p. 464.

## 3501

B"H, 23 Iyar, 5715
Brooklyn.

...What is happening with [name]? He should be told that, together with all of Klal Yisrael, he must prepare himself to receive the Torah with joy and inwardness. ## 3102

B"H, 23 Iyar, 5715
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 3 Iyar, in which you write that your health has improved, though you have not yet returned to your full strength: it is highly probable that the lingering weakness is merely a perceived state. Therefore, diverting your attention from it—which, it is understood, does not contradict following the doctors' instructions—will complete your recovery.

Regarding your question about the *hidurim* (stringencies/refinements in mitzvah observance) that you have been accustomed to for many years, but which your husband has not yet adopted: I am confident that if you explain the *hidur* of the matter to him, he will not only refrain from hindering you in your practice, but on the contrary, he will also conduct himself in this manner. For this is a clear instruction from Above that this *hidur* is relevant to him. As is well known, the Baal Shem Tov’s adage—which we have heard many times from my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory—is that everything a Jewish person sees or hears contains a lesson for him regarding his *avodah* to his Creator. Since this *hidur* has entered his "four cubits" in one way or another, he certainly has the ability to conduct himself accordingly, and it is relevant to him.

It is understood that this, too, is subject to what is said about our holy Torah as a whole: "Its ways are ways of pleasantness, and all its paths are peace." When you explain all of the above without agitation, and in a manner of pleasantness and peace, it will certainly increase the peace in your home, and through this, the blessing of Hashem as well—for peace is the vessel that holds the blessing of the Holy One, Blessed be He, as our Mishnah rules.

With blessings,

**On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita**

**3102**

**The Baal Shem Tov’s adage:** See also above, letter 3811, and the references in the footnotes there.

3503

By the grace of Hashem, 24 Iyar, 5715
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

I received your letter of 13 Iyar in due time. I am writing to you regarding the primary matter at hand, the topic of the day, in continuation of our conversation regarding the United Front. According to reports, there is very little time left in which it is still possible to unite the lists. Given the magnitude of the matter, although we have already spoken about this and you are aware of my position and my reasoning, the instruction of our Sages is well-known: that when the time for action arrives, one is obligated to reiterate and emphasize matters of this nature.

I will focus on one point, which in my opinion is the essential one. I ask your forgiveness in advance if my words below contain a sharpness to which you are not accustomed—though surely it is clear to you that, Heaven forbid, I have no intention of attacking anyone personally. The point is as follows:

Everyone agrees—and certainly leaders of a party—that the benefit of the many (the party) supersedes the benefit of the individual, and consequently, that the benefit of the entire public supersedes the benefit of a part of it—the party. Regarding religious people—and in truth, all of Klal Yisrael are believers, the children of believers—the matter that stands above all else is the matter of *Das* (religion).

Just as a party demands from its members that they temporarily forgo their own interests for the sake of the party, and promises in return that in the final analysis the individual will also benefit from this concession, and so on—the same applies, and to an even greater degree, regarding the party’s concession of its own gains for the sake of the entire public. Needless to say, this applies to the concession of the individual, or the concession of the party or the public, for the sake of upholding **the Das** and fulfilling its requirements. Moreover, since our *Das* is the Torah of our infinite Hashem, the benefit resulting from a concession for the sake of the *Das* is also limitless in comparison to the concession itself.

In clearer terms: a religious person, and even a party that calls itself religious, must prioritize gains in the sphere of *Das* above all else, and only afterwards take into account the gains of the party.

Furthermore, it is impossible to deceive the voters indefinitely. Surely there will be those who will emphasize and highlight the glaring contradiction between the platform of a religious party and its actions, which cause **clear** damage to the *Das* for the sake of a **highly dubious** gain for the party members. This must inevitably bring damage to the party and its members as well.

It is surely unnecessary to remind you of the situation during the last elections to the Knesset, where the elections served as a battlefield for one religious party against another—a campaign of slander, abuse, and vilification of religious parties without any restraint, fulfilling in a "grand" and alarming manner the verse, "Your destroyers and those who lay you waste shall go forth from you."

All of this is appropriate when speaking to someone as a party leader. However, according to my belief, which is founded upon what is explained at length in the teachings of Chassidus—in the words of our Alter Rebbe (Tanya, end of Chapter 19)—the level of *Chochma* in the *nefesh elokis*, when it begins to exert its influence, causes all matters that oppose it, or that conceal and hide it, to be null and void, as if they never existed. As it is written, "**The mountains** melted like wax." This power is so mighty that it enables one to stand in the trial of *mesiras nefesh*, and so on. I am confident that if you contemplate for a brief moment that, according to all viewpoints, the failure to establish a United Front certainly does not escape the doubt that it is liable to damage the interests of the *Das* in the Land upon which the eyes of Hashem your G-d are from the beginning of the year to the end of the year, you will decide that in such matters, even a doubt—or a doubt of a doubt—obligates (and grants merit to) anyone who is able to do so to utilize all of their influence in the proper direction.

It is understood that the *Yetzer Hara* does not stand from afar just observing what is happening; rather, he invents for each and every person arguments suited to the nature of his soul. In the words of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, in the name of his father: "Sometimes he disguises himself in the garb of a pious, humble *tzaddik* with good character traits." There is room to say that he will come with the explanation that establishing a United Front is a deception of the people and contrary to the truth, and so on. And if that does not work, there is another piece of advice: "Who am I, and what am I? They will not listen to me, and it is not in my power to protest," and other various and strange arguments. But these arguments do not change reality, and in such cases, it is known only before the *Ribono shel Olam* whether or not it is in one's power to protest.

One of the instructions of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, is what is called in secular terms "optimism," and in the language of Chassidus—*bitachon* (trust)—that in the end, the true good will prevail. This applies not only to the distant future and the collective, but also to the individual and the near future.

Therefore, even though the thought nags that since only a few days remain in which it is still possible to establish a front, and I am certainly not the only one urging this, and all that is written above are simple and clear matters—for in any event, either the matter itself will lead to the establishment of the front, or my letter will also be of no avail—nevertheless, I have written these lines. For a person should always view himself as if he is balanced, and the entire world is balanced [with him]. I wish to trust that if special courage is needed to change a position held for several weeks, there will be no obstacle from that side. May it be the will of the *Ribono shel Olam* that you utilize this opportunity by exercising your influence to its fullest and with the greatest firmness for the establishment of the United Front of all four parties.

It is understood from the context that the intention of all that is written above is solely for a **technical** front for the sake of the elections. For anyone who links the establishment of the front to non-technical conditions that concern the day after the elections—even if they are one hundred percent correct—is, given the reality, **from the outset** nullifying the possibility of its establishment. Not only does he not fulfill it, he **destroys** this possibility.

It is my hope that, as our Sages say, a person is not held accountable for what he says in his distress, and you will not be offended by the few expressions above that may be slightly sharp. I thank you in advance if you bring me good news regarding the essential point. May it be the will [of Hashem] that my *bitachon* in the victory of the good and the truth be realized, even within the parties.

With respect and blessing.

## 3790

3790

B"H, 24 Iyar, 5715
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, etc., R' Tzvi Hirsch, may he live and be well,

Shalom u’Bracha!

In response to your letter from Lag B'Omer, in which you write that you are compiling selections from the words of our Rebbeim, arranged according to the weekly Parsha.

It is understood that this is a proper endeavor. However, for the matter to be complete, one must indicate the source from which the passage was taken, so that one who wishes to broaden his understanding of the subject may study it in its original context. It is also understood that it is not advisable to intermix into this collection sayings that are not from the aforementioned sources, even sayings from great figures of the world, and this is simple. In accordance with all this, it is also good to note above the subject matter being presented whether it is in the original language or a translation from another language. May Hashem grant you success.

With blessing,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

Secretary

## 3790

B"H, 24 Iyar, 5715
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing and learned, R' Nissan, may he live:

Peace and blessing!

Regarding your letter of 12 Iyar, in which you write that there is no one in your vicinity with whom you can study—b'li neder—the maamarim of Torah Or and Likutei Torah suitable for the Shabbos Mevarchim farbrengen before Chanukah: Our Sages have already said, "If one says, 'I have not labored but I have found,' do not believe him; if one says, 'I have labored and have not found,' do not believe him." It is obvious that the intention here is not to take away from the hours set aside for the study of Nigleh, but to add to them.

As for your observation regarding the beginning of the maamar, where it states that the one who establishes and sustains the "head" is the intellect, etc., to give birth from this understanding to *dover* (love and awe), etc., the aspect of the arms and the body in the soul, and why it omits the "head"—it is simple: this is the conclusion of the explanation regarding giving birth from this understanding to *dover*, etc., meaning the **Middos**, which are divided into three: Chesed, the right arm; Gevurah, [the left arm]; and Tiferes, the body. The reason it subsequently mentions sustaining the "head and the arms" is because it begins to explain the function of the loins, which sustain not only the Middos but also the intellect. The reason it does not detail the body here as well is: must one list everything like a peddler? All three lines were already detailed previously, **where** it enters into the **particulars** of the levels of the Middos, as it explains there, "the coals of fire, the fear of Hashem, and the shame," etc.

Regarding your observation on what is written further on in brackets, "And regarding the establishment and sustaining of the aspect of the head, it says, 'She tastes that her merchandise is good' (*ta’amah ki tov sachrah*)," and you suggest that the intention here is to the word *sachrah* (merchandise) and that it is speaking of *makifim* (encompassing lights): In my opinion, this is not so. There is no mention at all earlier regarding *makifim*, and the precision is simply in the word **"ta’amah"**—taste and intellect. It follows the previous verse, "She girds her loins with strength and strengthens her arms," which refers to the loins and the body, etc., and in continuation of this—"ta’amah," matters of *taam* (taste) and *daas* (intellect).

With blessing,

B"H, 25 Iyar, 5715
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Rabbi and Chossid, G-d-fearing and learned, involved in communal needs, R' Yitzchak, may he live.

With a blessing—in the words of my father-in-law, the Rebbe—for the receiving of the Torah with joy and inwardness,

**M. Schneerson**

## 3,509

B"H, 25 Iyar, 5715
Brooklyn.

To the Avreich, Shraga Feivish, may he live,

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter in which you write regarding the study schedule you have in the yeshiva, and subsequently your teaching of students in the Talmud Torah, and you also mention the desire to travel to America.

According to the Gemara at the end of Kiddushin, "They were created only to serve me, and I was created to serve my Maker." From this, one understands that all matters of the world—not only yours—are dependent upon the fulfillment of "I was created to serve my Maker." Therefore, since Hashem has granted you success and has chosen you as His shaliach to bring the hearts of the children of Israel closer to our Father in Heaven through the avodah of teaching Torah to students, and also to have a positive influence in the yeshiva and Talmud Torah, you should for the time being think only of how to increase [your efforts], both in quantity and in quality, as much as is possible. It is well known what the Alter Rebbe said to one of his Chassidim: that one must concern himself with what is needed of him, and Hashem will then provide for what he needs. This applies to each and every one of us.

And as you increase in your hasmadah and shekidah in your own learning, and increase in your avodah b'kodesh to expand the Yeshiva Oholei Yosef Yitzchok Lubavitch in Melbourne—through this, the blessings of Hashem and His success will also be added to your personal matters.

With blessings to receive the Torah with joy and inwardness.

## 3511

B"H, 25 Iyar, 5715
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter from Erev Shabbos Kodesh. It is surprising that in my correspondence with members of Anash, I find it necessary to mention and reiterate time and again the saying of our Alter Rebbe (which has long been printed and publicized): "You say what you need, and you do not say what is needed of you."

This is not a matter of moralizing. When my father-in-law, the Rebbe, related the above, he added the conclusion: when the Chassid of the Alter Rebbe corrected his conduct in accordance with this instruction, his situation improved—and improved even more than it had been initially. Once this was made known, the paths to this conduct and its results became easy for each and every one of us. May it be the will of Hashem that from now on, your letters—and the letters of Anash in general—will begin with good news regarding an increase in the study of Nigleh and Chassidus, in the avodah of tefillah, and in influencing others in these matters. Only afterwards should the other matters follow, for "G-d made man upright," meaning that the physical unfolds and comes about as a result of the spiritual.

As you requested, I will mention you for livelihood in abundance, with peace of mind, regarding the business matters you wrote about.

I will also mention your wife and all your children, may they live, for whatever each of them needs, as you wrote in your letter.

I conclude with a matter relevant to the day, and in the words of my father-in-law, the Rebbe: to receive the Torah with joy and with inwardness.

## 3414

B"H, 26 Iyar, 5715
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and meticulous in his communal work, R' Peretz, may he live.

Greetings and blessings,

In response to your letter of 24 Iyar, in which you write regarding the consistency of studying both the revealed Torah and Chassidus, and mention that after the holiday of Shavuos, many of anash travel to the countryside—surely, well in advance, you should begin to speak and arouse them regarding the consistency of study they should maintain in the countryside, and indeed, to increase it. For "G-d has made one thing corresponding to the other," and when the body is occupied with strengthening its health through simple, physical matters—through vacationing, trips, and the like (and the intention is not always openly to serve Hashem)—this demands an increase in the health of the neshamah as well, even more so than in the health of the body. This is because the environment in the countryside draws one toward the aforementioned simple matters more than in the city. At the very least, the increase in spirituality should match the increase in physicality.

It is brought that this is one of the reasons for studying Pirkei Avos immediately upon the onset of summer, for that is when nature strengthens, the trees blossom, and so on. It is also understood that this in no way contradicts the instruction of the Baal Shem Tov regarding "you shall surely help him" [to unload the burden of the body], and not through fasts and self-affliction, for the power of desire must be clothed in holiness, and so on, until the hoped-for promise is fulfilled: that the body will not only cease to distract the spiritual, and not only assist it, but rather, "the female shall encompass the male."

With blessings, in the words of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, for a healthy and happy summer, and with success in all matters.

## 3416

B"H, 26 Iyar, 5715
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter—which lacks a date of writing—I have already written to several of anash, and I have told you specifically several times that physicality and spirituality must walk together in everything in this world. This is especially true regarding a Jewish man and woman; when one requests success in material matters and blessing in this, it is essential to enlarge the channel and the spiritual vessels for the drawing down of these matters from Above, and these are the matters of Torah and mitzvos, as is understood. Yet, despite all the words of inspiration, they remain merely words spoken orally, and even in your letter, you evade mentioning even one word regarding the purpose of man’s creation, which is, as the Mishnah at the end of Kiddushin teaches: "I was created to serve my Maker."

Surely it is also simple to you that the soul did not descend from a high roof to a deep pit merely for the sake of business, brokerage, or similar matters. My intention is simple: to study **literally** every single day a shiur in Nigleh and a shiur in Chassidus, in addition to the three well-known daily shiurim in Chumash, Tehillim, and Tanya. And with a smile and silence, one accomplishes nothing.

With blessings for good tidings in all the above,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

Secretary

## 3,518

B"H, 28 Iyar, 5715
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter of 24 Iyar, in which you write that you have begun to study the holy Tanya and were moved by it, and that your desire to know and learn more Lubavitcher Chassidus is intense.

It is already a known ruling of the Mishnah regarding the qualities through which the Torah (every part of it) is acquired: "the companionship of friends." Therefore, it is appropriate that you connect with anash in your vicinity—the Chabad community—and you will certainly be able to find friends for this study. After all, there is nothing that can stand before one's will, especially if—as you put it—it is intense.

However, even in the teachings of Chassidus, as in all other parts of our holy Torah, the instructions of our Sages apply: "If one says, 'I have labored and not found,' do not believe him," and "The study is not the main thing, but the action." This means following its guidance and customs, though the order in this is that study leads to action.

Regarding your question as to why one must specifically study Chabad teachings:

This matter requires a lengthy explanation that is difficult to commit to writing, especially without prior knowledge of your familiarity with this system. The fundamental point is analogous to the answer to the question of why one must study Gemara and not only Mishnah or the Written Torah. The answer to that question is simple: the study of Gemara adds to, explains, and reveals what is hidden and hinted at in the Mishnah and the Written Torah. The same is true regarding Chabad teachings—they explain, clarify, and consequently reveal what is hidden and hinted at in the teachings of the Baal Shem Tov and his disciples, and in the inner dimensions of the Torah in general. If in years past, the study of the inner dimensions of the Torah was (for various reasons) reserved only for the select few, in our generation, it is a mitzvah to reveal this part of the Torah, and indeed a necessity. This is explained in the Iggeres HaKodesh of our Alter Rebbe, Epistle 26, citing the Arizal (and see at length in the introduction of his disciple, R. Chaim Vital, in Shaar HaHakdamos). It is explained at greater length in the Kuntres Eitz Chaim by my father-in-law, the Rebbe—the father of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory. This is especially true for those who sit and study in the beis medrash.

May it be the will of Hashem that your aforementioned desire overcomes the concealments and obstructions and achieves its effect—that you merit to connect with the "Tree of Life," as explained in the aforementioned Iggeres HaKodesh, based on the statement of Moshe Rabbeinu, the faithful shepherd.

With blessings to receive the Torah with joy and inwardness.

## 3519

In it, he discusses the necessity of *mitzvos ma'asiyos*, using the analogy of someone whose senses have become dulled, such that one can only connect with him through physical contact. He also discusses there how the knowledge of Torah is bound up with the refinement of the person studying it, unlike—to make a distinction—external sciences. It is surely unnecessary to remind you to leave an opening—I mean that you should have the ability to meet with them again afterward. May the *Ribono shel Olam* be with your mouth and grant you success in awakening the internal point that surely exists within every Jew, especially those who are searching for the truth.

## 3520

B”H, 1 Sivan, 5715
Brooklyn.

...Upon reading the story included in your letter, as well as your book... I must, with apologies, offer a comment:

In any translation—whether into another language, and certainly when moving from one medium to another, such as from the oral transmission of a narrator to the written letters of a scribe—it is inevitable that the translation will bear the imprint of the translator’s own perception. Most often, this is not merely an imprint, but an actual interpretation and explanation. Consequently, it is impossible for a translation to fully exhaust the multiple facets (as the Sages say: "seventy faces to the Torah," etc.) inherent in the original Torah teaching, story, or aphorism. Even when the intention is to convey the matter through its explanation—or at least through one’s interpretation of it—it is possible to achieve both: by presenting the matter in its original form, as the first recipient heard it, and adding the explanation or interpretation alongside it. In this way, both are preserved. This is all the more true regarding the teachings of the holy Nesi’im and the stories about them; for aside from the teachings recorded in the *bichlach*, the matters were preserved in their original form only by a select few individuals of exceptional caliber.

There are people who lack the ability to grasp and subsequently transmit a matter exactly as it is, without it passing through the prism of their own soul—and specifically, to use the terminology of Chassidus, in a manner of complete *hislabshus* (clothing) rather than as a mere conduit. However, as I believe I know him, if he truly desires to, he can demonstrate this "feat" of transmitting matters in their original form. The merit of the many depends upon him. If these lines of mine assist in this, that will be my reward...

With respect and blessing—in the words of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe—for the receiving of the Torah with joy and with inwardness.

## 3524
