## 3527

3527

B"H, 3 Sivan, 5715
Brooklyn

To the Administration of the Beis Medrash Nusach HaAri z"l...
May they live long.

Peace and blessing!

I have received your letter of 24 Iyar, written by the secretary, R'..., on behalf of the administration—as he writes—and in response:

Generally, when there are differences of opinion between two sides, and it takes on the form of *machlokes*, publicly and with sharp expressions, almost always both sides are at fault. Even if in varying degrees, and sometimes one side to a much greater extent, there is some fault in every side. It goes without saying that a difference of opinion is a normal phenomenon, for "their opinions are not alike," but it should not lead to *machlokes* and in a sharp form.

All the more so when this is connected to a *shul*, which is a *beis tefillah* to Him, blessed be He, where Yidden come to daven and beseech Hashem Yisbarach for what they need in *gashmius* and *ruchnius*. And the *Ribono shel Olam*, who is the *etzem hatov*, wants to fulfill their requests and prayers. However, there is a condition: that all the *mispalelim* and all those who voice opinions in the *shul* remember the ruling of the *Mishnah*: "Hashem did not find a vessel that holds blessing for Yisrael other than *shalom*." This ruling of the *Mishnah* makes it even more understandable how much *shalom* must prevail in a *beis knesses*, in addition to the general obligation of *shalom*.

It is difficult to hear the claims of one side, and while being at a distance, to issue decisions in such matters. But I am certain that with good will, there is no need to arrive at decisions from elsewhere. It is sufficient that you sit down together, remembering the statement of *Rabbeinu HaZaken* in *Tanya*, beginning of *Perek* 41, that the *Ribono shel Olam* "leaves the heavenly and earthly beings and stands over him, and looks at him, and searches his kidneys and heart." This means, quite literally, **each and every one** of those gathered, including when they will discuss the matter about which you write in the letter.

Everyone must reflect on the truth of the matter and take into account, to the fullest extent, that this is a *makom kadosh* which must draw down *kedushah* while one is there, and to a certain extent, also take home from this *kedushah*.

And surely you will find ways to ensure that there is *shalom* among everyone for long days and good years, and that all together, with a peaceful heart, will spread the *hashpaah* of their *beis medrash*—as befits a *shul* that bears such a name, *Nusach HaAri z"l*—throughout the entire vicinity.

And especially these days, days of preparation for *Matan Torah*, are suited to this, for as the *pasuk* relates, Yidden received the Torah through the fact that "Yisrael encamped (*vayichan*) there before the mountain"—*vayichan* in the singular, "all as one man."

Hoping to receive good news soon regarding this matter, and with a blessing for the receiving of the Torah with joy and *pnimiyus*.

3528

*[3 Sivan, 5715]*

Namely: a) This is not the way to excuse oneself from one’s avodah regarding the affairs of the beis medrash and the shul; on the contrary, one must increase one’s efforts in this. b) Since Hashem requires of each and every one of us the matter of peace in the context of ahavas Yisrael, in the manner of "love your fellow as yourself," it is understood from this that just as regarding oneself, "love covers all transgressions," so too, at the very least, a similar approach must be applied in fulfilling the commandment to "love your fellow." This is especially true since it is impossible for a person to be one hundred percent certain of their own claims, for according to the Torah—the Torah of life—a person cannot testify about himself. May it be His will that you bring me good news very soon that there is peace in the shul, and consequently, joy within your borders...

## 3529

3529

B"H, 3 Sivan, 5715

Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter of 27 Iyar, in which you write about the difficulties you encounter in your avodah of Hashem, and that the hisorerus you sometimes experience does not always translate into actual practice, etc., and you ask for guidance on certain matters, noting that in terms of physical health you are able to handle everything.

I have already written many times to various people who have asked about such things: the avodah of a person to his Creator is not meant to be miraculous or to involve "tricks" (and only in exceptional, temporary circumstances do such things occur). This is not the correct path, nor is it the path accessible to every soul—especially not the paved, public thoroughfare, and even more so the path of the path itself. As our Sages have taught regarding such matters (Bava Basra 10b), one should not be enticed to seek out crooked paths, for one cannot be certain where they lead.

The general guidance regarding this matter is based on what is written in Tanya, Chapter 27: "Therefore, let not a person’s heart fall..." and the note there that in these generations, which have grown weaker, fasting and self-affliction are not the paved path or the instruction for everyone. This applies only in **extremely** unique cases, specifically for a yeshiva bochur whose primary occupation is the study of Torah. It is well-known from our Sages regarding such a person that he fasts, etc., but he should consult from time to time with his mashpia. He should engrave in his heart what is said: "Little by little I will drive them out" regarding the conquest of Eretz Yisrael in the physical sense; the same applies to the conquest of the spiritual Eretz Yisrael. May Hashem grant you success.

With blessings for the receiving of the Torah with joy and inwardness.

#### ***3529***

**Fasting and self-affliction:** See also above, Letter 3389, and the references in the notes there.

## 3130

B"H, Sunday of the Three Days of Preparation, 5715
Brooklyn, N.Y.

The esteemed, pious, and lofty individual, a man of merit,
who sits in judgment and leads his community directly, etc.,
Rabbi Yehuda Shitrit, Agadir,
May he be preserved and live.

Peace and blessing!

I have received your letter, and as you requested, while I was at the Tziyun of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, the leader of Israel, I mentioned you that... they should raise their children for Torah, for the chuppah, and for good deeds, with joy and a glad heart. As is well known, the instruction of the Baal Shem Tov, transmitted by our Nasi, of blessed memory, regarding the absolute necessity to fulfill "Serve Hashem with joy," is in truth a definitive halacha in the revealed Torah, the body of Torah. This is based on what the great teacher wrote in Hilchos De'os, which is cited in the Tur and by Maran HaMechaber in Orach Chaim, siman 231, that a person serves Hashem, may He be blessed and exalted, in all his ways—in his eating, his drinking, etc., and all the other categories enumerated by the Rambam. From this, it is also understood that at all times, a person must perform the great avodah, the avodah of Hashem, with joy and a glad heart (Rambam, end of Hilchos Lulav).

In these auspicious days of preparation for the time of the giving of our Torah—both the revealed Torah and the hidden Torah, which in our generation is being revealed and explained in the teachings of Chassidus—may it be the will that each and every one of us merits, as per the saying of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, to receive the Torah (the revealed and the hidden) with joy and with inwardness.

With respect and blessing,

As you requested, I also mentioned you at a time of favor at the aforementioned holy Tziyun, even though you did not indicate your mother’s name in your letter, as is explained in the holy Zohar, Vol. 1, 84a.

## 3151

B"H, 4 Sivan, 5715
Brooklyn

To the Shabbos parties in Montreal, via Sarah Mindel, may she live.

Blessings and peace!

I was pleased to receive your letter, a report regarding the Shabbos parties and the manner in which they are conducted. And surely, in connection with the approaching Yom Tov of Shavuos, the time of the giving of our Torah, you have spoken specifically at these Shabbos parties, during the Shabbosot before Shavuos, about preparing the children for the Yom Tov of Shavuos. As our Sages, of blessed memory, tell us, when Hashem Yisbarach V'yisaleh gave the Torah to all Jews, His first condition was that Jewish children must be raised in the path of Torah; this guarantee is what brought about the giving of the Torah to all Jews.

So too, in every generation, the fact that Jewish children are raised as the Torah Hakdosha directs strengthens every Jew in all the lands where they may be found, and this brings the blessings of Hashem Yisbarach in whatever they may need.

This very thought should call forth even greater strength in each of you—among all the children of Israel, may Hashem protect them and let them live—to walk in the path of Torah and Mitzvos with renewed vigor, and to draw in all Jewish children whom it is possible to reach, so that they, too, will know that they are children of Avraham, Yitzchak, and Yaakov, and that they, too, accept the Torah from Hashem Yisbarach, the Giver of the Torah, who watches over them and blesses them in both material and spiritual matters.

With blessings for a joyous Yom Tov of Shavuos, the time of the giving of our Torah.

## 3132

B"H, 4 Sivan, 5715
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To Mr. Yechezkel, known as Prof. Kutscher,
Shalom U’vracha,

I acknowledge with thanks the receipt of your writings, a summary of your lectures on the language during the Talmudic period and the modern period, as well as the new texts written in Aramaic. I trust you will continue the good practice of sending the fruits of your labor to our library in the future, and I thank you in advance.

As is the custom of the Jewish people to connect letters to the topic of the day, and in connection with the days of the Giving of our Torah that are before us, I wish to highlight one point that has been publicized and explained thoroughly in Chassidic teachings. Even with a slight amount of contemplation, it is found in the first statement of the Ten Commandments at the standing at Har Sinai. This is the concept of Hashgacha Pratis, which the Baal Shem Tov emphasized many times and in many ways, followed by his students and the students of his students, and in Chabad Chassidus in particular. That is:

That Hashgacha Pratis is exactly as it sounds: supervision over every single detail of the created beings and over every single detail in the days of their lives.

This is unlike the opinion of many Jewish scholars and great thinkers, particularly in the Middle Ages, who held that the level of Hashgacha depends on the level and development of the one being supervised. Therefore, according to them, Hashgacha Pratis in the aforementioned sense exists only for those who possess a superior intellect, etc., etc.

However, in the first statement it says: "I am Hashem your G-d (Elokecha) who brought you out of the land of Egypt." It uses the singular form, and as is understood from the expositions of Chazal, the precision here is that every single person who stood at Har Sinai was specifically addressed. To each and every one, it was said "brought you out" in the singular, speaking to each individual, even though among them were men, women, children, and the Erev Rav, possessing varying levels of intellect, including those who were very simple.

With respect and blessing that Hashem should merit you to raise students who are G-d-fearing, the definition of which is the actual observance of Mitzvos, for this is the purpose of man’s creation, as it is written: "Fear G-d and keep His Mitzvos, for this is the whole of man."

And with the blessing for the Chag, in the traditional formula of Chassidic teachings: to receive the Torah with joy and in a spirit of Pnimiyus.

Since I have, in any event, allowed myself the time to leaf through the lectures you sent me, I will offer two or three comments, which are appended to this letter.

**A. The Talmudic Period.** This is also connected, as mentioned above, to the expression "Anochi" (I) and "Ani" (I). Surely you are aware of the wonderful teaching of Chazal (Pesikta Rabbati, Ch. 21; Pesikta D’Rav Kahana, Piska 12) that "Anochi" is said in the Egyptian tongue. A parable of a king of flesh and blood whose son was taken captive, etc. The Holy One, Blessed be He, said: "I will speak to them in the Egyptian tongue: 'Anochi Hashem Elokecha.'" See also the article by Prof. A. S. Yahuda in the *Yearbook for American Jews*, 5709.

**B. The Modern Period.** It is somewhat surprising that the school of thought—which was so captivating in its time—that emphasized the use of the Biblical language during this period was mentioned only in passing.

A general comment regarding both of the aforementioned lectures: there is no indication of sources at all. Even though these are only summaries of lectures, surely the intention of every lecturer is to awaken in the reader or listener the desire to contemplate the subject of the lecture and to delve into it. By providing sources, one not only enables this, but furthermore, by providing specific sources, one gives it the desired direction.

**C. Texts.** Page 235, column 1, the word *keshura*. It is worth noting the Targum Yonasan ben Uziel (Bereishis 19:8), "in the shadow of my beam" (*tichos talal keshura*), which is cited in the margin of the Gemara, Bava Kamma, there. And in the Targum to Shir HaShirim 1:17, which brings the languages of Targum Onkelos and Targum Yonasan on Bereishis there, *shari’ti* and *keshura*. Pesikta D’Rav Kahana 98a, and in note 182.

## 3,344

B"H, Erev Shavuos, 5715

## 3531

B"H, Erev Zman Matan Toraseinu, 5715

Regarding the efforts to bring a distinguished Sofer to your country, thank G-d, the efforts are bearing fruit and progressing. As for the details concerning his place of residence, his work, and so on, the esteemed Rabbi, the Chassid, G-d-fearing and learned, who engages in communal needs, etc., etc., Moreinu HaRav Binyamin Eliyahu Gorodetzky, may he live and be well, will discuss this with you—whether by correspondence, if possible, or in person when he visits your country in the near future. May it be the will of Hashem that through him and through me, the Name of the Holy One, Blessed be He, be exalted.

To fulfill your request, I am sending you the set of the *Sifrei* *Sdei Chemed*, ten volumes. May the desire of Hashem succeed in the hands of each and every one of us to instruct *halacha* in practice, especially regarding the *halachos* required in daily life. It has already been stated that the preparation and foundation for this is a pure *yirah* of Hashem that transcends the rationale and intellect of the rational soul and the conduct of the world. As our Sages of blessed memory stated (*Sanhedrin* 93b) regarding King David, that the *halacha* follows him in every place because **Hashem** was with him—the Essential Name, He was, He is, and He will be as one, completely above nature, and above the Name *Elokim* as it is clothed within nature. This is why our Sages of blessed memory said that *Elokim* has the same *gematria* as *HaTeva* (nature) (*Pardes*, *Shaar* 12, Ch. 2; and in *Shelah*, *Shaar HaOsiyos*, Ch. 9a, it is implied somewhat that this is so in the *Zohar* that was before him).

With respect and with blessings for *Moadim L'Simcha* and for the receiving of the Torah with joy and inwardness.

#### ***3531***

This letter is to Moreinu HaRav David Ovadia, of Morocco. Additional letters to him appear above in Vol. 7, B"H, and in the notes indicated there.

## 3256

B"H, Erev Shavuos, 5715
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of the 9th of Iyar, which arrived somewhat late, in which you write about your preoccupations and the lack of focus that consequently affects your shiurim in Nigleh and Chassidus, and your avodah of tefillah.

Regarding such a situation, the advice "acquire a friend for yourself" is well known. Beyond the fact that you surely speak from time to time with the elders of anash about everything, you should have a true friend—someone to whom you can reveal the afflictions of your heart. It is already known from our Sages that "if there is anxiety in a man's heart, he should speak of it," and the Mitteler Rebbe said regarding this that in such a manner, two nefesh habamis are fighting against one nefesh habehamis, and one can already see the benefit of this tangibly.

Regarding what you wrote about your putting on tefillin, and what you saw in the Responsa of the Tzemach Tzedek, etc.: it is obvious that your question as to whether there is an obligation to recite a blessing again when putting them on the second hand after davening has no basis, for "a doubt regarding blessings is to be resolved leniently." The question is only possible in terms of the phrasing, whether one should recite a blessing even the first time, since it is a matter of doubt. Surely, when you recite the blessing then, your intention is also for the putting on of the second hand later. Regarding the actual practice of how you should put them on, etc., the details are not sufficiently clarified in your letter; you should present them in detail to Rabbis who are authorities in halacha and possess yiras shamayim, and they will instruct you.

And last but not least, regarding your announcement of your engagement to [name], may she live and be well: may it be the will of Hashem that it be for good fortune and at a favorable and successful time, and may you build an everlasting edifice upon the foundations of Torah and mitzvos as they are illuminated by the "light of Torah"—which is the Torah of Chassidus.

With blessings for receiving the Torah with joy and inwardness.

P.S.
Regarding what you wrote, that the time for the wedding has been set for the month of Adar 5716, it is surprising that there is such a long time until the wedding, and surely both sides will agree to move it earlier, at a favorable and successful time.

## 3737

B"H, 8 Sivan, 5715

Agudas N'shei U'Bnos Chabad
Kinsman-Cleveland Branch

Blessings and Peace!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter from 2 Sivan, regarding the meeting held two weeks ago, along with the enclosure.

In these days associated with the *Zman Matan Toraseinu*, your check has been delivered to support those who study Torah without any specific "ulterior motive," but simply because it is our holy Torah, the Torah of Hashem. May the merit of this stand for every one of the participants in the branches, that they should have true Torah *nachas*—both *b'gashmius* (materially) and *b'ruchnius* (spiritually)—for themselves and for every member of their family. And, in the words of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, may every one of you and your families have a healthy and happy summer, among the rest of *Klal Yisrael*.

## 3398

B"H, 8 Sivan, 5715
Brooklyn.

To the avreich Yosef, may he live, Melamed,

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letter of 2 Sivan, in which you write that you are establishing an association of Yemenite yeshiva students, describing the purpose of the association, etc., and asking whether to join it.

In such matters, one should wait until the character of the association and its affairs are clearly revealed. This is not always dependent even upon the will of the founders, and especially when that will itself is not clear. As our Sages of blessed memory said, no person knows what is in the heart of his fellow. This is especially true in Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established, where one must be extremely cautious about affiliating with any organization or association until one has observed its activities over a period of time. Only then is it possible to know its essence, who the people behind it are, and so on—once their true nature is clearly and tangibly seen.

With blessing,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita

## 3540

3540

B"H, 9 Sivan, 5715

## 3511

B"H, 9 Sivan, 5715
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter from the eve of the time of the giving of our Torah, the essence of which is as our Sages of blessed memory have stated, and as brought down by the Rambam at the end of Hilchos Chanukah: "Great is peace, for **the entire Torah** was given to bring peace to the world, as it is written: 'Its ways are ways of pleasantness, and all its paths are peace.'"

I have spoken with you several times in person, and I have also written in my letters, that there must be peace among anash. As the saying of the Tzemach Tzedek goes: A.B.G.D. — *Achdus* (unity) is *Bracha* (blessing), *Ga'avah* (pride) is *Dalus* (poverty). This applies to material matters, and all the more so to spiritual ones. It is also understood that if there were no cause for the opposite of peace, there would be no need to urge it or warn about it in so many ways. Therefore, it must be that even if one’s intellect proves that the opposite of peace is necessary—and not only one’s own intellect, but even a "true" intellect or the intellect of the *nefesh habehamis* says so—one must nevertheless strive for peace. This is why there are so many warnings and wonderful promises regarding peace; see also *Likutei Torah* for the three *parshiyos*, end of *Parshas Noach*.

Furthermore, since it is said of everyone that he is "close to himself" and is therefore a "party to the matter," the bribe of self-love **cannot** fail to blind, as is brought in the *Shas* regarding the greatest of the *Amoraim* in similar situations. Therefore, there is no diminution of stature or loss of honor, *chas v'shalom*, if one considers that perhaps, to his own eyes, the situation and the matters appear differently than they are in truth, since he is a party to the matter.

After all this, even if we were to say that you are one hundred percent correct, it is impossible for any institution to be run by several people with differing opinions. It is already known: "One leader for a generation, and not two leaders." Even though "there is salvation in a multitude of counselors," one must rely on the decision of those who are the managers of the institution, even though they too are human beings and are therefore liable to err. There is no other way, for otherwise, it would introduce disorder into all the institutions—especially in an institution of holiness, where the *yetzer hara* stands and waits for every slight movement of a lack of *hischazkus* and every slight movement of a division of hearts, in order to magnify it, etc., etc.

I have already written to you once that when the Rebbe, my father-in-law, was the active manager of Tomchei Temimim in Lubavitch, even the Rebbe Rashab would not intervene in the affairs of the Yeshiva except through him. It once happened that for some reason there was a difference of opinion between them, and the Rebbe Rashab said that they should act according to the instruction of the Rebbe, my father-in-law. From this, we have a *binyan av* (a foundational precedent), and *kal v'chomer* regarding what you write about the administration...

***

**As the saying of the Tzemach Tzedek:** See also above, Vol. 8, Letter 2844, and the references in the notes there.

**I have already written:** See above, Vol. 8, Letter 2607.

## 3542

B"H, 9 Sivan, 5715
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter from before the festival of the time of the giving of our Torah, in which you write that you feel you are lacking something in Torah or in yiras shamayim, etc. However, you do not mention anything regarding your study of nigleh or your order of study in Chassidus, which are surely not as they should be. Consequently, it is no wonder that you have this feeling. Since you are asking for advice: before davening (on weekdays) in the morning, you should set aside a few coins for tzedakah and study a topic in Chassidus. These two things are the advice for your tefillah to be accepted. After all, the beginning of the requests for personal needs, which are in the middle twelve blessings, is *chonein hada'as* (granting knowledge). Likewise, be careful with *tevilas Ezra* and study Torah with *hasmadah* and *shekidah*, as Rashi explains from the Sifra on "If you walk in My statutes," that you must be **toiling** in Torah. It is already known that our Sages ruled: "If you have not **toiled** and found, do not believe it."

Surely you are aware of the three daily shiurim for everyone, from the takanah of the Rebbe, my father-in-law, of blessed memory, in Chumash, Tehillim, and Tanya. In any event, from now on, be careful to fulfill them. My hope is strong that if you do all of the above, your situation will improve little by little. And even though your awareness that you are lacking and need to improve will strengthen, at the same time, during your study and in the performance of mitzvos with *hiddur*, there should be joy in your heart, as is explained at length in Tanya that these two matters do not contradict one another.

With blessings for Torah study with yiras shamayim.

## 3544

3544

B"H, 11 Sivan, 5715
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter of 1 Naso, in which you write regarding the peace and well-being of your family, may they live and be well, may it be the will of Hashem that you always have good news to report regarding each and every one of them. This is especially true for those who reside in the *ohel* of Torah—that is, within the four *amos* of Torah study—where they study both the *gufa d’Oraisa* and the *nishmasa d’Oraisa* together. As is explained at length in the holy *Zohar*, Volume 3, page 152a, how **essential** the study of *pnimiyus haTorah* is, for it provides vitality to the study of the *nigleh* portion of Torah and to the performance of *mitzvos* with *hiddur*; see there at length, and for even further explanation, in the introduction of Rav Chaim Vital, the disciple of the holy Arizal, to *Shaar HaHakdamos*. This applies especially to those who descend from a lineage of *Chassidim*, for surely the souls of their ancestors find no rest or *nachas ruach* except when they see their descendants observing the guidance of *Toras HaChassidus* and engaging in its study. To elaborate on such a simple matter would be superfluous.

May it be the will of Hashem that this matter be internalized by you, and consequently, you will find the appropriate words to explain this to your sons, may they live. May it be His will that they merit *siyatta d’shmaya* and begin this as soon as possible, for in Torah in general, and in the study of the *nishmasa d’Oraisa* in particular, every moment lost is an irretrievable loss, while in a single hour and a single moment, one can acquire his world. And to the wise, a word is sufficient.

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita

## 3545

Brooklyn.

In response to your letter via the distinguished student... may he live, in which he writes that he suffers from the issue of forgetfulness:

Before Shacharis on weekdays, he should set aside a few coins for tzedakah. He should also establish a regular time to study that part of the Torah which the holy Zohar states is the "soul of the Torah." From this it is understood that it adds vitality to the study of the revealed Torah (nigleh), which is referred to there as the "body of the Torah," and vitality is a segulah for memory, as it is written in Tehillim (31:13), "I am forgotten like a dead man from the heart," etc. He should also study the Laws of Torah Study by our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe, chapter 2, end of paragraph 10. May Hashem grant him success in studying Torah with yiras shamayim.

## 3596

3596

B"H, 11 Sivan, 5715
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

...Regarding what you noted concerning the discourse *Ki Tavo* 5666, that for the Baal Shem Tov, place and time were not limiting factors, and he perceived them as an actual vision. You raised a difficulty regarding this, etc.

The matter discussed in that discourse refers to the place and time of this world of Asiyah, which did not limit him. He saw the matters of this world without limitations, etc. It does not relate to the concept of *mah* (whatness) and existence, and the like. See the story in the book *Derech Emunah*, page 129; in the book *Derech Mitzvosecha*, at the end of the *mitzvah* of *Emunas Elokus*; and in my notes there.

## 3547

B"H, 13 Sivan, 5715
Brooklyn.

To the distinguished Rabbi and Chossid, G-d-fearing and learned, involved in communal needs,
Rabbi Mordechai [HaKohen]

Peace and Blessing!

In response to your letter from Motzaei Chag HaShavuos—regarding the esrogim: It would be appropriate—without causing a stir—to send a suitable person to the orchard’s location. This person should also be someone who knows the local language and can speak with the orchard owner in a way that leads him to speak naturally about how the trees are grown, etc. It would be best to speak about this as well with third parties who live in that area, who have no personal stake in the matter but, as neighbors, certainly know how the orchards are maintained. In this way, there is room to clarify the aforementioned detail. Furthermore, it is worthwhile to take three esrogim from different trees in the orchard and examine them in accordance with the signs brought in the Acharonim, which are also cited in Shaar HaKollel. It is understood that the sooner this is done, the better, especially since there is a possibility that others might get there first.

Since there is no reason to assume that only this specific orchard is free of grafting, and there are certainly other such places, it would be worthwhile to check in other locations as well and clarify the matter as mentioned above. It is understood that I will also participate in the expenses for this, at a fair price.

Since you do not mention the young man... it seems you have no information about him. Surely he, too, could assist in this. Perhaps Mr. ... [may he live and be well] could assist you; he is surely well-known to many in his city and country, and among them are those who would agree to make such a trip and would be diligent and clever enough to clarify all of the above.

In connection with this—they should also find a place to obtain seeds and saplings, as I do not believe that this can only be done in the month of Teves.

I was pleased to hear that what you wrote regarding the matters of Pesach in the local language has already been printed. It is surprising that you did not enclose it in your letter, and you do not even write whether it was published in a newspaper, a booklet, or something similar. You should certainly send the printed material here as soon as possible, and thank you in advance. The same applies to the matters regarding Chag HaShavuos that you write about...

## 3548

B"H, 13 Sivan, 5715
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Rabbi and Chossid, G-d-fearing and learned, engaged in communal needs,
Rabbi Chaim Shaul, may he live.

Greetings and blessings!

As you requested, I will mention your wife, may she live, at the holy resting place of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, for the improvement of her health. May He who heals all flesh and performs wonders—for whom nothing is too difficult—grant her a complete recovery.

I was pleased to read in your letter that next week you are laying the cornerstone for the building of the Yeshiva Achei Temimim in Rishon LeZion. May it be the will of Hashem that this Yeshiva becomes a "cornerstone." As is explained in Chassidus, there are three crowns: the crown of Kehunah, the crown of Torah, and the crown of Malchus. And there is a fourth—the stone which the builders rejected (which subsequently) became the cornerstone—which is the crown of a good name that rises above them all. The precision of the term **"above them"** is explained by the fact that, ultimately, even Torah, Malchus (influence, acts of kindness, "a daughter was given to Avraham"), and Kehunah (avodah) are contained within it.

With blessings for success in your holy work and for good tidings regarding all the above.

**M. Schneerson**

## 3550

3550

B"H, 13 Sivan, 5715
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter from before the holiday of Shavuos, in which you write that you were raised among Chassidim and that Hashem has granted you the merit and success to recognize the necessity of knowing Hashem, etc., and you ask for guidance on the path you should follow in the study of Chassidus, in the avodah of tefillah, etc., and what preparation is required, etc.

It is understood that the manner of study, and especially the avodah of the heart, is not the same for every soul, even though everyone is obligated in them, for they are commandments of Hashem and are among the constant mitzvos at all times and in all places, etc. As is explained in the introduction to Sefer HaChinuch, the **manner** of study and avodah depends on the characteristics of the soul and its talents.

Therefore, it is best that you meet with the elder anash in your vicinity, and primarily with a mashpia of the teachings of Chassidus, and consult with them. Hashem will grant them the correct insight, so that the manner [of your avodah] will also be good before Him in every detail.

However, one fundamental preparation is necessary for **everyone**, and it is this: Just as it is understood and simple that the acceptance of the Torah in its entirety is possible only through the prerequisite of *na'aseh* before *nishma*, as is explained in the discussion regarding the receiving of the Torah (Shabbos 88a and onward)—and furthermore, regarding us, who are complete, it is written, "The integrity of the upright shall guide them," and regarding them [the nations], it is written, etc. (ibid. 88a, end)—so too is it exactly with all parts of the Torah. This is all the more true regarding the study of the inner dimension of the Torah, which is called in the holy Zohar the "soul of the Torah," since a person’s yetzer hara fights against this study with even greater intensity and strength. See the Kuntres Eitz Chaim by my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory. But on the other hand, every single person is given the ability and the strength to overcome it. Hashem helps him, especially in our generation—this orphaned generation—where it is a mitzvah and an absolute necessity to study this part of the Torah and to publicize it. May Hashem grant you success in all of the above.

It is surely unnecessary to remind you to be careful regarding *tevilas Ezra*, and to keep the three daily study portions that are incumbent upon everyone, as instituted by my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory—the well-known portions of Chumash, Tehillim, and Tanya.

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

Secretary

## 3551

B"H, 13 Sivan, 5715
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

...I have already replied to your letter, and I am certain you have received the response and read it with the appropriate attention. My hope is strong that you will fulfill the requests made in my letter, the core of which is that you should not act as a sole judge. As the Mishnah states, "One should not judge alone, for there is only One who judges alone, and who can compare to Him or be likened to Him?" Furthermore, there is no diminution of one's stature or honor in acting according to the instruction of the many and in consultation with them, as well as with the instruction of the school administration. You must remember—and it should be engraved upon your mind and heart—that several students have been entrusted to your care, and regarding each one of them it is said, "You are children to Hashem your G-d." You bear the responsibility, and it is far too great for you to carry based solely on your own judgment, understanding, and intellect. This is not the case when the opinion of the administration as a whole is involved, for then the merit of the many assists in steering toward the desired outcome. It is also understood that your own personal development, as an individual and in private matters, has no place at the expense of a loss regarding your students.

In truth, the phrase "has no place" is a refined way of putting it; see the Laws of Talmud Torah by our Alter Rebbe, Chapter 1, Section 12, and the sources noted there. I hope that I will not need to write further regarding all of the above. Even if, in your opinion, there are those among the members of the administration who are lesser than you, our Sages of blessed memory have already said, "Fortunate is the generation in which the great listen to the small..."

Awaiting good news regarding all of the above.

## 3552

B"H, 13 Sivan, 5715
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

...Regarding your notification concerning the state of your wife’s health, may she live and be well: It should have been explained to you that each and every one of us asks—and at times even demands—from the Ribono shel Olam, the Creator of all worlds, that He bestow upon us all our needs and even fulfill our desires, without taking into account how worthy we are of this, and how appropriate it is that the Hakadosh Baruch Hu—of Whom it is said, "To whom will you liken Me, that I should be equal? says the Holy One"—should concern Himself with our needs. Furthermore, He even fulfills our desires in matters that, even in the eyes of man, are trivial. Yet, despite this, we ask and demand the aforementioned, and the Hakadosh Baruch Hu, in His kindness—a kindness of grace—fulfills the prayer.

When, alongside this, the Hakadosh Baruch Hu comes and asks that one do something to draw close the heart of His only child—which refers to each and every one of the Bnei Yisrael, son or daughter, who for various reasons does not know what is required of them in matters of Torah and mitzvos—and the Hakadosh Baruch Hu says that He created all the worlds for the purpose that this specific person, with the assistance of his wife, may she live, should make for Him a *dirah b'tachtonim* in the heart of this specific boy or girl, and for this purpose He leaves the higher and lower realms, etc., as explained in the Tanya in several chapters—then it is a simple matter that not only must one fulfill the request of the Hakadosh Baruch Hu completely, but one must do so with joy and great happiness that they have merited that the Hakadosh Baruch Hu turned to them with this request, and gave them the opportunity to fulfill His desire. Moreover, He promises in return for this matter both physical and spiritual good for them and for their children, may they live.

If you contemplate all of the above even for a brief moment, I see no room for any complaint or any bitterness, but rather, on the contrary, only for great and immense joy...

## 3553

B"H, 13 Sivan, 5715
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter, you inform me regarding the state of your health, which is not as it should be. According to your own assessment, you are not fit for your work of traveling to increase and glorify Torah, and you therefore request that your travel obligations be eased.

I have become accustomed to various and strange requests, but I did not imagine that you would write a request ending in such a manner. Consider this: according to your own assessment, your health is not as it should be, and therefore, in your opinion, your work is difficult for you. Consequently, you are not asking for an improvement in your health, but rather to be relieved of your work—the opposite of the logic of the *nefesh habehamis*, the opposite of the logic of the *nefesh hasichlis*, and so on.

It is well known how the verse is explained: "You satisfy the desire of every living thing" (*masbi'a l'chol chai ratzon*)—He satisfies every living thing according to its desire **and craving** (*ta'avah*). This means that Hashem, in His kindness—a kindness of grace—fulfills not only one's desire but also one's craving. But this applies only where there is no harm involved. Even though in human law one is exempt regarding oneself, in the laws of Heaven it is not so. Therefore, my request on your behalf is that your health situation should improve to the point that even according to your own opinion and assessment, you will be able to continue your holy work with success.

We conclude with good news, regarding what you wrote that a year has passed since the wedding of your son, *shlita*. May it be the will of Hashem that their home be a true Chassidishe home, from which vitality and Chassidishe warmth will spread to their surroundings. This will add to the blessings of Hashem in all that they require, with children, life, and abundant sustenance.

With blessings for proper health and for good tidings in all of the above.

## 3554

B"H, 13 Sivan, 5715
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter from the day after Shavuos, in which you write that you find it difficult to study for a length of time with the appropriate concentration unless you are in the company of friends, and that you lack the strength for diligent study, etc.

It is well known that *dveikus chaverim* (bonding with friends) is one of the forty-eight ways through which Torah is acquired. Regarding your statement that you are naturally lazy and lack the strength for diligence: you can change your nature by yourself. Although the way to do this is as it is written, "little by little I will drive them out," and not from one extreme to the other all at once. The procedure for this is to add just a few moments of study from one day to the next. Furthermore, the study itself should be, as our Sages said, in a place where your heart desires. Additionally, do not spend a long time on one subject; rather, when you feel you are becoming weary, switch to studying a second subject that matches what your heart desires, as mentioned above.

The statement of our Sages is famous: "Were it not for the Holy One, Blessed be He, helping him..." and our Sages also said that the Holy One, Blessed be He, only makes demands of a person according to his strength. From this, it is understood that everyone is given the strength to overcome their own *yetzer*. Since one needs *siyata d’shmaya* (heavenly assistance) in everything, you should frequently set aside a few coins for *tzedakah* before *davening* Shacharis. After *davening* Shacharis, recite the daily portion of *Tehillim* according to the monthly division. Also, establish a regular *shiur* in the *nishmata d’oraysa*—the inner dimension of the Torah, which in our times has been revealed in the teachings of Chassidus. I am confident that if you conduct yourself according to all the above, then little by little, step by step, the situation will improve for the better.

Regarding what you wrote about the condition of your wife, *tichyeh*:

It would be worthwhile to have the *mezuzos* in your home checked (if they have not been checked within the last twelve months), and also to have your *tefillin* checked. Your wife, surely, follows the custom of virtuous daughters of Israel to set aside *tzedakah* before lighting the candles every *Erev Shabbos* and *Erev Yom Tov*.

May the *Ribono shel Olam* cause her pregnancy to be completed properly and with ease, and may she give birth to a healthy child at the proper time, properly and with ease.

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, *shlita*,

Secretary

## 3505

B"H, 15 Sivan, 5715
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

...Regarding what you wrote, that there are those who criticize him and his actions, etc. — he should divert his attention from all of this. Surely, a large part of this is merely imaginary, and as for the remainder, it should be nullified through the principle of "as water reflects a face to a face," etc.; he should improve his attitude toward those individuals. **And if** anything still remains, there is no need to be distracted from the *avodah* in holiness, in spreading the teachings of Chassidus, its guidance, and its customs...

Regarding what you wrote about the fear at night: He should have his *tefillin* and *mezuzos* checked, be more meticulous in *krias shema al hamitah*, and before going to sleep, recite by heart or contemplate a few lines of *Tanya*. He should study *Shaar HaBitachon* in *Sefer Chovos HaLevavos* a few times, and divert his attention from the fear—meaning, do not even fight it. It will weaken on its own until he is completely rid of it. And surely, he should keep a picture of *k'vod kedushas moreinu v'rabbeinu Admur* in a pocket-sized format.

## 3550

B"H, 15 Sivan, 5715
Brooklyn.

To the Administration of Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim in Lod,
To the Administration of the Vocational Schools in Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established,
May Hashem grant them life,

Peace and blessing!

... In the list of students for the vocational school, there are several who are thirteen or fourteen years old. Seemingly, this is too young an age to be satisfied with only a few hours of kodesh studies a day, while the rest of the hours are dedicated to secular studies.

And even though the Sephardim are not accustomed to such an arrangement, and it is possible that they are even threatening that, regardless, they will instruct their sons to enroll in a different institution—nevertheless, even regarding this, as mentioned above, special propaganda is necessary among the students. Even after they have entered the vocational school, they should interrupt their studies to learn for a period of time, whether in Lod, Tel Aviv, or similar places, in order to fill the void in their knowledge of Torah...

Regarding the buildings in Teveria and the rationale for opening a yeshiva there, it appears that this is a complicated matter from all sides—regarding the landowners, the owners of the buildings, etc. Since, in addition to this, there is the difficulty of the distance and so on, perhaps the entire matter should be reconsidered from the beginning. Is it worth the distraction and all the effort for a matter that is doubtful from all sides? In exchange for this, it would perhaps be more appropriate to invest the energy into organizing additional students in the Kfar buildings that are being vacated by those moving to the new Kfar. By doing this, several issues would be solved at once, and furthermore, the supervision and the like would be incomparably easier. There is also room to say that even regarding receiving assistance in this very Kfar from similar institutions, there are many people who have a special relationship with the matters located in the Kfar.

With blessing,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

A. Quint
Secretary

## 3557

3557

B”H, 15 Sivan, 5715
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter from 7 Nissan. It is understood that what I wrote in my previous letter—that it is appropriate to refrain from internal examinations—applies only during the months of pregnancy and is not relevant before or after the birth.

Regarding what you write, that you cannot take on more work in the vineyard of Chabad due to your financial situation: I have already written to several people among Anash that the work in Kfar Chabad is not a favor they are doing for our holy Rebbe, but rather, primarily, a favor they are doing for themselves. This is not only regarding matters of the World to Come, but also regarding matters of this world—in health and in livelihood. Consequently, if one finds themselves in a situation where their health or livelihood is not as it should be, Heaven forbid, one of the *segulos* for their improvement is to increase one’s efforts in the vineyard of Chabad. One should not say that only after they recognize the benefit will they take the "remedy" for their situation; rather, it is straightforward. This is similar to the teaching of our Sages, "Salt for money is lacking [i.e., salt preserves money]." May it be the will of Hashem that these words be absorbed by you with the intent to act upon them, and may you be *tofeach al menas hatpiach*—moist enough to moisten others—regarding this as well.

With blessings for good tidings in all the above, and for livelihood.

## 3558

B"H, 16 Sivan, 5715
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

After a long silence, I was pleased to receive your letter from Beha'aloscha. Although, you should have been more cheerful, for you are only complaining about the fact that **according to your calculations**, your material debts have increased by a few hundred dollars. From this, I infer that your health and similar matters are in order. If that is the case, since this is nothing more than a temporary matter for a short time, and it is only a question of a few hundred dollars, it is not worth being unhappy—especially since you had a simcha, as your daughter and her husband celebrated the Pidyon HaBen of their son, shlita. On the other hand, it does not surprise me so much that you are thinking so much about a debt of a few hundred dollars. The reason for this is that you do not attend Chassidishe farbrengens often enough; these refresh the nefesh elokis and help a person rise above daily life. Even if the impression of the farbrengen is only visible for a short while, one feels it internally for a much longer time, as one discovers on various occasions.

Regarding the matter of the debt itself: there is the advice that our Sages of blessed memory provide, "Salt for money is lack" (meaning, if one feels a lack in money, one should begin to give more tzedakah). This helps to have an increase in parnassah, just as Hashem has promised, "Give tithes so that you may become wealthy." It is not always necessary to demand that Hashem should provide an increase in parnassah, after which the person must then stand in a test; one may take the other path: to begin giving more tzedakah first, and be certain that the Holy One, blessed be He, will fulfill His promise. May Hashem grant you success in giving tzedakah fully and with a cheerful heart. Also, take care to recite the daily portion of Tehillim as it is divided throughout the days of the month—after davening—and take part in the shiurim that are studied in public. This will hasten good tidings in all the aforementioned.

With blessings.

## 3549

16 Sivan, 5715
Brooklyn

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and learned scholar, R. Moshe Halevi, may he live:

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letter of 12 Sivan. I am returning the list as you requested. Regarding what you noted once again from the letter you received from the heir of the Rebbe, R. Y. Z. Margalit, etc., I have already written that I am surprised by his position on this.

1) His claim that it is explicitly stated in the writings of the Arizal that the *mitzvos* are *mochin d’Abba* and not *keilim* is incomprehensible. He did not need to "bring his bread from afar," for in the *Chassidus* of our holy Rebbes, this is cited **at length** and explained: in *Likutei Torah*, in the *Siddur*, in *Derech Mitzvosecha*, and so on. And yet, the Rebbe, my father-in-law, stated in the name of his father, the Rebbe Rashab, that the *mitzvos* hint to *keilim*. It must therefore be that there is no contradiction here at all.

In truth, his difficulty is incomprehensible: a) Within *mochin d’Abba* themselves, there are both *oros* and *keilim*. b) The *mitzvos*, like all matters of Torah and *mitzvah*, hint to several concepts in *Beriah, Atzilus*. It is well known that *mitzvos* are *mochin d’Abba*, yet they are also *k’neged* the Patriarchs—that is, *k’neged Chesed, Gevurah, Tiferes*—and together with this, they are in *Malchus*, the "bread of affliction," etc., as brought in the writings of the Arizal, and even in the *Zohar* and *Tikkunei Zohar*.

The same applies to his claim that there is no source in the Arizal to say that what is placed upon the *mitzvos* hints to *oros*. This is also as stated above: a) The concepts hinted at by the six things placed upon the *mitzvos* include both *oros* and *keilim*. b) These six things also hint to several concepts, as mentioned above. I do not have the time now to search the writings of the Arizal for the aforementioned location (but see *Ma’orei Or*, *Klal HaYedios*, etc., under their respective entries).

However, a) it is clear that it is impossible for you to find a contradiction there, since the aforementioned was stated by the Rebbe Rashab. b) It is **highly probable** that a source for this can be found in the writings of the Arizal, and perhaps even in the *Tikkunim*.

As for the rabbi’s concluding remark that if these words had come from the mouth of the Alter Rebbe, they would be important and acceptable to him just as if they came from the Arizal—the Rebbe Rashab, who is the successor of our Alter Rebbe, is certainly worthy of being relied upon in such matters, and in matters far greater than this.

Compelled by the words of our Sages to judge every Jew favorably, it is possible that he did not write to the aforementioned person that these are the words of the Rebbe Rashab, and that is why he wrote what he wrote.

Regarding his statement that there are Kabbalists who skip over certain words from the *Chaverim* in *Pri Etz Chaim*—it is obvious that this is not our tradition. Matters from the *Chaverim* are cited in *Chassidus*, including in *Likutei Torah*, etc. Furthermore, there is what is brought in *Chassidus* in many places—the tradition of the Ramak, the tradition of R. Y. Sarug, etc., which differs from many of the Sephardic Kabbalists. The matter can be explained by the fact that the later authorities did not want to enter into an area of doubt, whereas the Baal Shem Tov, the Maggid, the Alter Rebbe, and their successors—who had a tradition from one to another, and the Baal Shem Tov from Achiyah HaShiloni (who was one of those who received from Elijah the Prophet)—knew in which matters one should rely. As is also known, this is why they relied on what is written in *Emek HaMelech* (and see *Likutei Torah*, *Shir HaShirim* 27a: "And in *Etz Chaim* it is not mentioned at all," and in the places marked in the indices to *Torah Or* regarding the disputes of the Kabbalists and the like).

2) Regarding his statement concerning participation in the elections: We have nothing but the words of our Rebbe, the Rebbe, my father-in-law, who even now stands in his place and serves, and here as well. For the elections to the first Knesset, he commanded and exerted effort that they should participate, from which it is understood that it is not only permitted, but that one is obligated to do so.

Even though entering into a coalition, in my opinion, is forbidden because of participation in the decreeing of laws against, etc.—anyone who holds a citizenship card, and consequently has the right to vote (and by the very act of taking the card, he acknowledges, not under duress, the administration there), if he then does not participate in the elections, and others follow his lead, there is room to say that because of this, a decision on a "major" or even minor law might be tipped—when they vote on a law improperly, the stumbling block of the many, G-d forbid, rests upon him as well. And I have not found the man with "broad shoulders" who can bear such a stumbling block upon himself.

It is understood that these words do not apply to those who do not recognize the administration **at all**, or who do not wish to travel to Eretz Yisrael for this reason, etc. But for those who are there and participate in whatever matters there are, and only regarding the specific detail of participating in the elections they highlight their zealotry—this is the exact opposite of what is reasonable.

Moreover, they are harming the many, as mentioned above. Especially after having seen in practice over the past years that the deciding vote of one representative could have prevented matters that cause the many to stumble in prohibitions of the Rabbis and even prohibitions of the Torah. A word to the wise is sufficient.

It goes without saying that you are permitted to write to the aforementioned person everything I have written here regarding the elections, and you may also add sharpness to it—for however much you add, it will not exhaust the entire matter. It is specifically after the Giving of the Torah that there was no room for the conduct of Noah, who saved himself but did not rebuke the people of his generation **as required**, as is stated in the holy *Zohar*. This is not the case after the Giving of the Torah, when all of Israel is one complete stature. As is also explained regarding the Giving of the Torah, that we follow the majority, for if the six hundred thousand minus one (and consequently also Micah, who set up an idol—included in this) had not been present, the Torah, G-d forbid, would not have been given. As is stated in *Devarim Rabbah*, ch. 7, 8, and in the *Mechilta d'Rashbi*.

The books of the aforementioned person that you mention in your letter are not with me; they are *Tikkun HaYesod*, *Yishev Ruacho*.

With blessing,

**M. Schneerson**

## 3661

B"H, 17 Sivan, 5715
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter of 12 Sivan.

Your reasoning and opinion are correct: to seek a suitable shidduch for yourself specifically in Morocco, rather than rushing to make aliyah to Eretz HaKodesh—may it be built and established by Moshiach Tzidkeinu. After all, one of the thirteen principles of our faith is the belief in the coming of Moshiach; we believe every day that he will come. If thousands and myriads of Yidden are waiting and anticipating his arrival while in Chutz LaAretz, then you, too, can be included among those who fear Hashem and serve Him in Chutz LaAretz through the study of Torah and the performance of mitzvos with hidur.

This is especially true given that Hashem has enabled you to stand in a place of light, bringing the hearts of Yidden closer to our Father in Heaven through proper chinuch—there is no finer portion than this. Remain at your post where you are currently working, and speedily in our days, the promise of the coming of the true Redeemer will be fulfilled, and he will lead us upright to our land in the true and complete Geulah.

With blessings for success in all the above.

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita

## 3762

B"H, 17 Sivan, 5715

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter from the first of Beha'alotcha, in which you write regarding your state of health, feeling weakness, forgetfulness, etc.

Surely you are keeping the three daily study portions established for every person by my father-in-law, the Rebbe—the well-known Chumash, Tehillim, and Tanya—as well as the chapter of Tehillim corresponding to your age. We have heard several times from my father-in-law, the Rebbe, that in such matters it is appropriate to study Mishnayos in general, and Mishnayos by heart in particular. It is also good that when you study a certain subject for a while and feel fatigued, you should switch to a different area of Torah study, as our Sages have said, "in the place where his heart desires." Through increasing your avodah of tefillah—which is the "conversation and discussion" that elevates Torah study to the highest levels, as explained in the Zohar and Tikkunim and cited in Tanya, chapters 39 and 40 (the source of which in the revealed Torah is already known in the name of the Alter Rebbe from Pesachim 56b)—you will rise above the world of forgetfulness in general, and the power of memory will be strengthened. This is also brought down from what the Alter Rebbe wrote in his Hilchos Talmud Torah, chapter 2, paragraph 10, at the end. May Hashem grant you success for long, good years, to spread the light of Chassidus and its illumination in your immediate surroundings, and also in surroundings that for the time being are **not yet** close.

With respect and blessing.
