Due to a certain reason, the sending of this letter was delayed. In the meantime, your two letters were received, along with the news that you are traveling to "green pastures" (which the Midrash Tehillim at the end of Psalm 23 explains as: the goodness of the world). May it be the will of Hashem that it be in a good and auspicious hour, and in the words of my father-in-law, the Rebbe: a healthy summer.

## 3663

B"H, 18 Sivan, 5715
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 13 Sivan, in which you write that you are studying in the yeshiva and attending shiurim without the assistance of a teacher, and you ask in what manner, path, and method you should approach the study of our holy Torah—whether you should focus more on *girsa* (breadth/memorization) or *iyun* (depth/analysis), and whether to study with a *chavrusa* or by yourself.

It is well known that our Sages ruled that both are necessary: both *girsa* and *iyun*. The proportion of one to the other depends on the talents and the inclination of the student’s soul, and no hard and fast rules can be set in this regard. However, *girsa* and proficiency in the *halachos* required for daily life are essential—especially in our Holy Land, may it be built and established, where additional *halachos* pertaining to the land have been added, and few are proficient in them. This is the whole of man: "Fear Hashem and keep His *mitzvos*."

Furthermore, in our generation—and especially for members of the Sephardic communities, whose ancestral tradition is to study the inner dimensions of the Torah—it is essential to set a fixed time for the study of the *neshamta d’oraysa* (the soul of the Torah), the hidden aspects of Torah, which in our generation has been revealed and explained in the teachings of Chassidus. It would be appropriate for you to meet with the esteemed Rabbi and Chossid, Rabbi Nachum Shmaryahu Shunkin, who resides at the Refugees’ Rabbis’ housing in Jerusalem, may it be rebuilt and established. He will advise you on a study schedule, and through him, you will be able to meet with *avreichim* and *bochurim* who have a similar study schedule.

2) It is already a known teaching of the Mishnah that among the forty-eight things through which Torah is acquired is "the attachment of friends." Therefore, it is proper to arrange to have a study *chavrusa*, although it is obvious that one should not, *chas v’shalom*, refrain from Torah study even if one does not have a partner. Our Sages have already said that even for one person who sits and occupies himself with Torah, it is said, "I will come to you and bless you" (*Avos 3:6*). See also *Iggeres HaKodesh* by our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe, author of the *Tanya*—the authority on the hidden aspects of Torah—and the *Shulchan Aruch*—the authority on the revealed aspects of Torah—*Siman 23*.

With blessings for Torah study with *yiras shamayim* and for good tidings regarding all of the above,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

Secretary

## 3664

B"H, 18 Sivan, 5715
Brooklyn

To the esteemed Rabbi and Chossid, G-d-fearing and learned, engaged in communal needs,
Rabbi Schneur Zalman, may he live and be well,

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter, in which you write regarding your birthday (you are surely aware of the custom of the ancients, which was publicized by my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, to recite the chapter of Tehillim corresponding to the number of one’s years, as brought in *Kovetz Michtavim*).

May it be the will of Hashem that for many more years to come, you will engage in Torah and mitzvos and the *avodah* of the heart, and that you will merit and succeed in spreading the *maayanos* in your immediate surroundings, and also in surroundings that are currently not as close—*chutza* (outwardly). May this be with proper health and peace of mind. It is already known that the vessel that holds the blessing of the Holy One, Blessed be He, is only the matter of *shalom*—and not only *shalom* in the upper realms, but also *shalom* in the *familiya shel mata* (the family below), which is the main thing. This means, in the literal sense, in the place where one is called *mara d’atra* (the local authority). The ways to achieve this are through all the ways of the Torah, which are specifically "ways of pleasantness," yet they must be carried out with the necessary strength, as hinted at in the giving of the Torah, which requires both *oz* (strength) and *tushiya* (wisdom). This is also hinted at in the verse and its Targum (Tehillim 76): "From heaven You pronounced judgment; the earth feared and was still"—which refers to judgment regarding the matters of the *nefesh habahamit* (as in *Likutei Torah*, discourse *Tov lachasot baHashem*), and through this, the matters of the *nefesh elokit*, the "Land of Israel," become still.

With blessings for long life and good years in all their interpretations, and for good tidings in all the above.

P.S. Regarding the study of *halachos* that are dependent on the Land, a judge has only what his eyes see; therefore, you should make use of the books that are available and accessible in your surroundings.

## 3,565

B"H, 18 Sivan, 5715
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 9 Sivan, bearing good news that you and your friends—may they live—are worthy, and I have already written that you are worthy and will continue to be worthy to succeed in fulfilling the true purpose of man, which is the teaching of the Mishnah: "I was created to serve my Maker," through the study of Torah and the performance of mitzvos with hiddur. Among these is the fundamental matter of disseminating the wellsprings of Chassidus, its guidance, and its customs, until they reach even the "outside," and may this be for you and your friends in good health.

It is already known the allusion in the Targum to the verse, "And the Children of Israel went out with a high hand" (*b'yad ramah*), that this must primarily be in matters of the inner dimension of the Torah—this is the Torah of Chassidus—that they go out "in public" (*b'rish gale*), where *rish* is an acronym for Rabbi Shimon bar Yochai. This is also alluded to at the beginning of the Zohar, with the word *b'rish* (*b'rish hormana*); see there in the glosses of *Derech Emes* and *Nitzutzei Oros*...

## 3660

[19 Sivan, 5715]

In response to your letter from before the time of Matan Torah, and the one preceding it with holiday greetings. Indeed, whoever blesses others is himself blessed with the blessing of Hashem, as it is written: "And I will bless those who bless you" (Sotah 31b). Therefore, the reference to a *Kohen* there is not exclusive. This is also the case in the *Midrash Hagadol* there, and it is likewise proven in the *Yerushalmi* (Berachos 8, cited in *Tosafos Chullin* 49a), that the addition is greater than the primary element.

Regarding your comments on the additions to the Kehot edition of the Haggadah shel Pesach:

1) Regarding the name *Shabbos HaGadol*, see *Torah Shleimah*, Vol. 11, and the *Miluim* there, which references several books that discuss this.

2) Regarding the fact that my father-in-law, the Rebbe (Maharash), of blessed memory, would say *Hashta hacha* (this year we are here) *l’shanah haba’ah b’ara d’Yisrael* (next year in the Land of Israel), with the word *haba’ah* accented on the penultimate syllable (*mil’eil*), meaning it is in the past tense—and you ask how this is to be interpreted: Although I have not heard an explicit explanation, it seems to me that it should be understood simply: that this is a **period** that has already begun, within this very year of Pesach, and *l’shanah haba’ah*—accented on the final syllable (*mil’ra*)—meaning "next year," we will be *bnei chorin* (free men), which refers to the future. One must add to these preparations, especially in their spiritual dimension. For "next year in the Land of Israel" depends only on the person himself, as he has free choice, especially in the spiritual aspects of these matters. Eretz Yisrael is a place that is under the constant *hashgacha* of Hashem our G-d from the beginning of the year until the end of the year—a constant and unique *hashgacha* that depends on whether one does not "walk with Him in a casual manner," but rather "walks in His statutes." Therefore, when one says and resolves "next year in the Land of Israel," it is within his power to make it so immediately, even an hour earlier. This is not the case with becoming *bnei chorin*—that is, to be freed from subjugation—for as in the revealed law, this requires a document of manumission or similar matters. In the spiritual sense, this is as it is said, that only the Ribono shel Olam slaughters the *yetzer hara*, at which point one becomes a *ben chorin*, as per the Sages: "Do not read *charut* (engraved), but *cheirut* (freedom)."

* * *

Regarding what I wrote above concerning the interpretation of "haba’ah"—see *Zohar*, Vol. I, 265a; *Rambam*, *Hilchos Teshuvah*, end of Chapter 8.

* * *

3) Regarding your desire to explain the difference in the *Rambam’s* terminology—that sometimes he writes *merorim* (bitter herbs) in the plural, and sometimes *maror* in the singular—suggesting that *merorim* refers to the time when the Beis HaMikdash was standing, and *maror* in the singular refers to after the destruction: To refute this interpretation—which was my own initial thought—I pointed to *Rambam*, *Hilchos Chametz U’Matzah*, Chapter 1, Halacha 4, where he writes *maror* in the singular, and in his own *Seder Haggadah*, where in one place he writes *merorim*—which contradicts the aforementioned interpretation.

4) Regarding your desire to interpret the words of the *Tosefta*, etc.—see *Tzafnas Paneach*, which is also noted in the additions.

5) Regarding your comment that the text in the additions stating that the learning on the eighth day occurred after Matan Torah is connected to the discussion of whether the mitzvah of *milah* was only repeated at Sinai: This is not my view. That is why I specifically cited the *Tosefta* and not the discussion in *Shabbos*, because the concept of it being "repeated at Sinai" applies to what was said before Matan Torah, and regarding the mitzvah of *milah*, to the matters learned from the parsha of *Lech Lecha*. This is not the case with "on the eighth day," which is in a parsha that was stated after Matan Torah.

6) Regarding the interpretation of *Yefeh Toar* that they were circumcised on the day of Erev Pesach and not at night, and an even stronger point is found in the *Rivav* (Parshas Bo), that they were circumcised on the tenth of the month: It is impossible to interpret it this way in *Shemos Rabbah*, which I cited there, because it explicitly states that they were circumcised only after they smelled the scent of the Pesach offering that Moshe roasted. Based on the above, it may be that these are differing *midrashim*, or that there were different groups. As for your difficulty—how they were counted for the Pesach offering and ate it, etc., and your attempt to compare this to a convert who undergoes conversion, etc.—the comparison does not seem correct to me, because in Egypt, **everyone** was commanded to offer the Pesach sacrifice. As for them eating from Moshe’s Pesach offering, it can be said that he counted them all for his offering for this reason, and one can "act for the benefit of another in his absence" in such matters. Especially regarding the Pesach of Egypt, which involved many novel aspects and was connected to the Redemption and salvation from the plague of the firstborn, as in the expression "And Hashem passed over," in which all are equal.

* * *

Regarding what I wrote in the additions—and mentioned above—that they were circumcised at night because the parsha of *Tazria* had not yet been stated: I have now found this in the *Reshash* on *Shir HaShirim* 1:12.

## 3767

3767

B"H, 19 Sivan, 5715
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

...Regarding your question: because you have become accustomed to praying at length, you do not hear Kedushah from the Chazzan. You ask whether you should continue this practice or shorten your davening in order to hear Kedushah.

It is understood—based on the principle that *kavanah* is **the essence** of tefillah, to the extent that there is a general *kavanah* without which the tefillah is invalid —that one should not shorten one's *hisbonenus* during tefillah or shorten the tefillah itself, even for the sake of hearing Kedushah. This is also understood from the ruling of the Tzemach Tzedek in his Responsa—printed in *Shaar HaMiluim*, Siman 11—see there and in the seforim he cites.

With blessings,

**M. Schneerson**

***

3767
Printed in *Likutei Sichos*, Vol. 9, p. 281.

 See Rambam, *Hilchos Tefillah*, Chapter 4; *Shulchan Aruch HaRav*, 98, end of subsection 2; *Kuntrus Acharon* in *Tanya* (154b); *Chiddushei R' Chaim HaLevi* to the Rambam there.

## 3668

B”H, 19 Sivan, 5715
Brooklyn

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and industrious one, engaged in communal needs, R’ Saadia, may he live:

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letter of 13 Sivan: May it be the will of Hashem that your borders expand with students in quantity, and consequently in quality as well. May the increase come easily, in accordance with the general rule that from a thousand who study Scripture, a hundred enter to study Mishnah, and so on. It is somewhat surprising that this increase has not yet occurred, given that you wrote that several students were sent to them from Casablanca. I await good news.

2) Regarding what you wrote concerning the mikveh: Although the details are not clearly articulated in your letter, it seems the intention is that the water from the mikveh exits and is blocked by an iron stopper that plugs a hole in the floor of the mikveh. I was alarmed to read this, and perhaps this is not the correct interpretation. The authorities have already cried out against the leniency of [using] a plug *ab initio* in order to set it in place, etc. Surely you have a copy of the letter from the Rebbe Rashab, of blessed memory, who did not want a hole to be plugged even with rubber (*kautchuk*) due to the opinion that it can become ritually impure. He advised making the plug in several places using simple wooden implements that are fashioned to be extremely smooth. Since it is difficult to seal and tighten the connection between wood and stone, the advice for this is to make a portion of the floor corner out of wood, with a hole inside it that is plugged by a wooden stopper; tightening wood against wood is easier. However, what is even better—and this is the custom everywhere my reach extends—is that there should be no hole in the floor at all. The water should be removed via a pump (*nasas*), and it is even better to use a pump called a siphon, as is known to those who deal with such matters.

Enclosed is the response to... and I will rely on your understanding to provide further explanation if it is needed. As also seems to be the case from your letter, it is worthwhile that he travel, after appropriate preparation, to study in Brunoy.

With blessings for good news in all the above,

**M. Schneerson**

## 3529

B"H, 19 Sivan, 5715
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter from Motzaei Shabbos, in which you write that you are in doubt from a halachic perspective whether it is permitted to change the *nusach* of *davening* to *Nusach Ari*—presumably, you mean changing from *Nusach Ashkenaz* to *Nusach Ari*.

Regarding this, there is the *maaseh rav* (precedent of a great authority) that thousands and myriads of *Bnei Yisrael* in the generations of the students of the Baal Shem Tov and their students changed their *nusach* of *davening* in this manner. The halachic reasoning can be found in *Shu"t Minchas Elazar*, Part 1, Siman 11, and in *Shu"t Pri HaSadeh*, Part 2. The conclusion is that it is permitted to change to *Nusach Sefard* and *Nusach Ari*, but not the reverse. The places where this is discussed are explained there, with the proviso that the change must be made with the intention of *davening* with that *nusach* permanently from that point forward, and not merely on an occasional basis.

2) Regarding your question about the order and method of studying *Toras HaChassidus*: it is understood that this depends on the nature of the student’s soul, his talents, and his inclinations. Therefore, you should speak with some of *Anash* who are in Yerushalayim, *ir hakodesh* (may it be rebuilt and established), and they will guide you. In general, one should begin with *Tanya* Part 3, then Part 2, and then Part 1, as well as specific topics in the *sefer Derech Mitzvosecha*, and others.

The essential foundation for all of the above is the same as for the general acceptance of the Torah: the precedence of *naaseh* to *nishma*. This applies even to the study of Torah itself. The intention is that even if there are concepts that are not understood, or that even seem difficult to you, you should nonetheless study with complete confidence that, in time, you will also merit understanding and comprehension. This is true all the more so regarding the study of *Toras HaChassidus*—the *pnimiyus haTorah*, the "soul of the Torah" in the language of the *Zohar*—and with even greater intensity and strength. This is because, in our times, the *yetzer hara* is most opposed specifically to the study of *pnimiyus haTorah*, as is explained in the *Kuntres Eitz Chaim* by my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory.

I trust you are careful with *tevilas Ezra* and are keeping the three *shiurim* that are equal for every soul, as established by my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory—the *Chumash*, *Tehillim*, and *Tanya*—as is well known. May Hashem grant you success.

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, *shlita*,
Secretary

***

**Changing the *nusach* of *davening*:** See also above, Letter 3500, and the references in the footnotes there.

**Precedence of *naaseh* to *nishma*:** See also above, Letter 3550, and the references in the footnotes there.

## 3575

B"H, 19 Sivan, 5715
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 3 Beha'aloscha, in which you suspect that [Name] did not deliver your letter to me, etc.

This suspicion is unfounded, for I receive all the letters that arrive addressed to me and read them myself. Although the response to them sometimes comes with the signature of one of my secretaries to whose department the matter belongs—as is the case with the matter of sending printed materials, which I do not handle personally—this is why you received the response to your letter with the signature of the other person, as that is his department. I am writing this letter solely to remove this suspicion from a fellow Jew.

Regarding the substance of the question: every matter has its own order of *avodah*. The matter of distributing printed *seforim* in Europe in general, and in France in particular, has been entrusted to the *lishkah* in Paris, which is also directed from here. Therefore, regarding all these questions, you should turn only to the *lishkah* in Paris.

Surely you have heard of the three *shiurim* that are equal for every soul, established by my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, *ztzukulleh"h, nbg"m, zy"a*: 1) To recite a *shiur* of *Tehillim* every day after *davening* in the morning (according to the division of *Tehillim* by the days of the month). 2) To study a *parshah* of *Chumash* with the commentary of *Rashi* from the weekly *sedra* every day—Sunday from the beginning of the *sedra* until *parshah sheni*, Monday from *parshah sheni* until *shlishi*, and so on. 3) To study a *shiur* of *Tanya* every day, according to the division of *Tanya* by the days of the year. If you will observe this, at the very least from now on, *Hashem* will grant you success.

With blessings.

## 3571

B"H, 20 Sivan, 5715
Brooklyn

Agudas N'shei U'Bnos Chabad
Toronto Branch
May they live

Blessings and peace!

Through the esteemed Rabbi, the Chossid, G-d-fearing and learned, who engages in communal needs and accomplishes much for Hashem and His Torah, etc., R' Dov Yehuda Shecht, I received a check for $1,200 for the benefit of the young orphans...

May they live, to be utilized in an appropriate manner at the appropriate times. Enclosed is a receipt from Machne Israel, which occupies itself with similar matters.

The very act itself—your generous donation of heart to collect this sum for the orphans—demonstrates that it is unnecessary to explain the great value of the matter of helping orphans in general, and in particular, helping orphans who find themselves in the *ohel shel Torah*, receive a *chinuch al taharas hakodesh*, and walk in the path of Torah and *mitzvos*, which, with the help of Hashem, they will also use to arrange their own lives.

I only wish to underscore here the words of our *Rabbeinu HaZaken*, author of the *Tanya* and *Shulchan Aruch*, who writes regarding the virtue of *tzedakah* in general: that the money one gives away for *tzedakah* elevates the remaining property, so that the **entirety** of it becomes a *machon l'shivto* (a dwelling place) for Him, may He be blessed.

From this, it is understood that where Hashem, may He be blessed—who is the essence of goodness—is found, there will be goodness and kindness throughout. In other words, the entire sum will be utilized only for healthy and joyous matters.

And especially when it concerns helping young orphans stand on their own feet—each of whom will, in his time, build a *bayis b'Yisrael*, an everlasting edifice—all those who participated in this current assistance also receive a share in that everlasting edifice, for their *tzedakah* endures forever.

And the attribute of the *Ribono shel Olam* is *middah k'neged middah* (measure for measure), to draw down for each of the participants in this—men and women—blessing and success in their personal matters. And may you be able, in good health and with happy hearts, to continue and expand your work in the matters of Torah and *mitzvos*, which, along with their reward, are eternal and endure forever.

With blessings to each and every one—them and their households, may they live,

**M. Schneerson**

## 3573

[20 Sivan, 5715]

...Every *hisorerus* is, **at its inception**, mostly light; consequently, one stands in a state of *hispaalus* and vitality that is revealed.

However, its **purpose** is to effect action **in practice**, day after day—which is to "clothe the light in vessels." Therefore, it is necessary for the *hispaalus* to be concealed, and for the vitality to be less palpable, so that only the **actual deed** is felt. And this is the **purpose**. One should not listen to the *yetzer hara’s* temptation that the aforementioned should bring one to sadness, *chas v’shalom*. Rather, one must perform an orderly *avodah*, specifically with many *oros* and *keilim*. The order in *kedushah* is **"little by little** I will drive them out," both in the study of Torah and in the fulfillment of *mitzvos* (among them—*ahavas Yisrael*), and not all at once or by leaping [except in **special** cases].

Therefore, this is necessary—the body is *biah*, and therefore one must conduct oneself in a manner appropriate to this regarding matters of eating, drinking, sleeping, etc.

And as the language of the *Tanya*, Chapter 7 [states: "One who eats fatty meat of Torah, etc., to broaden his mind for Hashem and His Torah, etc., as a *olah* and as a *korban*"]. And since the **Torah** has given permission to the physician—when there is any doubt regarding this, or any ailment—one must consult him and act according to his instruction. And when one proceeds in all the above **step** by step—one succeeds in *ruchniyus*, and consequently also in *gashmiyus*.

And the *Ribono shel Olam* has commanded us regarding joy in all of this, and we see tangibly that anything done with joy is done with greater perfection and *hiddur*. And it is effective for *brius* in *guf v’nefesh*...

## 3596

B"H, 23 Sivan, 5715
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter, in which you write:

a) Regarding my suggestion to study chapters 27–29 of the holy Tanya, along with the preceding and following chapters, you suspect there is some ulterior motive. I do not understand what compelled you to think this; it is meant simply as it stands—that the detriment of sadness and the loss it causes are explained there, and that through contemplation it is possible to nullify it even through intellect, even when it seems, or actually is, sadness stemming from worry over sins.

b) You are in doubt regarding what I wrote about giving tzedakah—that one should give a *prutah* or **two** before davening—in the event that you do not find a poor person on the spot. It is well known that in such cases, one gives the tzedakah to a *gabbai tzedakah* or puts it into a *tzedakah pushkeh*.

c) You are in doubt regarding what I wrote about *mikveh taharah*. In my letter, it is written not with a *vav* [i.e., *mikveh tahorah*], but as *mikveh **taharah***. My intention was at least regarding *tevilas Ezra*; one should be careful with this. It is also very good to immerse in a *mikveh* that adds holiness to holiness, as we find similarly in the *Gemara* (namely, regarding the immersion of the *Kohen Gadol* on Yom Kippur between the various *avodos*).

It is surprising that you do not mention the recitation of the daily *Tehillim* after davening. May it be that this was merely an omission in your writing and not a failure in practice.

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita

## 3599

B”H, 23 Sivan, 5715
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 15 Sivan and the one preceding it:

Regarding what I wrote to you concerning your influence in spreading the wellsprings outward (*hafatzas hamaayanos chutzah*), my intention was regarding your visit to the yeshivah... I hoped that my prompting you on this matter would awaken in you a desire to continue these lofty activities with even greater intensity and strength. The necessity for this—and not specifically in the aforementioned yeshivah—is extremely great. It also relates to the fulfillment of the promise regarding when the Master will come—"when your wellsprings spread outward"—which will bring that time closer. Since this is demanded of each and every one of us, we have certainly been given the strength and the possibility to fulfill this demand, as is understood.

2) Regarding what I mentioned in my letter about the third line of *gemilus chasadim*, this is in addition to the completeness of the matter, and it also relates to the content of my letter, etc. For engaging in *hafatzas hamaayanos chutzah*, and in influencing others in general, is a matter of *gemilus chasadim*.

3) I was pleased to hear that you are continuing to deliver *shiurim* at the yeshivah... and *yasher koach* for writing that the spirit of learning has been awakened more than in the past. You should certainly add from your side to matters of *yiras shamayim* as well, since you are now in greater need of the words of our Sages (Berachos 6b): "Any person who has *yiras shamayim*, his words are heeded." This applies to the study of Torah, and especially when teaching the many.

4) Regarding what you wrote about your power of memory, which you feel has weakened recently: the known practice for this is to study in a place where your heart desires. When you feel that you are becoming weary and your power of concentration is flagging, switch your study to a different *sugya* or a different topic. Among the *segulos* for this is to memorize *Mishnayos*—as mentioned above, without straining—as it is written, "He who gathers *al yad* (little by little) will increase." It is also appropriate to learn the *maamar* "Ve'hadarta Pnei Zaken" in *Likutei Torah*, at the end of *Parshas Kedoshim*, by heart.

5) Regarding your notification of your birthday—and you surely observed the customs of a birthday: an *aliyah* to the Torah (and if it falls on a day when there is no Torah reading, then on the Shabbos preceding it); giving *tzedakah* before *davening* (when it falls on a weekday; if it falls on Shabbos or Yom Tov, then on the day before the birthday); studying an additional *shiur* in *Toras HaNigleh* and *Toras HaChassidus*; and keeping the three daily *shiurim* that are for every soul—*Chumash*, *Tehillim*, and *Tanya* for that day—may it be the will of Hashem that this be a year of success for you in your Torah study and in the performance of *mitzvos* with *hiddur*.

With blessings.

## 3580

B”H, 23 Sivan, 5715
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, learned, and distinguished, engaged in communal needs, a man of character,
Rabbi Moshe HaKohen, may he live.

Greetings and Blessings!

It was a pleasure to see you here and to receive regards from Anash in Chicago, may they live, and to hear about what is happening with them in general, and specifically regarding the Shaarei Tefillah Bnei Reuven Nusach HaAri synagogue. Following our conversation:

1) I was pleased to hear your report regarding the lot that was purchased with the intent of building a synagogue there. The main point is that it is located in a central area where Jewish people reside. As is well known, the saying of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, regarding the interpretation of the phrase in our Sages’ words, "Whoever engages in Torah, engages in a mitzvah"—which on the face of it seems to mean that one who studies Torah performs a mitzvah—is that the term "engages" (*osek*) implies business (*esek*).

A Jewish man and woman’s involvement in Torah and mitzvos must be like a business. As is clearly understood, a businessman does not sit in his home or office waiting for someone to come to him and say, "I have a good business proposal for you; if you agree, I will give you a title of excellence and seat you in a place of honor," etc. Rather, since it is clear to him that the business is for his benefit and the benefit of his household, he pursues the business in the marketplaces and streets, forgoes his own honor and personal matters, and exerts himself with both soul and body, just so that the business will be conducted properly and develop and grow from time to time. Furthermore, even at times when he cannot actively trade, he is preoccupied with it—what he must do tomorrow and the day after, and how he can utilize even this moment to prepare for that time. One of the requirements for this is that the business must be in a place where many people are found, in the widest possible circles, to facilitate their visiting the business and to build connections with them. All these things apply to Torah and mitzvos, and the details are explained accordingly.

How much more so is this true regarding choosing a location for a synagogue, where the term does not deviate from its literal meaning: a place where Jewish people must gather to pray to the King, the King of Kings, the Holy One, blessed be He, and to study His Torah. And it is stated, "In the multitude of people is the King's glory."

2) Throughout the Diaspora, and certainly in the United States, the days of Selichos and the month of Tishrei are auspicious for drawing the hearts of the Jewish people to our Father in Heaven, and for drawing hearts together. Therefore, every holy endeavor should utilize this opportunity as much as possible, and this is relevant for the entire upcoming year.

Therefore, in my opinion, even though it is understood that there is not enough time—even with the greatest effort—for the synagogue building to be constructed on the purchased lot by the coming Tishrei, one should strive energetically to rent, in the vicinity of the aforementioned area, at least a large room or hall where the people of that neighborhood can pray during the auspicious days of the coming Tishrei. Likewise, it should serve as a place to establish a branch of their Talmud Torah for the children of that area. Through this, the residents of the neighborhood will be united to become congregants and members of their synagogue when it is built, in a good and auspicious hour. Similarly, their sons and daughters will study in their educational institutions. Both of these matters depend on the beginning of the year—the school year and the year of prayer—for in the vast majority of cases, the synagogue where one prays during the month of Tishrei is where they continue to pray all year round, and the educational institutions where they begin to study at the start of the school year are where they continue until its conclusion.

3) Regarding your report that there is a proposal from another synagogue or Beis Medrash to join with them in building their synagogue on the condition that there be a change of name, and you ask for my opinion on this:

In my view, it is simple that the name of your synagogue, which has been known for decades in Chicago and its surroundings, should not be considered for change at all. It must remain in its entirety—the name that has merited glory and praise. In response to the aforementioned demand, one may agree that their name also be added, but it is understood that the name "Shaarei Tefillah Bnei Reuven" must be the first and primary one. It would be best if there were a separation of the words "and the synagogue" or "and the Beis Medrash." My intention is: "Shaarei Tefillah Bnei Reuven Nusach HaAri Synagogue, and the [Name] Synagogue (or Beis Medrash), etc."

May it be G-d’s will that even in the new neighborhood, you will merit and succeed in establishing a Chassidic synagogue and Beis Medrash, from which the candle of mitzvah, the light of Torah, and the "light of Torah"—which is the teachings of Chassidus, its guidance, and its customs—will spread throughout the entire vicinity.

With blessings and regards to all the congregants, the members, and the leadership at their head, may they live.

## 3581

B"H, 24 Sivan, 5715
Brooklyn.

In response to your letter from Erev Shabbos Kodesh, in which you write regarding the reasoning for traveling to... and ask my opinion as to whether you should consider organizing your affairs there in general, and a shidduch in particular—this is a correct approach, and may it be Hashem’s will that it be successful and that you bring good news.

This is especially true given that such activity adds success to one’s own personal matters as well.

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

B”H, 24 Sivan, 5715

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter of 13 Sivan: It is understood how distressing the content of the letter is. This is especially true when it is done in public, and in particular when it is done at a Chassidic farbrengen, where everyone looks at each of us who identifies with the Chabad community as an example—to see what a Chabad Chossid is, and what the effect of the guidance of the Torah of Chassidus and the instructions of our Rebbeim, of blessed memory, is. This is especially true when taking into account the content of Iggeres HaKodesh, end of Epistle 25. There is no need to elaborate on such a distressing matter.

And if you will listen to my opinion: in addition to asking for forgiveness as required by law, you should fast for one of the days. However, since you are occupied with Torah study, you should divide the fast into two half-days, give the value of the meals for that day to tzedakah, and study the aforementioned Iggeres four or five times until its content is properly engraved in your minds. May it be the will of Hashem that regarding this, the words of the Rambam in Hilchos Teshuvah 2:2 be fulfilled in you—that He who knows all hidden things will testify that you will not return [to such folly], and from this pit you will ascend to a high mountain, to succeed in spreading the wellsprings outward with an expanded mind, and to succeed in the study of Torah, both in Nigleh and in Chassidus, with outstanding success.

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita

## 3587

B"H, 27 Sivan, 5715
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and diligent in communal affairs, R' Chaim Hillel, may he live.

In response to your letter of 20 Sivan and the one preceding it, along with the enclosures.

Through this, they increase the blessings of Hashem in whatever they and their families require, both materially and spiritually. Since the *pidyon nefesh* will be read at the gravesite of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, in order to establish a *hiskashrus*—so that he may serve as the conduit and vessel for receiving the blessings bestowed through his arousal of Divine mercy—there must be an action on their part that is connected to him in some way. This means establishing a regular *shiur* in his Torah teachings, or at the very least in the teachings of Chassidus, as he is the *Nasi* who fills the place of the founders of the teachings of Chassidus. It also includes observing his *takanos*, at the very least regarding the daily recitation of Tehillim. As our Sages have said, words that come from the heart enter the heart.

May Hashem add His blessing to each of them in whatever they require, materially and spiritually.

3) It is my hope that the success of the aforementioned endeavor will inspire you to strive energetically to do similar things a few more times throughout the summer. While it is understood that this can take a different form and have different content, the main thing is to provide provisions for the journey for the students during their vacation days.

4) Regarding your notification that they will send their children to the *yeshiva* for the summer months, this is the right thing to do. May it be Hashem's will that this leads to an improvement in their spiritual health, and consequently, to the strengthening of their physical health as well.

With blessings for good tidings in all the above.

P.S.

## 3588

B"H, 29 Sivan, 5715
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and meticulous in his mitzvah observance, etc.,
Rabbi Elimelech, shlita,

Shalom u’Bracha!

I have received the news that in the near future you are planning to return to Eretz Yisrael—may it be built and established by Mashiach Tzidkeinu speedily in our days. May it be the will of Hashem that your journey be successful and auspicious, and that upon your arrival, you will increase your strength in your endeavors to fortify Yiddishkeit and disseminate it in the spirit of our ancestors, for "it is a people that shall dwell alone, and shall not be reckoned among the nations."

And this is precisely the path to achieving the goal of being "one nation in the land"—to draw down the unity of Hashem into this world as well. This is done by beginning with one’s own affairs and within one’s own "four cubits," instilling the realization that there is only one Truth and one goal: to proclaim that Hashem is One and His Name is One. This is achieved by walking in His Torah—one Torah, without any compromises or concessions. As our Sages declared regarding King Solomon, whose kingdom was complete and whose era was the kingdom of Israel in all its glory: "Let Solomon and a hundred like him perish, but let not a single letter of the Torah be lost."

How much more so in this wandering and confused generation, where we have nothing but our Torah (from the word *hora'ah*—instruction) in **every** matter and detail, and it is the very essence of our life and existence, both as individuals and certainly as a nation.

Furthermore, there is an added merit and responsibility upon all those who are descendants of the Baal Shem Tov, the Maggid, and their disciples: to disseminate the wellsprings of the teachings of the Baal Shem Tov (*nishmata d’orayta*—the soul of the Torah) until they reach the "outside." This means the dissemination of the study of Chassidus and the practice of its paths and customs within circles that are constantly expanding, until they become the heritage of all the Jewish people.

It has already been lamented, "They made me the keeper of the vineyards" (meaning, the true vineyard), "but my own vineyard I have not kept." My intention here is simple: since Hashem has graced you with the ability to influence even those circles that, for the time being, do not know or recognize the light within the teachings of Chassidus, it is a holy obligation and a primary task to introduce them to the teachings of the Baal Shem Tov and his successors. This should continue until this awareness penetrates their day-to-day lives—in thought, speech, and action. *L’fum gamla shichna*—according to the camel is the load—and especially since the merit of your ancestors assists you in being a channel through which these wellsprings can reach many, many Jews. The magnitude of this matter surely requires no further explanation for one such as yourself.

With blessings for success in the above.

## 3,489

B"H, 29 Sivan, 5715

For the measure of Hashem is "measure for measure": when one fulfills a promise and adds to it, then from Above, too, what has been promised to us is fulfilled, and even more is added. In the language of Chassidus: there is the *is'arusa d'le'eila* that is commensurate with the *is'arusa d'letata* and comes as a result of it, and the *is'arusa d'le'eila* that follows, which is not commensurate at all. And just as you, may your light shine, were the one to begin this matter, it is said to you: "complete it." May you merit to "kindle the lights" ("the candle of Hashem is the soul of man") in this specific matter as well, until the flame rises of its own accord. This is especially true as the aforementioned matter is connected to **chinuch** according to the *Torah Temimah* (the revealed and hidden aspects of Torah), and in this generation of the footsteps of Moshiach, when the sun is setting —it is specifically these lights that endure forever, as is understood from the commentary of the Ramban on the Torah on the verse "When you kindle the lights."

With blessings for success in all of the above.

Your letter from 26 Sivan was received. Thank you for the story contained within it. In accordance with the words of our Sages, "He who gives a gift..." (which is also proof that it brings satisfaction to his own soul), I have mentioned you and your family, may they live and be well, at the tziyun of the Baal HaGeulah of the upcoming month.

## 3,194

B"H, Rosh Chodesh Tammuz, 5715
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

...The source for the law regarding the hair of virgins is explicitly stated in Shulchan Aruch Orach Chayim, section 75. See also Shulchan Aruch Even HaEzer, section 21, subsection 2.

The reason for the distinction can be explained by the fact that the verse "And he shall uncover the woman's head" (see Kesuvos 72a) is written regarding a married woman. The essential point is as stated in the introduction to the Rambam’s Commentary on the Mishnah: regarding matters received from generation to generation since the days of Moshe Rabbeinu, it is impossible for there to be a dispute (and see similarly in Yerushalmi Pesachim, beginning of chapter 6: "It is impossible for two to swear..."). In the aforementioned case, they observed the custom of virgins from generation to generation. Furthermore, according to the opinion of Rabbi Yishmael (Sifri to Bamidbar 5:18), the verse mentions that virgins would go with their hair uncovered. The inner reason for this, according to the revealed Torah, can be explained by the fact that the covering of a woman's hair came as a punishment for the sin of the Tree of Knowledge (Eruvin 100b), for she caused her husband to stumble; therefore, it does not apply to a virgin. It is understood that this does not pose a difficulty from the laws of menstruation (Eruvin ibid.)—for that is a matter that occurs in the nature of the body, whereas the aforementioned [covering of the hair] is different...

#### ***3,194***

Printed in Likutei Sichos, Vol. 8, p. 285.

This is also understood from the *maamarim* of *Hechalotzu*—beginning with the *maamar* of the Alter Rebbe printed in *Likutei Torah*, Parshas Matos, through to those of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, the Nasi of our generation, in the supplement to the *Kuntres Hechalotzu* 5659.)

This serves as the immediate preparation for settling in *Eretz Yisrael* in a physical sense as well, through Moshiach Tzidkeinu, speedily in our days, together with all of *Klal Yisrael*.

See *Bereishis Rabbah* 49:4 and *Ohr HaTorah*, *dih* *Vayishma Avraham*).

## 3594

3594

B.H., 2nd day of Rosh Chodesh Tammuz, 5715
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the Committee for the Gathering of Religious Physicians
New York
May Hashem grant them life

Peace and blessing!

It was with pleasure that I received the news regarding your gathering, the purpose of which is to organize an association of religious physicians. If in all times the unification of those who tremble at the word of Hashem is a good thing, how much more so in this generation of ours—a generation of confused minds due to the shocking events that have caused and brought many to complete disillusionment with their false opinions and ideologies, and have stirred them to search for the truth with seriousness.

An association of religious physicians has the potential to influence this trend of thought by making an open declaration regarding several points about which many are mistaken and led astray:

To declare that true science, whose goal is solely **the truth**, cannot have conclusions that contradict our Torah, the Torah of truth. On the contrary—the deeper one investigates, the greater the recognition of the veracity of the foundations and even the details of our religion, the religion of Israel.

As physicians in particular—to categorically reject the doctrine of the supremacy of matter, while noting the extent to which the health of the body is dependent on the health of the soul. If from ancient times the medical adage has emphasized a "healthy soul in a healthy body," in our day we have come to realize how a slight disturbance in the soul leads to a great disturbance in the body. The healthier the soul, the greater its control over the body and its ability to rectify physical deficiencies, to the point that even many physical treatments are far more effective and beneficial in healing the body if they are accompanied by the strength, will, and powers of the soul of the patient.

This principle of the dominance of form (quality) over matter (quantity) is also emphasized by the fact that even in bodily matters, the recognition is growing that vital bodily functions are not dependent on quantity; for the glands and their products (hormones, vitamins, etc.) are minute in quantity.

— And as a note: It is said, "From my flesh I shall see Elokus"—from recognizing the rule of the soul over the body (the *olam katan*), it is only a small step to recognizing the rule of the Ribono shel Olam over the world (*adam gadol*). In the words of our Sages: Just as the soul fills the body, sustains it, sees but is not seen—so too does the Ribono shel Olam fill the world, sustain it, sees and is not seen.

***

The above are general points. There are many questions that relate directly to the physician’s professional work, some of which are *halacha l’maaseh*, for example:

Publicizing the immense benefit in observing the laws of family purity (*taharas hamishpacha*).

Observing the laws of kashrus of food.

*Milah*.

Reproductive organs in general: rejecting treatment that causes sterilization and replacing it with other treatment.

Specifically—prostate surgery.

Medicinal drugs—many of them can be prepared in a way that they are kosher, and it is only due to a lack of interest and attention that they are made otherwise.

Autopsies and desecration of the dead: to study the structure of the body, use models or diagrams instead.

Determining the cause of death: in many cases, this knowledge is not necessary at all. In a case where it concerns saving a life **on the spot** (such as clearing someone of blame for poisoning the deceased by examining the body, etc.)—perform the autopsy only where necessary and bury the parts afterward.

And other matters of this nature.

***

It is superfluous to emphasize that in what was said above—regarding the health benefits of observing the mitzvos—it is not my intention to explain the reasons for the mitzvos. For, as is known, one must observe the mitzvos because they are the command and will of the Creator, may He be blessed, and the reward for a mitzvah is the performance of the mitzvah itself. For this is the whole of man: to connect and unite with his Creator through the performance of His mitzvos.

However, my intention in the above is for those who are spiritually ill, *r'l*, whom it is not yet possible to bring closer to the observance of mitzvos in any other way. One must do everything possible to bring them to the actual performance of mitzvos, even if only by emphasizing their physical benefits.

I will conclude with my wishes that it may be fulfilled in you, "Then those who fear Hashem spoke one to another," and may the desire of Hashem succeed in your hands to bring about tangible results. And as the verse concludes—"And it was written in a book of remembrance before Him," for a remembrance before Hashem and for the merit of the public, for the merit of the public depends upon them.

**M. Schneerson**

## 3,595

B"H, 1 Tammuz, 5715
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed and distinguished R' Avraham, known as Dr. Aharonov,

Peace and blessing!

I was pleased to receive regards from you through the esteemed Rabbi and Chossid, who toils for the needs of the community, R' Eliezer Kresik. He writes to me that in his youth he studied at the Tomchei Temimim Yeshiva in Lubavitch, where the vitality, light, and fire that were absorbed there are an "eternal fire that shall not be extinguished." Ultimately, they exert their influence even in a revealed way, although, naturally, not all people are the same regarding the time required for that influence to be revealed, nor in the types of matters in which they exert that influence. If even the smallest part of physical matter is never lost, but merely changes form and transforms, then certainly this is true of spiritual matters, which are what vivify and sustain the physical. Surely, for someone like you, further elaboration on this is unnecessary.

In connection with this, I was doubly pleased by your expressed desire to participate in the building expenses of one of the institutions in Kfar Chabad, in the Holy Land, may it be rebuilt and established. In my opinion, it would be appropriate for this to be directed toward the buildings associated with the vocational schools, as this is the demand of the hour, fitting the nature of the new immigrants among our Sephardic brethren, who constitute the majority of the new immigrants of late. Furthermore, in addition to the previous period, when we take a youth into a school of proper education, we are not only providing him with the knowledge necessary for his spiritual and material life, but even greater is the assistance of "turn from evil," as we save him from a life of idleness—for idleness leads to, etc.—as has always been seen tangibly, and all the more so in the recent period of our generation, which is shaken to its core.

You have surely seen the letter of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, regarding the analogy between the healing of the body and the healing of the soul (printed in the *Kuntres* of 18 Elul, 5708). My hope is strong that you have set times for Torah study in general, and for Chassidus in particular, and the statement of the scholars is already well-known: that the foundation of physical health comes specifically from the spiritual.

With respect and blessing.

## 3,596

B"H, 1 Tammuz, 5715
Brooklyn

To the esteemed and distinguished individual, engaged in communal needs,
Rabbi Yaakov Yosef, may he live, Shochet and Bodek

Greetings and blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter from Monday, in which you write about the schedule of the shiurim during the summer months and the changes that have occurred in this regard. Surely, from time to time, these will increase; it is already well-known that there is nothing that can stand before the will, and that all beginnings are difficult.

Regarding what you wrote—that you feel a sense of discouragement because the effect and change are not apparent in those who attend the shiurim at such-and-such synagogue—surely this only appears so to you. It is impossible that words of Torah in general, and words of Chassidus in particular, should not have an effect—both in the hidden realms and in the revealed world—until eventually, even a person who only sees with physical eyes will recognize the change. However, this does not always happen in a short amount of time, and not all mashpiim and recipients are equal in this regard.

In truth, these are two separate matters: every Jew must do what is incumbent upon him, while the effect upon the recipient is a separate matter. There is a sense of satisfaction in the latter, which is also a form of receiving a reward. Nevertheless, we are assured that it is a certainty that outreach does not return empty, and words that come from the heart enter the heart. Consequently, you should continue your good work in spreading the wellsprings everywhere, until they reach even the "outside," and you will see good fruit from your labor in those who hear the shiurim, and Chassidic nachas from your children, may they live.

Enclosed is the continuation of the list of the maamar, and surely you will merit to share it with the many in an appropriate manner.

With blessings,

**M. Schneerson**

P.S.
It is surely unnecessary to urge you to utilize the days of redemption, the upcoming 12th and 13th of Tammuz, as much as possible, but in a way that the people of London will also see that these are ways of pleasantness.

## 3597

B"H, 1 Tammuz, 5715
Brooklyn

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing and learned, engaged in communal needs, R' Nissan, may he live:

Greetings and blessings!

I was pleased to receive your letter of 27 Sivan, in which you write regarding the arrangement of the students in the new classes. Surely, as per your letter, you are already preparing a program for the summer vacation days, especially since there is already experience from last year. May Hashem grant you success.

It is surprising that you do not mention anything regarding the group of older girls that you began to gather and organize (and it has been some time since I have received any news regarding this). Surely you will explain this at the next opportunity.

I am also interested to know if you are making an effort to turn the students of the higher grades into guides, and even a form of educators for the students of the younger grades (and it is understood that my intention here is not to give them a formal position, etc., but rather to accustom them to the matter of guidance and education). There is also a great advantage in this, as it provides them with a boost of spirit to increase their diligence, to add to their knowledge, and to be precise in good conduct. There are many ways to bring this into practice, whether by appointing a *mashgiach* from among them who rotates from week to week—meaning, a *mashgiach* over his peers in his class—or guides and *mashgichim* during the rest periods between one *shiur* and the next, etc., etc.

Please convey what is stated here to the esteemed Chossid, R' Shlomo Matusov, may he live, and may there be salvation through much counsel. In this regard, too, one should utilize the summer vacation days, since that is when the number of students—both boys and girls—who are new to the walls of the Yeshiva and Beis Rivkah increases, and they are like guests in comparison to all those who study throughout the entire year.

I was pleased with what you wrote regarding the *mikveh*, and the main point of all points is that the number of those visiting has increased... But on the other hand, it is worth striving to increase the number as much as possible by lowering the entry fee and improving the conditions there, etc. Furthermore, in addition to the actual beautification of the *mikveh*, one must teach the woman who supervises the *tevilah* the necessary *dinim* regarding this, and instruct her to inform **each and every** one of the visitors of all the *dinim* (since I have heard that there is ignorance in this matter as well in certain circles, and to the wise it is sufficient). May Hashem grant you success in bringing good tidings in all of the above.

Enclosed is the continuation of the list of the imprisonment, which you will surely merit to share with the public in an appropriate manner.

With blessings.

## 3,599

B”H, 2 Tammuz, 5715
Brooklyn

To the Honorable Rabbi and Chossid, G-d-fearing, learned, and distinguished, engaged in communal affairs, etc., etc.,
Rabbi S.Y. [Zevin]

Shalom u’Bracha!

In response to your letter from before the holiday of Shavuos (which was somewhat delayed in transit) and the one preceding it.

It is understood how distressing it is that the matter of the United Religious Front did not come to fruition. It is even more astonishing that after seeing with one’s own physical eyes the reality of partisanship—where even party leaders who are truly religious in their private lives, in matters of party politics, without any hesitation, sacrifice the clear benefits to religion that would result from a religious front for the sake of a dubious "mess of pottage" of party interests—how great is the power of the concealment and darkness, a double and redoubled darkness of our exile. This is especially true of the concealment stemming from the level of the *Sitra Achra*, which has been granted permission to "dance in the King’s palace," in the land upon which the eyes of Hashem are from the beginning of the year until the end of the year. Not only do they themselves not feel what they are doing—and it seems they do not even understand it—but they succeed in deceiving G-d-fearing people, convincing them that their actions are motivated solely by pure *yiras shamayim*, and that there is no element of personal interest here, nor even party interest, etc., etc.! And although our Sages of blessed memory ruled that regarding a matter destined to be revealed, everyone is believed, then surely this applies all the more so to a matter that has already been revealed. Yet, the party members have the audacity to declare the exact opposite, and this also succeeds—even though everyone has the ability to read what was printed in the newspaper of each respective party just **a few days** earlier, written by the very people who now declare the opposite!

2) From all this, one can understand how great the light of the true Redemption will be, since Hashem has promised that then they will say, "I will thank You, Hashem, for You were **angry** with me." For even the aforementioned concealment, which is brought about specifically by those who have a "reflection of a reflection," etc., etc. (and this is understood with even greater intensity and strength than what is written in *Tanya*, end of Chapter 24), even for this they will offer thanks when *Mashiach Tzidkeinu* is revealed and brings out our brethren in exile—both the exile in the Holy Land, may it be rebuilt and established, and the exile abroad—from the deep pit and the darkness that is terrifying even to the eyes of human intellect, provided it is healthy.

3) Thank you for having made contact with our friend, etc., etc., Mr. Shazar. Regarding your addition that he is writing to me, I have not yet received any letters from him.

4) Regarding what you wrote about the book *Pelach HaRimon*, the part on the Book of Shemos has now been completed in print, containing over 400 pages, and it is understood that when it is required, it will be sent to you.

5) Surely, when you have good news regarding the state of your son’s health, may he live, you will not withhold the good from informing me. And thank you in advance...

7) Regarding what you wrote about the change concerning Lag B’Omer, which in the *maamarim*, etc., is written with a *beis*, even though the formula of the *Sefirah* on all days—and Lag B’Omer included—is with a *lamed*, and you explain this at length: The reasons you bring for the change in phrasing also have a place in the other days of the *Sefirah* when writing letters, etc. Conversely, regarding Lag B’Omer, the matters explained in *Chassidus* also concern the days preceding it, since the *birurim* and the *avodah* are from level to level, and it is impossible to reach *Hod sheb’Hod* until one has passed through the preceding levels.

- In the meantime, only one reasoning occurs to me for the aforementioned change, and it is very simple: There were many opinions on whether to count with a *beis*, and in practice, the **innovation** was our custom to count with a *lamed*. It is understood that they were particular about the formula of the *Sefirah* itself—to change it to fit all the opinions stated regarding the difference between the formula "in the Omer" (*ba’omer*) and "to the Omer" (*la’omer*). However, they were not particular about the change in matters that are not so precise, such as in the dating of letters and the like. This is similar to how in the first three parts of *Tanya*, the places where it says "G-d" versus where it says "He," etc., are precise (which, in my opinion, the reason for this is as our Sages of blessed memory said, "Every passage," etc.), but in *Iggeres HaKodesh*, they were not precise in this. As I noted in the introduction to the *Mafteach* (Index) to *Tanya*. For an understandable reason, I did not want to publish this reason.

8) Enclosed is the booklet *Hemshech HaMaamarim*, which will surely interest you.

With respect and blessing,

**M. Schneerson**

P.S.
Just now, information was received that the *Keren Hatzalah* meeting will be on the coming Monday. I requested to send a telegram regarding this to you, and through you also to Rabbi Hutner, who is surely in contact with them, so that they might have time to urge the aforementioned regarding the support for the Encyclopedia, since this year they are threatening to give them much less than last year, and consequently, a special effort is necessary. And perhaps, just perhaps.

Regarding the difference between *ba’beis* or *ba’lamed*, and until the above, note also *Iggeres HaKodesh*, end of Chapter 13.

Regarding what I wrote in my previous letter concerning what is written in *Shulchan Aruch Orach Chaim*, subsection 58:

1) That the *Taz* (and not only the "I heard it said" mentioned in the *Taz*) is more lenient than the *Magen Avraham* (as interpreted by the **Alter Rebbe**—there in his *Shulchan Aruch*, subsection 7)—is proven by his emphasis, "And so it is ruled—since he performed an **act** **for liquids**, etc., an act is created that is a liquid, etc."—unlike the *Magen Avraham*, who holds that it must be "when he crushed... he intended it for food only."

If so, the *Taz* and the *Magen Avraham* are in disagreement regarding all the scenarios between these two extremes, such as when he intended it for both food and liquids (whereby there is **no** definitive act, and consequently it depends on the subsequent act), and more.

2) Where the Alter Rebbe derives this interpretation of the *Magen Avraham*—this does not affect the above, for however the *Taz*’s opinion is understood, the *Magen Avraham* disagrees—according to the Alter Rebbe’s interpretation—with the "I heard it said." It must be that the Alter Rebbe has proof for this interpretation, and it is not because it is impossible to say otherwise. It is possible that his proof is because the *Magen Avraham* brings support for his ruling here in *Netilas Yadayim* from *Shabbos* 19b: "Honey is initially food, and now it is food."

3) What you noted regarding the Alter Rebbe’s language, "to be lenient also in this"—it is simple that it refers to what was written prior to this, "And nevertheless, etc., one may eat with a spoon or a knife," and he concludes with that same language, "one may be lenient also in this by means of a spoon or a knife."

4) The reasoning that a non-Jew’s intention during the crushing would not be effective (and I only brought it as a secondary point)—is because there is no—that it will be food or liquid in the future—any **practical difference for the non-Jew.** This is unlike every case that you noted. And as if there is no reality yet for the question and the doubt, and consequently there is no place yet to determine and decide. And there are many examples of this.

It can also be said that intention is effective as a result of the ownership of the one intending, and therefore in many matters, there is no intention for a non-Jew, based on what is written in *Tzafnas Paneach HaShleimah* to Part 4, page 14. But this is not the place to elaborate.

## 319

B"H, 2 Tammuz, 5715
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter: I was pleased to read that your financial situation has improved. Therefore, I wish to be certain that when one sees the kindness of Hashem in that matters have improved in the material realm, one immediately understands the hint within this: that it is within one’s free choice to improve matters in the spiritual realm. For the material is derived from the spiritual, and if Hashem precedes the material to the spiritual, then all that is within a person must immediately make it known that he must do his part to strengthen and enlarge the channel and the vessels for receiving the blessings of Hashem.

Regarding what you write—that it seems to you that there are matters that "the world has not laid aside," and that you do not have great knowledge in Torah, etc.—in all these matters, one must utilize the perspective that my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, brings in the name of his father, the Rebbe (recorded in *Hayom Yom*, 23 Sivan): that if something prevents one from Torah and *avodah*, these are tactics of the *yetzer hara*.

It is surely superfluous to remind you that for *siyata d’shmaya*, one must be careful regarding *tevilas Ezra*, to give a few coins to *tzedakah* every weekday before *davening*, to recite *Tehillim* every day after *Shacharis* (the portion of *Tehillim* as divided for the days of the month), and to have a daily *shiur* in the study of *pnimiyus haTorah*.

I hope that you are acting with the appropriate energy and in the manner appropriate for a *Chassidishe* *avreich* regarding *shidduchin*, and may Hashem grant you success in bringing good tidings in all of the above.

## 3701

B.H., 2 Tammuz, 5715
Brooklyn.

Blessings and Peace!

In response to your letter—which was delayed in transit—

1) Regarding what you write once again about the doubts you have as to whether you are suited for your role and the demands of the work, etc.:

I have already expressed my opinion on such matters to many who have asked, both from *anash* and those not from *anash*, and I wrote to you specifically about this in one of my previous letters. Upon the shoulders of every man and woman who remained as "brands plucked from the fire" after the terrible era of the decrees in our generation, rests the task of also fulfilling the role of our brothers and sisters who were killed *al kiddush Hashem*. Since the *Ribono shel Olam* only asks according to our strength—that is, the strength of each individual—it is certain that the powers and possibilities were granted from the outset. The matter depends only on one’s *ratzon* (will). This is especially true when one is already in a specific field of work and sees success. It is understood and simple that this does not mean the person is utilizing all their powers, nor does it even mean that they have brought their powers from *he'elem* (concealment) to *giluy* (revelation). For there is *bechirah chofshis* (free choice) for the son and daughter of Yisrael. Even though the *Ribono shel Olam’s* request, after saying "See, I have set before you life and the good... therefore choose life," emphasizes "life," it also emphasizes "choose." Therefore, one often sees that a worker could have worked to a greater degree, and consequently succeeded to a greater extent, but does not utilize their powers for various and sundry reasons. However, since the ability is given, the matter depends only on their *ratzon*.

2) It is understood and simple that every educator and teacher, and indeed every communal activist, must know that one of the essentials of their work is to raise up helpers and assistants in their work from among their students and those they influence. The work with each individual is too great for one person to handle alone, whereas if, alongside their own work, they strive to educate those among their students who are capable of it to fulfill a portion of their own role, the result is different. The analogy regarding your work with those you influence is understood.

3) It is also understood that the plan you write of—to visit with your students a partisan institution whose affairs are in many respects the opposite of the teachings of *Chassidus*, and even of Torah in general (such as the matter of the mixing of boys and girls, and several other matters that are not so overt, but are fundamental)—is liable to cause damage in essential matters, even if one hopes to bring benefit in matters that are secondary to the aforementioned essentials. After all, it is impossible to explain to the students that upon arriving at a certain place, they should only contemplate a specific part or matter, and remain oblivious to or not negate several other matters.

4) In general, I do not see such a great need to visit that specific institution. The matters you write about can be found in more *chareidi* institutions, or you can create a model yourself without visiting questionable institutions.

5) Following the above, it was pleasant for me to read in your letter that some of the girls have been awakened with a desire for guidance and educational work among the youth of [D...]. You should certainly develop this movement among them, and it is to be hoped that after not too long a time, they will adapt to the work and succeed in it.

6) It is certainly unnecessary to remind you of the greatest necessity to utilize the days of vacation from school attendance through a suitable program for the girls for these weeks, as it is possible to conduct several activities outdoors. Surely there is already experience in this from previous years, and it is easier to know what was lacking then and to add to it. May the *Hashem Yisbarach* grant you success in bringing good news in all of this, and primarily in the fact that you are dedicating yourself to the work of education in purity and holiness in the vineyard of Chabad.

Awaiting good news,

On behalf of the Rebbe, *shlita*,
Secretary

For its content, see above, Vol. 10, Letter 3101, and the references in the notes there.

## 3,202

B"H, 2 Tammuz, 5715
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter of the 25th of Sivan; surely you have already received the response to your previous letter.

May it be the will of Hashem that your official receipt of the stipend for your holy position—as you have informed me—will reveal deeper inner strengths for the fulfillment of your duties in this position with greater intensity and vigor. Furthermore, may the preparation of those whom you influence also improve, so that they may receive your holy guidance to fulfill their own roles in the world, in accordance with the Mishnah’s statement: "I was created to serve my Maker."

In our times, when the darkness of galus is doubled and redoubled—concealing and hiding to such an extent that people call light darkness and darkness light, and even where healthy human intellect recognizes something as a lie—one is compelled to turn to the "light that is in the Torah." This is the study of the inner dimension of the Torah and the following of its guidance and conduct. This is what is called (by the Ra'aya Mehemna, the shepherd of all Yisrael, and not only the first redeemer but also the final redeemer) the "Tree of Life," in which the sitra achra has no hold whatsoever, as the language in Ra'aya Mehemna, Parshas Naso, cited in Iggeres HaKodesh by our Rebbe HaZaken, Epistle 26. Then the statement of our Sages regarding the study of Torah in general is fulfilled: "He merits that it becomes for him a potion of life," as explained at length in Kuntres Eitz Chaim by the Rebbe Rashab, of blessed memory. This is also understood through what Rabbi Chaim Vital wrote at length regarding this in his introduction to Shaar HaHakdamos, which contains awesome and wondrous matters.

With blessings.

## 3303

3303

B"H, 3 Tammuz, 5715
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Agudas N'shei U’Bnos Chabad
Branch: ...
May they live

Blessings and peace!

In connection with the approaching days of 12-13 Tammuz, the days of liberation of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, which also commemorate and signify the victory of mesiras nefesh for Torah and mitzvos against all the forces that fought against it—

I am certain that the thought of this strengthens in every Jew, man or woman, their commitment to Torah and mitzvos, to conduct themselves in accordance with this in their daily life. It also strengthens their bitachon in the Creator of the world, who directs the entire world at every moment and every hour, that He will grant His blessing so that one’s way of life will be successful, and that the difficulties one sometimes encounters will not discourage them, but will gradually diminish until they disappear entirely.

I expect that you will find a suitable time during the days of 12-13 Tammuz, or in the days close to them, to meet, to strengthen one another in the aforementioned, and to take with you refreshment and warmth for the coming weeks and months.

In particular, taking into account that the time is beginning when children are less occupied with studies, and as is the custom of the world, one takes a few weeks to rest or at least to reduce work, which strengthens the body—

It is self-understood that at the same time, a suitable program must also be prepared to strengthen the neshamah.

For the body and the neshamah of a Jew—who are "one nation on earth"—are one entity. And when is a Jew truly happy? When the neshamah leads the body, so that the body conducts itself according to the instructions of the neshamah.

According to the well-known saying of our Alter Rebbe, a Jew neither wants to nor can be severed from Elokus.

And by walking in this path, one is then healthy physically as well, and one is calm and happy, being permeated with strong bitachon in Hashem Yisbarach that He guards each one of us within the collective of Klal Yisrael, and directs matters so that it should be good, both in gashmius and in ruchnius.

I hope that at your aforementioned meeting, you will also discuss how to structure the work of your branch for the coming months, and how to best utilize the opportunities that exist during the summer months and the increased free time.

With blessings for a healthy and happy summer to each one of you and your families, and for good tidings in all the above.

## Yisro

B"H,

In anticipation of the upcoming Chag HaGeulah of 12-13 Tammuz, I suggest studying the continuation of the Chassidic discourse "Rachav D'Amar" by my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory. It is printed in *HaKriah VeHaKedushah*, Tammuz 5704 and onwards, as well as in *Sefer HaMaamarim Yiddish*, p. 165 and onwards.

In connection with these days of redemption, we are also publishing the fourth part of his personal account regarding his final imprisonment.

This account was written by him during the period of his imprisonment, 15 Sivan 5688, in Riga. The first part was published for 12-13 Tammuz 5712 (*Likutei Diburim* 34), the second part for 12-13 Tammuz 5713 (*Likutei Diburim* 35), and the third part for 12-13 Tammuz 5714 (*Likutei Diburim* 36).

As an addendum, included at the end of the booklet is a transcript of words from my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, which he spoke on Sunday, Parshas Balak 5687, prior to his departure for his city of refuge, Kostroma, as recorded by one of those present.

* * *

The purpose of this celebration was already explained by my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, in his letter for the **first** 12-13 Tammuz celebration in 5688:

To establish it as a day of gathering and inspiration for the strengthening of Torah and Yiddishkeit in every place, according to its requirements.

And he blessed "all our brothers, lovers of Torah, those who study it, and those who teach it in public—may Hashem protect them and grant them life—that Hashem may open His good treasury and bestow upon them, and upon all our brothers, the children of Israel—may they live—an abundance of life and great blessing, without measure. May He strengthen their hearts to increase their courage in disseminating Torah and upholding Yiddishkeit, and may we all merit to see children and grandchildren occupied with Torah and mitzvos in comfort and with good livelihood."

May the Ribono shel Olam fulfill the blessings of the Tzaddik, the Nasi of our generation, in their entirety.

**M. Schneerson**

3 Tammuz, 5715
Brooklyn, N.Y.

## Gimmel Tammuz

B"H, Gimmel Tammuz, 5715
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

After the longest of intervals, your letter has finally been received—though it was delayed somewhat in transit. It is surprising that you allow such long gaps between letters, and that sometimes, even after you have written, you do not send it until several weeks later, as you mentioned in this letter.

Regarding what you wrote—that at times you feel more *goshmedik* (coarse)—the advice for such a state is to immerse this feeling in the waters of Torah in general, and the waters of the teachings of Chassidus in particular. This clarifies and refines, even if one does not feel it at the time, as is known that *tevilah* (immersion) shares the same letters as *bitul*.

It is surprising that the men are not assisting the women in their holy work within the organization of N'shei U’Bnos Chabad, even though the words of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, regarding the great necessity of this work of theirs have been publicized among *anash* for a long time. May it be Hashem’s will that, in addition to the men’s own work in their respective areas, they utilize the principle of our Sages that a woman is under the authority of her husband to further the aforementioned goal. May you have good news to report regarding all of this. The attribute of the *Ribono shel Olam* is *midah k’neged midah* (measure for measure), and may it be that you increase the *Chassidishe nachas* that you and your wife, *shichyu*, receive from all your children, *shichyu*.

With blessings,

## 3708

B"H, 3 Tammuz, 5715
Brooklyn.

In any case, it is simple that there is a distinction between the matter of contracting tumah for a Nasi or a Tzaddik at the time of burial, and visiting the gravesite after time has passed, a subject which many have already discussed.

I am certain that you are taking an **active** part in the affairs of Tzeirei Agudas Chabad in Eretz Yisrael, may it be built and established, and it is surprising that you do not write about this in detail.

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita
