## 3,319

B"H, 3 Tammuz, 5715
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Mrs. Rachel, may she live,

Blessings and peace!

I was pleased to receive your letter of 29 Sivan, in which you write about the women’s gatherings that have been held for some time now, which have been successful, and most importantly, that new members have joined. I hope that you will not be satisfied with the current format, and that you will work to expand it—both in the number of members and in the content. We see that when one truly desires something and acts with the proper energy, Hashem Yisbarach grants success beyond the natural order.

Regarding the suggestion that there should be a collection of money at every gathering—even a small sum—one must be very careful in such matters, so as not to discourage women for whom even a small sum is not always easily available. Furthermore, this is to ensure that the gatherings do not take on the character of a fundraising institution, which at times can cast a shadow on the entire endeavor. I believe that if a certain sum is needed for expenses, it is better from several standpoints to organize a separate gathering for that purpose, rather than having every gathering associated with a collection of money.

Enclosed is a copy of my general letter to Agudas N'shei U'Bnos Chabad. I hope you will find an opportunity to convey the letter in its entirety, or its content, to the members of your group, who are in truth included in that general category. Even if, as you write, your gathering has a different name, the name is not the main thing; the content is.

With blessings for success and for good tidings in all the above, and this is understood also regarding yourself, your husband, and your children, may they live,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

Secretary

## 3111

B"H, 6 Tammuz, 5715
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 28 Sivan, in which you outline the main points of your life story and your current situation, serving in the army, etc.

It is surely unnecessary to remind you that, just as in a flesh-and-blood army the primary requirement is the discipline of *kabbalas ol* (accepting the yoke), and even if at first one does not fully grasp the necessity of this, within a short time anyone with a healthy mind will realize its necessity even toward a human commander—how much more so, and with infinitely greater force, is this true for every Jew, who is part of the *tzivos Hashem* (armies of Hashem), regarding the commands of the Commander-in-Chief, the King of Kings, the Holy One, blessed be He. And just as in the analogy, it is not the way of the Commander-in-Chief to approach each and every soldier personally to deliver orders without any intermediary, but rather delivers them through officers whose rank and position are closer to the soldier, and since he is appointed by the Commander-in-Chief, he is a *shaliach* (agent) of the person, and his act is as the act of the sender.

**Likewise**, this is true in the parallel: those who received the Torah, the *Tanaim* and *Amoraim*, the teachers of instruction in Israel according to the laws of our Torah, the Torah of Hashem—through them are the instructions of the King of Kings, the Holy One, blessed be He, delivered. And just as in the analogy, the discipline and *kabbalas ol* are not intended to suppress, humiliate, or harm the soldier, but on the contrary: the stronger he is in his discipline and *kabbalas ol*, the sooner he will advance from rank to rank, and it will be better for him in all his affairs—so too, and **all the more so**, is this the case regarding the *kabbalas ol malchus shamayim* (acceptance of the yoke of Heaven) that leads to the acceptance of the yoke of Torah and the yoke of *mitzvos* in daily life. Further elaboration on this is surely unnecessary.

Since you have been privileged to know the light of the teachings of Chassidus, at least to some extent, and you know its guidance and customs, you must conduct yourself accordingly even in the army. You bear the privilege and responsibility to make all of this known to your friends in your group and company, and to serve as a symbol and example of how a descendant of the family from which you come, and one who has been privileged to spend time within the walls of Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim, conducts himself and acts. There is nothing that can stand before the will; if you truly desire it, this *shlichus* of yours will succeed in your hands.

Surely you have set times for Torah study each day, both in the revealed Torah and in the teachings of Chassidus, and most importantly, in the *halachos* required for daily life.

Regarding your specific question about the *shidduchim* being suggested to you, it is appropriate that you look into this, especially since you write that those facilitating it are your friends from Tzeirei Agudas Chabad. May Hashem, who oversees each and every one with *hashgacha pratis* (Divine providence), guide you on the path that is good for you, both materially and spiritually.

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,
Secretary

As is understood.

## 3713

B"H, 6 Tammuz, 5715
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing and refined, occupied with communal needs, R' Mordechai Tzvi, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

Following your long silence, your letter from the beginning of the month of Tammuz was finally received. Thank you for the news that all is well in your home; may it be the will of Hashem that this continues and increases, as is explained at the end of Esther Rabbah.

Regarding what you wrote about the *avreich*... the two points are understandable and straightforward: first, that the harm of the many outweighs the benefit of the individual. Consequently, if there is a basis to believe that the presence of the aforementioned individual among the many will cause them harm, it is impossible to put them at risk, etc. Second, according to our Sages, whoever sustains even one soul of Yisroel, etc.—certainly this *avreich* is also included in this. Therefore, one must search and search again for ways to place him in a positive light. As you describe his situation in your letter, it appears that there is also a matter of illness involved (I mean that his undesirable tendencies, at least in part, should be addressed through medical treatment). One should consult with a specialist in this field, and perhaps it would be worthwhile to do so initially without the *avreich's* knowledge, and only afterwards (and in the manner the doctor instructs) should they meet together.

It is surely unnecessary to remind you of what I have written to the educational institutions where I have influence: that one must prepare provisions for the journey for the students for the vacation days well in advance. How good it would be to arrange a method so that the connection with them is not completely severed during these weeks. On the contrary, during the vacation days, when they are free from secular studies, there is room to act even more in matters of holiness. We see tangibly that things and matters said as if in passing—that is, not as a formal *shiur* but during a conversation or a walk—are absorbed and accepted better and more easily...

With blessing.

## 3714

B”H, 6 Tammuz, 5715
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter—which lacks the date of writing—in which you write regarding your son, may he live, that perhaps he should learn a trade, etc., because you are burdened by the expenses of moving into a new apartment, and therefore you have no room to think about a *shidduch* for him, as arranging matters for your son would amount to several thousand *lirot*.

Consider the beginning and the end of your letter: to find thousands of *lirot* for an apartment, you feel it is worth going into debt, even though you were already living in an apartment previously—it is just that the current one is better. Yet, regarding the fulfillment of the *mitzvah* of "And you shall teach them to your children," and subsequently to marry him off—which is a *mitzvah* of the father toward the son, as ruled by our Sages—it is simple in your eyes that not only do you not need to do this, but, in your own words, you have no room to even think about it. And yet, you have lived in *Eretz Yisrael* for so many years; surely it has not escaped your notice that the children of the truly poor, may Hashem protect us, marry off their sons and daughters even in these recent times, and they strive to ensure that they remain specifically in the "tent of Torah." Among them are even those who did not have the means to pay thousands of *lirot* for an apartment.

This is the craftiness of the *yetzer hara*: at first, you yourself were in the "tent of Torah" all day, and later, due to various strange circumstances, you established your livelihood elsewhere and became an official. Naturally, it is understood that this caused a weakening in your study of *nigleh*, your study of Chassidus, and your *avodas hatefillah*. The *yetzer* is not satisfied with this; it teaches a *binyan av* (a precedent) for the son, that he too must do the same even before he is standing on his own two feet, even though the father only did so when he was at the age of maturity. How great is the *he'elem* and *hester* (concealment) that the aforementioned is truly clear and simple, yet people do not recognize matters as they are, and instead clothe them in an entirely different form.

Regarding the *bochur*, may he be well, you should consult with the *hanhalas hayeshiva* so that your son may study *hora'ah* (rabbinic ordination) or the profession of *shechitah*, whichever is more appropriate. May the *Ribono shel Olam* grant him success.

With the blessing that your son will succeed in going from strength to strength in truth, and that you, too, will begin in this, and may the *Ribono shel Olam* grant you success in attaining the level you were at several years ago, and to add even more to that.

With blessings.

## 3115

B"H, 6 Tammuz, 5715
Brooklyn

To Anash and the Temimim in Melbourne,

In connection with the upcoming days of redemption, 12 and 13 Tammuz—the redemption of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, the Nasi of Israel, which is our own redemption and the deliverance of our souls—I suggest that in addition to the farbrengens that will surely be held on these days on the grandest scale, you should convene a special meeting.

The sole purpose of this meeting should be the yeshiva named after him, Ohalei Yosef Yitzchok Lubavitch in Australia, and to formulate a plan for its support, development, and expansion. They should send the list and the pledges of their hearts and hands here, and it will be read at an auspicious time at the tziyun of my father-in-law, the Rebbe. I have already stated many times that this is not merely a spiritual matter, but a physical one as well, especially since, in general, physicality and spirituality must go hand in hand, and specifically when they are "one nation in the land."

With blessings for the Chag HaGeulah and for good tidings regarding all of the above.

## 3,716

7 Tammuz, 5715
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the participants of the annual convention of the Rabbinical Council, may Hashem grant them life,

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your notification regarding your annual convention, I hereby express my wishes that your gathering be a "gathering for the sake of Heaven." When it is so, success is guaranteed—meaning that the *hisorerus* (inspiration) of the days of the convention will lead to tangible actions throughout the entire year. These actions should be taken by each of the participants—both regarding themselves and, most importantly, regarding the community in which they serve and wherever their influence reaches.

It is unnecessary to elaborate on the responsibility that rests upon the shoulders of every Rav. It is surely also unnecessary to elaborate on the holy obligation that rests upon each member of the Rabbinical Council in particular, as almost all of them are natives of the United States. This allows them to influence the members of their communities and their flock directly; caring for their livelihood and their spiritual needs is their duty and their privilege, with even greater intensity and strength. "Fortunate is he who considers the poor" (*Tehillim 41:2*); "your own poor come first" (*Bava Metzia 71a*); and there is no "poor" except one who is lacking in the knowledge of Torah (*Nedarim 41a*). This means (according to the *Zohar*) that *Torah* comes from the word *hora’ah* (instruction)—instruction for daily life, so that it may be according to the "Torah of life," in action, in speech, and even in thought.

As is known, the primary cause for everything that is not in order in the lives of Jews in the United States is rooted in a lack of knowledge, or in plain terms—the staggering *am ha’aratzus* (ignorance of Torah) that has taken hold of life. When one traces the cause of this terrible *am ha’aratzus*, one must conclude that a major factor is the preoccupation of the Rav and spiritual leader with various matters in his community, including transient and fleeting affairs, such as participating in family events or various and sundry celebrations in the neighborhood and society, and other such matters that have no connection to religious concerns. As a result, whether willingly or under pressure, he neglects his primary role: to lead his flock on the path that ascends to Hashem through the dissemination of Torah study and the strengthening and spreading of Yiddishkeit. Instead of dedicating his time, strength, and energy to being a *moreh hora’ah* (a teacher of law) in the literal and full sense, the entire essence of the rabbinate has been reduced to being a "good speaker." Over time, this is done not for the sake of the moral lesson in the sermon, but so that it should be pleasant to the listener. Thus, the Rav becomes a preacher whose duty is to provide a "good time" for his congregants for half an hour on Shabbos and Yom Tov, while simultaneously being a successful "social worker" in his community.

Reflecting on the fact that a fundamental change in this distressing situation is necessary, and on the other hand, that a total transformation of society does not happen overnight, it is my opinion that the suggested advice is as follows: One of the primary tasks of a Rav in the United States—especially a young Rav beginning his work in a new community and environment—should be to seek out individuals within his community who possess influence and for whom Yiddishkeit is close to their hearts. He should make them, as it were, "assistants" to the Rav in fulfilling his primary duties, namely, the strengthening and dissemination of the faith in all circles of the community in daily life. In other words, he should train religious *baalei-batim* (laymen) to be activists in spreading religious observance in the community. The Jews of the United States are particularly capable of this, because one of the characteristics of the residents of this country, in the vast majority, is individual energy and activity, and the aspiration to be a leader in a more or less broad circle. If this is true in trivial matters, then it is certainly true in matters of religion, for the heart of every Jewish man and woman is awake to Hashem, His Torah, and His *mitzvos*, even when in *galus*—as the well-known saying of our Sages goes.

Another characteristic point in this country is the physicality and materialism in which life in general is immersed. It is impossible that this would not influence the attitude toward the religion of Torah and *mitzvos*, which have become highly "materialized." I do not wish to dwell at length on this painful and distressing matter; surely everyone who observes the state of religious life in this country recognizes this, and no further explanation is needed. Therefore, it is essential—in this country even more so than overseas—that every single person have a fixed daily *shiur* in a study that infuses spirituality into daily life and clarifies and refines it. As our *Rabbeinu HaZaken*, the author of the *Tanya* and *Shulchan Aruch*, puts it: "to transform physicality into spirituality," which is achieved through the study of *mussar* and Chassidus. Since the role of a Rav is to be a *moreh hora’ah* not only in speech but, primarily, in his own conduct—to serve as a model for the *baalei-batim*—the Rabbis must establish this *shiur*, and not only as a fixed time, but also as a fixed commitment in the soul. Even though my hope and confidence is that the vast majority of the participants in this convention have such a *shiur* regardless, this decision is worthwhile even for the sake of one single soul among the participants, for he is an entire world.

And most importantly—a decision accepted in public by many (even if it is *bli neder*, and not a vow made with the intent of the public) has more endurance and lasts for a longer time. This is seen tangibly.

It goes without saying that not all opinions are the same, and therefore there is no place to mandate the specific book or method by which this study should be conducted. However, it is possible to establish the minimum amount of time to be dedicated to this. Perhaps one could also suggest a list of books, and the individual can choose what is suitable for the nature of his soul and for the areas in which he needs to be more careful.

And since I have come to this:

It has been a wonder to me for several years—for everything mentioned in the *Shulchan Aruch* is *halacha pesukah* (decisive law) for **practical application in reality**. Even a matter that is subject to a dispute in the *Shulchan Aruch*—there are rules as to whose opinion is the *halacha*, and we perform and fulfill his words. Yet, as an exception, in certain circles of the Jewish people—and even among those who are meticulous in *mitzvos*—there is a **law that is explicit and without any dispute**: that before *davening*, everyone is obligated to contemplate "the greatness of Hashem, may He be exalted, and the lowliness of man, and to remove all human pleasures from his heart" (*Shulchan Aruch Orach Chayim, siman 98, end of seif 1*, based on the *Mishnah* as noted there). Since the obligation of *davening* is three times a day—and nowadays it has been established as an obligation a third time as well, *Ma’ariv*—then this law is also an obligation at least three times every day, and it is binding upon every single person who is obligated in *davening*.

How long and why do the Rabbis, the *morei hora’ah*, the *Roshei Yeshiva*, and the *Roshei Yeshiva* remain silent about this *halacha*—a *halacha* where those who fulfill it have become so few, even among those who know of it?

I will conclude my letter with heartfelt wishes that the desire of Hashem will succeed in their hands.

*Havayah*—the Name that testifies—that He is within **all** existence (*Havayah*), and He was, is, and will be (*Zohar Vol. III, 257b*), meaning—in every place and at every time, for the desires of Heaven are eternal.

To strengthen the Jewish communities in the United States, which, due to our many sins, in our time of the darkness of *galus* which is growing heavier—and there is no day without its curse—have remained the majority in number and the majority in stature of our nation as a whole. They have no one to rely on to receive spiritual strengthening from another country; on the contrary, all those [other countries] are in need of encouragement in matters of Torah and *mitzvos* and their fulfillment in the spirit of our ancestors—from the Jewish people of the United States. For the time being, the responsibility and the privilege are theirs, first and foremost—to disseminate the Torah of truth with *yiras shamayim* (fear of Heaven), and to strengthen the breach of the House of Israel without compromises,

Until Hashem has mercy on the remnant of His people and the prophecy is fulfilled, for which all who believe in the Torah and in Moshe Rabbeinu are waiting:

That a man will arise who is learned in Torah and occupied with *mitzvos*, and he will compel all of Israel to walk in it and strengthen its breach, and he will gather the outcasts of Israel and lead us out of our *galus*—in the true and complete *Geulah*.

With respect and blessing,

**Menachem Schneerson**

## 3718

B"H, 7 Tammuz, 5715
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter, as you requested, I will mention all those you wrote about at the holy resting place of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory.

Regarding your question as to whether one should maintain the three daily study sessions on Shabbos and Yom Tov: it is obvious that one should, and in fact, it is even more appropriate to do so. As for what you wrote—that it is not the custom to recite Tehillim on Shabbos and Yom Tov—this is not the case; it is the custom in all Jewish communities to increase the recitation of Tehillim on Shabbos and Yom Tov.

Regarding what you wrote concerning a *tikkun* for the known sin: one must be careful with *tevilas Ezra*, and keep words of Torah engraved in one’s memory. This includes studying Mishnayos and increasing one’s involvement in the letters of Torah and *tefillah*, giving *tzedakah* before *Shacharis* every weekday, and engaging in matters of teaching and education in a spirit of pure holiness. Most importantly, one should divert one’s mind from the entire matter—even from the *tikkun* itself—until after marriage.

With blessings for success in Torah study with *yiras shamayim*.

## 3119

B"H, 7 Tammuz, 5715
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

I was pleased to receive the telegram regarding your safe arrival home, as well as the regards Dr. Mindel conveyed to me from the letter he received from you. I am sure you found your family in good order and in peace, and that you also conveyed regards to all of Anash, may they live, and to your brother, may he live, as we discussed. When one sows a seed in a Jewish heart—for Jews are called an *eretz chefetz* (a land of desire)—it eventually bears fruit, even if at times it is difficult to predict how long it will take, as it is written, "so that no one is cast out from Him." Especially since the merit of doing favors for fellow Jews does not allow one to be drowned in *gashmius*; whether one wills it or not, it draws one (even if the beginning was under duress) toward the true good, and there is no good other than Torah and the fulfillment of *mitzvos*.

Since you are, thank G-d, successful in other matters, one must hope that you will have success in this as well. It goes without saying that you may tell him this in my name if you find it necessary. It is a known final conclusion, even among secular scientists, that nothing is ever lost and nothing can be destroyed if it possesses a *metzius* (an existence). If this is true in *gashmius* (material-physical matters), then it is certainly true—to an incomparable degree—in *inyanim ruchniyim* (spiritual realities), which include the proper *chinuch* that parents instill in their children.

Enclosed is a booklet, the continuation of the *maamar* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, which will surely interest you, especially the *hosafah* where it speaks about *galus*. The greatest *galus* may not be the state of being among strangers, but rather being in *galus* under one’s own *yetzer hara*, as is understood.

With blessings for good health for you, your wife, and the entire family, may they live, and that you may be able to accomplish much in matters of Torah and *mitzvos* in general, and in the affairs of the Lubavitch institutions in particular.

## 3220

B"H, 8 Tammuz, 5715
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your question in your letter of 20 Sivan... It is surely known to you that when one Yid wishes to connect with another Yid—which is truly a necessity, for this is the essence of the mitzvah of Ahavas Yisrael, as explained in the Sefer HaMitzvos of the Tzemach Tzedek regarding the interpretation of this mitzvah, and as stated by Rabbeinu HaZaken at the beginning of Chapter 32 of Tanya, that all are equal and we all have one Father—the most direct path when separated by distance is to study the same subjects in Torah. As is explained in Tanya, beginning of Chapter 5, one should also influence others in this, for the attribute of the Ribono shel Olam is measure for measure.

I trust you are keeping the three daily study portions established for every soul by my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory—the Chumash, Tehillim, and Tanya—which are well known, and which also relate to the aforementioned.

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe

## 3721

B"H, 8 Tammuz, 5715
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Rabbi, G-d-fearing, and diligent scholar, Rabbi Yechezkel HaKohen, may he live:

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letter from the beginning of the month of Tammuz, thank you for the information you provided regarding the estate and the Torah novellae of the late Rabbi Alfandari, of blessed memory.

Regarding your observation concerning what is mentioned in various places in the study of the hidden dimension of Torah: a) that all seven lower Sefiros (Z'T) clothe themselves in the world below, and b) that the Sefirah of Malchus clothes itself in the world below—and how both of these can be reconciled*:

The rule for understanding such matters is known, for regarding this it is said: "From my flesh I shall perceive Elokus."

We see in the human being that his influence upon others comes through his power of action or his speech. However, the **content** of that speech and action consists of matters of Chesed or matters of Gevurah, etc., and likewise matters of his intellect—meaning, from his Chochma and Binah. Yet, this is not from the **essence** of his Chochma and Binah, as is known from the words of our Sages: "A person does not grasp the mind of his teacher..." Rather, it is only the lowest level of his intellect, which is relative to the student. And how is it possible for a very young student to grasp the intellect of the teacher? It is only because of the teacher’s closeness to the student—that he **loves** him and wishes to bestow upon him even from his own Chochma and Binah. However, since he knows that the student cannot receive the teacher’s intellect as it is, he constricts the intellect into a suitable measure—this is his **Gevurah**.

The analogy in the "higher man" is that everything that **comes** to the worlds comes through the Sefirah of Malchus (as mentioned above, speech and action). What **pertains** to the worlds are the seven lower Sefiros (as mentioned above, Chesed and Gevurah—the content of the speech and action), or even the Mochin. But they do not come as they are; rather, through Tzimtzumim, they become Mochin that are in a form [suitable for the recipient]. See also Igeres HaKodesh by our Alter Rebbe, Epistle 15, where, upon careful study, you will find further explanation of what has been stated above.

With blessings for success in your holy work and in setting fixed times for the study of Chassidus, which leads to the fulfillment of the commandment, "Know the G-d of your father" (and consequently, to the completion of the commandment as required), "and serve Him with a whole heart."

P.S. Regarding your question about purchasing books published by Kehot: I believe I have already written to you that they are available in Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt speedily. You should contact Agudas Chabad regarding this at 22 Feierberg St., Tel Aviv.

#### 3721

**Regarding... Alfandari:** See Epistle 3655 above.

*) See Etz Chaim, Shaar Arich Anpin, Chapter 6: The higher does not clothe in the lower, only its Z'T.

Ibid., Shaar Abba v'Imma, Chapter 6: The higher does not clothe in the lower except for its Malchus alone.

Ibid., Shaar Seder Atzilus, Chapter 2: And the intention is not, G-d forbid, the Sefirah itself, but rather the illumination of its Z'T. And in the gloss of the Tzemach Tzedek there, Chapter 1, it is noted that it is not even the Z'T of the Sefirah itself.

Ibid., Shaar Mochin d'Tzelem, end of Chapter 4: In every world and in every Sefirah it is thus, that the Malchus of the Malchus of the Malchus of Atzilus clothes in Beriah, etc.

## 3222

B"H, 9 Tammuz, 5715
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings,

I have just received your letter dated Monday, and I am hastening to reply because I was surprised by its opening. After all, it is a mitzvah d’oraisa to pray for long life and good years, and since we are obligated in this, it is certainly a good thing not only in a physical sense but also in a spiritual one. Therefore, I accept with willingness and joy your request to bring this prayer to the holy resting place of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory.

However, regarding what you wrote in your letter—it is already known that one of the thirteen principles of faith is that we are obligated to await the coming of Moshiach Tzidkeinu every single day. He will take us out of our exile and lead us, souls in bodies, to our holy land, may it be rebuilt and established soon. Consequently, there is no room for the question or the request [you posed].

May Hashem fulfill your desired request and lengthen your days and years in goodness and pleasantness, together with your wife—may they live—and may you disseminate the concepts of Chassidus in general, and matters connected to my father-in-law, the Rebbe, in particular, in your good camp. For then, according to what is explained and well-understood in Tanya, Chapter 5, that it is a wondrous unification, etc.—which has no equivalent at all in the physical realm—souls in bodies are united together with my father-in-law, the Rebbe, through his Torah and his guidance, in which he gave over his very soul—and not only his nefesh, but also his ruach, neshamah, chayah, and yechidah—as is also understood from Iggeres HaKodesh, Epistle 27, and its explanation.

Enclosed is the continuation of the maamar of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, which was written by him. Surely you will merit to share its content with the many, and the merit of the many will depend upon you.

With blessings for a long life and good tidings.

## 3,623

B"H, 9 Tammuz, 5715
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter—which lacks a date—in which you write that some time ago you studied in a yeshiva and were successful in your studies, but that subsequently, in your opinion, this success has departed from you, and you are unable to connect to your learning, etc., and consequently, you feel a sense of inferiority and doubt whether you will succeed in your studies, and you ask for my opinion on this matter:

If you will listen to my advice, you should banish this feeling, as well as these thoughts, entirely—not only from your heart but from your immediate surroundings as well—and continue your studies in our Torah, the Torah of life. You should, however, ask the Rosh Yeshiva to place you in a class suitable for you, and to arrange your studies for the initial period, at least, in a subject that your heart desires. These concerns have no basis and are merely temptations of the Yetzer.

However, since in every matter and for every person, Siyata Dishmaya is required, and the measure of the Holy One, Blessed be He, is "measure for measure," it would be most appropriate for you to become a mashpia for a group of boys—naturally, younger than yourself. In the time you have free from your own studies, you should learn with them, or more accurately, converse with them about topics from the weekly parsha and the halachos necessary for the daily life of such boys, and guide them in the customs of Yisrael appropriate for them. Since I am confident that you will succeed in this, this will also serve as further proof that the aforementioned concerns have no basis whatsoever, and you will surely ascend in your learning and succeed in it.

You should certainly keep, from now on at least, the three daily shiurim that are equal for every soul, as established by my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory—the well-known daily portions of Chumash, Tehillim, and Tanya. Likewise, you should set aside a few coins for tzedakah every weekday before davening—it is understood that all of this should be done without a neder.

With blessings for good tidings regarding all of the above, soon,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

Secretary

## 3224

When Yidden are in a state of *simcha* (joy)—and naturally, one also speaks of a Torah topic—this is a *simcha shel mitzvah* (joy of a mitzvah), which serves as a *segulah*, a conduit, and a vessel for everything one needs, up to the most sublime revelations. See also *Torah Or* 20b.

With blessings for the *Chag HaGeulah* and regards to all those participating in the *farbrengen*.

## 3210

B"H, 11 Tammuz, 5715
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and Blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter from the 8th of Tammuz, along with the enclosed lists, which will be read at an auspicious time at the holy resting place of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory.

I was pleased to read what you wrote regarding your efforts with the family of the *avreich* [may he live and be well]... and regarding the fact that, for the time being, it seems to you that you are not seeing results—do not, Heaven forbid, become discouraged. It is a certainty that efforts in *ta'amulah* do not return empty. Moreover, they bring great benefit and "fruits of fruits," even if it sometimes requires a bit more time. It is already well-known what is brought in *Avos D'Rabbi Nosson* (Chapter 6) regarding the verse, "Water wears away stones"—drop after drop, it eventually makes an indentation in the physical stone. How much more so is this true regarding the "heart of stone" of a son or daughter of Israel, which is merely a borrowed term and not truly stone, even in a spiritual sense. As is explained in the teachings of Chassidus, the inner essence of every single man and woman of Israel is complete and desires to fulfill the command of Hashem. As our Sages of blessed memory said, "The daughters of Israel are beautiful, but poverty (and there is no poverty but in knowledge) disfigures them." May Hashem grant you success so that you will see good fruit from your labor soon.

With blessings for the *Chag HaGeulah*.

P.S.

## 3330

11 Tammuz, 5715
Brooklyn

To the distinguished Rabbi, man of action and accomplishment, etc.,
Rabbi Shimshon Raphael, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

In connection with the days of the redemption of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory—his redemption from his imprisonment for his work with mesiras nefesh to uphold the Torah and its mitzvos.

At the time, this was a victory that served as a model over the forces opposing Hashem and His Torah. For the years and generations that followed, it serves as a clear instruction that the Torah governs reality, even when one cannot find a place for this within human logic.

It is our custom to publish, especially for these days, a book or booklet on the theme of the day, containing matters of inspiration regarding this.

Enclosed is the booklet published this year, containing a portion of the memoirs of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, regarding his imprisonment. Added to it are the words of the Nasi of Israel, based on the point that in matters of Torah and mitzvos, every single man and woman of Israel is a free person, and has no master other than Hashem, their G-d.

If we are in need of remembrance and inspiration regarding this—concerning exile among non-Jews and their decrees, where they have no choice and are merely like an axe in the hand of the one who hews with it—then how much more so is this inspiration necessary regarding exile among Jews, who possess free choice. As it is written, "See, I have set before you today life and the good... therefore choose life." Even though the request of the Ribono shel Olam (which is also help and assistance) is "choose life," it is emphasized that **just as** the matter of "life" is emphasized, **so too** is it emphasized that there must be "choosing."

It is my hope that you will utilize what is stated in the booklet in your own work. Despite the progress and the increase of light that has occurred in this environment, there are many matters that require rectification.

Their rectification is connected in a significant measure to the recognition of the aforementioned truth. For, as mentioned above, this is an "exile" of concealment and hiddenness, which creates room for error—to call darkness light.

It is a wondrous thing that specifically in our generation, the *ikvesa d'meshicha*, the time of the prophecy that "many will be purified, whitened, and refined"—or in the language of our Sages, "either entirely innocent or entirely guilty"—in these final days of a double and redoubled exile, the blurring of boundaries increases, and consequently, the confusion. Through the craftiness of the yetzer hara, this ultimately leads to calling evil good and good evil (and as a result), "putting darkness for light and light for darkness" (in the realm of intellect and opinions), and "putting bitter for sweet and sweet for bitter" (in the realm of emotions and action). Many of the "leaders of this people" are misleading them (some out of fear, and some out of a lack of understanding and contemplation; but regarding those they influence, the results are similar—those who lead them cause them to err). May it be the will of Hashem that—for His sake He will act—He will sprinkle upon each and every one of us, within the entirety of Israel, pure waters, the waters of pure Da'as, until "they shall all know Me, from the smallest to the greatest." A knowledge in the mind and in the heart, a knowledge that brings "this mitzvah" to be "in your mouth and in your heart to perform it."

With respect and with a blessing for success in your work in the aforementioned direction.

P.S.
Thank you for your attention in sending me the booklet of the annual report of "Young Israel."

## 3,331

B"H, 11 Tammuz, 5715
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 8 Tammuz, in which you ask my opinion regarding the timing of your trip to France:

During the summer months, there are several changes to the yeshiva’s schedule there. Therefore, it is not particularly advisable to arrive precisely when the schedules are not the regular ones. It would be better to wait with this trip until the end of the summer or the beginning of the winter.

It is understood and obvious that the trip will be beneficial if you decide with absolute resolve to conduct yourself in the yeshiva in accordance with its regulations. Since it is not easy for a person to change themselves from one extreme to the other all at once, there is also a benefit in delaying the trip. During the intervening months, you must accustom yourself, step by step, to the aforementioned conduct. This should be done by studying in the meantime at Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim in Montreal—and not merely by keeping to the summer schedule, which is surely not the regular schedule in Montreal either, but rather by adhering to the regular schedule followed throughout the entire year. Study with persistence and diligence, and conduct yourself as befits a student of Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim in speech and in action. May Hashem grant you success and may you have good news regarding all of the above.

## 3332

3332

B"H, 14 Tammuz, 5715
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

In connection with the days of redemption, 12 and 13 Tammuz, which we have just passed, it is surely unnecessary to urge you to carry the inspiration of these days throughout the entire year. It is also certainly unnecessary to explain what this inspiration should be—since the matter concerns the redemption of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, it is self-evident that the inspiration and its results must be consistent with his will and his instructions.

From this, there is also an answer to the claim made in your letter of 12 Iyar, that you only value acting "for the sake of My Name, Hashem will be honored" (and so there would be no doubt as to where the emphasis lies, you explicitly emphasized and drew a line under one of those four words). Since this is not consistent with the aforementioned, then, at the very least, after 13 Tammuz of this year, you no longer hold by that position. It is understood that this is the remedy required for Chassidim. For if it were not so, and you were to see in your writing "for the sake of My Name, He will be honored"—who is the one saying this? You would not have held by that, even without the aforementioned remedy.

Now, in what context and to whom does this apply? To Michael, the great prince who records the merits of Yisrael. Naturally, he is interested in having every action performed without ulterior motives and not "for the sake of My Name," for then he can record a greater merit—not only in quantity, but also in quality. However, regarding my letters to Anash in the Holy Land, may it be rebuilt and established—in my general letters, where the discussion concerns the activities and not the individuals—it is understood that my intention is that the activities be carried out. If someone mixes in an ulterior motive, receiving a reward in this world, the World to Come, or both together, it is understood that I do not begrudge them this. Only when they ask me, with the intent of receiving an answer and acting in accordance with that answer, will I begin to consider what is better: whether it should be done for the sake of My Name, or for the sake of the name of Lubavitch in its entirety, which also includes the details—namely, the individuals of Anash.

#### ***3332***

**For the sake of My Name:** Meaning, if the instruction comes in His Name, then he will carry out the instruction.

**Who is the one saying:** The Holy One, Blessed be He. If so, how can the writer attribute this to himself?

## 3,333

With respect and blessing.

## 3714

B"H, 14 Tammuz, 5715
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed Rabbi, G-d-fearing, and distinguished scholar, engaged in the needs of the community,
Rabbi Yitzchak HaLevi, may he live and be well,

Shalom u’Bracha!

In response to your letter of 8 Tammuz, I would have liked for us to have gathered together during the days of redemption, 12 or 13 Tammuz, from which we "go forth" (*d’azlinan minei*).

As is known, the precision of the expression "from which we go forth" is explained in Chassidus to mean that through this, one creates "journeys" (*mahalachim*). This is the superiority of Bnei Yisrael—souls in bodies—over the angels, who are called "those who stand" (*omdim*); see *Ohr HaTorah* 24b.

It is distressing that the construction of the mikveh in your camp is being delayed. We cannot know the extent of the benefit that could have been achieved had the matter been expedited, for who can fathom the secret of the souls? Since you write that only the lack of funds is delaying this, you can surely arrange a loan against the future collection, provided that you do everything possible to bring the matter to fruition. May Hashem grant you success.

Enclosed here is the continuation booklet of the maamar of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory. I am certain that you will merit to share its content with the many, and the merit of the many will depend upon you.

With blessings,

#### ***3714***

**Rabbi Yitzchak:** Levi, Reading, PA.

## 3336

B"H, 15 Tammuz, 5715
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter of 9 Tammuz, in which you write regarding the financial situation in your home, and that this raises several considerations regarding your future arrangements:

You should present the details of the matter before three of your friends, one of whom should be your mashpia, under whose guidance you are. May Hashem grant them the correct insight to advise you in a way that is good for you, both spiritually and materially.

Regarding what you write—that you lead the davening at the yeshivah for all three tefillos, and that this is causing differences of opinion among the students who are davening at that time:

In such a matter, the instruction of our Alter Rebbe in his Iggeres HaKodesh, section 2 (162b), is well known: that one who leads the davening should pray in a balanced manner—neither prolonging it excessively, nor shortening it, rushing, or—Heaven forbid—skipping parts. Furthermore, in a yeshivah, one must also take into account the yeshivah’s schedule, the times for davening, and the times for Torah study. May Hashem grant you success.

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,
Secretary

## 3337

B.H. 15 Tammuz, 5715
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter, in which you express surprise at the content of my letter—which was a reply to a note from your wife, the Rabbanit, may she live and be well:

1) My suggestion that the mezuzos be checked is not because I suspect anyone, Heaven forbid. Rather, as in similar cases, and also taking into account the opinion in the Mechilta regarding the checking of tefillin and mezuzos (see Rosh, end of Hilchos Tefillin) every twelve months—even though the halacha is that checking twice every seven years is sufficient—I wrote what occurred to me: that the mezuzos should be checked now. The fact that they were kosher some time ago does not contradict the need to check them, as we see from the very law that they must be checked twice in a shmittah cycle. It is understood that sometimes the ink flakes off, or a bit of moisture gets under the casing of the mezuzah. Just as in matters of health, one addresses even minor doubts to improve one's well-being.

2) Regarding the fact that my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, wrote to your wife, may she live, in language of a promise and a firm assurance, while my letter contains no such expression—the reason for this is quite simple: Because he was a Nasi Yisrael, a Tzaddik Yesod Olam, he possessed entirely different powers. Therefore, according to the dictum of our Sages, "A Tzaddik decrees," he was able to write in the language of a promise.

3) It is self-understood that I read your wife’s note myself, and I dictated the text of the reply to her word for word. I open all letters that arrive in my name myself, and there is no basis for the suspicion you wrote of—that someone else had done so, etc.

4) And since these days we have celebrated the days of redemption, 12-13 Tammuz, of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory—our redemption and the deliverance of our souls—may Hashem help that the blessings he gave to your wife, the Rabbanit, may she live, be fulfilled to the fullest measure. Together with you, may you both have much Yiddishe nachas for long, good years from all your descendants, may they live.

With blessings,

P.S.
Enclosed is the continuation of the maamar of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, which will surely merit you and the many, and the merit of the many depends upon you.

## 3440

B"H, 16 Tammuz, 5715
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Peace and Blessing!

Following your long silence, your letter of 6 Tammuz was received. May it be the will of Hashem that, in accordance with what is explained in Iggeres HaKodesh, end of Chapter 9, and the analogy of a rope that is severed and then tied back together, your avodah will be redoubled—at the very least, twofold and manifold —both in quantity and in quality. May the statement of our Sages in Esther Rabbah (at the end) be fulfilled in you as well: that there be peace in abundance, blessing in abundance, etc. (see there). You have surely made a good start in this by utilizing the days of redemption, 12 and 13 Tammuz—the redemption of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, which is our redemption and the salvation of our souls.

Based on what is explained regarding the statement of our Sages that "his eyes are downward, but his heart is upward," it is understood that even his eyes being downward relates to his avodah—so that after davening, he will not be impressed by the sights of this world, and that such a new experience will not cause him to fall from his level. This is unlike one who has already been tested in this and naturally emerges unscathed. My desire is to be strong in my confidence that after you have passed through [the recent challenges], none of you will be impressed by trivial matters anymore, and that from here on, you will work together without interruption. On the contrary, you will ascend from level to level. This will serve as a vessel to receive the verdict of the Heavenly Beis Din, that in every matter of Torah, yiras shamayim, and good character traits, the hand of those who are connected to him and follow in his footsteps will be on top (see Kitzurim VeHe'aros LeTanya, p. 122, at the end).

You should certainly consult as soon as possible on how to utilize the vacation days—when many of the bochurim have more free time (although, naturally, the custom of a "vacation" for Torah students and avreichim in the middle of the summer is astonishing to me; if only I had the strength to abolish it!). The main point is that the students of the school are free and are not under the influence of undesirable teachers. It is worth considering the possibilities of gathering them for several days during the vacation in a garden or similar setting, to begin with distributing sweets, etc., and afterwards to speak about the Beis Hamikdash and the galus. Everyone believes in the coming of Moshiach speedily in our days, when all of Yisrael will do teshuvah and he will redeem us; this is preparation in the manner of Elul, and more.

[You should also provide] an exposition of the laws of these weeks, their customs, etc. There is a special budget for the expenses—as is customary—involved in this.

With blessings for success and for good tidings in all that is mentioned above.

## 3742

B"H, 16 Tammuz, 5715
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of Sunday, Parshas Balak, in which you ask how to conduct yourself regarding the elections for the Knesset.

The question is somewhat surprising, as this is the third time elections have been held, and the position regarding them is well-known. As my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, made public his opinion during the first Knesset elections: that every individual who possesses an identity card—and consequently has the right to vote—should participate in the elections, and it is understood that he should vote for the most charedi parties.

It is already a known ruling of our holy Torah that "a person should always view himself as if he is balanced [between merit and guilt], etc., and the entire world is balanced." Regarding elections, sometimes, through the votes of a few people, one can influence over time that a certain decree not be passed, or even cause the cancellation of decrees that already exist. Who is there in these days who can say, "I have saved my own soul," and let the **tzibbur** in Eretz Yisrael, may it be built and established, have what it will, and if they pass a decree, what does that have to do with me? Especially when, at the same time, he pays taxes to all the government offices, which is a **direct** form of **assistance** to those matters. He took their identity card, and furthermore, when he writes letters, he surely knows that what he pays for stamps goes into the tax office, and from his money, funds are taken for various and strange matters.

It is even more surprising that you do not mention your study of the inner dimension of the Torah, the teachings of Chassidus, about which I wrote to you previously. Studying Chassidus is your primary obligation, in accordance with the ruling of our holy Torah (see Hilchos Talmud Torah by the Alter Rebbe, Chapter 2, Section 10) that everyone must arrange their studies so that they can learn the entire Oral Torah at least once. From this, one can understand the astonishment and wonder regarding someone who has been made aware of this and yet does not occupy himself at all with the part of the Torah that is its inner dimension; there is no need to elaborate on such a startling matter.

I do not know your intent in your letter to me clearly, only by way of conjecture. Therefore, I do not wish to withhold my response to your aforementioned question. In any case—divert your attention from matters of politics, and establish a study session in the inner dimension of the Torah **every single day**. May it be the will of Hashem that a spirit from on high be poured upon you to do this soon and with a whole heart.

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,
Secretary

***

**Regarding the elections:** See also above 3559, and the references in the notes there.

## 3743

B"H, 16 Tammuz, 5715
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter, in which you write regarding the various events that have occurred to you recently, and concerning your claims against the insurance company as well as the company where you were employed when the incident occurred.

You are surely consulting with a lawyer who is well-versed in these laws and regulations, and who knows whether there is a basis for your claims and to which venue to turn regarding this matter.

In addition to this—and this is the main point—if, as you say, such unfortunate incidents, Heaven forbid, have occurred during the recent period, you should certainly increase your observance of the mitzvos of Hashem and conduct your daily lives in accordance with the instructions of our holy Torah, the Torah of life. For this is surely a hint from Above that there are matters and behaviors that require rectification. When things are rectified in the spiritual realm, Hashem will rectify them in the physical realm as well. You should have your husband’s—may he live and be well—tefillin checked, and he should daven every day. On weekdays, he should set aside a few coins for tzedakah before davening. You yourself should be meticulous in lighting candles on Erev Shabbos Kodesh and Erev Yom Tov, and before lighting the candles, you should also set aside a few coins for tzedakah. Furthermore, ensure that there are kosher mezuzos, according to the law, on all the doors of your home. May it be His will that you will be able to share good news soon regarding an improvement in the situation in all the matters mentioned above.

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita

3444

B"H, 18 Tammuz, 5715
Brooklyn

To the esteemed and distinguished Torah scholar, R' Naftali, may he live, Shochet and Bodek.

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letter of 4 Tammuz, in which you ask regarding:

1) The matter of a synagogue where fewer than ten are Shabbos observers, and the rest are not, G-d forbid.

When you passed by there on Shabbos morning, they asked you to enter and serve as the Shaliach Tzibbur for the first minyan, as they were in a hurry to get to work. Nevertheless, they wished to daven with a minyan, and a large portion of them recite Kaddish, etc.

The doubt is whether you should accede to their request and stand before the Amud.

From your description, it appears that they themselves did not wish to stand before the Amud, due to their own awareness that one who does not observe Shabbos should not do so. If you do not take it upon yourself to be the Shaliach Tzibbur, the minyan will be cancelled, and it is highly probable that a large portion of them will not daven at all.

If this is the case, I am not comfortable with a stance of zealotry that is entirely out of place, where one tells a person to commit a minor sin in order to save his fellow from a grave sin. Even though some say this applies only where one has no part in the other’s sin, this is not the case according to the standard of Chassidus*. In the present case, one should add—at least as a supporting factor:

a. The opinions that public desecration of Shabbos is only regarding certain melachos and in the presence of ten Jews, etc., as noted by the Acharonim on Shulchan Aruch, Yoreh Deah, Siman 2, Seif 6.

b. If you were not to fulfill their request, it would be considered by them as a rejection with both hands, etc., and a form of Chillul Hashem.

2) Whether to daven in a synagogue where one is not so certain about the character of those who stand before the Amud, but by entering there, you have the ability to improve matters regarding the order of davening and the learning.

It is understood that the answer to this depends on the nature of the deficiency in the Chazanim or the congregants. What we have seen in the vast majority of cases is that even if they do not daven there [regularly], but enter from time to time and participate in their learning—this is sufficient for them to accept suggestions and the like, when one explains to them the necessity and benefit of it. It is understood that according to the above, this must be done diplomatically, so they do not feel that you are davening by yourself or in a different place.

At a time of favor, I will mention all those you write about at the holy gravesite of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, and your son, Dovber, may he live, for a livelihood with peace of mind and fixed times for Torah study, as both these matters are required of every one of the Jewish people. May Hashem grant you merit, and may you succeed in bringing good tidings regarding all of the above.

I am certain you have fulfilled my request to convey at least some matters from the farbrengen to Anash, may they live, in your camp.

And thank you in advance.

With blessing,

**M. Schneerson**

## 3740

B"H, 18 Tammuz, 5715
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

After a long interval, your letter from Erev Shabbos Chazon was received. May it be the will of Hashem that by the time you receive this letter, your state of health will have improved significantly, until you return to your full strength—to your strength in the literal sense, as well as in its deeper meaning and all the interpretations found in the maamar *Maskil L'Eitan* by our Alter Rebbe, printed in the *Kunteres Limud HaChassidus*.

I was pleased to hear of your efforts to influence others—both adults and children—in drawing their hearts closer to our Father in Heaven, and also in the essentials: namely, in practical action and the *halachos* required for daily life, which certainly cause a change for the better in their conduct. It is understood, however, that this does not exempt you from attending to your own physical health and following the doctor’s instructions, for the Torah has granted the physician permission to heal. On the contrary, as the Alter Rebbe states in *Tanya*, Chapter 7, one must serve Hashem with one's body. This is also explained in the *Rambam*, *Hilchos Deios*, and in *Shulchan Aruch*, *Orach Chaim* 231—all based on the verse, "In all your ways, know Him."

Even if it is very difficult to arrange an entire day during the week to be **only** for matters of physical health, on the other hand, there is no need to go to extremes. You should arrange for times of rest even during the work week. Rest of this kind is preparation for more capable and active *avodah*, and therefore, it is itself *avodah* in its essence.

Regarding your general situation: while none of us knows the secret of the *birurim* and in which field a particular person is meant to act and work, based on simple logic—and relying on the words of our Sages that even a woman’s work, if performed by a man, is considered backbreaking labor when it is not his proper task, even if the work itself is easier—it remains a wonder to me why your work is in tending others' vineyards, and not in your own vineyard, which is the vineyard of Chabad...

It is understood that you are already connected to several matters in your current location, and my intention in the above is not that you should immediately change your place of work. It is merely an expression of wonder, and perhaps also a partial explanation as to why you do not feel so at home in your current work. After all is said and done, may it be the will of Hashem that since *avodah* requires the best of one's strengths, this will bring about a strengthening of your health in the physical sense, and also a strengthening of your health in the spiritual sense. The *nitzotzos* that you were meant to refine in another place will be brought to you by the Cause of all causes and the Prime Mover in your current location, and there you will refine them with tranquility and an expanded mind.

Enclosed is a booklet of the *hemshech* of the *maamar* published in connection with the days of redemption of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory—12 and 13 Tammuz, our redemption and the liberation of our souls. Surely you will be privileged to share this with the many, and the merit of the many will depend upon you.

With blessings.

## 3550

B"H, 18 Tammuz, 5715
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and distinguished, etc., R' Yitzchak Dovid, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

It has been some time since I have received any news from you, both regarding your personal affairs and your communal activities. May it be the will of Hashem that this is a sign that everything is in order and in peace.

You are surely aware of our custom in connection with the days of the redemption of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory—his liberation from his imprisonment for his work with mesiras nefesh to uphold the Torah and its mitzvos.

At the time, this was an exemplary victory over the forces opposing Hashem and His Torah, and for the years and generations that followed, it serves as a clear instruction: that the Torah governs reality, even when one cannot find a place for this within human logic.

It is customary to publish, especially for these days, a book or booklet on the theme of the day, containing matters of hisorerus regarding this.

Enclosed is the booklet published this year, a portion of the reshimus of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, regarding his imprisonment. Added to it are the words of the Nasi of Yisrael, based on the point that in matters of Torah and mitzvos, every single man and woman of Yisrael is a free person, and they have no master other than Hashem their G-d.

And if one is in need of a reminder and hisorerus regarding this—concerning exile among non-Jews and their decrees, where they have no choice and are merely like an axe in the hand of the one who hews with it—then all the more so is this hisorerus necessary regarding exile among Jews, who possess free choice. As it is written: "See, I have set before you today life and good... therefore choose life." And although the request of the Ribono shel Olam (which is also help and assistance) is "choose life," it is emphasized that just as the matter of "life" is stressed, so too is the requirement that it be "you shall choose."

With blessings for good tidings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

Secretary

**3550**

**R' Yitzchak Dovid:** Gartner.

**And if one is in need:** See also above, letter 3547.

## 3551

B"H, 20 Tammuz, 5715
Brooklyn

To the esteemed Rabbi and Chossid, G-d-fearing and learned, engaged in communal needs,
Rabbi Schneur Zalman, may he live,

Peace and blessing!

My letter for your birthday was surely received in due time.

Regarding the question that is surely being brought to you: how one should conduct themselves when, for some reason, a woman is afraid to conceive. Although several of the Hungarian responsa are stringent in this matter, in many cases—see there—the opinion of the Tzemach Tzedek in his responsa, Even HaEzer, siman 89, is different. He is lenient in several ways, even regarding the placement of a *moch* (a barrier) or similar methods prior to the *tashmish*, provided there is a doctor’s instruction to do so.

Since the primary concern here is to avoid the well-known sin, if the one being asked instructs [the couple] to practice abstinence, in the vast majority of cases—and in our generation, G-d forbid, it is even more likely—this leads to *shichas zera levatalah*, G-d forbid, which is the exact opposite of the intent of those who are stringent in this matter. Even if there were no other permitted path, one would have no choice; however, with the aforementioned responsa before our eyes, in my humble opinion, one should not be so stringent as to require the doctor to state explicitly that [pregnancy] constitutes an actual danger, etc. Especially in our weakened generation, abstinence leaves an impression on the nerves and on general health, both of the husband and of the wife.

If one were to explain to the doctor that they are not like the Egyptian midwives, and that even those who stumble into the sin of *shichas zera levatalah* subsequently regret it and fall into bitterness and, even more so, into depression, etc., etc.—and the final consequences of this are unknown—the doctor would surely express his opinion in more severe terms.

Therefore, it can be said that one who is lenient in giving instruction in this matter—despite the severity of the subject in and of itself, as explained in both the revealed Torah and in Chassidus—not only does not cause a loss to the one asking, since in any case the questioner would most likely have transgressed, but [he actually prevents] a different, worse situation (also because in the latter case there is no restraint or limitation from a second person, whereas with the placement of a *moch*, the matter is not dependent on him alone, and there are several non-pure days in the interim, etc.). Furthermore, he will actually be of benefit to their physical health and also to their spiritual health. For someone like you, the above will surely suffice.

With blessing.

## 3552

B"H, 20 Tammuz, 5715
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed and distinguished individual, a scion of noble ancestors, a man of fine character, etc.,
Rabbi Schneur Zalman, may he live,

Peace and blessing!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter dated the day upon which it was doubled in goodness (Tuesday). It was also a pleasure for me to receive regards from you via the esteemed and distinguished Chossid, who toils for the needs of the community, Rabbi Menachem Shmuel Dovid, may he live, HaLevi, the shaliach, who writes to me that he has visited you several times.

Regarding the content of your letter: your request concerning matters of a will is appropriate, as this is a segulah for long, good years. May Hashem lengthen your days and years in goodness and pleasantness. May you begin and succeed in spreading the wellsprings outward in your city now. Surely, the "outward" can be found there as well; the wellsprings and Torah in general are in every place and at every time. The matter lacks nothing but one who strives to spread them. The merit of your ancestors and the merit of the many who await this in your camp will assist you. May it be His will that this be accomplished in good health. Although it is possible that at the beginning you will need to accept the yoke in order to initiate the dissemination, once the beginning is past, you will see good fruit from your labor, and consequently, the desire and taanug in this will increase. The scholars have already said that the beginning of a matter (and this applies to the end and completion of a matter as well) is only the first point, and once one has passed this point, one is already in the middle.

With blessings to you and your wife, may she live, for a healthy and happy summer and for good tidings.

## 3353

B"H, 20 Tammuz, 5715
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed and distinguished individual, occupied with communal needs, Moreinu Harav Menachem Yisrael, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

After the longest of intervals, I have finally received your letter from Motzaei Shabbos, containing news regarding what is happening at the Yeshiva Achei Tmimim in Rishon LeTzion, as well as regarding the laying of the cornerstone. Regarding what you wrote about sending a shadar to South Africa for this purpose: There is currently a shadar from Tomchei Tmimim Lubavitch from here who is there, and he will certainly be spending a few more weeks there. I do not know if there is room for another shadar from a Lubavitch institution to arrive in close proximity to him, especially since the aforementioned individual is also speaking about the Lod Yeshiva, etc. Now, all of the above is to provide information on where the funds will come from, but regarding the actual outcome, we have seen tangibly since the beginning of Lubavitch activities that, in the end, the means were found and the matter was resolved—provided that those involved do not slacken their efforts and that their confidence and energy are not weakened. Fortunate is his portion that he participates in this, and may it be Hashem’s will that you increase your energy and efforts, and may Hashem add His blessing to the success of these matters.

With blessing.

## 355

B"H, 20 Tammuz, 5715
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter from the end of Sivan, in which you write regarding Mr. [Name]—may he live—who is involved in a legal dispute and promises that if he wins the case, he will improve his conduct regarding matters of Yiddishkeit.

Certainly, you can explain to him that this is not the proper approach: to first want the Ribono shel Olam to place trust in his promise and fulfill his request, and only afterwards to have the choice of whether or not to stand by his word. This is true even though every Jew possesses two souls—a nefesh elokis and a nefesh habahamis, a yetzer tov and a yetzer hara—which struggle within him. However, if he truly believes in the Ribono shel Olam, then everything is possible, and there is, chas v'shalom, no impediment to the matter. Even if, as a temporary measure, his request is granted in the aforementioned manner, he must know that he is obligated to conduct himself by observing the mitzvos as commanded in our Torah, the Torah of life. Then, it will be good for him and his family, both materially and spiritually.

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

Secretary

## 3757

By the Grace of Hashem
21 Tammuz, 5715
Brooklyn

Rabbi Sh. Y. Zevin
Shalom u’Bracha,

In response to your letter of the 15th of Tammuz.

Thank you for the good news that the surgery for your son, may he live, was successful. I will mention him before the Ribono shel Olam at the holy gravesite of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, for a complete and speedy recovery, and that things should go from good to even better.

It is surprising that you do not write about the content of the farbrengens of the *Yemei HaGeulah* (Days of Redemption), and in particular, regarding concrete resolutions. It is already known that the matter of *dvarim b’teilim* (idle talk) does not necessarily mean only when one speaks about trivial matters, but rather when speech—whose purpose and goal is to lead to action—remains in the realm of speech, and no impression is evident regarding *po’al mamash* (actual practice).

I acknowledge with thanks the receipt of the book *Sipurei Chassidim*. As is my way, and relying on our Sages’ teaching, "Do I not know that you speak well?" (i.e., that you are a scholar), I have included some notes in the margins. I ask your forgiveness for this.

I am certain you have received my letters in response to your previous ones, and I look forward to good news regarding what was written therein.

With respect and blessing,

**M. Schneerson**

P.S. **General Notes.**

1) In this confused generation of ours, the more one clarifies matters and adds precision, the more effective it is. Even if the necessity for this is not so apparent in the present moment, it is possible that in another place, or at the very least in the near future, the necessity will become clear. This also applies to a collection of stories about the *Nesi’ei Yisrael* (leaders of Israel) of all times and places. One should note—whether in the margins or at least at the end of the book—the source of each story, and most importantly, its authority. If this is true regarding all *Nesi’ei Yisrael*, it is all the more so regarding the leaders of the Chassidic movement, as inaccurate information—and sometimes fabricated matters with undesirable motives—has caused great damage to the dissemination of Chassidic teachings and the integration of its guidance and customs into wider circles. Since it appears from the final lines of the book, and generally from the two pages of source references, and knowing your love for order, that you have recorded the source of every story in your book, it would be worthwhile to at least print a list of sources for every story now—in a separate sheet—so that you might correct what was mentioned to a significant degree, if not entirely. And it would be even better if it were possible to append a few lines regarding the value of the authority of the various story collections and the various narrators—for as is known, there are two extremes here: those who are completely authoritative and those who are the opposite, with most falling between the two. It is understood that one can publish a collection of stories as mentioned even if the authority of the stories is unknown, since it at least reflects the spirit of the Chassidim or the subjects, as the saying goes: "If the story is not true, it could have been true." However, given your position among *Anash*, it is highly probable that people will rely on your stories as if you had checked them and found them reliable, especially when they are printed in a book; therefore, an explicit disclaimer is necessary.

2) Following the above: In general, there are Chassidic stories that arouse bewilderment, and the conclusion of some listeners is that surely such-and-such a person—about whom the story is told—acted against the law or at least against the standard of *lifnim mishuras hadin* (beyond the letter of the law). This also affects their entire attitude toward the bearers of Chassidic teachings and toward Chassidus itself, at a time when a small change in certain expressions in the story would remove all bewilderment. Since the vast majority of stories have passed through many channels, it is certain that the expressions are not entirely accurate, especially when translated from one language to another.

I will bring two examples:

a) **The story on page 309 and onwards.** It contradicts the entire concept of the *Maggidim*. Consequently, many come to the conclusion that those who used *Maggidim* and the like did not pay attention and did not want to take the trouble to be *ameilim* (toil) in Torah, etc.

I will admit the truth: I, too, was troubled by this matter for some time, until I heard a story from my father-in-law, the Rebbe, in the name of the *Tzemach Tzedek*, who said that in his youth, the *Alter Rebbe* wanted to give him knowledge of Torah as a gift. He answered in the style of the aforementioned story, that Torah must come through toil, and therefore he wanted to learn by himself and toil. But after some time, he regretted not having accepted the gift. There is a reason for this: he could have toiled and delved into the study of Torah even after he already knew what had been given to him as a gift, for "its measure is longer than the earth," and he would have had both: a broader knowledge and the toil of Torah.

b) **Story 313:** That the holy *Rabbi Meshullam Zusya* commanded to dig up the grave and search there, etc.—it is difficult to justify this instruction according to the *Shulchan Aruch*. However, with a small change—that the matter was not specifically in the grave, but in its vicinity or within its four cubits—all bewilderment is removed. Surely, in the transmission of all these stories, it was not specified that it was the grave itself, as the reader of the book will interpret.

By the way, it is mentioned in this story that this is explicitly stated in the *Yerushalmi*. I would be interested to know if you also know its location. Thank you in advance.

***

Regarding the funds that were set aside for the benefit of the eldest daughter of... may they live: In my opinion, it would be correct to place them in a secure *Gemach* fund for *Hachnasas Kallah* (wedding expenses) in the Holy Land, may it be rebuilt, or here, until she becomes engaged and needs them.

Are you working on the publication of the manuscripts of the late *Rabbi A. Y. Rivlin*?

Perhaps, of course, without this preventing the above, you could publish his book *Oholei Yosef*, which has been out of print for decades. Publication via photocopying can be done in a short time. It has just been ninety years since his passing. Surely you could append a list of the main chapters of his life, his parents, his descendants, the manuscripts in his estate, his travels to Lubavitch, etc.
