## 3751

B"H, 7 Menachem Av, 5715
Brooklyn

To the esteemed Rabbi and Chossid, G-d-fearing and learned, our teacher Rabbi Yosef Boruch, may he live:

Peace and blessing!

I received your letter dated Monday, 29 Tammuz, with pleasure. (Regarding a contradiction such as this between the beginning and the end of the letter, it is not a matter of deciding whether to rely on the first or the last word, for we see clearly that people are precise about the day of the week—especially a Rav in Yisrael, as it relates to the Torah reading, etc. And there is nothing that is not hinted at in the Torah. The parsha of the second day—according to the takanah of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, to study each day the corresponding portion of the week’s sedra, and on the second day, the second portion—speaks specifically of the role of a Rav and teacher in Yisrael, particularly regarding monetary laws, which require a higher level of *hemshech* than do matters of *issur v’heter* according to *nigleh*. This matter is explained according to Chassidus in the *kuntres* enclosed herewith.) It was a pleasure for me to read your interpretations and allusions regarding the booklet of the *Reshimas HaMaasar* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe. Surely you will continue to write in this vein in your future letters, for just as the advantage of light is from darkness, so too is the advantage of joy from sorrow. When a letter containing the "precepts of Hashem that gladden the heart" is received amidst several letters containing matters of sorrow, the advantage of the former is felt all the more.

Regarding what you wrote concerning the timing of the bringing of the Korban Pesach and its consumption as a single appointment: aside from the fact that the Korban Pesach unites them (and especially the Korban Pesach, whose essence is specifically the eating—unlike other sacrifices, where the eating is merely a detail; and in the language of the Mishnah (Pesachim 76b), and as Rashi explains there, "because it is so beloved to him, he was commanded to eat it"), it has already been discussed at length why it is specifically with Pesach that we find the opposite as well—that its slaughter and its consumption are counted as two distinct mitzvos, unlike other edible sacrifices (and in *Sefer Yereim*, Siman 405, it is implied that the reason is because they are **specifically** at divided times).

However, because of this, regarding *shelamim*, one could say that the two days and the night between them are also united by the *chivus* of *hekdesh*—and this is in addition to Pesach, where in any case, regarding *kodshim*, the night follows the day. I do not have the sefer *Otzros Yosef* with me, which you mention in this regard.

For a known reason, we have now printed the *maamar* "Tzion B'Mishpat Tipadeh" by the Alter Rebbe, with the annotations of the Tzemach Tzedek. It is enclosed here, and surely you will merit to share its contents with the many, and the merit of the many depends upon you.

With blessings for success,

**M. Schneerson**

## 3702

B"H, 7 Menachem Av, 5715
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter from Rosh Chodesh Menachem Av. May it be Hashem’s will that very soon the concept of "a merciful father, and specifically a Chassid" will be fulfilled. As is well known, my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, emphasized in the famous *Iggeres HaKodesh*, Epistle 22 (134b) in the *Tanya Kadisha*, that the title "father" is written in both ways. He noted that when he loves him and "seeks him out with discipline," the title "Chassid" is not used; however, when he acts as a defense attorney so that it will be specifically in a way of revealed and manifest good, he adds this title as well.

As you requested, I will mention you and all those you wrote of in your letter at the holy resting place of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, in accordance with the content of your letter. And surely, when you have good news to share, do not withhold the good from informing me.

Enclosed is the *Kuntres* of the *Maamar* by our *Rabbeinu HaZakein*, "Tzion B'Mishpat Tipadeh," with the annotations of the *Tzemach Tzedek*, which for a known reason has now been printed.

With blessings.

## 3703

B"H, 8 Menachem Av, 5715
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and diligent in communal affairs,
Rabbi Refael Nachman, may he live and be well, HaKohen

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letter from Erev Shabbos Chazon, in which you explain your long silence by saying that you have nothing to write about: the distress caused by such a situation is understandable. Although, to my great regret, this is the conduct of the majority of Anash in Eretz Yisrael—may it be rebuilt and established—it does not change the matter at all. At a time when, at every hour, it is possible—and sometimes even easy—to be active in general, and especially in Eretz Yisrael now, in spreading the wellsprings outward, in addition to strengthening Yiddishkeit in general, tens and perhaps even more of Anash—including Temimim who were privileged to have our holy Rebbes invest their energies in them so that they would be "lamps to illuminate"—are sitting with folded arms, "waiting" for an awakening from the outside. And when that awakening does come, it is like that which is brought in Likutei Torah regarding "giving birth to a female," and in the vast majority of cases, even this birth does not occur, as it is written: "Clouds and wind, but no rain."

It is certainly clear, even to the physical eye, that hundreds of yeshiva students and Bnei Yisrael in general are thirsty and yearning for someone to show them the truth, for they have already realized that the "other side"—or in common parlance, the *sitra achra* and all its affairs—has no substance and no existence.

Based on the above, it is understood that this is not merely a loss of profit or a private matter concerning a specific Tomim or a specific individual among Anash. Rather, the matter also concerns the energies of our Nasi, the head and intellect of the entire generation, which are not being utilized. It is akin to what is said, "A king is bound in the tresses"—and who are the kings? The Sages. I have already grown weary of repeating this again and again, since it seems my letters only produce a momentary sense of low spirits, more or less fleeting, after which things return to their previous state, as it is written, "For it is a stiff-necked people." May it be the will of Hashem that each of us utilizes this "stiff-neckedness" specifically in the side of holiness, and may the verse be fulfilled in us: "For it is a stiff-necked people, and You will forgive."

With blessings for health and good tidings,

P.S.
It is understood and simple that all of the above is directed not only to you, but to the vast majority of Anash, as mentioned above. You have permission to publicize this in an appropriate manner—provided that the conclusion is not omitted, for based on the presumption of the past, there is a concern that even regarding these words, the reaction will be as mentioned above—namely, a lack of action...

## 375

B"H, 8 Menachem Av, 5715
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Rabbi and Chossid, man of action and vigor, etc.,
Rabbi Chananya Yom Tov Lipa, shlita,

Greetings and blessings!

I was pleased to receive your letter from Monday, in which you write of your improved health. May it be the will of Hashem that you go from strength to strength, in accordance with the ruling of our Sages that "we elevate in matters of holiness." Indeed, it is said of every individual among the Jewish people that they are a "holy nation"—a term that applies to the neshamah and the body together. For these words were spoken in preparation for the giving of the Torah, and the Torah was not given to the ministering angels, nor to the neshamah as it exists on high. As our Sages said, "You descended to Egypt; the yetzer hara is within you." Furthermore, the ruling of the great teacher in his *Yad HaChazakah* (*Hilchos Deios*, beginning of Chapter 4) is well known: that maintaining a healthy and sound body is among the ways of Hashem.

— I have already noted elsewhere that, were I not afraid, it is clear that a word was omitted here (though I have not yet found it in previous printings). It should read: "is among the ways of **avodas** Hashem" (as is implied by his language there, preceding this), or "is among the ways of **yidias** Hashem" (as is implied by the conclusion of his language here).

Regarding your announcement that you are holding a *seudas hodaah* on the first day of the week of the parsha *Ekev tishmaun*—"And Hashem your G-d will keep for you the covenant and the kindness..."—I join with those who offer blessings that your **strength** (*chayil*) may grow in Torah, which is a "potion of life" when one studies it in purity and with *yiras shamayim*.

[This is achieved] with *dichilu* and *rechimu* (fear and love) that "ascend on high," as is proven in *Yoma* 72b: if one is *zocheh* (meritorious), it becomes a "potion of life." Rashi explains this to mean studying for its own sake and fulfilling it. It is explicitly stated in *Pesachim* 50b that study and action "for its own sake" is the mode of "greater than the heavens." The *Tikkunim* (*Tikkunei Zohar*, Tikkun 10—cited in *Tanya* in many places, including the end of Chapter 39 and in *Kuntres Acharon*) explain that it is specifically through *dichilu* and *rechimu* that it "ascends on high" to stand before Hashem.

The Gemara there concludes that if one is *zocheh* (and has refined oneself to study for its own sake), it brings one joy, as it is written: "The precepts of Hashem are upright, gladdening the heart." The end of that verse is "the fear of Hashem is pure"—the study of Torah in purity. See there.

And how does one attain *dichilu* and *rechimu*? This matter has already been addressed by our Rebbe, the author of the *Tanya*—the authority on the *nistar* (hidden) dimension of Torah—and the *Shulchan Aruch*—the authority on the *nigleh* (revealed) dimension of Torah. They establish that love is the root of all positive *mitzvos*, and the *mitzvah* of fear is included as well. We are commanded regarding the *mitzvah* of love, even though, on the face of it, how can the language of command and action apply to love, which is in the heart? Rather, "This is what I received from the Maggid of Mezeritch, and this is what he, of blessed memory, received from the Baal Shem Tov: that the *mitzvah* of 'And you shall love' means to fix one's thought and mind (in Yiddish, he said: *men zol zich arayn ton*) on the matters that awaken love," through studying the teachings of Chassidus, contemplating the greatness of Hashem, etc., as explained in the holy *Tanya* in many places.

It is a definitive ruling that every person is obligated in this at least three times a day. In the words of the students of R. Yitzchak, copied in the *Rema* (*Hilchos Tefillah*, beginning of Siman 98): "One should contemplate the exaltation of the Almighty before prayer," etc. This is also a paved path to be meticulous in a minor *mitzvah* just as in a major one, because when one studies and performs for its own sake, without any ulterior motives—not even for the reward of the World to Come, as cited in the *Rambam* (end of *Hilchos Teshuvah*)—but solely with the intention to fulfill the will of one's Creator, one becomes meticulous even in matters that a person "treads under his heel." This is because it is impossible for him to be separated, G-d forbid, even for a moment from His unity and oneness. "In absolute truth, even with a minor transgression, the one who commits it violates the supreme will of Hashem, and is in a state of total separation from His unity and oneness to a greater degree," etc.—as explained thoroughly in *Tanya*, Chapter 24 (and regarding the aspect of the blemish and the punishment, and in a positive sense—regarding the reward, there is a difference; see there). See also *Zohar*, *Miketz* 197, beginning of side a, and *Tanchuma*, beginning of Parshas *Ekev*.

May it be the will of Hashem that through the effort in all that is mentioned above—and all the more so in guarding against the "sin of the heel," and according to the language of our Sages (*Sanhedrin* 108b), "the heels of your feet" (see Rashi there, that this is the well-known sin that brings about the length of the exile)—we will see fulfilled speedily in our days the end of the verse in our parsha: *Ve'ahavcha*—(with a *patach*, not *ve'ahavcha* with a *kamatz*), meaning the *siyata d'shmaya* (heavenly assistance) that He will make you a lover of Hashem—"and He will bless you and multiply you," etc., "upon the land which He swore to your fathers to give you," through Moshiach Tzidkeinu speedily in our days.

With blessings.

## 3756

B"H, 10 Menachem Av, 5715
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter from 1 Va'eschanan: Thank you for the good news regarding what you have managed to accomplish in matters of practical mitzvos. This will surely inspire you with renewed courage—all the more so, and *kal v'chomer*: if the efforts made until now yielded results, how much more so will they succeed when you exert all the necessary effort. There is no need to elaborate on such an obvious matter.

Regarding what you wrote—that you derive no satisfaction from your avodah, that it is difficult, etc.: It is contrary to reason that there are those who have convinced themselves that one must not show a smiling face or satisfaction with the way the Ribono shel Olam conducts the world in general and their own affairs in particular. They fear that this might be interpreted as being content with what they have, and since things can always be better, they feel they must constantly complain about the difficulty and express bitterness at every step.

It is understood that this is the opposite of the instruction of our holy Torah, and *kal v'chomer* contrary to the words of our Sages on the verse, "Let every soul praise Hashem" (Tehillim 150:6)—that for every single breath, one must offer praise. How much more so when one achieves success in the avodah of "gathering physicality and sowing spirituality." Furthermore, the holy Zohar rules that when one shows a sad face, one draws down, *chas v'shalom*, a similar response from Above regarding the flow of Divine influence. Conversely, when a person remains in a state of joy and satisfaction regardless of their situation, that very attitude improves the situation and leads from good to even better (see Zohar Vol. III, 184b).

I do not wish to elaborate, as I doubt this will change your established habit (though I hope it has not yet become second nature to you). In any event, these lines are sufficient to clarify the situation as it truly is. May the Ribono shel Olam grant you the merit to see your good fortune in having been placed in a position of light, and you must offer thanks and praise for having succeeded in "gathering physicality and sowing spirituality" through the efforts made until now, and all the more so through the efforts to be made in the manner described above...

With blessings.

## 3,199

B”H, 12 Menachem Av, 5715
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter from 1 Va’eschanan: It is surprising that apparently, during all the time you have been there, you have not found an intermediary who is an expert in the field of *shidduchim*. Furthermore, it seems from your letter that you are overly particular about trivial matters, and even about matters that are trivial to the trivial, at a time when it is already known from our Sages, "Descend a step and take a wife," and especially since it has already been said, "The daughters of Israel are beautiful, but..." May Hashem guide you on the correct path to focus on the essence and the core, and as a result, you will not exaggerate the importance of external matters, and may He bring your suitable *zivug* before you, in both *gashmius* and *ruchnius* alike.

Regarding your doubt concerning an action (such as *hekdesh*, *hachanah*, and the like) performed in error—whether the error merely negates the action, or whether it also creates an effect opposite to the intended action, and you conclude that it is the latter—this is extremely puzzling and absurd to suggest. For how is it possible that his statement that he is preparing something should cause the designation of an object **that otherwise would not** have been *muktzah*? And as for the proof you brought from the *Baal HaMaor* at the beginning of *Beitzah* regarding *hachanah* in error—the discussion there concerns lean [animals]; lean animals are not fit for eating, and it is not the error that makes them *muktzah*.

With blessings,

## 3710

B"H, 13 Menachem Av, 5715
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed and distinguished individual, whose work is the work of Heaven,
R' Ze'ev Tzvi, may he live and be well,

Peace and blessing!

I acknowledge receipt of your letter from the 2nd of Menachem Av. May Hashem grant you the merit and success to increase your studies, particularly in the study of Chassidus, with health and peace of mind—for the "Tree of Life" is where there are no difficulties, etc.—and may He nullify any matters that distract you from the acceptance of the yoke of Torah and the yoke of mitzvos.

Regarding what you wrote concerning the giving of tzedakah before davening and its precise timing: The source cited in Shulchan Aruch, at the end of Siman 92, and mentioned in the introduction to the Alter Rebbe’s Siddur, is based on the statement of our Sages, "One should give a coin to a pauper and then pray" (Bava Basra 10a). The word "then" (v'hadar) proves that this is done before beginning the davening, which generally refers to the Shemoneh Esrei. This is also indicated by the fact that this law is codified in Shulchan Aruch Orach Chayim between the laws of Krias Shema and Shemoneh Esrei. However, in the writings of the Arizal (and similarly in Pri Etz Chayim, Shaar Zayin, Chapter 5), it is written that this tzedakah is given during "Vayevarech Dovid," at the recitation of "Moshel B'kol." This is also explained in the Pri Megadim.

It is possible to suggest—based on the revealed dimension of Torah—that the giving was placed before "Yishtabach" so as not to interrupt the davening from the moment the Chazzan descends before the bimah, which begins at "Yishtabach" (Tur Shulchan Aruch, beginning of Siman 53).

Since nowadays they descend before the bimah even earlier, and it would be strange to interrupt in the interim—and it is also possible to argue that it might appear as arrogance (yohara)—one can justify the fact that the vast majority of people are accustomed to giving tzedakah before beginning the entire davening.

It is understood that giving tzedakah after Shemoneh Esrei is a separate matter, and is not the same concept as giving tzedakah before davening, which is based on the aforementioned statement of our Sages—even though several of the Acharonim mention both customs in the same breath.

Regarding your question concerning the change in the Alter Rebbe’s ruling in his Shulchan Aruch regarding whether the recitation of "Parshas HaKorbanos" must be done while standing—this has already been noted by Rabbi Naeh in his sefer *Pesukei HaSiddur*. It is not a difficulty, as there are several changes in the second edition of the Shulchan Aruch (compared to the first edition), and in the introduction to *Shaar HaKollel*, it is written that in the second edition, he leans more toward the Kabbalists. This is the case here as well. See the various opinions on this in the *Nitzotzei Zahav* on Shulchan Aruch Orach Chayim, Siman 48.

With blessing,

## 3711

B"H, 13 Menachem Av, 5715
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and distinguished directors of the youth group
at the Chabad Beis Medrash in the Meah Shearim neighborhood,
may they live.

Peace and blessing!

In response to your question regarding the fact that in your group there are two types of youth: those from strictly Chareidi families, who only require advancement in Torah and mitzvos, and those from families that are not Chareidi at all, who require education in the conduct of observing mitzvos and in the study of Torah. It is understood that it is difficult to combine these two types together, and you also foresee difficulties if you organize them into separate groups.

It is understood that one must not forgo either of these groups, for even one soul of Yisrael is an entire world, and certainly a group; and one does not know which of them will be refined. According to the promise of our holy Nasi, both will certainly be refined, in accordance with the ruling of the Heavenly Beis Din that because of this mesiras nefesh for Toras HaChassidus, in every matter of Torah, yiras shamayim, and good character traits, the hand of those who are connected to him and follow in his footsteps will be uppermost. My hope and confidence is that you will strive to overcome the difficulties and increase the quantity—that is, the number of both groups—and engage in guiding them on the path that ascends to the House of G-d with the necessary vigor. May Hashem grant you success and may you see good fruit from your labor, and may it be His will that this happens soon.

Since it is possible that this question may arise in other places where Tzeirei Agudas Chabad is involved in matters of education, I request that you convey my perspective mentioned above to the administration of Tzeirei Agudas Chabad, and they will disseminate it to the places facing this situation.

With blessings for success in your holy work.

## 3713

B"H, 14 Menachem Av, 5715
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

I am in receipt of your letter from 3 Menachem Av, along with the enclosed note, which will be read at an auspicious time at the holy resting place of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory. I have also enclosed your responsa, as you requested.

Regarding the matter at hand, we have no instruction other than that of the Tzemach Tzedek in his responsa, Even HaEzer, end of section 9 (Part I), where he is lenient in such cases since it concerns health. This is especially true in your specific situation, as you write that the doctors are of the opinion that every time she conceives, she is in danger. This ruling can be further justified, particularly in our generation—this orphaned generation—because even those who are stringent do so because of the gravity of the sin of *shichsas zera levatalah*. However, being stringent in a case like this leads, in the vast majority of cases, to abstinence for longer or shorter periods of time, which consequently causes *shichsas zera levatalah*, Heaven forbid. And, unfortunately, this occurs more frequently than it would through the use of a *moch*, since in that case the matter depends on two people, and the days of *hefsek taharah* in between do not make a difference, etc. Ultimately, through these stringencies, one causes the **opposite** of the intended goal, and the wise will understand. Even though it is a matter of debate whether this should be publicized to the masses—so that the immodest do not learn from the modest, nor the weak from the healthy—one must certainly rule in accordance with the opinion of the Tzemach Tzedek.

With blessings.

P.S.
Enclosed is the *kuntres* "Tzion B'mishpat Tipadeh" which I have published. Surely you will merit to share its contents with the many, and the merit of the many will depend upon you.

Regarding the opinions on the law of using a *moch*—aside from the books mentioned in the responsa of the Tzemach Tzedek there—see *Sdei Chemed*, *Asifat Dinim*, *Ma'arechet Ishut* 1, 32. And in *Pe'at HaSadeh* there, *Ma'arechet Ishut*, subsection 1 (where they ruled—**in practice**—to permit it).

Regarding what you brought from the responsa of the Maharsham, Part I, section 58, that one should not engage in marital relations close to her *tevilah* or close to her *veset* because that is when most women conceive, unlike at other times, and based on what is written in *Shulchan Aruch*, Orach Chaim, section 506—I do not have the aforementioned responsa before me to examine the inside text. However, with all due respect, such a novel restriction is highly puzzling, as not a single one of the *Rishonim* or *Acharonim* has ever suggested such a limitation. In my humble opinion, as stated above, a stringency in this case is to be feared, as it will likely cause the very opposite of the intended goal. We should not add stringencies of our own accord to the rulings of those from whose waters we drink, etc. One might note the teaching in *Eruvin* (63b), "Whoever is [too] humble..."

Regarding your note on the gravity of the sin and its rectification—see *Tanya*, end of chapter 20, and *Iggeret HaTeshuvah*, chapters 3 and 9.

## 3415

B"H, 14 Menachem Av, 5715
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 7 Menachem Av, along with the enclosure, which is a response to my proposal to you...

Since the number of those who possess the oral traditions—who know the matters as they occurred in person—has diminished, especially regarding Chassidus, Chassidim, and their Nesi'im, and given that very few recorded these events and matters at the time they occurred, and even more so regarding matters passed down through family tradition—a significant portion of which were unknown even to the Chassidim, except for those closest to them—

It is my opinion that it is the sacred duty, as well as a privilege, for all members of the family who retain in their memory sayings, events, etc., from this entire period, to record them with the greatest possible precision, without embellishment or artifice.

...Regarding the denunciation in Starodub, I do not have material on this at hand, although it is possible that it exists among the writings of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, in the portion that has not yet been organized. I only recall that my father-in-law, the Rebbe, once related that in his youth he knew Rabbi Neimark from the city of Starodub, who sat in prison after taking the blame upon himself. He said a poignant word about this: *Zeyne a sho...* [His hour...]. My father-in-law, the Rebbe, explained to me that he meant that a single hour of confusion for the Rebbe Maharash was so precious to him that he took the blame upon himself...

With respect and blessings.

***

**The denunciation in Starodub:** See Igros Kodesh of the Rebbe Maharash, letter 19, and at length in the book *Kocha Shel Sanegoria* by Fishel Schneersohn.

**Rabbi Neimark:** Chaim Meshulam Zalman, Rav of Starodub, Vitebsk, and Nevel.

## 3716

B"H, 14 Menachem Av, 5715
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

...Regarding those teachers whose dedication is not at all as it should be, who are also unsuited for teaching, in whom no progress is seen in their methods of avodah, etc., and who do not accept guidance:

It is surprising that there is even any doubt about this. The main point is the last factor—for who knows what a day may bring? The recognition that the entire body of teachers must stand firm on the point that the schools—and primarily the spirit and chinuch within them—belong to Chabad, and are not subject to any other authority. Since this feeling must exist **throughout** the entire school year, i.e., for about ten months, it is understood that this cannot be maintained through mere kabalas ol and coercion alone. Therefore, for those to whom this matter is foreign and who do not wish in any way to accept guidance (and it is impossible that this will not also impact their day-to-day influence on the students), it is better that they find a position in a place that suits their own spirit, and the Reshet schools will find teachers suited to the spirit of the Reshet...

It is understood that all of the above is a general directive regarding the method by which the Reshet administration should conduct itself, but this is not a directive regarding specific individuals; that is for the administration to decide, knowing their nature and conduct in the past. It is worth adding that the students are the many, and the teachers are the few, and a **doubt** regarding harm to the many overrides the benefit to the few—especially in light of the above, that there is still time now for the individual to arrange himself in a place more suitable for him.

It is surprising that you do not mention the "provisions for the road" that were given to the students for the vacation days. Surely you will fill this in at the next opportunity. Likewise, regarding the professional development of the teachers during these weeks, which relates to the upcoming school year—it is also worthwhile that you indicate to them general points and guidelines regarding the subject in which further development is most needed.

With blessings for success in all the above and for good tidings.

## 3717

3717

B"H, 16 Menachem Av, 5715
Brooklyn.

The Administration of the Oholei Yosef Yitzchok Lubavitch Schools

Surely, you should arrange this with effort well in advance so that there will be no delays in this regard from the various offices...

In the hope of receiving a detailed letter soon, with thanks and blessing.

## 3118

B"H, 16 Menachem Av, 5715
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed and distinguished individual, who engages in communal needs, Rabbi Yosef Halevi 
May he live and be well,

Greetings and blessings!

...It would be worthwhile, despite what you write in your letter, to visit the city of Elizabethville, since one does not travel to Africa every month or even every year. If it was worthwhile for the Rebbe Maharash to travel specifically from Marienbad to Paris for the sake of a single soul—as the story regarding this is well-known—even though he valued every moment and hour of his time, then how much more so does this apply to each one of us. This is especially true when it concerns several souls, and particularly when there is also a material gathering involved.

Although it is obvious that we do not possess the strengths and the certainty that the Rebbe Maharash had in his travels, one must pray for *siyata d'shmaya* (Heavenly assistance), without looking at one’s own qualifications and by minimizing one’s own reality. For then, one comes closer and closer to being an emissary of the Higher One, "like Him," so to speak. All of this is explained in *Likutei Torah* at the beginning of *Parshas Vayikra*, and as explained in the works of the *Acharonim* regarding the concept of *shlichus* (agency). There are several aspects to this: whether the act merely brings out the intent of the sender, whether the act becomes the act of the sender, or whether the emissary himself becomes the sender, etc. (This is along the lines of what is explained regarding the virtue of a simple servant in *Hemshech 5666* and in many other places).

With blessings for success and for good news regarding all of the above.

***

 Rabbi Yosef Weinberg. Additional letters to him: see above, 3058, and the references in the notes there.

 As the story is well-known: *Sefer HaSichos 5705*, p. 30.

 Regarding the concept of *shlichus*: see also above, Vol. 4, letter 890.

## 3719

B"H, 16 Menachem Av, 5715
Brooklyn

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and learned, engaged in communal needs, R' Yechiel 
Shlita

Shalom u’Bracha,

Following the long hiatus, I received your letter dated 12 Menachem Av (from which the reason for your silence is also not understood).

I was pleased to read therein about the shiur you are giving to classes and individuals in the inner dimension of Torah, the *Ilana D’Chayei*. May it be Hashem’s will that the ruling of our Sages, "I have learned more from my students than from all of them," be fulfilled in you as well. This is especially true regarding the study of the inner dimension of Torah, which is dependent to a greater degree than the study of the revealed Torah upon *siyata d’shmaya*, and engaging with others in *hafotzas hamaayanos* draws down this assistance in even greater measure.

Regarding what you write concerning a curriculum: it is understood that not all classes and not all individuals are the same, as this depends primarily on the nature of the recipient. In general, with yeshiva students, one should take an interest in what pertains to the study of *Kuntres Eitz Chaim*; for those accustomed to *mussar*, *Kuntres U’Maayan*; and for those accustomed to *chakirah*, *Shaar HaYichud VeHaEmunah* in *Tanya*, the *mitzvah* of *Emunas Elokus* in *Derech Mitzvotecha*, etc. It is understood that during special times of the year, there is a place to study *maamarim* that are relevant to that time, such as now, with the *drushim* for Elul and Rosh Hashanah, etc. In any case, one of the primary points in a study session such as this—where the time you have with them is limited—is that it must be conducted in a manner that awakens the appetite and desire in the recipient to continue this study on their own, or at the very least, to review what was learned with you and to expand upon the explanation.

It is surely unnecessary to urge you that from time to time, it is worthwhile to speak with the recipient about *Chassidus*, as there are matters explained as necessary in *Sefer HaSichos*, *Likkutei Dibburim*, etc. From this, one should conclude the conversation with them regarding *avodah* in practice, such as *hisbonenus* before *davening* on the subjects being studied, observing *tevilas Ezra* at the very least, reciting *Tehillim*, etc., and conducting oneself in the ways of *Chassidus*.

***

 **R' Yechiel:** Blumenfeld. Another letter to him appears above, 3722.

## 3720

B"H, 16 Menachem Av, 5715
Brooklyn

To the G-d-fearing, learned, and distinguished individual, occupied with communal needs, R' Moshe, may he live:

Shalom and blessings!

I was pleased to receive regards from you via the distinguished, learned, and G-d-fearing individual, occupied with communal needs, R' Mordechai Dov, may he live, the shaliach Talishevsky. Although he did not write details regarding your situation, I wish to remind you of the established principle that a Jewish person must be healthy so that the body does not distract from the service of the soul. Furthermore, as required by the teachings of Chassidus, one must be able to serve Hashem with one's body in its entirety, for which the body must be whole—as is understood from the beginning of Chapter 7 of Tanya, and see also Rambam, Hilchos De'os, beginning of Chapter 4.

It is surely unnecessary to urge you to assist Rabbi Talishevsky in his work to support the Tomchei Temimim yeshivos. For our Sages have already said, "Throw a stick into the air, and it will land on its base"—surely the days of light you witnessed while in the Tomchei Temimim yeshiva in Lubavitch in the past still shine within you, as do the words of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, regarding the students of Tomchei Temimim being "candles to illuminate"—meaning, to also influence others and one's surroundings. I only mention this as a prompt and an encouragement to assist the aforementioned with even greater effort, especially since this is the demand of the hour. And if regarding the act of tzedakah in general it is said that not only does it not diminish, but on the contrary, it adds to one's previous state—"give tithes so that you may become wealthy"—how much more so when the matter concerns tzedakah in the field of education, where we are raising the younger generation to be fruits and fruits of fruits that are in accordance with the instruction of our Torah, the Torah of life.

Enclosed is the continuation of the maamar of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, which you will surely merit to share with the many, and the merit of the many depends upon you.

With blessings.

## 3721

B"H, 17 Menachem Av, 5715
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Rabbi and Chassid, who is involved in communal affairs,
Rabbi Mordechai [Hakohen], may he live,

Peace and blessing!

I received your letter from Motzaei Shabbos. Regarding what you wrote about seedlings and seeds, and your inclination specifically toward seedlings—since it is permitted *ab initio* to plant a branch from a grafted tree—the authorities have already discussed this at length in the Shulchan Aruch, Yoreh Deah, end of section 295, regarding whether a grafted tree is subject to the prohibition of maintaining or planting. However, this provides no proof whatsoever as to which **species** it is considered. The concern is that the grafted tree is not an esrog, or is a deficient esrog; if so, what help is the ruling that there is no prohibition in the planting itself? Furthermore, even according to your view, it is impossible that from one tree, the fruits produced from its seedlings would be kosher, while those produced from its seeds would not be kosher—is that logical? And the main point is that, **on the contrary**, the fruit is more lenient than the branch (Chullin 115a), and this is not the place to elaborate.

In general, it is not understood what the responsibility is if they also take the seeds, since there is certainly no extra effort involved in that. Especially since, in all the above, my intention was regarding those trees that—as one mentions incidentally—are still known not to have been grafted, in addition to their external appearance, etc. And since the Calabria [esrog] has been established up until the generation before ours as being non-grafted, one must maintain it on this presumption—in addition to the aforementioned proof—as a supporting factor.

I received the article regarding Pesach in its [Italian] translation. There are a few points to note: a) It seems that the publication in which it was printed is intended for communal activists and the like—that is, for a limited circle—as is apparent from the articles preceding and following it. There is room to say that the youth are not interested in this at all. If there is no other publication read by our brethren in Italy, then necessity dictates otherwise; but if there is such a newspaper, it is worth the effort to have matters of Chassidus printed in it as well. And certainly, if the other publication is printed in [...] etc., not in our camp, one must find connections with the editors of the publication through the people [...].

The language of the translation seems heavy to me, or perhaps even difficult, to the point that it would not draw the reader to want to read the article to its end, and certainly not to read it a second time. It is obvious that this is not at all the style of articles for youth and young people.

Although the content of the article is appropriate for the season and contains words of inspiration, since it is so difficult to get articles printed, one must utilize this opportunity for matters that cannot be "done by others"—that is, as mentioned above, taken from the teachings of Chassidus and Chassidic articles. The content of this article is suitable for books of *mussar* and *drush*, not necessarily Chassidic, but general. Surely you have at your disposal *Likutei Sichos*—from the *sichos* of the Pesach holiday, and especially now, regarding the matters of Tishrei, and also regarding Simchas Torah, etc., which contain accessible articles with stories of Tzaddikim and lessons in *mussar*...

I believe I have already drawn your attention to the fact that regarding a woman, one should not write "248 limbs," as is understood from the *sugya* in Bechoros 45a. Likewise, one should not write "252 limbs," as there is a dispute regarding this; see there. Therefore, the phrasing is "all her limbs." It is understood that if someone is not particular about this, we are not particular with them, and all is peace.

Just now, the community bulletin, issue 11, two copies, was received. Many thanks.

3722

B"H, 19 Menachem Av, 5715
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter—which lacks the date of writing—it is surprising that you also fail to mention in this letter, and even more so that you lack details regarding, your consistency in setting times for the study of Chassidus, the "Tree of Life"—as the *Ra'aya Mehemna* terms it—and in following its guidance and customs. Surely you are doing so to the best of your ability, for it is obvious that the purpose of informing another is not for the sake of the report itself (though that, too, is a mitzvah, for causing joy to a fellow Jew is one of the foundations of the mitzvah of *ahavas Yisrael*, which is a great principle in the Torah). Rather, when one informs someone else about good conduct, it is easier to strengthen oneself in it and maintain it. Conversely, when no one knows, the *yetzer hara* finds many more pretexts for how to weaken the observance of that conduct, and subsequently attempts to abolish it entirely. This is something we see clearly.

Regarding what you write, that there are those who insist on conduct in the manner previously accepted, and who consider any deviation to be a departure from the truth:

This is astonishing, even as a premise for such an approach. For one of the things revealed to Moshe at Sinai is that everything a veteran student will ever **innovate** was already told to Moshe at Sinai. It is understood, of course, that this innovation must be in accordance with the principles of our holy Torah, which is eternal and unchanging. However, one who says that he accepts the views of the *Rishonim* and the early *Acharonim* but refuses to accept the guidance of the *Nasi* of our generation—it is understood from the ruling of our Torah in the *Nigleh*—*Choshen Mishpat*, beginning of section 25*—that he is like one who errs in a matter of *Mishnah* during the time of the *Amora'im*. See there for the practical legal implications. If, G-d forbid, the aforementioned approach were accepted, they would not even allow the study of *Mussar* in the yeshivos. As is well known, the opposition to that study some eighty years ago was **extremely** fierce, coming from the overwhelming majority of yeshiva leaders, and with far greater intensity than the opposition regarding the study of Chassidus. You should read carefully the introduction of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, to the *Kunteres Eitz Chaim*. Based on the principle of the Torah that "the deed of the master is a sign," and as is also brought in that introduction regarding the wonders that the *Chaim* (the Rebbe) demonstrated, we have seen in our own days that among those who were under the Soviet regime, of all the yeshiva students—to our great sorrow—the only ones who stood the test throughout all the decades they were there were those young men who studied Chassidus. They were not those who sufficed with the study of the *Nigleh* of the Torah alone, nor even those who studied *Mussar*. Based on the tens and hundreds of witnesses who were there—a large portion of whom are now in the Holy Land, may it be rebuilt and established—the matter is confirmed, and "that which is well-known requires no proof."

Cease the hair-splitting and debate regarding the study of *Da"Ch* (*Divrei Elokim Chaim*—Words of the Living G-d). For every moment that passes is a loss, and a loss that cannot be reclaimed. At the same time, as our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe writes in the holy *Tanya*, end of chapter 25, one could have been standing in such a state of *yichud* that is eternal forever and ever, yet he wastes time on hair-splitting to refute the arguments of those who wish to deprive him of his portion in Torah. This is not only in the *Pardes* of the Torah**, but also in the *Pnimiyus* of the Torah, the "hidden" part of the Torah that connects the hidden part of the soul to the hidden part of *Hashem*, as stated in the *Zohar*, Vol. 3, 221a. How great is the darkness, the concealment, and the hiddenness! The reasons for the opposition during the time of the Baal Shem Tov to the study of his teachings were public and printed***, and the books still exist today. The arguments are explicit—that they suspected it would lead to leniency in the observance of *mitzvos*, and even more than mere leniency, etc. (I do not wish to elaborate on the arguments that existed—which even then had no basis). Yet, throughout the two hundred years since, we hear and see at every step that those who followed in the footsteps of his students and his students' students are the ones who are meticulous in *mitzvos*, even in the slightest detail of the words of the Scribes, and they strive to bring all the children of Israel to this *avodah* with joy, unlike others, etc.

With the blessing that immediately upon receiving this letter, you will increase your study beyond what it has been until now in all the above, and you will pay no attention to all the doubts that someone wishes to bring into your four cubits from the outside. As is explained in the *sefarim*, the word *safek* (doubt) has the same *gematria* as *Amalek*, and *Amalek* wars against all the children of Israel (who are on the path, even when they have already left Egypt), and "the war of *Hashem* against *Amalek* is from generation to generation," even in the generation of *Mashiach*, as is stated in *Targum Yonasan*.

In the name of the Rebbe, Shlita,
Secretary

## 3723

B"H, 19 Menachem Av, 5715
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 8 Menachem Av, in which you write regarding the doctor’s advice concerning your health: It is already well-known that our Torah grants permission to the physician to heal, and therefore, one must follow his instructions.

Regarding what you write once again about sadness: You should consult with the *avreichim* of Tzeirei Agudas Chabad. This is in addition to the fact that you surely have a daily, fixed time for studying *Chassidus*, which adds flavor to the ruling of our holy Torah, "Serve Hashem with joy" (see also Rambam, end of *Hilchos Lulav*). The aforementioned young men will assist you so that, ultimately, you too will stand in a place of light and joy. It is understood that the sooner this is done, the better, especially since the month of accounting for the past year is the month of mercy, the month of Elul, in which one must rectify the eleven months that have passed.

As for your question regarding the distinction between *hashgacha pratis* (divine providence) and *hashgacha klalis* (general providence), this is explained at length in many places, including *Moreh Nevuchim*, *Shomer Emunim*, etc. As a *ben yeshiva*, you will find this in the books standard to *yeshiva* study, such as *Sefer HaChinuch*, Mitzvah 169. However, subsequently, a bright light and innovation was revealed by the *talmid vasik*—as if stated to Moshe at Sinai—regarding the absolute reality of *hashgacha pratis* specifically. The proof from *Chullin* (63a) is well-known, and there is no need to elaborate here.

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,
Secretary

P.S. Regarding what you wrote about your new insights in your studies at the beginning of *Maseches Chagigah*, concerning the reasoning of Rashi and Tosafos, as well as the dispute between the *Bavli* and the *Yerushalmi*, etc.:

You should examine all of this in *Turei Even* on the spot, *Minchas Chinuch*, Mitzvah 430, and in the *Hagahos Maayan HaChochmah*, *Meleches Shlomo* on the *Mishnayos*, and elsewhere. It is explained **well** at length in the commentary of the *Ri"f* Perla to the *Sefer HaMitzvos* of the *Rasag*, Mitzvah Aseh 46. There is a great innovation there, namely, that some say that what is included in the count of the *mitzvos* is specifically the *re'iyas korban* (the appearance of the offering) and not the *re'iyas panim* (the appearance of one's face).

## 3424

B"H, 19 Menachem Av, 5715
Brooklyn.

To the avreich Yitzchak Yehuda, may he live,

Shalom u’Bracha!

In response to your letter of 12 Menachem Av, in which you write that you are studying at the Tomchei Temimim Yeshiva in Lod, and that your Bar Mitzvah will take place on the eve of the upcoming Yom Kippur, and that you have begun to lay tefillin.

May it be Hashem’s will that this be at a good and auspicious time. You should ask your Rosh Yeshiva and your Maggid Shiur to teach you, with the necessary emphasis, the beginning of Chapter 41 in the Tanya Kadisha, regarding what is stated there concerning tefillin. For just as those who begin laying tefillin physically as a preparation for the time they become obligated according to Shulchan Aruch, so too is the law regarding preparation in spirituality. May Hashem grant you success.

It is worthwhile that, without a vow, from today until your Bar Mitzvah, you set aside a few coins for tzedakah every weekday before davening, and that you recite Psalm 13 after davening, in addition to the daily portion of Tehillim as divided by the days of the month. May Hashem grant you success in this as well.

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

Secretary

## 3705

B"H, 19 Menachem Av, 5715
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

...Regarding what you wrote, that your son’s birthday falls on Erev Yom Kippur, and when to hold the celebration:

It is understood that one should make a beginning on the day itself, especially during the first half of the day. As brought down in the sicha of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, it is customary to conduct oneself then as on a Yom Tov—not only regarding eating and drinking, but also with a cheerful countenance. One should conclude it on Motzaei Yom Kippur, which is an *eis ratzon* (a time of favor), according to the accepted custom to say "Gut Yom Tov" then. May Hashem grant that it be a *chassidishe farbrengen*, and may the Bar Mitzvah boy grow up to be a *yirei shamayim*, a *chossid*, and a *lamdan*...

With blessings.

## 3726

B"H, 19 Menachem Av, 5715
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter of 15 Menachem Av, in which you write that you wish to correspond regarding matters concerning our religious brethren in general, and the Chabad institutions, Anash, and the Temimim—may they live—in particular, but you are requesting my consent.

It is understood that there is no need for consent for this. As is well known, the ruling of our holy Torah, the Torah of life, is that anyone who has the ability to be of assistance in any matter of Torah and mitzvos has a holy obligation and privilege to do so, for all of Israel are responsible for one another. Bringing about benefit is possible in many ways, among them what is said, "In the multitude of counselors there is salvation," which is a great principle in a person's conduct...

It is surprising that you do not mention anything regarding your shiurim in the revealed Torah, your shiurim in Chassidus, or your involvement in the vineyard of Chabad. For this is the whole of man, as it is written, "Fear G-d and keep His commandments, etc." It is for this that our holy Rebbes sacrificed themselves—to plant this within the Chassidim and those connected to them, so that through them this conduct would reach all of Israel. This is especially so since you write that you were a student in Tomchei Temimim. It is a well-known saying of our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe that a *lamdan* does not mean that there was a time when he studied, etc. The same applies to the title of Chassid; it does not mean that there was a time when he was a Chassid, and that he has no dedication other than to his place and his time.

Surely you are aware of the three daily shiurim for every soul, established by my father-in-law, the Rebbe—in Chumash, Tehillim, and Tanya—which are well known. In any event, you should observe them from now on.

With blessings.

#### ***3726***

**Lamdan:** See also above, Vol. 7, Letter 1929.

## 3726

With blessings for good news regarding all of the above.

## 3727

3727

B"H, 22 Menachem Av, 5715
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

I acknowledge receipt of your *pidyon nefesh*. It is surprising that even regarding this, one must be prompted several times. When submitting a *pidyon nefesh*, it is far more relevant to report on *tzedakah* in spiritual matters than *tzedakah* in material matters—even though it is understood from the *Iggeres HaKodesh* of the Alter Rebbe that material *tzedakah* draws down [blessings] to the lowest levels. By "spiritual *tzedakah*," I refer to matters of Torah and *mitzvos* in general, and influencing others in these matters in particular.

In your letters, you do not mention anything regarding this. I hope that the lack of writing does not also imply a lack of action.

It is also understood that my intention is not so that others may know of your activities—although that, too, is a *mitzvah*, as it brings joy to one's fellow Jews. Rather, the main point is that the knowledge that you will eventually need to write about your activities to another fellow Jew adds strength and courage to do more.

And what is seen in practice requires no further proof...

With blessings,

**M. Schneerson**

## 3730

B”H, 22 Menachem Av, 5715
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of the 12th of Menachem Av, in which you write about the completion of your studies, your state of mind, and the fact that you perceive a lack of independence in yourself. You feel that you are in a state of confusion, etc., and therefore you have an idea to travel to... for about a year. You feel that when you are in a new environment, without the possibility of receiving instructions from your parents (may they live long) regarding every matter and step, the independence within you will be revealed, and you will emerge from the confusion and doubts, etc. You ask for my opinion on this.

Now, according to your letter, your intention in traveling to... is not to seek comfort or matters of pleasure, but on the contrary, to pave a path for yourself through your own strengths, and to be forced by the situation to rely on your own judgment. Consequently, you will mature, and your inner strengths will come to expression.

If this is indeed your true intention, then there is no purpose in traveling to... It is highly doubtful whether you would be able to utilize the talents you possess to their full extent there, and it is even doubtful whether you could utilize a portion of them. It is understood that a visit there, as you write, for the seven days of the holiday, and the reception you found, proves nothing regarding the situation when one comes to seek work and a position and wants to accomplish something. For the aforementioned goal, there is no place better to test your own strengths than in Eretz Yisrael. Life there is extremely diverse, and every young person can find a place for activity and fulfilling work—especially in the field of education and instruction, and particularly when these must be founded upon Torah and mitzvos, rather than being swept away by the current that says, "I prefer lawlessness."

In the current situation, traveling from there to... is not a matter of seeking work and challenges in order to reveal what is hidden within. In the vast majority of cases, it is a way to evade entering into responsible work, at least for a few months—even though it is understood that not everyone recognizes this. In the vast majority of cases, it seems that the desire to travel stems from a desire to pave a new path, and the like. If there is a basis for your concern—as we see in many homes where the supervision of parents and their love, when one is within their "four cubits," limits the possibility of discovering one's own strengths—then it is possible to arrange that at the beginning of the time for studies and teaching, you live apart from them. In the manner mentioned above, you would be forced to decide based on your own judgment due to the lack of possibility to rely on your parents and their instructions.

Now, everything stated above is in response to your own question. In the following lines, I will touch upon a primary point for which I did not find an answer in your letter: More than ninety percent of the youth, the sons and daughters of Yisrael in our Holy Land (may it be rebuilt and established), are struggling on their path and are full of doubts regarding the arrangement of their lives and their future, and which path they should choose. In the overwhelming majority of the youth, a large part of their doubts is caused by a lack of knowledge and ignorance. From this, it is understood that everyone who has been graced by Hashem with the power of influence over others—especially those who are in a position to know the truth of the responsibility of the lives of the youth and their birth pangs (spiritual birth and maturation)—must dedicate an important part of their energy and talents to helping these youth in their situation. Every day and week that passes while the youth is left to their own devices, their entire future is potentially endangered because they decide based on their own judgment in an undesirable manner due to a lack of instruction and knowledge.

Whoever has succeeded, through Divine Providence, in not being in a state of such fundamental doubts (through appropriate education received in an appropriate environment, etc.), their work in the aforementioned direction is nothing but the repayment of a debt for what was given to them in this very matter. Even with their greatest effort, it is only a repayment of a portion of the debt, not the whole of it. No one has the right to exempt themselves from this holy work, as is understood. I would be interested to hear of your activities in this direction, which, in my opinion, is incumbent upon every young man and woman, and all the more so for those who are in our Holy Land (may it be rebuilt and established), a place where there is a situation of *pikuach nefesh* for thousands and tens of thousands of souls of the sons and daughters of Yisrael.

It is possible, and it seems from your letter, that you have not contemplated yourself from this point of view. My hope is that, in any case, upon reading these lines, you will contemplate with the necessary attention everything stated above and reach the conclusions which, in my opinion, are clear and simple. As soon as possible, you will begin to fulfill your role in this holy work with the greatest energy. May it be the will of Hashem Yisbarach that you succeed in this and find complete inner satisfaction, and afterwards, [I look forward] to good news.

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, Shlita,

Secretary

## 3731

B"H, 23 Menachem Av, 5715
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Rabbi, the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, meticulous in his mitzvah observance, etc.,
Rabbi Sh. Y. [Zevin] – may he live and be well,

Peace and blessing!

Regarding what you wrote concerning my comment about the stories: I agree with you—as our Sages of blessed memory said—that it is a mitzvah to fulfill the words of the Sages, and especially the words of the Nesi'im. However, this applies when it is at least plausible to say that the words were transmitted accurately. But in a place where there is great doubt, since the stories have certainly been passed down from narrator to narrator and from mouth to mouth, it is impossible that there would not be changes in the phrasing—especially in the details that people do not pay close attention to. Therefore, instead of seeking and searching for forced explanations, etc., it is more reasonable to say that one or two words are not exact, and the difficulty does not exist from the outset...

Enclosed is the Kuntres (which was published for a known reason), the Maamar "Tzion B'mishpat Tipadeh" by our holy Rebbe the Alter Rebbe, with the annotations of our holy Rebbe the Tzemach Tzedek. Surely you will merit the public with it as well, and the merit of the public depends on you.

With respect and blessing,

***

## 3732

B"H, 23 Menachem Av, 5715
Brooklyn

To the esteemed Rabbi, G-d-fearing, learned, and meticulous scholar, R' Isser, may he live:

Greetings and blessings!

I hereby acknowledge with thanks the receipt of the two books from your pen: 1) *Yechidei Segulah*, and 2) *R' Meir Yechiel of Ostrovtza*. I trust you will continue this good practice in the future by sending your works to my library, especially since your books are being utilized for the benefit of the many.

As a matter of interest: while leafing through these books as time permitted, it occurred to me that these essays would be greatly enhanced if you were to add, at the end of each essay or at the end of the book, a list of sources where the reader and researcher could find more details regarding the subjects presented in the essay in summary form. It would also be beneficial to add a list of the books or essays written by the subject of the article, as this often provides clarity for understanding these *yechidei segulah*. Since I see on the book’s jacket that you are planning to publish a second volume, this is not a case of "one does not cry over the past."

This is especially true since, in the second volume, you could also add the sources for the essays in the first volume. The chronicles of our complete Torah giants should not be like the chronicles of their idle talkers, which are cluttered with extraneous matters—bibliographies, lists of dates, etc. This is particularly relevant in our generation, this orphaned generation, where certain circles can perhaps be drawn toward the "source of light" only if they see, at first, the beauty of external matters. This will arouse their interest, and from the "secondary of the secondary," they will eventually arrive at the essence. It is already known how the Rambam elaborated on the method of educating children, and it is understood that these matters are even more applicable to those of "small intellect" (see his elaboration on this in the Commentary on the Mishnah, Sanhedrin, beginning of Chapter 10; see also *Yad HaChazakah*, end of *Hilchos Teshuvah*).

One more small note, which is of great necessity in our generation—a time when many call darkness light and light darkness: your book mixes together individuals of different types, and even opposites. According to the adage in the *Zohar*—that the burial of Moshe is in the Torah, and that one does not bury one next to the other unless they loved one another—this principle is not always maintained in your book. There is room to separate them into different sections if, for whatever reason, you wish to write about all of them—or at least, ensure that one essay does not immediately follow another if the personalities are contradictory. This is of the utmost importance, as mentioned above, to avoid causing the innocent reader to err by assuming that all those appearing in one book are also neighbors in their greatness in Torah and *yirah*. A word to the wise is sufficient.

Seeing in the list for Volume II that it includes the Rebbe, the Rashab, I am sending you in a separate package an outline of his biography, which was published some years ago based on the notes of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory.

With respect and blessings that you succeed in strengthening the spirit of true Judaism of the "elder Israel" within those you influence—imbued with Chassidic light and warmth.

**M. Schneerson**

P.S.
For reasons of caution regarding holy writings, it does not seem appropriate to me at all to print verses in *ksav stam* (Torah script), even in books of *halacha* and *aggadah*, and certainly not in biographical works. Therefore, I was surprised that you did so at the end of the book. It is understood that this is not comparable to printing a page from the *Megillas Esther*, as that does not contain the Divine Name. Furthermore, that served as a form of instruction to the many regarding the manner of writing the *Megillah*, which is not the case here.

## 3733

B”H, 24 Menachem Av, 5715
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to the second sheet enclosed in your letter... it is understood that I derived pleasure from what you wrote regarding the diverse group of people who gather in your home on Shabbos, like a *farbrengen*. It is certainly unnecessary to remind you of the words of our Sages, and in the *Mishnah*: "The primary thing is not the study, but the deed." In the language of Chassidus, every *farbrengen* must result in a "therefore"—a practical application, at the very least in the realm of thought, and certainly in the sense of the superiority of the one who acts over the one who merely contemplates, and even more so. After all, they said that one who errs in a matter of *Mishnah* must retract; this means that there cannot be differences of opinion or error in this regard. This is especially true since each of those you mention in your letter has their own circle of influence; therefore, any change for the better regarding the practical action brought about in one of them is multiplied many times over in those they influence. The analogy of a small candle whose light is multiplied many times over by a lantern is well known. It is true that we see tangibly, and it is also understood intellectually, that the practical aspect is accepted with more difficulty than matters of thought, and certainly more than thoughts about thoughts. However, our Sages have already informed us that Torah is acquired only through *yissurim*, and *yissurim* and inner struggles are the essence of this...

## 3734

3734

B"H, 24 Menachem Av, 5715

Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter, in which you write that at times during your studies you do not understand the shiur being taught to you, and that this causes you sadness, etc.

This is generally a common occurrence for many students, and therefore one should not be overly distressed by it, although it is understood that one must gradually decrease the number of moments of such lack of understanding. Among the suggestions for this is to study from the sefer itself; that is, while listening to the shiur, the place in the sefer where the shiur is being taught should be open before you. Sometimes it is also worthwhile to close your eyes for those moments, as by narrowing the vision, one’s hearing and concentration are enhanced. Furthermore, one should not exaggerate this lack of understanding, which surely only lasts for a few moments and arises because the mind is wandering to other matters.

Regarding what you wrote—that due to focusing on the explanation of the words, you fall slightly behind the minyan—you should consult with your mashpia regarding your learning and the avodah of tefillah, and act according to his instruction.

As you requested, I will mention you and your brother, may he live, at the holy tziyun of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory. Surely you are keeping yourself, and you should also encourage your older brother to keep the three daily shiurim that are incumbent upon every person, as instituted by my father-in-law, the Rebbe—the well-known shiurim in Chumash, Tehillim, and Tanya. Even though it should be done according to the custom of Yisrael, without a neder, one must be meticulous in keeping them. May Hashem grant you success in the study of Torah with yiras shamayim, and to fulfill what is written: "Serve Hashem with joy."

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

Secretary

3734

Published in the *Yagdil Torah* (Jerusalem) collection, issue 12, p. 15, and completed based on the secretariat's copy.

## 3735

B"H, 24 Menachem Av, 5715
Brooklyn.

Agudas N'shei U'Bnos Chabad in Eretz Yisrael, may Hashem protect them, [City] Branch...
To them, may they live,

Blessings and peace!

We acknowledge receipt of your letter... It is surprising that there has been such a long pause in receiving news from you.

Surely the initial period, in which "all beginnings are difficult," has already passed. You should expand your activities more and more, in accordance with the demands of the hour, which are also constantly growing. And there is nothing that can stand before the will. One of the main points, as it appears from here, is maintaining a constant and growing connection with the mothers of the students of the schools—and in particular, the Chabad schools—in order to strengthen them and encourage their spirits. [This is to ensure] that the atmosphere in the home will be a continuation of the atmosphere in the school, and not, G-d forbid, in opposition to that spirit—which is the most effective way to hinder the education of the students. It is understood that the material assistance provided to them is not enough, even though it is very important and correct. There must also be meetings with them from time to time to explain to them the great value of education in the spirit of our Torah, the Torah of life, and to encourage them to ask questions and reveal the problems weighing on their hearts. Then, it becomes possible to resolve them in the desired manner, and thereby remove many obstacles and difficulties in the life of the student and in the lives of the parents.

In connection with the approaching school year, it is understood that this is work that is timely, especially since the month of Elul, the month of mercy, begins in these days—a month in which the heart of every man and woman of Bnei Yisrael is aroused, and the inner point, which has always been faithful to Him, may He be blessed, is revealed. Its aspiration and desire is, as the Sweet Singer of Israel said: "One thing I have asked of Hashem, that I will seek: that I may dwell in the house of Hashem, etc."

With blessings for success in your holy work.

## 3736

3736

B"H, 1st day of Rosh Chodesh Elul, 5715
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To Dr. Avraham and Miriam Aharonov, may they live:

Shalom and blessing!

In response to your letter of 12 Menachem Av, which follows up on my letter—a response to your question regarding how to actualize your desire to assist the work of Chabad in Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established, in a broad manner—you write in this letter about the establishment of a "Revolving Fund for Vocational Training for the Youth of Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim (Lubavitch) in the name of Dr. Miriam and Avraham Aharonov."

If this matter has already been decided, may it be the will of Hashem that it be in a good and auspicious hour, and may it bring forth good and abundant fruit.

However, if the matter is still in the stage of deliberation, I cannot withhold my perspective on this, which is as follows:

Considering that we are living in a period of great significance for the world, and specifically in a period of crisis regarding traditional education and Chassidic education in particular, every moment in which it is possible to save the "human material" of the young generation is precious. In such a time of emergency, immediate educational work takes precedence over work that brings its fruits only after a long time, because in the interim, we are losing—Heaven forbid—tens and perhaps hundreds of Israeli youth.

From this point of view, the conclusion is, of course, that all means and resources that can be mobilized should be prioritized to focus on maximum effort in immediate education. Consequently, this should not be in the form of a revolving gemach fund, nor necessarily for vocational training for avreichim and graduates, but primarily to provide the means for educational institutions to be able to absorb a greater number of young students—the "kids of the flock."

And even if we assume that from the perspective of quality, this work does not surpass the idea you had in mind, we have already seen tangibly many times that an increase in quantity eventually leads to an increase in quality, as is hinted at in the words of our Sages: "A thousand enter for Mikra (Scripture), a hundred emerge for Mishnah, ten for Gemara, and one for Hora'ah (instruction)."

In any event, I wish you success in your endeavor, however you decide to implement it, and I am certain you will inform me of the continuation of the matter. Thank you in advance.

With respect and with the blessing of *Kesivah V'chasimah Tovah*.

#### ***3736***

May He who guards His people Yisrael, who neither slumbers nor sleeps, guard each and every one of them within the collective of Yisrael with an open eye, both in material and spiritual matters, and may you succeed in your holy work beyond the natural order, with peace of mind and peace of body.

Enclosed is a *Likutei Elul*, which I am certain you will merit to use to bring merit to the many, for the merit of the many depends upon you.

With the blessing of *Kesivah v'Chasimah Tovah*.

Just as the *Ribono shel Olam*, in writing His Torah, [said] "Anochi" — "I have written and given My own soul" — so too it is regarding our *Nesi'im*, the *Nesi'ei* Chabad, who have written themselves into their holy *maamarim* and *sichos*, and from them one must draw [inspiration]. As the saying of my revered father-in-law, the *Admur* the Tzemach Tzedek goes: "Business, business, until the coming of Moshiach."

## 3738

B"H, 1 Elul, 5715
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

...Regarding what you write, that you daven before the amud: you are surely aware of the long-standing custom in this regard, that for several days before davening for the tzibbur, one reviews all the tefillos and piyutim, in order to know at the very least the literal meaning of the words. One should act this way all year round, reviewing even that which one already knows, and, it goes without saying, one should be familiar with the laws of tefillah in general, and those that pertain to one who davens before the amud in particular. May Hashem Yisbarach grant you success in all of the above.
