## 3339

B"H, 1 Elul, 5715
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

Following your long silence, your letter of 22 Menachem Av, along with its enclosure, was received. I was pleased to learn that Divine Providence has provided you with an opportunity to disseminate the *maayanos* in a certain yeshiva, as well as among *bochurim* of a certain type, etc. You can see tangibly that this is an *is'arusa d'leila* (arousal from Above) regarding the *bochurim*, the yeshiva, and yourself as well. Consequently, it is understood how much extra effort is required in this matter; for while on one hand an *is'arusa d'leila* can, G-d forbid, be without results, on the other hand, when one draws it down below, it comes from a place that is higher than an *is'arusa d'letata* (arousal from below), as is understood. Therefore, from the other side, there is a lack of complete joy, as it appears that the effort in the aforementioned matter is extremely weak—even though it is certain that with even a slight effort on your part, there would be a matter of clear *parnassah* in both spirituality and physicality. In what manner do people exert themselves in this, even if there were a doubt or a double doubt? From this, one can learn *kal v'chomer* regarding the effort required for the aforementioned matter.

I have already written to several of *anash* that we have merited to reach a time when many will be clarified, refined, and purified. Consequently, along with the difficulty of the trials, in many matters—and especially in the matters of *anash* in the Holy Land, may it be rebuilt and established—I am confident that they will see with physical eyes *parnassah* in physicality if they engage properly in *parnassah* in spirituality. To my regret, I have not yet merited that these words of mine be accepted. I have already written to some of *anash* in the Holy Land, may it be rebuilt and established, that their situation is similar to that which is brought in *Tanya*, end of Chapter 40: like one who stands in a river and cries out for water to drink, but is unwilling to lower his head to the water in the river, the source of living waters, even though through this there would also be water and bread—that is, *parnassah* in physicality, in the literal sense.

With blessings for success in all that is mentioned above, and for a *ksiva v'chasima tova*.

## 3740

B"H, 1 Elul, 5715
Brooklyn.

To the Avreich Shalom, may he live,

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letter of 21 Menachem Av, in which you write regarding your thought to travel to study at Tomchei Temimim here: You ought to persevere in your studies at Tomchei Temimim in France, and exert yourself in influencing others—specifically and especially the avreichim who have come from Morocco to study at Tomchei Temimim in France, who require special attention. Fortunate is the portion of anyone who engages in this, both in the capacity of a teacher, and even more so in the capacity of a friend, as our Sages of blessed memory said: "I have learned much from my teachers, and from my friends more than from my teachers." The attribute of the Ribono shel Olam is "measure for measure," only that it is multiplied many times over, as explained in the words of our Sages of blessed memory cited in the introduction to the Tanya regarding the verse, "Hashem illuminates the eyes of them both" (*Mishlei 29:13*).

Regarding your notification of your birthday: You should surely follow the custom of anash on one's birthday: receiving an aliyah to the Torah (or on the Shabbos preceding it, if there is no Torah reading on the birthday itself), giving tzedakah before davening Shacharis and Mincha (and if it falls on Shabbos or a Yom Tov, then on the day before), and studying an additional shiur in Nigleh and in Chassidus, beyond the three daily shiurim that are incumbent upon every soul—in Chumash, Tehillim, and Tanya—as is well known.

May it be the will of Hashem that this be a year of success for you in the study of Torah and the performance of mitzvos with hidur.

With the blessing of *Kesivah v'chasimah tovah*.

## 3751

3751

By the grace of Hashem, 3 Elul, 5715
Brooklyn

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing and learned, engaged in communal affairs,
R' Menachem Zev, may he live, Halevi

Shalom u’vracha!

I acknowledge receipt of your letter from Monday. The following is the content of the response:

I was astonished as I read it to see how little you feel the weight of your own arguments. In this very letter, you dismantle all your own contentions—both those in this letter and those in the previous one—by admitting that it is permissible to vote in the municipal elections in Eretz Yisrael (may it be rebuilt and established). If it is permissible in such a case, then surely, it requires explanation. With all due respect, according to your own logic, all the reasons you cite for a severe and absolute prohibition apply here as well, since all the parties participating in the Knesset are the very same ones presenting themselves for the municipal elections. Consequently, the argument that associating with them is forbidden—that one who assists them is "assisting [transgressors]," that the women elected by them sit in a manner contrary to the path of modesty, etc.—is the very same argument you make in your letter. The only difference between them is the matter mentioned at the end of Maseches Kesuvos, that they should not "go up like a wall," and nothing more. One should not conflate this with the matter of the three cardinal sins for which one must be killed rather than transgress. Especially since, in the inner dimension of things, the issue of "not going up like a wall" applies here as well, for the matter of the Jerusalem municipality is a "going up like a wall"—more so than any other political issue in all of Eretz Yisrael, since it is precisely on this that the opposition has been greatest, even until now.

2) Regarding the other points in your letter: As for what you cite from the Rambam about moving to the wilderness, and your attempt to justify this by saying that the same applies in the Diaspora—here, too, there is a contradiction in your own letter, where you write that in the Diaspora it is a matter of "the ignorance of the masses," whereas in Eretz Yisrael it is a matter of "rebellion." In truth, the distinction is much sharper, for in the Diaspora there is no issue of coercion contrary to the religion, G-d forbid; there is only room to fear that "the eye sees and the heart desires." This is not the case in a city that is majority or entirely Jewish, and a word to the wise is sufficient. Consequently, all the justifications you offer for this are, with all due respect, fundamentally flawed.

3) Similarly, regarding what you write about paying for various services, and bringing an example that one pays for the labor—this, too, is not comparable at all. Surely you know that when paying for water, etc., one is not paying only for the labor; rather, these funds are used for general expenses. And not only—as you write—for "cleanliness," but also for the maintenance of things that prevent the fulfillment of the explicit commandment in the Torah, "You shall utterly destroy," etc. Furthermore, they provide for the support of their houses of worship, and what is even worse—the missionary activities and their maintenance. There is no need to elaborate on such a terrifying matter.

As for your claim that there is "no choice," in addition to what was written in the letter and in our *Chomoseinu*, all of the above falls under the three known sins for which one is obligated to give one's life. According to your own logic, the *mesiras nefesh* of the rest of the Jewish people in Eretz Yisrael—by not going to the elections—results in adding several more representatives (deputies) from the ranks of the deniers. They then proclaim, both abroad and in Eretz Yisrael, that this is proof of the majority opinion in Eretz Yisrael, and there is no greater *chillul Hashem* than this. If this is one of the three sins mentioned above, then there is no excuse that they are "forced to take it." Especially since it is possible to use candles and kerosene, and to use spring water and the like. It is understood that these lines are not intended to cause you pain, but to prove that regarding one's own physical needs, people are lenient, yet when it comes to tens of thousands or even hundreds of thousands of Jews who could more easily fulfill the commandments of our G-d in their daily lives, it is precisely there that one uses a zealotry that is entirely misplaced.

4) Regarding your statement that there is room to say that a protest from the outside is necessary, and not a protest from the inside—it is not understood what the contradiction is between the two, since one can protest from the outside and one can protest from the inside. Just as was the case with the demonstration in the United States, in which several members of Agudas Yisrael participated, at the same time that members of that party sat in the Knesset.

5) Regarding your statement that they wanted to form a front between Agudah and Mizrachi, and that the Chabad people in Eretz Yisrael were the "brokers"—you were not precise in your hearing, for the broker in this was also the Rebbe shlita, as he said explicitly. As for why your honor is making such a commotion about this, you would have been better off asking: since you yourself write in your letter that one must vote in municipal elections, surely you know that in many places there was a municipal front of Agudas Yisrael with parties *far* more leftist than those mentioned, and a word to the wise is sufficient.

6) Regarding your listing in your letter of all the types of Jews with whom one should have no discourse, no contact, and for whom one should not strive or act, etc.—the answer to this has already been given in the commandment of *ahavas Yisrael* by the Rebbe the Tzemach Tzedek. *Nit tzu keiner geredt* (this is not directed at your honor). In truth, this approach—that with all those who took part in the elections, and certainly all those who voted for the Mizrachi, Poalei Mizrachi, or even Mapai parties, there should be no discourse—is, as mentioned, *nit tzu geredt*. Its root is in the *kelipah* of Midian, who fought against Hashem, G-d forbid, as explained in the *maamar* "Hechaletzu" by our Alter Rebbe. It is astonishing that your honor—especially since it is a matter of *milta* (a significant matter), and you begin with the name Yeshaya—would act this way. As is known from the story of our Sages when he wanted to touch the honor of the Jewish people, even though Achaz and his generation had many forms of idol worship among them, and even in the Temple, etc. All of the above was in the realm of speculation before the elections, but now, and especially in the month of Elul when every Jew surely awakens to make an accounting: the calculation is clear. If there had been a united front of Agudah and Mizrachi, and if everyone who was able to vote had gone to vote for the Charedi list, then all those who understand this testify that several more people would have entered the Knesset as representatives of the Agudah and Mizrachi parties. Consequently, there would have been a *shortage* of that number in the leftist parties. The Almighty can certainly cause this not to have a negative impact on the legislation of decrees in Eretz Yisrael, but if one takes into account the words of our Sages that "one does not rely on miracles," then anyone who prevented tens, and perhaps hundreds, of Jews from voting in the elections bears the responsibility for the fact that there are four or more representatives of the parties that rebel against Hashem in the Knesset, and that the number of representatives of the Agudah and Mizrachi parties is reduced by that amount. This requires great reflection. *Ver hot dos di breite pleitzes* (who has the broad shoulders) to take this responsibility upon themselves? And not only that, but to invert the matter and say that this is precisely "pure fear of Heaven," etc.

9) Regarding the main point of your letter, I am most astonished by it. For we have nothing but the instruction of the Baal Shem Tov and his students, which was *clearly heard and later transmitted* during his soul's ascent on Rosh Hashanah, that the coming of Moshiach—which is the *redemption of the Shechinah and the redemption of the Jewish people*—depends on the dissemination of the wellsprings (the teachings of Chassidus) outward. (This matter is explained at length and with clarity in the *sicha* of Simchas Torah 5690 by the Rebbe Rayatz; see there.) This is also *obligatory* according to what R' Chaim Vital writes in his introduction to *Shaar HaHakdamos*, about how the redemption is delayed by the lack of study of the inner dimension of the Torah, etc. How is it possible to say [...] that someone who has influence—through Divine Providence—over several thousand Jews, and for the time being *nothing* is heard from him giving any instruction to all those people to study the inner dimension of the Torah, the "Tree of Life"? At the same time, regarding other matters, he repeats and triples his words, even though they do not emerge from the realm of doubt. Yet, precisely regarding this great matter, *which the King Moshiach said*—and he said this to the Baal Shem Tov during his soul's ascent in the Palace of Moshiach, in clear words that leave no room for doubt—he has not a word to say. Even though it is beyond any doubt that if he had shaken the world—even a tenth or a hundredth as much as they shook Eretz Yisrael regarding the voting—thousands of Jews, and perhaps tens of thousands, would have begun studying the inner dimension of the Torah that very day, and consequently, they would have brought the end of the redemption closer *on a paved and clear path*.

I ask your honor's forgiveness for all that is said above, but for each of us, it is said, "Distance yourself from a false word," and in such a case, silence is equivalent to admitting to a falsehood. It is necessary to say the truth, clearly and openly, without taking into account, etc.

10) Incidentally, regarding what you wrote, as mentioned above, about all those types with whom there should be no connection, and whom one should not defend, etc.—I am astonished. For in the *Zohar* that I cited in my previous letter regarding the conduct of Moshe, the faithful shepherd, which is as it should be—unlike even the conduct of Avraham Avinu, as explained there—the words are spoken regarding the makers of the Golden Calf. The story of our Sages is known regarding the verse "And they rose up to play," that at that time all three cardinal sins were present: forbidden relationships, idolatry, and bloodshed. And it is known from our Sages that this was when "the King was at his table." Yet, if Moshe, the faithful shepherd, had not said, "If not, blot me out," etc., then, etc.

11) Regarding what you wrote about the device, "Chashmal"—not to use it, etc.—I am in doubt as to the basis for this.

As for what we find in Gemara Chagigah (and see also Rashi's commentary on Yechezkel 1:27), it speaks there regarding the concept, not regarding the device. Especially according to what is explained in many places in *Etz Chaim* and in general in the books of Kabbalah, that this belongs to *kelipas nogah*. See *Etz Chaim*, *Shaar HaChashmal*, and in the *maamar* of the Rebbe the Tzemach Tzedek printed in the supplement to *Torah Or* (Kehot Publication Society).

With the blessing of *Ksivah v’Chasimah Tovah*,

On behalf of the Rebbe shlita,

A. Quint
Secretary

P.S.
Surely, in your letter to the aforementioned, you will also mention the writings of the late R' Alfandari.

## 3742

B"H, 3 Elul, 5715
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and distinguished R' Yona, may he live:

Shalom and blessings!

...Regarding your observation concerning what is written in the *Akeidah*, at the beginning of the 50th Gate: that the Divine ability cannot be described as... "gathering opposites," yet we say that He is **"All-powerful" (Kol Yachol)**—

You are completely correct.

The Jewish philosophers who hold by the opinion of the *Akeidah* explain that **"All" (Kol)** refers to everything that is possible according to logic, as is brought briefly in *Mekor Chaim* on that passage—though the forced nature of this interpretation is understood.

However, the great *Rishonim*, the *Mekubalim*, and the teachings of *Chassidus* have long ago ruled that the ability of the *Ribono shel Olam* is **unlimited—"All-powerful" (Kol Yachol)** in its literal sense. See *Shu"t HaRashba*, Vol. 1, 413; *Sefer HaChakirah* by the *Tzemach Tzedek*, p. 68; *Dah V'Taher Libenu* (5637), and elsewhere.

A definitive proof is brought by them from the words of our Sages (Yoma 21a): **"The place of the Ark is not included in the measurements,"** even though it **had** to be, according to the command of the *Ribono shel Olam*, two and a half cubits long and a cubit and a half wide and high.

#### ***3742***

**R' Yona:** Dresher. Another letter to him—see above, 3736.

## 3743

3743

B.H., 4 Elul, 5715
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed and distinguished scholar, etc., R. Shmuel Yehuda, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letter of 26 Menachem Av, together with the enclosures (the photographs and their explanations are being returned to you separately, sent via registered mail).

In general, regarding the form of the letters and the like, this is a matter that is received orally and through diagrams; it is difficult to explain the details in writing. Therefore, you should seek out among Anash in Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established, those who are expert in these matters. It is possible that those you write about can be relied upon—provided they received this through a tradition from experts and authoritative books. They will certainly be able to clarify this, and from them, you will learn the details.

Regarding what you write about the logic of including Chabad customs from the *kuntreisim* when you publish the book, it is imperative that for every single custom, you indicate the source (the *kuntres* or booklet from which it was taken) and that it be proofread with the utmost precision.

Regarding what you wrote concerning the *tefillin* of *Shimusha Rabba* and the *Ra’avad*: The opinion of the *Shimusha Rabba* involves three things: regarding the *tagin* (the *Ribam* style), regarding the measurement of *etzba’os* by *etzba’os*, and regarding the placement of the *parshiyos* to the right of the wearer. From this, it is understood that *tefillin* that are precise even in only one of these points are called *tefillin* of *Shimusha Rabba*. However, it is simple in many places that for *Shimusha Rabba*, they must be to the right of the wearer, according to the opinion of the *Ra’avad*. See the *She’eilos U’Teshuvos Rema mi’Pano*, *Matzas Shimurim*, *Emek HaMelech*, and *Ma’ayan HaChochma* by the Arizal—and as he elaborated on all of this in *Mishmeres Shalom*, Section 4, in the second edition; see there. He also brings the language from *Pri Etz Chaim* that those who disagree wish to rely upon. He also brings there the *Tiferes Shmuel*, which you mention in your letter. See also in the book *Me’asef Lechol HaMachanos*, beginning of Section 34, subsections 3 and 9. But there is no proof for the aforementioned—that for *Shimusha Rabba* it must be to the right of the wearer—from this, for it is possible to add *tagin* and make Rashi *tefillin* of *etzba’os* by *etzba’os*, and they would also qualify for *Shimusha Rabba*. Therefore, it must be that there is another distinction regarding Rashi, for there is a reason based on *Sod* for the placement of Rashi *tefillin*, and this is not the place to elaborate.

Regarding the *chulyos* of the *tzitzis*, it is known that our custom is to make three, three, one, and then two, three, three, etc., in order to join the two to the one, as is understood. As for what you brought from *Sha’ar HaKavanos*, etc.—it is not understood what the proof is from their language, as it has no connection to all of the above.

I do not know if this expert exists in Jerusalem, may it be rebuilt and established, but in the book *Ta’amei HaMinhagim*, the material pertaining to this from Chabad books has not been included until now, as they were not available there at that time. It would be worthwhile to fill this great void now if it is at all possible, for we have been promised that "your springs will spread outward."

With the blessing of *Kesivah V’Chasimah Tovah*,

**M. Schneerson**

Regarding your note on the *peirush* of the Baal Shem Tov (brought in *Kesser Shem Tov*, Part 2, 34) on "she said 'flour'" (*solet*), whereas according to Rashi she said "meal" (*kemach*) (*Bava Metzia* 87a)—it has already been noted in the book *Baal Shem Tov* that this is discussed in the book *Meir Nesivim*, Part 2, and in the *chiddushim* in *Kuntres HaSheimos* in the book *Tvu’os Shor*.

## 3444

B"H, 4 Elul, 5715
Brooklyn

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and learned, who engages in the needs of the community, R' Betzalel, may he live, Shochet and Bodek.

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letter from 1 Elul, even after reading it, the bewilderment remains regarding the long hiatus in our correspondence. Regarding what you write about your studies in the Yeshiva, it is a definitive ruling that a *chazakah* (presumption) applies even to propaganda—that it does not return empty-handed, and certainly so regarding actual *peulah* (action). It is also a known adage that one action is better than a thousand sighs. In matters of Torah and mitzvos, we infer the positive from the negative; since no fruits are seen, it is certain that there is no action. And yet, these are the days when one should speak only of the positive side and the good deeds of each individual, and not of the lack thereof, etc.

May it be the will of Hashem that, in the end, the *anash* of Australia will reconsider what I have written in several letters: that if they were to increase their activity in the institutions of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, Nasi Yisrael, their work would be blessed, including in matters of simple livelihood. It is a known adage brought in *Chassidus* that "one cannot stop a head [from thinking]," and therefore, they themselves must come to the decision to reconsider the aforementioned. May it be the will of Hashem that they reach a decision in accordance with the true situation, for then the decisions will be good ones. It is a pity about the time that has passed until now, similar to the question of our Rebbe, the Alter Rebbe, in Tanya, end of Chapter 40, regarding one who stands in a river and cries out, "Water to drink!"—it is incomprehensible, why must he cry out? Each one of them is standing in a position to draw down livelihood from Above, which is through the occupation of spreading the *maayanos* in general, and in supporting and expanding the institution in particular, yet they cry out for livelihood specifically through crooked paths...

With blessings and regards to all *anash*, and wishing you a *kesivah vachasimah tovah*.

Your letter from 3 Elul has now been received. In response to it: My intention in my letter was that each person should **increase** their current activities regarding the affairs of the institutions, and there is both room and ability for such an increase. To strengthen this matter, it is good that the decision of each person regarding this increase be made in the presence of others, and, of course, this is also from the *maamar* "Chalutzu..."

Your *farbrengens* with the *bochurim* bring great benefit; would that they were more frequent...

## 3745

B"H, 4 Elul, 5715
Brooklyn

To the esteemed and distinguished Rav, Moreinu HaRav Chaim, may he live.

Shalom and blessing!

In response to your letter from Rosh Chodesh Elul:

1) Regarding the formation of the letters in Sifrei Torah, Tefillin, and Mezuzos according to the Chabad custom: there are several differences from what the Alter Rebbe wrote in his Shulchan Aruch. This has been discussed in several places regarding the reason for the differences between the rulings of the Alter Rebbe in his Shulchan Aruch and the rulings in his Siddur, as well as his practical conduct. See also the beginning of *Shaar HaKollel*, the *Kuntres Piskei HaSiddur* by Rabbi Naeh, and others. Regarding Tefillin in particular, it is known what is written in *Beis Rebbe*, Chapter 10, that the Alter Rebbe rectified the Tefillin according to the tradition of the Rishonim and the tradition of the Arizal in their writing, their repair, and their donning; see there. These are matters learned orally from scribe to scribe, and it is difficult to explain them fully in writing; the writing serves only as an aid to what is said orally. Therefore, regarding a question such as this and similar matters, you should speak with a **sofer** (scribe) of Sifrei Torah, Tefillin, and Mezuzos who follows the Chabad custom, and he will clarify the details.

2) Regarding what you wrote about the measurement of "two fingers by two fingers" concerning Tefillin: several of the Acharonim in *Shulchan Aruch Orach Chaim*, Section 32, Paragraph 41, explain that this refers to the *titura* (the base). However, the *Pri Megadim* there explains that according to Rashi, it refers to the *batim* (the boxes themselves). This is also implied by the language of the *Rosh*, and it is cited in the *Tur* that it refers to the *batim*, as was also noted in *Os Chaim* there, subsection 19-20. Therefore, those who are meticulous make the size of the *batim* two fingers by two fingers.

With the blessing of *Kesivah V'chasimah Tovah*,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita

## 3746

6 Elul, 5715
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To all those gathered at the Melaveh Malkah on Motzaei Shabbos Parshas Ki Seitzei in Monsey, and foremost among them the esteemed Chossid, who toils in communal affairs, R’ Moshe Pinchas Hakohen, and the esteemed Chossid, who toils in communal affairs, R’ Gershon, may they live:

Greetings and blessings!

I was pleased to hear of your gathering for the Seudah of Dovid Malka Meshicha. Surely, as you will speak words of Torah, it will be a Seudas Mitzvah. It is well known, the saying of our Rebbe (the Alter Rebbe), that what a Chassidishe farbrengen can accomplish, the angel Michoel cannot accomplish (see at length in *Kovetz Amirah Tehillim*).

Based on the well-known principle that the weekly parsha is connected to the various events of the week, and that one can derive guidance for daily life from the parsha: The parsha that begins this Motzaei Shabbos is *Ki Tavo*, which recounts the mitzvah of bringing Bikkurim (first fruits). These had to be from the finest fruits produced by our Holy Land—may it be rebuilt and established speedily in our days through Moshiach Tzidkeinu—when it was a land flowing with milk and honey. They were taken from the very first ripening fruits, before one had taken anything for oneself, and brought to the Beis Hamikdash to thank Hashem Yisborach for the blessing He, blessed be He, placed into the fruits of the earth. These Bikkurim were not like other korbanos, which were burned upon the Mizbeiach; rather, they were given to the Kohen.

From this we learn a lesson regarding both extremes: that the produce and fruits of the earth, which grow only after one has plowed, sown, harvested, and performed all the other labors associated with the growth of the earth’s fruits, were not taken for oneself first. Instead, one created holiness from them by giving them to the Kohen. Certainly, at times, a grievance arises: after all the toil and effort one has invested, if one must take a portion for oneself and give it to holy causes, why must it specifically be the best and finest? But when one reflects upon this, one arrives at the understanding that such a grievance can only exist when there is a lack of emunah—the belief that the fruit of the earth is **"that which You, Hashem, have given me,"** and not that "my strength and the might of my hand have made me this wealth." Consequently, upon reflection, one sees that this [grievance] is the opposite of *emunah peshutah* (simple faith), which is present in all Jews without exception; one only needs to bring it forth so that it also influences daily life.

The second lesson to be learned from this same mitzvah is that the fruits were not burned upon the Mizbeiach in the Beis Hamikdash, but were given to the Kohen, who was to consume them—as per the law of Bikkurim. This demonstrates that even the taste and enjoyment of physicality, if one prepares oneself properly and sanctifies oneself, can be utilized for holiness (through the Beis Hamikdash and the Kohen). One can serve Hashem Yisborach through eating these fruits, just as one serves Hashem Yisborach with other korbanos by burning them in the Beis Hamikdash, like a *korban olah* and the like.

This is one of the foundations of Toras Hachassidus: that one must serve, and can serve, Hashem Yisborach not only while davening and learning Torah, but also while eating and during the act of eating, and while conducting business—and during the business itself. It is, of course, self-evident that this latter form of serving Hashem Yisborach requires deep preparation, but the reward for it is greater.

In this sense, the mitzvah of Bikkurim exists even in the time of Golus, even in Chutz Laaretz, and even on a simple weekday: when one says from the depths of the heart regarding everything one possesses that it is **"that which You, Hashem, have given me,"** it becomes sanctified, to the point that the very use of it can be an avodah—an avodas Hashem Yisborach.

Regarding the mitzvah of Bikkurim in its literal sense, when it was performed in the Beis Hamikdash, there was subsequently a blessing that in the coming year one should again be able to fulfill the mitzvah with joy. So too today: utilizing and employing the assets—the property—that Hashem Yisborach gives, in the manner that Hashem Yisborach requires, brings the blessing of Hashem Yisborach that in the coming year, too, one will be able to fulfill it to an even greater extent, and with even more satisfaction and joy.

With blessings to be aroused with good resolutions and to fulfill them in the days ahead for us and for all of Israel for the good, and with the blessing of *Kesivah Vachasimah Tovah* for a good and sweet year.

## 3747

B"H, 6 Elul, 5715
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and distinguished individual, occupied with communal needs,
R' Yechiel Michel Yehuda Leib, may he live,

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter from Rosh Chodesh Elul, I look forward to hearing continued good news regarding the matters mentioned therein. Regarding what you wrote concerning the *yemei iyun* (study days), if the matters are suitable for the conditions of *Eretz HaKodesh*, may it be built and established, it is possible to endeavor to arrange them during the days of *Chol HaMoed Sukkos*, the time of our rejoicing.

I was pleased by what you wrote regarding the study of *Chassidus* during the *Yarchei Kallah*. Surely you are utilizing some moments to speak *in dem arum fun Chassidus* (about the environment/context of Chassidus), and the main thing is regarding the study of its teachings and following its guidance and conduct in the days that follow, for ultimately, that is the essence. It is surprising that you do not mention the extensive activities of *Tzeirei Agudas Chabad*, and you are also brief regarding the activities of *Neshei Chabad*. I hope this is merely an omission in writing and not, G-d forbid, a deficiency in actual practice. May Hashem grant you success and enable you to report good news in this regard as well.

We received the *Machanaim* booklet, issues 22-24. The first letter, in response to mixed dancing, is alarming. Indeed, there was no response to this letter. It would be worthwhile to transcribe the excerpts from the *Sefer Yaaros Devash*, etc., exactly as they appear, indicating the source and the page, and to ask the editor to print them, accompanied by a simple question: How is it that after such clear words from the great *Acharonim*—who have been accepted as *poskim* among **all** the children of Israel—there are still those who hesitate and wish to argue, even if the actual consequences of mixed dancing, which are known to all, were **not** known, etc.?

With blessings for a *Kesivah Vachasimah Tovah* and for good news in all the above,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita

## 3749

[7 Elul, 5715]

In response to your letter from the end of Menachem Av, in which you describe the nature and quality of the students at... surely, when you read (a copy of) your letter once more, you will arrive at the immediate and most simple conclusion: that it is the duty of the administration and the teachers, in particular, to elevate the third category to the quality of the second, and both of them together to the quality of the first. The very existence of students of the first category will make this work easier for them, and the matter depends solely on their will. It is already known that separating the *chavrusa* of the most problematic students also assists in this. This is *kal v’chomer* from what is related regarding the reason Yosef bound Shimon. From this, it is also understood that the remedy for what you write—that those of the third category have no sense for *Chassidus* matters, etc.—is that their stay at... and the efforts made with them in this direction will certainly influence them for the good. May it be the will of Hashem that this happens very soon.

Regarding what you wrote about the room and board conditions, etc., which perhaps also influences the deficiencies in the quality of the students: please write a detailed proposal for improving the situation, and it is possible—according to our capacity—that it will lead to tangible changes. It is understood that it will not be known that the information about the situation came from you.

As for your concluding remark, that teaching in places far from civilization, etc., exempts one from service—and you are in doubt as to whether you should do this—you do not provide details. In any case, it is good for you, both materially and spiritually, to take advantage of the fact that Divine Providence has brought you to... so that you, specifically, will raise it to the appropriate level, or at the very least, to the highest level possible. It is not understood: if you were to move to another place, what would you be able to accomplish there, when this is your beautiful portion? May it be the will of Hashem that you will be happy with this most exalted portion mentioned, and that you will work in this with true *simcha*—a *simcha* that breaks through the boundaries of the material body and refines the physical body, through which success increases more and more.

## 3751

B"H, 7 Elul, 5715
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

...I will mention once again the point I have raised in several of my letters to various members of anash and institutions: that in reality, there is no basis whatsoever for the mistaken assumption that one institution can exist at the expense of another’s destruction. Furthermore, the existence of a Chabad institution is not dependent in the slightest on the general state of Chabad affairs in Eretz Yisrael—may it be rebuilt and established—and consequently, it is of no relevance, and certainly not worth any effort on the part of the institution’s personnel, to concern themselves with raising the banner of Chabad in general throughout Eretz Yisrael.

Beyond the fact that this notion is baseless due to the spiritual nature of these matters, even on a simple level, anyone who considers what will be tomorrow and the day after, and who wishes to take into account what happens outside of their own limited four cubits, understands that the aforementioned approach is not only generally harmful, but first and foremost, it harms the very institution whose administration adheres to this approach. From this, it is understood that if the administration of an institution... takes into account only the gains of its own limited yeshivah and sees only the immediate profits, then one must pray—and prolong this prayer—that the time until the aforementioned consequences occur, G-d forbid, will be delayed. Perhaps, in the meantime, they will reconsider their position and their approach...

With blessings for good and detailed tidings regarding all of the above, and for a *kesivah v’chasimah tovah*.

## 3754

B"H, 8 Elul, 5715
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

It has been some time since I received word regarding what transpired between you and [Name] shlita. As I understand it, they have sought your forgiveness and pardon, yet it appears you have not granted it to them.

If this report is accurate, it is surely unnecessary to remind you of the law of our Torah, the Torah of Life, regarding one who has been insulted when he is asked for forgiveness for that insult. This is all the more true given what is brought in this regard in many places in the teachings of Chassidus. Furthermore, we are currently in the month of Elul, the month of *cheshbon hanefesh* for the entire past year. When one takes stock of his conduct in his *avodah* over the past months, he asks the *Melech Malchei HaMelachim*, the Holy One, Blessed be He, to forgive, pardon, and atone for all of it, so that no trace remains, G-d forbid. Moreover, as stated in the language of *Iggeres HaTeshuvah* by our Alter Rebbe, Chapter 2, he desires to "see the face of the King," etc. It is self-evident what the effect of such a request is when one acts in a completely opposite manner regarding an insult from flesh and blood, a person of one's own stature, etc. There is no need to elaborate on something so simple and understood; see also *Iggeres HaKodesh* by our Alter Rebbe, Epistle 25.

It is possible that the aforementioned report is incorrect, and I will await good news in your reply in any event.

With blessings for a *kesivah v'chasimah tovah*,

On behalf of the Rebbe shlita

## 3,355

B"H, 10 Elul, 5715
Brooklyn

To the esteemed Rabbi, the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing and learned, occupied with communal needs,
R' Alexander Sender, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letter from the end of Menachem Av, as well as the *pidyon nefesh* that reached me through the esteemed Rabbi Stencil, may he live.

Regarding your question as to the meaning of what I wrote concerning activities in the surrounding environment: the saying of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, in such matters is well known: it is "with all the interpretations." Certainly, when you contemplate it, you will find additional modes of activity beyond those you wrote of, and I intended those as well. The space is too short to detail everything that can be done, especially in this generation—where "behold, He stands behind our wall," and we see clearly that we are granted unimaginable success, even though we also see the magnitude of the *he'elem v'hester* (concealment) in the lack of activity and the failure to utilize the success and the possibilities granted through *is'arusa d'le'eila* (arousal from Above)...

Regarding what you wrote, that *anash* and the *temimim* should unite in a fraternal association and so on: while it is superfluous to elaborate on the greatness of this matter—for our predecessors have already cried out about it, and what more do we need than the *maamarim* of *Hechalotzu*, starting from the Alter Rebbe down to my father-in-law, the Rebbe—and there is no need for my own addition, it is also simple that anyone who ties the activities that are on the daily agenda to the realization of this union is merely "mocking the poor," if not worse. That is to say, it is a desire to nullify the possibilities of activity from their very core, since the actualization of such an association—if only it would come about after an eternity of eternities.

As you requested, I will mention all those you wrote about at the holy *tziyun* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, for whatever they need as per your letter. May Hashem grant you the merit to succeed and to bring good news regarding all the above, and may you be written and sealed for a good and sweet year.

With blessing,

**M. Schneerson**

## 3756

B"H, 10 Elul, 5715
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the participants of the 33rd National Convention
of the Tzeirei Agudas Yisrael Organization
in America
May Hashem grant them life,

Peace and blessing!

In response to your notification regarding the national convention to be held on the 15th–18th of Elul.

May it be the will [of Hashem] that the convention be one of fear of Heaven, wisdom, and great action, and that your gathering will bring about positive, tangible results in strengthening authentic Yiddishkeit and disseminating it in daily life in all the places where your influence reaches.

The recognition of the alarming neglect in the field of activity for improving the religious life of the younger generation will surely lead you to the conclusion that Divine Providence has placed upon each and every one of you the holy and most responsible task to strive with all your strength—and even more—to improve this situation.

And it is understood that along with the duty and the privilege that Providence places upon each individual, the strength is also given to fulfill that task completely, as our Sages of blessed memory said: "He does not demand [of His creatures] except according to their strength." The strength of youth is especially potent, for it is filled with energy and enthusiasm, provided that it is utilized to its fullest in the wars of Hashem to strengthen the breaches of Yiddishkeit by rejecting compromise, and all the more so by rejecting any association of any matter whatsoever with the Name of Heaven, the Torah, and the mitzvos, for the Torah, the Holy One, blessed be He, and Yisrael are all one.

And the conclusion and crowning achievement of your gathering, which takes place on the auspicious day of the 18th of Elul—the birthday of the Baal Shem Tov and the birthday of our Rebbe, the Alter Rebbe (author of the Tanya and Shulchan Aruch), who taught us a paved path in the love of Hashem, love of Torah, and love of Yisrael, and how they are all one, and who illuminated the hearts and eyes of Yisrael for generations to come—may it be the will [of Hashem] that this day will cause and bring blessing and success to this convention, to make resolutions and bring those good resolutions into practice.

With respect and with the blessing of *Kesivah v’chasimah tovah* for a good and sweet year.

## 3757

B"H, 10 Elul, 5715
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

Through the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing and learned, engaged in communal needs, R' Ben Zion Shem Tov, shliach, I received news regarding the state of your health. My hope is strong that everything has been in order and successful, and that you will bring me good news regarding this. It is surely unnecessary to remind you of our Sages' teaching that whoever is careful with the wine of Kiddush* and the wine of Havdalah** adds to the light of his eyes.

In these days of the month of Elul, the month of accounting for the entire year, one may also say regarding this, by way of allusion and moral instruction, that whoever is careful with the wine (when wine enters, intellect and understanding emerge; the secret of man and creation is revealed) of Kiddush (in that which he must sanctify in his life and in his portion of the world through "do good" (positive mitzvos)) and of Havdalah (in that which he must separate and distinguish himself from through "turn away from evil" (negative mitzvos)), this adds to the light of a person's eyes, so that he will see the truth in his entire surroundings and within himself—the truth of Hashem is forever. As the Rambam phrases it (beginning of Yesodei HaTorah), "He alone is the Truth, and there is no other truth like His truth," and all that exists only exists from the truth of His existence.

With blessings for a speedy recovery, for good news, and for a *Kesivah Vachasimah Tovah*.

And regarding Havdalah, it is through the songs, for until the time of the end, when "I will remove the spirit of impurity from the earth," they only delay the calamities, as the language of *Pirkei D'Rabbi Eliezer* puts it, rather than nullifying them entirely from the whole earth—which is the action of the mitzvah itself. And this is not the place to elaborate.

***3757***

**Whoever is careful:** See also above, Letter 3688, and the references in the notes there.

*) Shabbos 113b and Rashi there.

**) See *Pirkei D'Rabbi Eliezer*, chapter 20, and the commentary of the Radal there. — *Iyun Tefillah* in the complete *Siddur*.

## 3358

B"H, 11 Elul, 5715
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter from Wednesday, in which you detail the various considerations regarding the choice of your place of residence after your wedding—may it be in a good and auspicious hour—and ask for my opinion on the matter.

In my opinion, first and foremost, you should take into account settling in Kfar Chabad, as my hope is strong that it is at the beginning of its development, and fortunate is the portion of each and every one who participates in this development to the best of their ability. If, for any reason—or for the reasons you write in your letter—this is not a consideration in your view, then you should settle in close proximity to your place of work in the holy labor of Heaven—that is, close to [the location of your work]—so that you will not need to waste time on travel, back and forth, in addition to the implications for your health and the peace of mind. Especially since there is room to say that for your bride, may she live, there will also be found there a broad field to utilize the talents you write about.

Furthermore, I wish to add that, as it appears from your letter, you have evaluated an extensive plan regarding the arrangements that, in your opinion, must be made before the wedding. Although I do not know the prices in Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established, in detail, it seems from the general outlines you mention that it will amount to very large sums, which I doubt you have at your disposal. And even if you had all the sums, it is doubtful whether it is worthwhile to invest them in key money and furniture. **It is obvious** that neither the external beauty of the furniture, nor even the exterior of the walls of the physical home, are the essential foundations for building a home in Israel. There is no need to elaborate on this simple matter, especially for one who has merited being a student of a Chassidic yeshiva, Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim. May Hashem guide you in the best way for you and for your bride—may you both live—in both physical and spiritual matters alike.

With blessings to hear good news in true goodness regarding all that was mentioned above, and to be inscribed and sealed for good.

**M. Schneerson**

## 3,759

B"H, 11 Elul, 5715
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter from the end of Menachem Av, in which you write regarding your son, may he live, his study schedule, etc., and conclude with a question that has arisen because he is careful, as required by our holy Torah—the Torah of life—regarding the matter of covering the head.

Fortunate is his portion and the portion of his wife, may they live, for having raised and educated their son, may he live, in this path—a path that brings happiness in both material and spiritual matters alike. From this, it is also understood what their attitude should be: to strengthen their son and encourage him in the aforementioned matter and in similar ones. This is especially true when taking into account that for the youth, all the details of the laws of Yisrael combine into one complete and whole structure. When someone shakes or weakens one part of this structure—whichever part it may be—it naturally brings weakness and instability to the entire structure as a whole, as is understood. Specifically regarding this matter, where the head covering prevents your son, may he live, from participating in a competition between two schools in a soccer game, in my opinion, this should be interpreted as a hint from Above that they wish to protect him from some mishap, Heaven forbid, that might occur during the course of that game and competition between the schools.

If it is as you write, that the non-participation in the competition makes an undesirable impression on your son, may he live, then it is worthwhile that he transfer from the school he currently attends to another school, and if one exists—a more Charedi school. It is understood that there is no necessity to explain the aforementioned reason to your son, and then, surely, within a short time, the entire issue will be forgotten from his heart.

On this occasion, I wish to express the great satisfaction caused by the news of your good activities for the support and development of the Yeshiva... and I am certain that the Rebbe, my father-in-law, of blessed memory, whose name is called upon it, is surely awakening great mercies for you and for all your household, may they live, in both material and spiritual matters alike.

With blessings for a *Kesivah V'chasimah Tovah* and for good tidings in all the aforementioned.

#### ***3,759***

**Covering the head:** See above, letter 3,752.

## 3760

B"H, 11 Elul, 5715
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter of 4 Elul, in which you write that since you have increased the shiurim I wrote to you about, you feel an improvement, yet you are not satisfied with this and are not content at all, for you wish to be an entirely different person, etc., etc.

The answer to this is already stated in the holy Tanya, chapter 27 and onwards. These words are addressed to the *beinonim*, and regarding the level of *beinoni* as explained in the teachings of Chassidus, our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe—who is the *posek* in the *nistar* of Torah and the *Shulchan Aruch*—the *posek* in the *nigleh* of Torah—says: "Let a person’s heart not fall within him," etc. It brings *nachas ruach* before Him, may He be blessed, Above, through the *avodah* explained there—see there—which, in the words of the Rebbe, should be done with great joy, etc.—see there.

In general, the task of man is as the Mishnah states: "I was created to serve my Maker." What difference does it make what service is given to the *Ribono shel Olam*? After all, regarding the greatest *avodah*, it is said: "If you are righteous, what do you give Him?" Conversely, even the simplest and lowest *avodah* is also called a *mitzvah*, from the term *tzavta* (connection) and *chibur* (joining), through which one connects with the *Atzmus* and *Mahus* of the *Ein Sof*, *Baruch Hu*. It is a pity to waste time searching for a "purpose" when it could be utilized to influence others with joy—and "others" also includes one's own body and *nefesh habahamit*. When this is done with joy, the success is great and is visible even to physical eyes. May it be His will that you also influence your friends in this direction, for through this, the assistance from Heaven in your own *avodah* will be increased.

Regarding what you wrote concerning *hisbonenus* before *davening*, etc., it is difficult to explain these matters in writing. You should endeavor to speak with the elder *anash* and *mashpi'im* of *Chassidus* in Eretz Yisrael, *tizkeh l'mitzvos*, and they will advise you.

With blessings for the fulfillment of the general and constant command, "Serve Hashem with joy," and for a *kesivah v'chasimah tovah*.

## 3751

3751

B"H, 11 Elul, 5715
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and blessings!

I was pleased to receive your letter of 8 Elul, informing me that you are feeling much better. May it be His will that you be completely well, and not only that the doctor should hold this opinion, but that you yourself should feel it as well. It goes without saying that you must take the vitamins, and if the doctor also provides a regimen for eating and drinking, you must follow it, for the body of a Yid is a holiness, and since the Torah says "he shall surely heal," the doctor is a shaliach of the Torah in this matter.

Regarding what you wrote about fasts, I have not heard of such a path (except in exceptional cases). [It goes without saying, this is excluding the fasts that are according to Shulchan Aruch, and also provided that the doctor says there is no danger]. It is better to replace fasting with refraining from other things that one desires, such as speaking *devarim beteilim*—and certainly *lashon hara* and the like. This wears out the *yetzer hara* more than a fast, and it does not affect a person’s health. Consequently, one has more strength to perform *mitzvos*, and *tzedakah* and *chessed* in particular. May Hashem help you to report good news in this regard as well.

With the blessing of *kesivah v’chasimah tovah*.

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita

## 3762

B"H, 11 Elul, 5715
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter, in which you ask whether the contemplation of Chassidic concepts during davening must be done specifically using the precise wording of the Rebbe.

It is not strictly necessary. On the contrary, quite often, when one contemplates the concept without focusing on the specific wording, one is drawn in more deeply and gains more vitality. Since this comes after having studied and focused on the Rebbe’s wording, one will certainly not deviate from the core point.

Regarding your question as to whether one should contemplate Chassidic concepts before davening as well: this is correct, as it is a halachic ruling in the Shulchan Aruch that before davening, one should contemplate the greatness of Hashem, etc.

With blessings for a *kesivah v'chasimah tovah*.

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,
Secretary

## 3764

B"H, 12 Elul, 5715
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 10 Elul.

In accordance with your request, I will mention both of you, as well as your children—may they live and be well—at the holy resting place of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, for health, livelihood, and peace between you all.

You should have the mezuzos in your home checked to ensure they are all kosher according to the law. You should also have your tefillin checked. Furthermore, every weekday before davening, give a few cents to tzedakah, and after davening each day, recite at least one chapter of Tehillim.

Regarding what you write about the children’s attitude toward their parents—that it is not as it should be—you must investigate whether this is not, as in many such cases, due to the parents not having observed Taharas HaMishpachah at the time the children were born. If, Heaven forbid, this is the case, the parents must make a firm resolution to do everything possible to ensure their friends and acquaintances observe and strengthen themselves in this mitzvah. This rectifies, to a certain extent, the great transgression the parents committed—by not observing Taharas HaMishpachah—against themselves and against their children. Especially when Hashem Yisbarach sees that the parents truly regret their actions and are striving to protect themselves and others from this, and are strengthening them to walk in the path of Torah.

Regarding what you write that your wife is entering the hospital these days for observation: May it be His will that it should be at a good and auspicious time and that everything should be successful. Until she leaves, she should give a few cents into a tzedakah pushke every weekday. May Hashem Yisbarach bless you to report good news regarding all the above.

With the blessing of Kesivah V’Chasimah Tovah.

## 3765

B"H, 12 Elul, 5715
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter from the end of Menachem Av. As you requested, I will mention all those you wrote about at the holy gravesite of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, for whatever they may need, as per the content of your letter. You surely know that the conduit for matters of hiskashrus in such instances is to walk in the paths he taught us and to fulfill his takanos. I trust you are fulfilling—or at the very least will fulfill from here on—the three daily study portions (Chumash, Tehillim, and Tanya) that are known as the takanah of my father-in-law, the Rebbe.

I am interested in knowing in appropriate detail about the activities of [Name]—may he live—in the present and regarding the future. It is surely unnecessary to awaken him, and his brother mentioned above, to the *chovas gavra* (personal obligation) that has existed in every place and at every time—all the more so in our generation, this "orphaned generation," and in a land upon which "the eyes of Hashem your G-d are always upon it, from the beginning of the year to the end of the year." One must do their part to strengthen and disseminate Yiddishkeit, specifically in a spirit of pure yiras shamayim. The responsibility is especially great for those whose *zechus avos* (merit of the forefathers) assists them—forefathers who also labored in this direction for decades during their lives on earth. This is especially true when we have merited the revelation of the light of the Torah of the Baal Shem Tov, his students, and his students' students—the general Torah of Chassidus—as it has been deepened and explained in the Torah of Chabad Chassidus, and regarding the greatness of the concept of ahavas Yisrael. [We must realize] how "loving Hashem" and "loving your fellow as yourself" are one and the same, as is hinted at in the statement of Rabbi Akiva that "love your fellow as yourself" is a great principle **in the Torah**, and as stated by his teacher’s teacher, Hillel the Elder, that even in the mundane—which is a translation of *kodesh*—this is the entire Torah (Shabbos 31a). [This is also seen] in his statement and guidance to "love the creatures," and as explained in Tanya, Chapter 32, and in *Sefer HaMitzvos* of our Rebbe, the Tzemach Tzedek, regarding the mitzvah of ahavas Yisrael.

Because of the magnitude of this matter, one must fear that it is precisely here that the *sitra achra* will offer the greatest opposition, especially from the "strange god that is within you" (Shabbos 105b). Having no other choice, the *yetzer hara* disguises itself in the cloak and arguments of a *talmid chacham* and a *yirei shamayim*. However, as our Sages said, "I created the *yetzer hara*, and I created Torah as its spice." Thus, they have informed us of this deception in our Torah—the Torah of life—and especially in the Torah of Chassidus. Consequently, with the necessary firmness from the side of true holiness, one can nullify even this cunning and the arguments it bases upon...

With blessings to hear good news regarding all that was mentioned above, as well as regarding your own personal matters, and with blessings for a *kesivah v'chasimah tovah*.

## 3766

B"H, 12 Elul, 5715
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

I was pleased to receive your letter of 20/8, in which you write that you are feeling a bit better. I hope that this will continue to progress from good to even better, especially during these days as we approach the *kesivah v’chasimah tovah*.

Regarding what you wrote—that one looks at the world with a feeling of joy—this is not, as you phrased it, a way to hide from the truth. Rather, it is a means to make life significantly easier. As is already well known, and as medical science is increasingly recognizing, a person’s entire state—even their physical bodily reactions and the way they perceive the phenomena around them—depends to a great extent on the person themselves and how they choose to perceive them.

It is remarkable that among the proponents of optimism in life, one finds that their own lives were often filled with what are called "troubles," while among pessimists, one finds many whose lives were seemingly good, lacking nothing... except for inner contentment and inner joy. Knowing the childhood of your father and mother and what they went through, it is possible that this, too, can serve as an example, to a certain extent, of the above. Therefore, it is no wonder that Chassidus, which popularizes the highest and best ideals, holds as one of its fundamental principles that in every event one can find a way to serve Hashem Yisbarach, and that in general, the service of Hashem Yisbarach must be performed with true *simchah*, for only then is it in its fullest measure.

For the New Year, *haba aleinu v’al kol Yisrael l’tovah u’l’vrachah*, I wish you and all yours—*shichyu*—a *kesivah v’chasimah tovah* for a good and sweet year, both materially and spiritually.

With blessings,

The *esrog* was just brought; thank you.

P.S. You may continue to write to me in Russian, even though I am replying in Yiddish for the convenience of the secretary.

## 3767

3767

B”H, 13 Elul, 5715
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter, which does not indicate the date it was written:

Regarding what you wrote, that I should forgive you for not participating in the elections: It is obvious that this is not a personal matter of mine, and certainly not a personal grievance. Rather, as I have written and also publicized my opinion in public, it is clear that anyone who has the right to participate in the elections (meaning, he has taken an identity card, pays taxes to the state, **and assists** in its other affairs—because he fears that they might imprison him, or that he will not have the conveniences to which he has become accustomed, such as water service rather than water from a well, and the like)—is **obligated** to participate in the elections. This is especially true since there is no assistance here to any particular office, and a single vote less for the most *chareidi* list increases the relative importance of the lists of those who oppose Hashem and His Torah...

With blessings for a *kesivah v’chasimah tovah*,

On behalf of the Rebbe, *shlita*,

## 3768

B"H, 13 Elul, 5715
Brooklyn

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing and upright, engaged in communal needs, Moreinu HaRav Nissan, may he live.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 6 Elul, thank you for the good news regarding the health of the students, so-and-so and so-and-so, may they live, as well as the doctor’s opinion regarding the health of the others. May it be the will of Hashem that you be privileged to bring good news and kindness, both materially and spiritually, both regarding yourself and those you influence.

Regarding what you wrote about... surely you are aware of my opinion on this. As for the proof you bring from the students who came here, you are surely also aware that, with the exception of a very few, I was not pleased with their coming here. To my regret and sorrow, I have realized that if only they had listened to me and continued their studies in France or in Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established. Furthermore, if it were in my power and they would listen to me, I would send the vast majority of them back across the sea—and a word to the wise is sufficient. You know the saying of our Sages: "We are distressed over the earlier ones, etc." It is also understood that what I am writing here regarding the students applies *a fortiori* to the *avreichim*, and even to the older ones, in all the aforementioned details—and even more so. What I am adding in this letter is that you have permission to publicize this at the appropriate time, for it is a pity to write letters to me about this, since from time to time I am even more convinced of the above. And if one does not wish to listen, why ask beforehand and then not listen?

Regarding what you wrote about the custom of the Sephardic students to rise early and recite Selichos from the beginning of the month of Elul: it is obvious that they should be left to their custom, the custom of their fathers, in accordance with the ruling of Torah on this matter.

And what you wrote—that this disrupts their learning—is incomprehensible, for there are enough hours in the day. On the contrary, if they rise early, this is an addition of time, and at the very least, it is not a reduction.

With blessings for good news, for a *Kesivah V'chasimah Tovah* for a good and sweet year, and for the preparation of the students during these days of favor in the manner appropriate and required for their own *avodah* and for their influence on others.

## 3659

B"H, 13 Elul, 5715
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter from Rosh Chodesh Elul, in which you write that your physical health has improved and you attribute this to the improvement in your spiritual state regarding good character traits: indeed, it is true that the physical is dependent upon the spiritual. This is especially true for every individual among the Jewish people, who are "one nation on earth," for it is precisely on earth that true unity is revealed, as explained in many places and alluded to in the beginning of Rambam, Hilchos Yesodei HaTorah. It is simple that even in this, "the study is not the main thing, but the deed"—meaning that you should completely divert your attention from negative traits, and as a result, over time, you will also be able to nullify them.

Regarding what you wrote about the well-known matter and its rectification: in our time, one should divert one's attention from this until after the wedding, in a good and auspicious hour. This is also understood from the Responsa of the Tzemach Tzedek, printed in Shaar HaMiluim, Part 2, Siman 62, that thinking even about the rectification of the matter is liable, G-d forbid, etc. Furthermore, you should not increase in *sigufim* (ascetic practices) and fasts, as explained in Iggeres HaTeshuvah by the Alter Rebbe. In such a case, the meaning of "not to increase" is that you should not engage in this at all, since it weakens the clarity of thought and the ability to focus on the study of Torah, and consequently, this is an increase beyond your capacity. Instead of these fasts, there should be the "fasts" explained in the saying of the Rebbe Maharash (Sefer HaToldot, page 72, see there). Likewise, you should increase in the letters of Torah and *tefillah*. It is also good to increase in speech, provided it is without affectation, and you should influence the youth to bring their hearts closer to our Father in Heaven. It is understood that all of the above must be done with joy. It is a great wonder that you write at length complaining about your situation, yet you do not mention your *shiurim* in *Nigleh* and *Chassidus* in abundance, nor your activities within the framework of Tzeirei Agudas Chabad...

With blessings for good tidings and for a *Kesivah Vachasimah Tovah*,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,
Secretary

## 3709

B"H, 13 Elul, 5715
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter from the beginning of Elul, in which you write regarding the state of your health, and specifically concerning your bad breath.

It is well known that according to our Torah, the Torah of life, for anything in the body that requires correction, one must act both physically and spiritually. Spiritually, you should be careful and increase your efforts in matters pertaining to the mouth—namely, to be careful to avoid *lashon hara*, idle chatter, and improper conduct regarding eating and drinking, and the like. Furthermore, in the vein of "do good," you should increase your engagement in the letters of Torah and *tefillah*, and in words of inspiration to others to strengthen them in Yiddishkeit, our Torah, and its *mitzvos*. As you are precise and increase your efforts in this, the improvement of your physical health will also progress. You should also seek the opinion of a specialist doctor to arrange a regimen of eating and drinking, as well as appropriate medications, as there is room to say that this is dependent on the functioning of the digestive organs.

In these days in particular, you should check your *tefillin* and the *mezuzos* in your home, and ensure that always—and not only in exceptional cases—you are wearing a kosher *tallis katan* with checked *tzitzis* every day, according to the law.

With blessings for a *kesivah v’chasimah tovah*,

On behalf of the Rebbe Shlita,
Secretary

When you provide your mother’s name, you will be mentioned at the *tziyun* of the Rebbe, *ztzukulalleh*, *nivgama*, *ziya*, Nasi Yisrael, for a swift and complete recovery.

## 3792

B"H, 14 Elul, 5715
Brooklyn.

To the Administration of "Sanhedri" Talmud Torah,
May they live,

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letter from the beginning of Elul, in which you write regarding the difficult financial situation of the Talmud Torah, etc.

Certainly, you are also aware of the difficult situation of the Chabad educational institutions, including those located in Eretz Yisrael, may it be built and established. The instruction of our Sages regarding the verse, "If you lend money to My people, to the poor person with you," is already well known, and despite this, "I am a companion to all who fear You," etc. Enclosed is a check as a symbolic contribution toward the expenses of your Talmud Torah.

May it be the will of Hashem that what Hashem desires shall succeed in your hands: to educate a generation of G-d-fearing and wholesome individuals through the "candle of a mitzvah and the Torah of light," and the "light in the Torah," so that all who see them will recognize that they are the seed which Hashem has blessed. May they instill—through the vessel and conduit of Ahavas Yisrael—the love of Hashem and the light of His Torah and mitzvos within the hearts of the sons and daughters of Yisrael, with an ever-increasing influence and the study of the knowledge of Hashem. And may the connection to the "Tree of Life"—in the language of the Ra'aya Mehemna in Zohar, Vol. 3, 126b—add life, light, and knowledge to daily life, increasing more and more until the fulfillment of the prophecy: "And no longer shall they teach one another... for the earth shall be full of the knowledge of Hashem."

With respect and with a blessing for success in your holy work to teach the complete Torah, both the revealed and the hidden, with pure fear of Heaven, and with a blessing for a *Kesivah Vachasimah Tovah* for a good and sweet year.

## 3793

B"H, 14 Elul, 5715
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed and distinguished individual, whose work is the work of Heaven,
R' Tzvi Leib, may he live, HaLevi

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letter of 4 Elul... regarding what you wrote concerning the number of lines in Tefillin and the custom of the Sephardim in this regard. There are two types of customs in every country. There is a custom that is precise and specific, or a "custom" that is actually the absence of a custom—meaning that everyone does as they please, and there is no fixed practice.

It is understood that regarding the first type, one should leave them to the custom of their fathers, and only when an awakening comes from their side should one consult each time on how and what to do. However, regarding the second type, one should, in ways of pleasantness and peace, introduce the custom accepted among us, since for them, too, there is no contradiction in this—and this applies to the number of lines as you wrote.

Regarding what you wrote about your conduct on the second day of Yom Tov, since you and your entire household, may they live, are located in the Diaspora, I see no room for doubt; you should celebrate the upcoming festivals in peace on both the first and second days.

I was pleased by what you wrote, that your studies are progressing and that you are striving to influence the students even in matters that are not directly part of your subject matter with them. After all, the goal of all matters is one: the complete acceptance of the yoke of the Kingdom of Heaven, especially according to the explanation that all mitzvos are included within one another.

Enclosed is a *Likkutei Elul*, through which you will surely merit to benefit the many, and the merit of the many is dependent upon you.

With blessings for success in your holy work and for a *Kesivah V'chasimah Tovah*.

***

 *) And one must further examine what he writes, that they are not particular about this and most of them—in 5710—[use] six lines, for this is the opposite of what the Mechaber writes in *Shulchan Aruch* 32:3 (and there is no one who disagrees), at least *lechatchilah*. Furthermore, they were stringent about this in the writings of the Arizal, and according to the customs of the Sephardim, as is known. Perhaps he encountered a mistaken custom. If so, it is obvious that one should introduce [the custom of] seven lines. And as stated above.

## 374

B”H, 15 Elul, 5715
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

...It is surprising that you do not mention a single word in your letter regarding the start of the school year—the quantity and quality of the students for this term, and so on—for, after all, this is the internal and primary content of a yeshiva. It is already known from our Sages, of blessed memory, that "just as the hide of a deer..." (end of Kesuvos 112a), meaning that the skin shrinks and shrivels after it is flayed. From this it is understood that whenever one increases the inner content, the skin and the externality—that is, all the matters about which you write in your letter—expand and spread accordingly.

With blessings for good tidings and for success in your holy work with joy, and for a *kesivah v’chasimah tovah*, awaiting good tidings.

## 3009

B"H, 15 Elul, 5715
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter of Friday, in which you write that you studied for several years in a Chabad yeshiva and left for various reasons, and that while you have good aptitude for learning, you are not diligent in your studies.

It is astonishing that you do not realize how alarming such a situation is. As for the reasons you describe as "various," they are neither various nor new; it is already explained in our holy Torah that there is only one cause: listening to the voice of the "old and foolish king," which is the *yetzer hara*. He strives to prevent a Jewish person from accepting upon himself the commandments of the *Ribono shel Olam*, foremost among them the study of Torah, which is equivalent to them all.

I am surprised that you do not mention what you are currently occupied with. In any event, you should strive with all your might—for "if one says, 'I have labored and not found,' do not believe him"—to continue your studies in a yeshiva, and you should learn with diligence and persistence. The matter depends on nothing but yourself. May the *Ribono shel Olam* grant you a year of success in all the above, and may you be inscribed and sealed for good.

With blessings for Torah study with *yiras shamayim*,

On behalf of the Rebbe, *shlita*,

Secretary

## 3796

B"H, 17 Elul, 5715
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

...Regarding your question about the *hisorerus* of the month of Elul: It is already known what is explained in *Likutei Torah*, *Parshas Re'eh* 32b, that during these days, everyone can receive the King’s presence, and He receives everyone *b'sever panim yafos* (with a pleasant countenance). Consequently, the matter depends solely on one's own will. However, since the *yetzer hara* is engaged in its craft and expertise (even though, in absolute truth, it also wants to be defeated, as is understood from *Tanya*, end of Chapter 29), it entices the person by claiming that his specific trials are such that it is impossible to overcome them.

As for your writing that you asked several people about this and did not receive an explanation as to how this is possible: You should study *Tanya*, Chapter 26, and *Iggeres HaKodesh*, Siman 11 and Siman 22. What is stated there is sufficient, provided that you do not allow the *yetzer hara* to incite you into believing that you are an exception to this rule. In general, the method of dwelling deeply on one's own troubles—even though part of them belongs to the world of imagination and the remainder is exaggerated—this contemplation and depth of thought brings no benefit, neither in spiritual matters nor even in physical ones. This also applies to what you wrote regarding your health situation hindering you, etc. While you must follow the doctor's instructions and conduct yourself according to his orders, this has nothing to do with the power of thought and contemplation at all. When such contemplation is absent, the state of one's health also improves on its own.

Regarding what you wrote about your birthday: You should certainly observe the known birthday customs. May it be the will of Hashem that you have a year of success in both physical and spiritual matters, and that you occupy yourself with what you are required to occupy yourself with—the three pillars of Torah, *avodah*, and *gemilus chasadim*. Consequently, you will be healthy in both physical and spiritual terms.

With the blessing of *Kesivah v’chasimah tovah*.

P.S.
Regarding what you wrote concerning matters of *hiskashrus* in relation to putting on *tefillin* of Rabbeinu Tam: You should consult with your *mashpia* in the teachings of Chassidus.

## 3797

B"H, 17 Elul, 5715
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, man of action, R' Dovid Nosson, may he live:

This avodah encompasses all categories of service along the three lines: Torah (Elul is an acronym for *Ane Li Yado V’samti Lecha*—"He provided for him, and I will appoint for you"—referring to Torah, for the words of Torah are receptive, as our Sages of blessed memory stated in Makkos 10a); Avodah (Elul is an acronym for *Ani L’dodi V’dodi Li*—"I am to my Beloved and my Beloved is to me"); and Gemillus Chasadim (Elul is an acronym for *Ish L’re’ehu U’matanos La’evyonim*—"a man to his fellow and gifts to the poor," as brought in the sefer *Arugas HaBosem*). Their foundation and prerequisite is the pillar of Teshuvah (Elul is an acronym for *Es Levavcha V’es Levav*—"your heart and the heart of..." as cited in *Baal HaTurim* on Devarim 30:6).

May it be the will of Hashem that for many years to come, you will continue to share good news regarding the above, both for yourself and for all your family members, may they live, both materially and spiritually.

As we approach the New Year, which is coming upon us and upon all of Yisrael for good and for blessing, I hereby express my blessing to you and to all that is yours: a blessing of *Kesivah V’chasimah Tovah* for a good and sweet year, materially and spiritually.

With blessing.

B"H, 17 Elul, 5715

In response to your letter—which lacks the date of writing—in which you write regarding the state of education in the yeshivos and yeshivos ketanos, and specifically regarding the curriculum.

With blessing.

## 3739
