3780

B”H, 18 Elul, 5715
Brooklyn

To the Administration of Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim who...
May they live.

Greetings and Blessings,

On this bright day, the birthday of the two great luminaries, the Baal Shem Tov and our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe, we recall the instruction we were privileged to hear from my father-in-law, the Rebbe, that the days of accounting for the months of the year—a day for a month—begin on 18 Elul.

Since the beginning and the head includes everything, it is fitting that the month of Tishrei, for which 18 Elul is the day of accounting, is the general month for the entire year.

Therefore, on this day in particular, each person must engage in an accounting of the days, weeks, and months that have passed. It is obvious that the purpose of this accounting is to learn from the past for the future, in the two paths of "turn from evil" and "do good."

If this applies to an individual, it is all the more necessary for those who possess influence in their immediate or even distant environment, and in matters upon which the merit of the many depends.

Especially when these matters are in the field of the education of the sons and daughters of Yisrael—the foundation and basis for generations and generations, as it is written: "For I have known him, to the end that he may command his children and his household after him, that they may keep the way of Hashem."

It is simple that, as in all matters of *cheshbon hanefesh* (soul-searching), we are warned not to distort the accounting or incline it to any side. In particular, we are warned against the self-deception that arises because "love of self covers all transgressions." Many paths and counsels have been given on how to guard against these errors.

Regarding work in the field of education, the advised counsel is to examine the results of this method of education, and to learn from this examination to know what requires correction in the current method—what requires negation, or what requires improvement and addition.

Based on all the above, my suggestion and hope is that regarding the holy educational institution which Divine Providence has privileged you to manage, you will conduct a righteous accounting—a true and honest accounting—in accordance with all that has been said above. The litmus test to guard against bias should be to observe the results of your education and its fruits over the years that this institution has been in your camp.

Such a duration of time constitutes an entire period in the life of the youth who are of educational age. The method of examination in this is also simple: by observing what happens to the students within the walls of the Yeshiva after they have gone out into the world:

How many of them have remained in the "tent of Torah"—the revealed Torah and the Torah of Chassidus? How many of them conduct themselves in their homes and their business affairs outside in accordance with the instruction of the founders of the Yeshiva—our holy Nasi—and their hopes? How many of them conduct themselves at least in the observance of Torah and *mitzvos* as is proper, etc.?

Similarly, regarding the students of the younger classes, for whom information is surely kept in the Yeshiva’s records, from these one should calculate: the number of those who continue their studies within the walls of the Yeshiva until they complete them, and the number of those who remain within the walls of the Yeshiva only for the time they require for other studies or other pursuits that are not founded upon the "mountains of holiness," etc.

Regarding the part of *teshuvah* and true regret for the past, to a certain extent, **now** this is a private matter for each individual. But regarding the resolution for the future, it is a general matter, upon which the merit of the many—or G-d forbid, the opposite—depends. From this, one can also understand the magnitude of the responsibility of each and every member of the administration, and especially those who stand at its head—on one hand, the magnitude of the merit, and on the other hand, etc.

Since our Nasi, the founder of the Yeshiva, is certain that he bestows powers upon all those who have the ability to influence the course of the Yeshiva—powers as much as is necessary and in their fullness—and furthermore, he arouses great mercy so that the work should be with extraordinary success, beyond the value of the powers themselves, it is certain that if any matters are not currently aligned with the goal and purpose that our Nasi set—the intermediary that connects the institution and its students with the *Atzmus* and *Mahus* of the *Ein Sof* B”H—the hindrance is only from the recipients. And only an empty vessel can be filled.

May it be the will of Hashem that, according to the well-known saying regarding the content of 18 Elul, which infuses vitality into the *avodah* of Elul, and according to all the hints in this word, the contemplation mentioned above will be sincere and truthful. It will bring vitality to the bitterness that comes through it, and vitality and added courage to correct everything that requires correction and to add as much as possible in all details of the institution.

Then you will surely see good fruit from your labor, to produce students of whom the title chosen by the founder of Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim can be justly said: "Candles to illuminate."

With blessings for success in conducting the accounting, in reaching the true conclusions, and most importantly—in the administration of the Yeshiva from here on in, and with blessings for good tidings in all this soon, and for a *Kesivah V'chasimah Tovah*.

## 3782

B”H, 18 Elul, 5715
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter dated the 10th of the month of mercy, in which you ask:

1) Regarding the specific modes of avodah for these days.

It is understood that avodah in general, and the avodah of teshuvah in particular, is according to the essence and character of each individual, and it is not possible to establish fixed rules for this. In general, you should endeavor to meet a few times with the mashpi’im of Chassidus in Eretz Yisrael (may it be rebuilt and established), and they will instruct you based on their experience with hundreds of students and avreichim, in addition to the tradition they possess from their own mashpi’im. Regarding the sefarim of Chassidus that are particularly appropriate for this time—it is well known that the Mitteler Rebbe’s *Derech HaChaim* is suitable. However, as mentioned above, and in the language of the Alter Rebbe in his introduction to the *Tanya*, reading and studying in sefarim is not the same as hearing it face-to-face, for one person’s intellect is not moved and awakened by that which moves and awakens the intellect of his friend; see there. And it is already known from our Sages, “Acquire a friend for yourself.”

2) Regarding what you wrote about immersion in the mikveh, and citing someone who said that going to the mikveh is of no benefit because it is merely a matter of habit.

This is the opposite of the halacha, and one might even say that he is mistaken regarding a matter of simple Mishnah (see *Chagigah* 18b and there; *Chullin* 31a; *Shulchan Aruch Yoreh Deah*, end of section 198). Although it is certainly a greater benefit when one has kavanah, as the language in the *Siddur* regarding the kavanah of the mikveh states: The act of immersion itself is insufficient without the kavanah of spiritual nullification; see there.

3) Regarding what you wrote about the connection between immersion in the mikveh (before) davening, see the *Siddur* there. This can also be explained according to the nigleh, based on the words of the Rashba—cited in the *Magen Avraham* at the beginning of section 4—that when a person rises in the morning, he is like a Kohen preparing for the avodah, and one does not enter the avodah without first immersing. This, too, is a matter of Mishnah (*Yoma* 30a).

Although they did not establish this as an absolute obligation—just as they did not establish a greater obligation, the immersion of Ezra, because the **tzibur** does not have the strength to uphold it—this is as the Rambam states in Chapter 4 of *Hilchos Tefillah*; see also *Likutei Torah* by the Alter Rebbe, *Parshas Tavo*, end of 43a.

4) Regarding what you wrote about farbrengens, and that the drinking itself is not the purpose.

The matter is simple. The intention of a farbrengen is to awaken oneself to Torah and mitzvos with vitality, joy, and bitterness combined. However, we see tangibly what is stated in our Sages’ words, “Great is the drink, for it brings [people] close” (though, of course, caution is required in this). This is also understood: if in a matter of punishment our Sages decreed regarding their wine because, in the end, it will lead one to accept his faith (*Shabbos* 17b), how much more so in a matter of goodness, where through this we work together for the one G-d with ahavah, yirah, and knowledge of Hashem. All of this comes specifically through the study of the pnimiyus haTorah, as hinted at in the Rambam, *Hilchos Yesodei HaTorah*, beginning of Chapter 2: “And how does a person arrive at His love and fear, etc.?” And in *Chovos HaLevavos*, *Shaar HaYichud*, and in the language of the Alter Rebbe in *Kuntres Acharon* to *Tanya*, 156b: “Knowledge of existence through the Seder Hishtalshelus is also a lofty and exalted mitzvah; on the contrary, it surpasses them all, as it is written, ‘And you shall know today, etc.,’ ‘Know the G-d of your father, etc.,’ **and it brings one to a whole heart, etc.,** which is the essence.” May it be the will of Hashem that you contemplate all of the above as is fitting, and the main thing is that these matters should be translated into action: the study of the teachings of Chassidus and walking in its guidance and customs.

With blessings for good tidings regarding all that is mentioned above, and for a good inscription and sealing.

On behalf of the Rebbe,
Secretary

Some of his friends in the yeshivah are asking about the above—if you inform them of the content of the above in an appropriate manner, they will not struggle with these same issues.

## 3783

B"H, 19 Elul, 5715
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed and distinguished, etc., R' Nosson Dovid, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

Following your long silence, I received your letter in which you raised a point regarding my writing that I had not found anyone who agrees with the author of the sefer *Ohr HaShanim*, who counts the emission of *zera levatalah* among the **count** of the *mitzvos*. You expressed surprise at how I could have overlooked the explicit statement in *Maseches Niddah*, page 13a, in the name of *Tanna D'bei Rabbi Yishmael*.

It is obvious that I could not have overlooked this statement of our Sages, as it is the very foundation of the author of *Ohr HaShanim*, and he cites it **in situ**. I did not write that I could not find a basis for his words, but rather that I could not find a **peer** who counts the emission of *zera levatalah* among the **count** of the *mitzvos*—not the Rambam, nor the Rasag, nor the Ramban, etc. This is despite the fact that it is obvious that they were all aware of the aforementioned *sugya* in *Niddah*. Furthermore, according to many *Rishonim*, this is only a prohibition *derabbanan*, etc. See also the *Sefer HaMitzvos* of the Tzemach Tzedek, in the *mitzvah* of *Pru U'rvu*, where he mentions **only** the author of *Ohr HaShanim* as counting the aforementioned among the *mitzvos*.

It is surprising that you have not yet confirmed receipt of my letter responding to your question regarding the *nekudos* and their calculation according to the *Zohar* and *Kabbalah*.

As you requested, I will mention you and your family, may they live, at the holy *tziyun* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, *ztzukulleh"h, navgam, zya*. May you and your family be inscribed and sealed for a good and sweet year, both materially and spiritually.

With blessing.

## 3784

19 Elul, 5715
Brooklyn

To the esteemed Rabbi, G-d-fearing, learned, and distinguished, who engages in communal needs and possesses fine character traits, etc.,
R' Dov Yehuda, may he live and be well,

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letter of 14 Elul: Although I am compelled to be brief due to the matters specific to these days—as is known from the saying of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, that in the month of accounting itself, which is the month of Elul, the days from 18 Elul and onwards are the "accounting of the day for the month" of the coming year—nevertheless, for the sake of the inquirer and the matters inquired about, I am writing these lines. I am certain that for one such as you, this brevity will suffice. Please accept my apologies.

Regarding what you wrote concerning the end of Chapter 8 of Tanya, regarding the "wisdoms of the nations of the world"—whether the intent is only for the wisdom of philosophy or also for other wisdoms:

It seems you wish to distinguish between them, suggesting that in the wisdom of philosophy there may be a prohibition due to the engagement with the anti-religious matters contained within it, whereas this is not the case with the wisdom of mathematics, etc. However, it is obvious that the intent is for all wisdoms. Aside from the proof—that he says "wisdoms" in the plural—it is explicitly stated there that its impurity is from *kelipat nogah*, meaning it is not the wisdom of actual heresy, which is from the three completely impure *kelipot*, as is the case with other matters of idolatry. Furthermore, he explains, "unless one makes them a spade to dig with," etc. This is **explicitly** stated even more clearly in *Hilchos Talmud Torah* by our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe, Chapter 3, Halacha 7.

2) Regarding what you wrote concerning the *sicha* of Shabbos Mevarchim Elul, that it is not applicable to say that a person would jump into fire inadvertently (*shogeg*). You expressed wonder at this, though you did not specify your wonder. Perhaps you mean that one could imagine a person standing on a high roof who jumps off because he does not know he will fall into a bonfire or the like. But that is not the type of case I intended, nor is that the true definition of *shogeg*. My intent was that in guarding oneself from a transgression, one does not need intellectual grasp and understanding; the natural feeling itself is sufficient. Just as an infant, before he has reached the age of reason, will not jump into fire—because when he feels the heat from afar, this unpleasant sensation prevents him from approaching the fire, not because of his intellect, but because of his natural feeling. It is worth noting that just as every matter of the *nigleh* (revealed) Torah is explained—and even more deeply—in the *nistar* (hidden) and inner dimensions of Torah, so too, every matter of Chassidus has a corresponding practical application that can be found in the *nigleh* Torah as well. This is relevant to the case of a "beast" (*shoteh*). See *Avos D'Rabbi Nosson*, Chapter 16; *Bava Kamma* 62b, and elsewhere.

3) Regarding what you wrote about the punishments of the Torah, their nature and purpose: According to what is explained in Chassidus, **their purpose is to rectify** the blemish created by the transgression. Just as the blemish concerns the transgressor himself and his affairs, as well as his influence on his surroundings, the rectification must also address both matters. The rectification of the second matter is as the verses you cite indicate: "so that they may hear and fear," etc. See *Tanya*, Chapter 24, in the *Hagah* (gloss); *Likutei Torah*, *Bamidbar* 25c, 86b.

4) Regarding your attempt to reconcile and harmonize the views of the Jewish philosophers among the *Rishonim* concerning angels—whether they have a body—where you suggest that they all intended the same view, but that the concept of "body" brought by one differs from the concept of "body" brought by the other: It is impossible to say that they do not disagree. According to the first view, angels are within the category of "place," as is elaborated in *Likutei Torah*, *d'h* "Mizmor Shir Chanukas" (the first one). According to the second view, one cannot even attribute form or matter to them, to the point that they are called "separate intellects." See Rambam, *Hilchos Yesodei HaTorah*, Chapter 2, Halacha 3 and onwards, and the commentaries there. If your initial thought is that they have a body, only in a more elevated manner, this is not at all necessitated by what is written there in Halacha 5 (see there and in *Moreh Nevuchim*, Part 2, Chapter 3). This has already been noted in *Tzafnas Paneach* to the Jerusalem Talmud, *Chagigah*, Chapter 2, Halacha 4.

As we approach the New Year, which is coming upon us and all of Israel for good and for blessing, I hereby express my blessing to you and all that is yours: a blessing of *Kesivah V'Chasimah Tovah* for a good and sweet year, in both material and spiritual matters.

With respect and blessing,

## 3787

## 3789

3789

B.H., 21 Elul, 5715
Brooklyn.

To the illustrious Rabbi and Tzaddik, G-d-fearing, learned, and scion of holy lineage,
Rabbi Shalom Yechezkel Shraga, shlita,

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letter, including the enclosure in which you discuss the use of a safety pin (presumably what you mean by *zicher nadel*) on Shabbos.

Understandably, I was alarmed by the conclusion of your responsum, which suggests that not only is it forbidden, but that one should even be concerned about a Torah prohibition, Heaven forbid. Far be it from the descendants of my father-in-law [the Rebbe Rayatz] to label so many of the kosher daughters of Israel in our generation, and in generations past, as having transgressed in such a matter. Who is greater than the *Korban Nesanel* (Shabbos 87, section 6, which your honor cites in your responsum), who was careful even to avoid issuing an explicit prohibition, writing only that he was puzzled as to why the world follows this custom, etc.? It is understood that according to the principle that it is a mitzvah to uphold the words of the Sages, it is certainly a mitzvah to uphold the custom of the pious women of Israel from many generations past, without anyone protesting against them.

Regarding the reasons for the permissibility, there are several points which, when taken together, explain the aforementioned custom:

1) With metal, and with a metal wire, there is no [prohibition of] sewing. Although there is no explicit proof for this, there is a mnemonic in the fact that we derive all the prohibited labors of Shabbos from the Mishkan. Even though there was also gold thread in the weaving, it is obvious that they did not sew with these threads, for such a surprising matter would have required an explicit commandment. From what is stated in *Menachos* 41a, which mentions *sichi*—which, according to the *Aruch*, refers to pegs—it is understood that there must be an element of connection, and it is entirely irrelevant in what manner, whether by sewing or otherwise. Furthermore, it is simple that even regarding *kilayim*, the verse does not mention "sewing," but only "together." Consequently, there is no proof from there for a liability for sewing on Shabbos. Any instance where one finds a connection or "sewing" that is not done with threads is specifically in a case where it is the standard way to connect things in such a manner. It is a fundamental principle in all areas that a prohibited labor on Shabbos is only liable when the work is done in its standard fashion, not with a change or in an unusual manner (*k'le'achar yad*), unlike the laws of *kilayim*.

Regarding what your honor wrote in your responsum, that Shabbos and *kilayim* are equivalent, in my view, one cannot say such a thing, for the reasons mentioned above. The proof from *Shabbos* 48, top of side b, is already well-known: "This is a connection, and that is not a connection"—see there.

2) The opinion of Rabbeinu Yoel is already well-known, and the halacha is decided according to him (*Shulchan Aruch Orach Chaim*, 317:3), that there must be a "permanent sewing." In the context of Shabbos, we find the requirement of "permanence" explicitly regarding a "permanent knot." See the *Shulchan Aruch* of the Alter Rebbe, 317, at the beginning, which explains that this refers specifically to something intended to last forever. (Even here, the reasoning is simple: since that is how it was in the Mishkan, where all matters of sewing and connecting were intended to remain that way forever.) In our case, we must add that with a needle, and specifically a safety pin, we see tangibly in all instances where they are used for connection that it is impossible for them to remain that way forever.

3) The use of a safety pin is, in most cases, for a need of the day. In such a situation, we permit [the action] even *lechatchilah* based on a double rabbinic prohibition (*t'rei d'rabbanan*), as is brought in many places. Based on all the above, in my opinion, a single fastening of a safety pin provides no grounds for objection whatsoever, and there is room to say that even two or three fastenings are permitted; at the very least, it is no more than a rabbinic matter.

I have not elaborated on all the above as much as is required, for others have already elaborated on this in their discussions in *Ginas Veradim*, Orach Chaim, Rule 3, sections 17-19, in the book *Tal Oros*, which supports the view of the respondent, and in the new book *Orchos Chaim*, section 340. A collection of all opinions on this matter can be found in the book *Ketzos HaShulchan* by Rabbi Avraham Chaim Naeh, Part Eight, section 146, paragraph 12—see there **at length** regarding all the above.

Incidentally, regarding what your honor noted as proof from *Menachos* (as mentioned above), you have aligned with the view of the *Gedolim* in the *Kuntres Acharon* of the Alter Rebbe’s *Shulchan Aruch*, section 301, at the end, as was also noted in *Ketzos HaShulchan*.

With respect and the blessing of *Kesivah V'chasimah Tovah*.

P.S.
As you requested, your responsum is returned herewith.

## 3390

B”H, 21 Elul, 5715
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

...Regarding what you write about yourself, that you are a *misnagid*—you will not hold it against me if I do not believe you. As is well known, the saying of Rabbeinu HaZaken, the Baal HaTanya and Shulchan Aruch, is that a Yid neither wants to be, nor can be, severed from Elokus. And since everyone now acknowledges that Chassidus and its directives are connected to HaKadosh Baruch Hu, and that through it one connects even more to Elokus, it is impossible for a Yid to be an opponent (*misnagid*) to it. There can only be a difference in the degree of closeness and attachment. Just as in other matters of Torah, where not every person—and not even *lomdim*—can fathom its end, which is deeper than human understanding, there are those who know a certain part more, and there are those who know only more. So too is it regarding Chassidus. May HaShem Yisbarach help everyone, within the entirety of Klal Yisrael, that the new year should be greater than the previous year in being more educated and having more understanding, and may this be in good health and with joy.

With the blessing of *Kesivah V’Chasimah Tovah*,

On behalf of the Rebbe, Shlita,

Secretary

## 3791

B"H, 21 Elul, 5715
Brooklyn.

To the participants of the farbrengen on the auspicious day of 18 Elul, the birthday of the two luminaries, the Baal Shem Tov and our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe, may they live:

Peace and blessing!

With pleasure I received your letter informing me of the good news regarding your farbrengen, a gathering of friends and companions on 18 Elul. Surely, through this, you have added to the general theme of the month of Elul, which, in the words of our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe in Likutei Torah (Parshas Re'eh 32b), is that "the King is in the field, and everyone is permitted to greet Him, and He receives them all with a radiant countenance," etc. As is well known, the adage from the early generations of Chassidus—which we were privileged to hear from the mouth of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory—regarding 18 Elul is that it infuses vitality into the matters of Elul, which are comprised of the three pillars upon which the world stands: Torah (Elul is an acronym for *Anah Liyado V'samti Lach*—"He caused it to happen to him, and I will appoint for you"—Torah, for the words of Torah are "absorbed," as our Sages of blessed memory said in Makkos 10a), Avodah (Elul is an acronym for *Ani L'dodi V'dodi Li*—"I am to my Beloved and my Beloved is to me"), and Gemilus Chasadim (Elul is an acronym for *Ish L're'ehu U'matanos La'evyonim*—"a man to his fellow and gifts to the poor," as brought in the sefer Arugas HaBosem). Their foundation and prerequisite is the pillar of Teshuvah (Elul is an acronym for *Es Levavcha V'es Levav*—"your heart and the heart of," Baal HaTurim on Devarim 30:6).

In order that all of this may be without confusion or obstacles, it is necessary that Hashem remove from us all things that hinder, etc., and bestow upon us all the goodness that strengthens our hands to perform the Torah, etc., "free to study in wisdom and perform the mitzvos" (Rambam, Hilchos Teshuvah, beginning of Chapter 9), the entirety of which is included in the accepted phrasing among the children of Israel: a good and sweet year.

With blessings for a *Kesivah V'chasimah Tovah* for each and every one of you, for yourselves and your households, may they live.

**As is well known, the adage:** See also above, Letter 3797, and the references in the footnotes there.

## 3793

B"H, 24 Elul, 5715
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing and upright, engaged in communal needs, R' Yisroel Noach, may he live.

Shalom u'Bracha!

In response to your letter, in which you write regarding the matter of the mikveh and drawn waters (*mayim she'uvin*), and in connection with this—that the matters of Rosh Hashanah are general matters. It is understood that you are correct in that the matters of Tishrei in general, and Rosh Hashanah in particular, influence the entire year, as is known and explained in Chassidus (in *Ateres Rosh* and elsewhere) regarding the precision of the terminology *Rosh Hashanah* (Head of the Year) rather than *Techilas Hashanah* (Beginning of the Year). However, on the other hand, davening also pertains to the entire year, and consequently, the minyan and the congregants—whether they are from Anash, etc.—are relevant. As to which of these two to choose, this is a matter that depends on one's feeling, and he should decide accordingly.

As we approach the new year, which is coming upon us and upon all of Yisroel for good and for blessing, I hereby express my blessing to you and to all that is yours: a blessing of *kesivah v'chasimah tovah* for a good and sweet year, in both material and spiritual matters.

With blessing,

**M. Schneerson**

The three *pidyonos nefesh* were received.

## 3796

B"H, 24 Elul, 5715
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 17 Elul, in which you write regarding the matter of sleeping in the Sukkah and inquire about the custom of some of anash in certain places regarding this.

You should inquire with them regarding the basis for this custom, as they are well-known to be observers of Torah and mitzvos who are meticulous in their practice. It should be known that there is much to discuss regarding the matter of sleeping in the Sukkah, but this is not the place to elaborate. There are other matters of this nature that even the most pious individuals do not practice, even though, on the face of it, the law is explicitly stated in the Shulchan Aruch without dispute—and, in fact, even more clearly than the law regarding sleeping in the Sukkah. For example, the matter of lighting Chanukah candles at the entrance of one’s house from the outside, which is explicitly stated in the Gemara and the Mechaber, as noted by the Nimukei Orach Chaim, siman 671.

It is surprising that you limit your letter to a question alone, without mentioning a single word regarding your shiurim in the revealed Torah or in Chassidus. Furthermore, you have omitted the custom of all Israel—a custom rooted in the early authorities who established customs, such as the Maharil and others—that from the time Elul begins, when a person writes a letter, he should include a reference to the blessing for the New Year, for "from his hand it is fulfilled."

With blessings for a *Kesivah Vachasimah Tovah*,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita

## 3399

B"H, 27 Elul, 5715
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

...I was distressed to hear about the lack of shalom bayis between your daughter and son-in-law, may they live and be well. I fear that the situation lacks nothing more than "glue." It is well known that the nature of glue is that when two hard surfaces are placed against one another and do not bond well, one introduces a drop or two—or at the very least, an extremely thin layer—of a liquid or gummy substance between them, and the two things then bond together. If there were someone to explain to each side, separately, that all the conflicts between them should be weakened and ultimately nullified over time through the goodwill of both parties, they surely would not consider this a slight to their stature and would begin taking steps in this direction.

May it be Hashem’s will that this happens soon and without difficulty (especially since they have already endured the heartache they have experienced in the past), and may you be able to share good news regarding this as well...

## 3800

B”H, 25 Elul, 5715
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

I am pleased to receive news of you from time to time through the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing and distinguished, involved in communal needs, a man of many accomplishments, R’... In general, simply knowing of the good health of a Yid is a source of joy; it is one of the particulars of the general mitzvah of "Love your fellow as yourself." This is especially true according to what is hinted at in the Rambam, Hilchos Deios, beginning of Chapter 4, that a healthy and sound body is one of the ways of serving Hashem. Since it is clear that this applies to every one of the Bnei Yisrael—who are a holy nation—that their very bodies are included in this, it is understood that this is more than just a simple joy. It is an addition to the matters of holiness in the world, for the very existence of a Yid’s body in this world adds to its holiness and prepares the world to fulfill its purpose: to be a dwelling place for Him, may He be blessed.

How wonderful are the words of our Alter Rebbe in Tanya, end of Chapter 49, where he states: "With an everlasting love You have loved us... for He left all the holy hosts on high and caused His Shechinah to dwell upon us... and You have chosen us from every people and tongue"—this refers to the material body, which in its materiality appears similar to the bodies of the nations of the world—"and You have brought us near," and so on; see there. This is emphasized even more in the mitzvah of tzedakah, in its literal sense—tzedakah in a physical way. One gives from the toil of his hands—with which he could have sustained his own life—and separates it for tzedakah to sustain the life of a poor person or to support institutions that those who are physically needy require. Through this, he clarifies, refines, and elevates the material and the physical until the Elokus and the word of Hashem that brings it into being, sustains it, and gives it life are revealed within it. This is why tzedakah is one of the mitzvos whose fruits one eats in this world, and it is what brings the Geulah closer. For the literal Geulah comes together with the inner Geulah, as the prophet says: "And the glory of Hashem shall be revealed, and all flesh shall see together that the mouth of Hashem has spoken" regarding every single matter in the world. Therefore, my confidence is strong that your participation through your tzedakah in various institutions and matters during the year that we are now bringing to a close has added life and light to you and to all your household, may they live, both in their physical matters and in their spiritual matters. And surely Hashem will fulfill His promise, "Tithe so that you may become wealthy," so that from here on you will be able to increase this participation with joy, a good heart, and a generous hand.

As we approach the New Year, which is coming upon us and upon all Yisrael for good and for blessing, I hereby express my blessing to you and to all that is yours: a blessing of *Kesivah v’Chasimah Tovah* for a good and sweet year, in both physical and spiritual matters.

With blessings,

The *pidyon nefesh* was received.

## 3801

B"H, 28 Elul, 5715
Brooklyn

To the Administration of Tzeirei Agudas Chabad in Eretz Yisrael, may Hashem protect it
Tel Aviv Branch
May they live

Peace and Blessing!

We acknowledge receipt of your letter from Motzaei Shabbos, the eve of 17 Elul. It is surprising that even now, there is such a long interruption in our correspondence, and this letter also contains no response regarding this.

I was pleased by what you wrote regarding the activities of organizing study groups for youth and children in various locations. You should certainly arrange a program for this, with the goal of unifying the various groups, in addition to the general goal of preparing them to be qualified—both in terms of their knowledge and, primarily, their desire—to continue in Chabad educational institutions. Without such a program, there is no end to the matter, and there is a concern that their work will dissipate, as it will not be centered around a focal point, or at least several points that serve as the "thread" running through this work.

Likewise, the initial report regarding the farbrengen of 18 Elul was received, and we await, as you promised, the continuation of this report. Surely, even if you do not mention it, you are busy with a detailed program in connection with the upcoming days of Tishrei. As a symbolic participation, you will surely receive one hundred lira from the special fund for this.

As we approach the New Year, which is coming upon us and all of Yisrael for good and for blessing, may each and every one of you, together with your entire family, be inscribed and sealed among all of Yisrael for a good and sweet year, and for outstanding success in your work within the framework of Tzeirei Agudas Chabad, in accordance with the intent of our Nasi, my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory.

With blessings for success and for good tidings.

## 3802

3802

B"H, Days of Selichos, 5715

Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and distinguished R' Tuvia, may he live:

Greetings and blessings!

Your letter and *pidyon nefesh* were received.

As we approach the New Year, which is coming upon us and all of Israel for good and for blessing, I hereby wish to express my blessing to you and to all who are yours: a blessing of *kesivah v'chasimah tovah* for a good and sweet year, both materially and spiritually.

With blessings,

**M. Schneerson**

Regarding what you wrote concerning the calculation according to their [the secular] count: It is true that the custom is as you wrote, but in all our lands, it is common practice to do so simply when there is some need or reason (and it appears that a different custom existed—**at that time**—in the place of the *Shu"t Mahar"am Schick*, Yoreh Deah 171, and *Shu"t Pri HaSadeh*, Vol. 1, 3; and therefore they objected—so as not to **change** to their count). And who is greater than the Rema in *Shu"t* 151, R' Akiva Eiger, and also the Chasam Sofer in the book *Igros Sofrim* (p. 93, 105). And in *Shu"t Chasam Sofer*, Even HaEzer, Vol. 1, 43, and others (cited in the book *Kol Bo Al Aveilus* by Rabbi Grunwald, p. 381).

#### 3802

Published in *Likkutei Sichos*, Vol. 16, p. 574, and completed based on a photocopy of the letter.

**R' Tuvia, may he live:** Bloy.

## 3803

3803

B"H, Days of Selichos, 5715
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the sons and daughters of Israel, wherever they may be,
May Hashem keep them and grant them life,

Greetings and blessings!

As we approach the new year, I wish to extend to each and every one of you, within the entirety of Klal Yisrael—in accordance with the ancient formula—a *shanah tovah umetukah* (a good and sweet year).

Rosh Hashanah, the beginning of the year, was established by our Torah as the time of year when the world was created—yet not on the first day of creation, but on the sixth day, when man was created.

The greatness of this day and of that creation does not consist in the fact that another creature was added, even a creature one level higher than the previous ones—just as *chai* (living creatures) is higher than *tzomei'ach* (vegetation), and *tzomei'ach* is higher than *domeim* (inanimate matter, earth, etc.).

Rather, it consists in the fact that a creature was added that is incomparably **different** from those that came before.

For **he** recognized the Creator within the creation, and even more: he elevated the entire creation to that awareness, and thereby to its level of perfection.

For to perceive and see Elokus within the creation—that is the ultimate purpose of the entire creation.

***

One of the primary traits that distinguishes man from all other creatures is the *bechirah chofshis* (free will) that the Creator has granted him.

Man can utilize this in two opposing directions: either, *rachmana litzlan*, to walk the path that leads to self-destruction and brings ruin upon his surroundings; or, conversely, to choose the correct path in life, and thereby elevate himself and the creation to its highest possible level.

And in order to recognize that path and find the conduct of life that leads to that ultimate purpose, the Torah was given to us.

The Torah is divine and eternal, and its instructions are for all times and in all places.

***

With his own intellect alone, a person cannot reach this, for his intellect is, after all, limited.

The intellect can only serve him by discovering and bringing out the inner, absolute certainty that he possesses, along with the *emunah peshutah* (simple faith) in matters that are higher than the intellect. Through this, he can vivify his entire being and find the correct path in daily life—which is the path of Torah and *mitzvos*.

***

On Rosh Hashanah, a person stands not only before the divine judgment, but also before a judgment regarding himself.

He must resolve that he takes upon himself to fulfill his task and duty: to elevate himself and the world around him to the recognition of the declaration, "Come, let us bow down and kneel, let us bend the knee before Hashem our Maker" (as the first man, Adam HaRishon, did on the first day of his creation, the first Rosh Hashanah).

This means living a daily life *al pi Torah*.

And not, *chas v'shalom*, to take the path that leads to the abyss, to destruction and annihilation.

***

And let a person not think: "What am I, and who am I, to possess such tremendous power?"

For we have, unfortunately, seen what a very small material quantity can "accomplish" in destroying cities and countries through atomic power.

And if even destruction has such tremendous power in a small quantity—when destruction is, after all, against the intent and purpose of creation—

Then for building and ascending higher, it is certainly and manifoldly greater. The necessary power is present in every single individual. For this, the Creator gives him special *kochot* (powers) and possibilities, so that he can elevate himself to the necessary height, help others do the same, and elevate the creation ever closer to perfection,

Until we arrive, ultimately, at the state where "every **creature** will know that You created it, and **all that has a soul in its nostrils** will say: 'Hashem, the G-d of Israel, is King, and His kingdom rules over all.'"

With blessings for *kesivah v'chasimah tovah*,

**Menachem Schneerson**

## 3804

3804

*[Late Elul, 5715?]*

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and learned, engaged in communal needs, R' Dovber, may he live.

Your letter from Tuesday, along with the *pidyon nefesh*, was received... Regarding what you wrote about Chassidic matters and stories prepared in English: surely you have access to the Kehot publications in that language. It would be good for you to select those most appropriate for your location and the local residents. If minor corrections are needed, you will surely be able to make them on the spot, provided they are done according to his [the Rebbe's] instruction.

Regarding the *nusach* of *davening*: you are doing well by *davening* according to the *nusach* of the Alter Rebbe, as explained at length in *Shaar HaKollel* and its introduction. And when [you speak to] all those who listen to your voice, you should also explain to them the matter of this clarified and refined *nusach*. May Hashem grant you success.

#### ***3804***

**R' Dovber:** Levin. Another letter to him — see above, Vol. 7, 1955.

## 3770

3770

*[Late Elul, 5715?]*

To the esteemed and distinguished individual, occupied in the work of Heaven,

R. Ze’ev Tzvi, may he live.

Your letter of the 12th of Elul has been received. Regarding your question on the words of our Sages, of blessed memory, that "there is no blade of grass below that does not have a *mazal* above"—and if so, how is it possible for one *mazal* to distribute two different portions: to some, a mixture of good and evil, and to others, no good at all? Namely, the *nefesh habahamit* in a Jew, which is a mixture of good and evil, versus the souls of the nations of the world, which derive from the three *kelipos* that are entirely impure.

It is understood that this is not the same *mazal*, Heaven forbid. For the former is *kelipas nogah*, which is an intermediary and ultimately ascends to holiness, whereas the latter are the three *kelipos*, which have no [process of] clarification, as it is written, "I will remove the spirit of impurity from the earth." If your intent was regarding the manner in which evil comes into being in general, see *Torah Or*, the *maamar* beginning "Lehavin Inyan HaBrachos," and in *Likutei Torah* on the three *parshios* there.

#### ***3770***

**R. Ze’ev Tzvi:** Vaber. Another letter to him—see above, 3771.

\*) See also *Tosafos*, s.v. "Ein" (*Avodah Zarah* 5a).
